O vos, tres chiers filz, je vos ai acomplit cest livre qui est li derriens de la science de medicine ensamble l’emplissement de lui, et ai fait la fin per ses expositions et par ses declarations.	O you, three dear sons, I have completed this book which is the end of the science of medicine together with its fulfillment, and I have made the end through its explanations and through its declarations.
Et m’est venu en vision que je le vos acomplisse avec cest traitier, qui est partie de l’uevre de mains, c’est a savoir «cyrurgie».	And it came to me in a vision that I complete it with this treatise, which is part of the work of hands, that is to say "surgery".
Et por ceu que l’uevre de mains est fortraite en nostre region et est etraingie dou tout en tout, si est perie li science et decopee, et n’est riens demorez de li fuers que les petites descriptions en livres des anciens que les mains ont muees.	And because the work of hands is fortified in our region and is strange everywhere, so has the science perished and been cut off, and nothing remains of its force except small descriptions in books of the ancients that the hands have moved.
Et de ceu est venue li error et li vanitez, et sont closes les ententions et est aloignie li science.	And from this have come error and vanity, and are closed the understandings and is alienated the science.
Or me semble que je la vuel vivifier ensamble l’ordination de cest traitier selonc la voie d’exposition et de declaration et de l’abreviation;	Or it seems to me that I bring it to life together with the arrangement of this treatise according to the way of exposition and declaration and abbreviation; 
et venrai ensamble les formes des ferremens de cautere, et des autres estrumens de l’uevre avec l’ajostement de la declaration et de preparation de li, sicom il est mestier.	and I will bring together the forms of the instruments of the cautery, and the other instruments of the work with the adjustment of the declaration and preparation of them, as it is necessary. 
Et por la raison de ceu que nuls boins maistres de mains n’est trovez en nostre tens, est li ars de medicine eslongié.	And for the reason of those that no good masters of hands are found in our time, the art of medicine is elongated.
Et covient celui qui s’en entremet sormonter en la science d’anathomie, si com Galiens dit, tant qu’il saiche la juement des menbres, et les formes et les conjunctions et les separations d’aus, et aient connissance des osses et des nerf et des brais et le nombre d’ous, et le demenement et des voines movans et des reposans, et dou leu de lor issue.	And it is necessary for him who undertakes this to climb in the science of anatomy, as Galien says, until he knows the judgment of the members, and the forms and conjunctions and separations of joints, and have knowledge of the bones and nerves and veins and the number of vessels, and the movement and of moving and resting veins, and their place of exit.
Et por ceu dist Ypocras que li nons avec le non est mout, et avec l’uevre est poc;	And for this Hippocrates says that the name with the name is much, and with the work little;
et meismement en l’art de main.	and similarly in the art of the hand.  
Nos vos disons en l’introite de cest livre que qui n’est conissans des choses devant dites, si se gart qu’il ne chiece en error et qu’il n’ocie les homes;	We say to you at the beginning of this book that whoever is not acquainted with the things said before, if he does not beware lest he fall into error and harm men;  
ensi que j’ai veut maintes fois plusors de ces qui s’entremettent de ceste science et si s’abandonent sen science et sens experiment.	in such a way that I have seen many times more of those who interfere in this science and abandon themselves to their ignorance and lack of experiment. 
Car je vis un fol mire qui copa I apostume de scrophules ou col d’une femme, et copa les arteres dou col;	For I see a fool look at an abscess of scrofulous or the neck of a woman, and cuts the arteries in the neck. 
por coi tant de sanc issit hors que li femme cheit morte entre ses mains.	For because so much blood came out that the woman fell dead in his hands.  
Et vis I autre mire qui traït une piere d’un home d’eaige, et li piere estoit grans;	And I see another doctor treating a stone from a man's body, and the stone was large; 
si emporta avec li une piece de la vessie, et fut mors li hons dedens III jors.	so he took out with it a piece of the bladder, and the man died within three days. 
Et je i avoie ja esteit apelez por lou traire, et vis la disposition dou malaide et la grandor de la piere, et soi bien s’on lou tailloit il en morroit.	And I have already been called for this treatment, and I see the disposition of the patient and the size of the stone, and well if one cut it they would die.
Et vis I autre mire qui prist en cure I duc de nostre terre qui avoit la jambe brisie, et avec la briseure ot plaie;	And I see another doctor taking care of the Duke of our land who had a broken leg, and with the break there was a wound; 
et li mires plains d’ignorance estraint la brisure sus la plaie as esteles par fort lieure, et ne lassa a la plaie point de xalain, et le lassa ensi I termine;	and the doctor, full of ignorance, forced the broken bone onto the wound, and did not put any lint on the wound, and left it like that. 
et li comanda qu’il ne la desliast mie;	and he commanded him not to unbind it at all;
et demora ensi que li jambe fut toute enflee et li piez et vint a perdition.	and so remained until the leg was all swollen and the foot and came to ruin. 
Je fuis apelez por venir a lui, et me hastai por venir deslier la jambe;	I am called to come to him, and I hastened to come to untie the leg;  
et quant je l’oi desloie si fut em pais et ne sentit point de dolor.	and when I heard it dislocate, it was in peace and felt no pain.   
Mais toute voie li corruptions estoit ja confermee ou membre, et ne la poi saner;	But by all means the corruption had already been confirmed in the member, and I could not heal it;  
et ne cessa li corrution d’aler par le membre tant que li membres fut dou tout perdus.	and did not cease the corruption to go through the member until the member was entirely lost.   
Et vis I autre mire qui effondra I apostume enchancreit, et puis enflama per le malice de sa signorie.	And see another kind which breaks open the abscess and then inflames by the evil of its lordship.
Car chancre, quant il est purs d’umor melancolique, ne covient mie qu’on i(l) touche de fer s’il n’est en teil leu c’on puisse toute oster ce que est corrumpus.	For a sore, when it is pure of melancholic humor, it is not proper that one touch it with iron unless in such a place where one can remove all that is corrupted.
Et por ceu, treschier filz, vos est besoig que vos sachiez que oevre de mains est devisee en II divisions:	And therefore, dear sons, it is necessary that you know that the work of hands is divided into II divisions:  
c’est asavoir, huevre ou il a peril en plusors dispositions;	that is to say, works where there is danger in many positions; 
et je mostrerai en chescun leu de cest livre ou il a paour et peril.	and I will show in each place of this book where there is fear and peril.   
Por coi il est besoig que vos vos en gardez, si que li fol mire ne puissent mal parler de vos.	For which reason it is necessary that you keep guard, so that the foolish ones may not speak badly of you. 
Si prenez vos armes en cusenson, et entreprenez vos malaides legierement et fermement, et usez de la millor voie si que per la graice de Deu vos venez a salut et soiez loez;	If you take your arms in caution, and undertake your patients lightly and firmly, and use the best way so that by the grace of God you come to salvation and be praised; 
et lassiez les maladies espoantables de grief saniteit;	and leave the hopeful diseases to good health;
et ostez vos armes de ceu que vos fait douter, et aiez foit en vos si que vos puissiez venir de cestui monde a l’autre de gloire.	and remove your arms from those who make you doubt, and have done in yourselves so that you may come from this world to the other of glory. 
Galiens dist en aucuns de ses amonestemens:	Galians says in some of his admonitions:
«Ne prenez mie en cure male maladie, que vos ne soiez apelez fol mire.	Do not take care of any bad illness, lest you be called a foolish one." 
» J’ai deviseit cest traitier selonc III chapitres.	I have devised this treatise according to three chapters.
Li premiers chapitres est des cauteres de feu et dé cauteres de medicine ague, et est li chapitres ordenez de lou chief jusques as piez;	The first chapters are of fire cauteries and cauteries of medicine sharp, and are the chapters ordered from the head to the feet; 
et des formes des estrumens, et des ferremens de cautere, et de tout ceu qui est necessaire en l’ueuvre.	and the shapes of the instruments, and the tools of cautery, and all that is necessary in the work. 
Li secons chapitres si est de taillier et de percier, et des ventouses et des plaies, et des estractions des saiettes, et des semblans choses;	The second chapter is of cutting and probing, and of suction cups and wounds, and the extraction of arrows, and similar things; 
et est li chapitres ordenez et les formes des estrumens.	and this chapter orders and the shapes of the instruments.  
Li tiers chapitres est de restorer les dislocations et des torcions, et des semblans choses;	The third chapter is of restoring dislocations and twists, and similar things;
et est ordeneiz des lou chief jusc’as piez, et des formes des estrumens.	and it is ordered from the head to the foot, and the shapes of the instruments.  
Ainsois que nos nos remembriens de l’uevre, il covient que je die la qualiteit de l’aide et dou nuisement de chescune complexion.	Thus as we remember from the work, it is necessary that I say the quality of the aid and of the annoyance of each complexion.
Je dis que li qualiteis de l’aide, et dou nuisement, est li plus longe parole et subtilz science et li secrez reponus;	I say that the qualities of aid, and of nuisance, are the longest speech and subtle sciences and the secret answers; 
et de ceu parlerent li plusors des saiges, et s’acorderent a ceu;	and of this speak most sages, and agree to this;
et me soffisent poc lor paroles, car je redous la longesce.	and I suffice few their words, because I fear the length.  
Je dis que cautere aide universement a toute complexion ou il a matiere, fuer que II complexions:	I say that cautery helps universally to every complexion or it has matter, except for if there are two complexions. 
c’est a savoir complexion chaude sens matere, et complexion seche sens matere.	That is to say, hot complexion without matter, and dry complexion without matter.  
En complexion chaude et seche ensamble matiere, deviserent aucun et dirent que cautere i est grans aide;	In a hot and dry complexion together with matter, some have said and declared that cautery there is great help;
et li autre dirent le contraire:	and the others say the opposite. 
que cautere ne vaut a maladie que vient de chalor et de sechour.	That cautery is not worth for disease that comes from heat and dryness.  
Car li nature dou feu si est chaude, et ne doit mie estre cureiz de chaude maladie par chalor, ne per sechour;	Because the nature of fire is so hot, and it should not be cured for a hot disease by heat, nor by dryness;  
et dist cil qui dist lou contraire que cautere fait grant aide a maladie chaude et seche que vient en cors des homes.	and he who says the opposite states that cautery does great help to hot and dry diseases that come in the bodies of men.  
Car quant tu comperes le cors de l’ome et sa moistor a la complexion dou feu, tu trueves le cors froit.	For when you examine the body of man and his moisture to the complexion of fire, you find the body cold.
Et je m’acorde a ceste parole.	And I agree to this word.
Car je l’ai troveit aucune fois per experiment.	For I have found it never by experiment.
Et toute voie, ne s’en entremette mie fuers que cil qui l’a esproveit, et qui conoit par lonc usaige le chapistre des cauteres, et la diversiteit des complexions des homes, et les dispositions et les causes de lor maladies, et les sorvenues et l’espaice dou tens;	And in any case, do not interfere unless he who has proven it and knows by long usage the chapter of cauteries, and the diversity of complexions of men, and the dispositions and causes of their diseases, and the appearances and space of time.
des autres complexions n’avons nos mie paour, meismement em maladies froides et moistes.	Of other complexions we have no more fear, even in cold and wet diseases. 
Et tuit li mire s’asemblerent et s’acorderent au cautere.	And all the masters assembled and agreed on the cautery.
Et sachiez, filz, que cautere ensamble feu si est des secrez des cures, et de plus grant bonteit que cautere de medicine ardant.	And know, sons, that fire cautery together with secrets of the treatments and more good than cautery of burning medicine.
Car li feus est simples, et ne vient mie fuers que au membre qui est cuis, et ne nuit a autre membre se poc nom.	For the heat is simple, and does not come forth except to the member which is burnt, and does not harm another member besides that one.
Les medicines ardans vienent de membre a autre en aloignant, et font venir au membre maladies de grief sanation;	The ardent medicines come from member to member by removing, and bring to the member diseases of bad healing. 
et par aventure ocit lou malaide.	And perhaps it harms the patient.  
Li feus por sa hautece et por la bonteit de sa substance ne fait mie ceu, s’il n’i a superfluiteit.	The fire for its height and for the goodness of its substance does not do this, unless there is superfluity.  
Et ceu vos ai je troveit par experiment et par la longesce dou servise et de l’estude que j’ai mis en l’art, et esteit sus la verteit des choses;	And this I have found by experience and the length of service and study that I have put into the art, and was based on the truth of things;
et por ceu je m’escuse de la longesce de la parole, car il ne me plait mie que je vos oste le secreit qui est reponus ou feu, et la qualiteit de l’uevre, coment il deboute les maladies des cors, si com li philosophe le dit en demostrant;	and for this I excuse myself from the length of the speech, because it does not please me that I keep from you the secret which is contained in fire, and the quality of the work, how it cures diseases of the body, as the philosopher says in demonstrating. 
or le recevez en vos pensees.	or receive it in your thoughts.  
Et sachiez, fil, que il s’acorderent en quel tens doient estre faites les cauteres, et eslirent prientens.	And know, son, that it is agreed upon in what time cauteries should be made, and how long they are to be applied.
Et je dis que cautere est covenable en tous tens, por ceu que li nuisemens sorvenans est desoz mis par l’aide dou cautere;	And I say that cautery is suitable at all times, for this reason that the harms coming are diminished with the help of cautery; 
et meismement se li cauteres est por dolors necessaires fors et hastans que ne puent atendre le tens que plus grans malice ne veigne au membre.	and also if the cauteries are for necessary pains before and until they cannot await the time that greater evil does not come to the limb. 
Et n’i pensez onques, chier fil, si com font li fol mire;	And do not ever think, dear child, as the foolish ones do; 
car a la maladie qui est sanee par cautere n’a point de revenue;	because to the illness which is cured by cautery has no return;
et il le dient ensi;	and they say thus;
mais il n’est mie si com il cuident, por ce que cauteres nen est que medicine qui mue la complexion, et seche les humors que sont cause de la dolor, et vaut mues que medicine por le hastement de sa valor, et por la vertut de son oevre et de sa signorie.	but it is not as they think, because cauteries are not just medicines that change the complexion, and dry up the humors that are the cause of pain, and are more valuable than medicine for the speed of its effect, and for the virtue of its work and of its power.  
Et possans chose est que li maladie viegne aucune fois selonc la complexion dou malaide et lou leu de la maladie et sa vertut;	And a most important thing is that the disease often comes according to the complexion of the sick person and the place of the disease and its power. 
et sont assemblees en lui les superfluitez par l’aquisition des viandes et des semblans choses, se ce n’est cauteres administrez em leu ou il ait poc de superfluitez et de moistor, si com cauteres de dens por la dolor, et les semblans choses, et teil dolor ne revient mie;	And these excesses are assembled in him by the acquisition of meats and similar things, if it is not cauteries administered where there are few excesses and moisture, such as cauteries of fire for pain, and similar things, and such pain does not return. 
mais ce avient poc.	but this happens rarely.  
Et mout de gens n’entendent mie por coi cauteres est apelez li derriens de medecine, et c’est voir;	And many people do not understand why cautery is called the last resort of medicine, and it is true.   
mais il ne croient mie que cauteres vaille aprés medicine, mais lor ententions est fause, et est cauteres li derriens de medicine por ceu que quant nos aministrons manieres de cures en aucune maladie et elles ne valent, adonc administrons nos le cautere, et il vaut.	but they do not believe that cautery is worth after medicine, but their intentions are false, and it is cauteries the last of medicine for those when we administer manners of cures in any disease and they do not work, then we administer our cautery, and it works.  
Adonques apert bien que cauteres est li derriens de medicine, ne mie selonc l’entention des folz mires.	Therefore it is clear that cautery is the last resort of medicine, not according to the intention of foolish people.
Li ancien dirent que cauteres d’estrument d’or est muedres que de fer, et ne dirent ceu fuers que por la qualiteit de l’or et por la hautece de sa substance;	The ancients said that cautery of an instrument of gold is more effective than of iron, and they said this those who were learned because of the quality of gold and the height of its substance;  
et dirent que li leus de cautere ne fait mie porriture, mais ceu n’est mie voir car je l’ai esprovei, et ai troveit que c’est voir en aucuns homes;	and they said that the lesions of cautery do not cause rot, but this is not true because I have proven it, and I have found that it is true in some men; 
et cauteres d’or vaut mues que de fer, si com il lou dirent.	and cautery of gold is worth more than iron, as they said.  
Et toutevoie quant tu chaufes estrument d’or, tu ne seis mie quant il est chaus par la color de l’or, et s’est tantost refroidiez;	And anyway when you heat an instrument of gold, you do not know when it is heated by the color of the gold, and it is soon cooled; 
et s’on le chaufe trop;	and if one heats it too much; 
si font au feu;	if done to fire;  
et ensi i a assez d’empechement.	and thus there is enough impediment. 
Et por ce usons nos de cautere de feir que nos l’avons mues apparilliet a nostre oevre.	And for this we use our fire cautery which we have seen useful in our work.
Or vos ai ordeneit cest chapitre des lou chief jusc’a piez, por ceu que li voie soit plus legiere a trover.	Or I have ordered this chapter of the head down to the feet, so that the path may be easier to find.
dou cautere olivaire	of the olive cautery
Cist cauteres vaut a moistor et a froidor sus lou cerveil, et en i a dous c’on fait par la cause d’une maladie qui est apelee «soda», et par la cause de maintes humors qui dessendent dou chief as eulz, et as oreilles, et por multitude de songes et dolor de dens et dolor de gorge, et meismement a toutes maladies qui vienent de froidor si com paralisie et sode et apoplexie et semblans maladies.	This cautery is good for moisture and cold on the head, and there are two ways to make it by reason of a disease called "soda," and because of many humors that descend from the head as the eyes, and ears, and because of a multitude of dreams and toothache and sore throat, and also all diseases that come from cold such as paralysis and stroke and apoplexy and similar diseases.
Li forme de cest cautere si est que li malaides soit espurgiez par medicine solutive mondifiant le chief III nuis ou IIII, selonc ceu que li vertus et li eaige et li acostumance dou malaide le puet soffrir;	The form of this cautery is that the patient be purged by a medicinal solution modifying the head III or IV, according to what the virtues and the age and the custom of the patient can bear. 
et puis fai rere lou chief dou malaide.	and then make an opening on the head of the patient.  
Et puis le fai seoir croisiet entre tes mains, et mettre ses mains sor som peis;	And then make him sit crossed between your hands, and put his hands on your lap; 
aprés met la racine de ta palme sus la racine de son neis entre ses II eulz;	after put the root of your palm on the root of his nose between his two eyes; 
et lai ou venra tes dois moiens, si saigne d’enche puis eschaufe le cautere qui est apelé «olivare», de coi ci est li forme:	and where your two fingers come together, if it bleeds then cauterize with the tool called 'olivare', because this is its form: 
Et le met sor le leu signiet d’encre, et fai en dessendant et en estraignant ta main poc et poc en trestornant;	And put it on the spot marked with ink, and make as you descend and withdraw your hand slightly pulling back and forth turning it;
puis lieve ta main isnelement, et rewarde le leu se tu vois l’os I sol petit;	Then gently move your hand slightly, and look at the place if you see the bone small. 
et se tu ne lou vois, si rencomence le cautere tant que tu voies l’os si com je lou t’ai dit;	And if you do not see it, then restart the cautery until you see the bone as I have told you. 
aprés pren I poc de seil, et met en awe et molle coton dedens, et met sor le leu, et li laisse III jors;	After that take a piece of silk, and put in it soft and moist cotton, and put it on the place, and let it there for 3 days.  
aprés met sus cotun moilliet en burre;	After that put on moist cotton in butter.
et laisse sus tant que li eschaudure soit ostee;	And let it there until the burning is gone.
aprés cure la plaie de l’oignement qui est apelez «tetrafarmaçon», tant qu’il soit sanez.	After that treat the wound with ointment called "tetrafarmaçon", until it is healed. 
Et se dirent li ancien, que quant plus demoure overte li plaie, plus s’espurge;	And they say the ancients, that when the wound remains open longer, the more it discharges.  
et por ce si aide mues.	And for this reason, they help to move it. 
Et dirent aucun de ces que on doit tant lassier le cautere que partie de l’os soit arse, et puis rese on ceu qui est ars de l’os, et soit curez.	And they said any of these that one must let the cautery so long that part of the bone is burned, and then sew up what is burned of the bone, and be cured.
Et dient li autre c’on doit le cautere tant lassier sus, et bouter si fort c’on abaite de l’os ausi large comme I vertoil que les femmes mettent en lor fusez por ceu que les humors issent mues hors;	And they say others that one should leave the cautery on so long, and put it down so strongly that one lowers the bone as wide as the whorl that women put in their spindles for those that the humors might come out moved.
et doit on lassier la plaie longement overte;	and one must leave the wound long open; 
aprés le doit on curer et sodeir.	afterwards one must cure and dress it.  
Et ces II manieres de cauteres ne me semblent mie estre bones dou tout en tout, fuers qu’en aucuns homes ou il ait voie de paor;	And these two manners of cauteries do not seem to me to be good at all except in certain men where there is a way of fear;
et mues me semble que je lou doie laissier;	and I seem to myself that I should leave him; 
car li chiés li est afoiblis par les solutions continuees de nature, si com nos le tesmoignons ens autres membres;	for the shoulder is weakened by continued solutions of nature, as we testify in other members;  
et meisme quant li chiés dou malaide est foibles par nature, et li premiere semblance de cautere est plus salve et muedre por moi, et de celi use je oevre en donques emsamble salut.	and even when the shoulder of the patient is weak by nature, and the first appearance of cautery is more salutary and effective for me, and from this I operate in thus as a whole health.  
de l’anciainne dolor dou chief	Of the ancient pain of the head
Quant en tout le chief vient dolor croniques, et dure longement, si doit user li malaides yeris et pilules qui sont apelees «cochie», et d’espurgement de chief et d’oiles et d’emplastres;	When throughout the head comes chronic pain, and lasts for a long time, then the patient should use herbs and pills which are called "cochie," and from purgation of the head and oils and plasters; 
et s’on li fait le cautere que nos avons devant dit, et il ne vaut.	and if one does to him the cautery that we have said before, and it is not effective.  
Pren warde se li chiés dou malade est de fort nature, et qu’il ne soit trop froit;	Take ward so that the shoulder of the sick person is of strong nature, and that he is not too cold; 
adonques le cauterize desoz celui cautere un poc que nos avons dit desus.	Therefore, cauterize there below with that cautery we have said above.  
Aprés fai cautere sus chescune corne dou chief jusc’a l’os, si com devant avons dit, et fai I cautere ou leu qui est apelez «vasselz»;	After do cautery on each horn of the head up to the bone, as we have said before, and do cautery where it is called "vessels"; 
et est I leus en coi on met ventouses;	and put there those where one puts cupping glasses;  
et alige ta main si que tu ne voises mie jusc’a l’os:	and alight your hand so that you cannot see up to the bone: 
li malaides sent trop plus grant dolor en cest cautere que as autres, et je em parlerai aillors;	The patient feels much greater pain in this cautery than others, and I will speak of it later;   
et covient que li cauteres des cornes soient plus subtis que cil dont on cautere la moieneteit dou chief, et c’est li forme:	And it is necessary that the cauteries of the horns be more subtle than those with which one cauterizes the middle of the head, and this is the form:  
dou cautere dou chief	of cautery of the head
Quant en une partie dou chief vient dolor sodaine, et est estendue li maladie jusc’a l’oil, et li chiés est espurgiez par medicines mondifians, et on a fait les autres cures que j’ai dit en la division des maladies, et tout ceu ne profite mie:	When in one part of the head comes sudden pain, and it extends to the eye, and the patient is purged by medicinal fumigations, and one has made the other cures that I have said in the division of the illnesses, and all of these do not help:
adonques li fai cauteres selonc II manieres, c’est a savoir de medicine ague et de feir.	Therefore I do cauteries according to two manners, that is to say of hot medicine and of fire. 
Li cauteres de medicine ague si est que tu preignes une doce d’alz, et oste l’escorce et le recope I poc as II chiés, et puis fent la temple ou li dolor tient en teil maniere que tu puisses reponre la doce d’alz desoz le cuir;	The cauteries of hot medicine are such that you take a piece of lead and remove the rind and cut it into two pieces as big as your thumb, and then put the temple where the pain holds in such manner that you can replace the piece of lead under the skin. 
et quant elle sera reponuee si le lie et l’estraint bien et le laisse ensi XII houres;	And when it will be replaced, so tie and hold it well and leave it thus for twelve hours. 
et puis le deslie et trait fuers la doce d’ail, et laisse la plaie ensi II jors ou III;	and then untie it and treat the wound with lead, and leave the wound thus for two or three days. 
puis met sus cotun plongiet en burre tant que porreture en isse.	Then put a poultice soaked in butter on top until it heals. 
Aprés le cure d’oignement tant qu’il soit sanez;	After the cure of ointment until it is healed.
et se tu vues si fai ceu d’aucunes medicines comburans que j’ai escrites ou dozime traitier des medicines comburans.	And if you see such things done of certain medicines burning which I have written or do as I have treated burning medicines. 
Li cautere de fer si est selonc ceste meniere.	The iron cautery is done this way.
Chaufe le cautere de coi ci est li forme:	Heat the cautery of which here is the form:
Et est apelez «clos» por ceu que li chief est fait a la forme d’un clo ou il ait I poc de corbeure, et em mileu a une petite apparance;	And is called "closed" because the head is made in the shape of a clasp or it has the point of curvature, and in the middle a small appearance. 
et le met sor le leu dolorous, et tien ta main et trestorne le feir un poc legierement, tant que li moitiez de l’espés dou keur soit arse;	And put it on the painful place, and hold your hand and touch the iron lightly a little, until half of the thickness of the heart is burned.  
et lieve ta main que li artere n’arde, que est defuers, et decorre habundance de sanc.	And lift your hand so that the artery does not burn, which is outside, and flows an abundance of blood. 
Aprés met coton en awe de seil, et met sor le leu par III jors;	After put cotton in a wad of silk, and put it on the place for three days.
puis i met coton moilliet em burre, et puis cure le leu d’oignement tant qu’il soit sanez;	then put cotton moistened in butter, and then treat the place with ointment until it is healed. 
et se tu vuelz cauterize ceste emigraine avec le cautere qui est apelez «cultellare», a tout la pointe, et te garde de coper l’artere en ceste emigraine qui n’est mie anciaine.	And if you want to cauterize this migraine with the cautery called "cultellare," at its whole point, and keep from covering the artery in this migraine which is not ancient. 
de emigraine	of migraine
Quant tu cures emigraine si com nos avons devant dit en divisions des maladies, et ne profite mie, et vois que li cauteres devant dis de la medicine et dou fer ne li soffit mie, adonques covient il que tu eschaufes le cautere qui est apelez «cultellare» tant qu’il soit blans;	When you treat migraine as we have said before in the divisions of illnesses, and it does not profit, and see that the cauteries before said of the medicine and of iron do not help him, then it is necessary that you heat the cautery which is called "cultellare" until it is white; 
et seigne ainsois sor le leu doillant une ligne de demi doi de lonc, et oste ta main une fois, et l’estrain que tu ne coper l’artere et que ne viegnes jusc’a l’os;	and then reign so on the place ailing a line of half a finger of long, and remove your hand once, and strain that you do not cut the artery and that you do not come up to the bone; 
et te warde de la mandibule que muet quant on menjut, et li ners n’ait regart que la muet et que spasmus ne veigne a malaide, et te warde de decorrement de sanc de l’artere quant elle sera copee, ou copement ait grant paour et meismement a celui que ne s’i conoit, et qui n’est estudians et esprovez;	and guard the jaw that it moves when one brings it up, and the nerve is not looked at except by the movement and that spasm does not come to the patient, and guard against loss of blood from the artery when it will be cut, or cutting has great fear and even for him who does not know about it, and who is not studying and experienced; 
et laisse l’uevre em mi voie;	and let the work be halfway done; 
mais je vos dirai coment on restainche sanc quant li artere est copee, et je vos mostrerai a leu ou il afiert en cest livre.	But I will tell you how to restrain blood when the artery is cut, and I will show you where it appears in this book. 
Et se tu vois que cist cauteres ne soffise mie a la maladie, et li malaides est soffrans, cauterize le enmi le chief ausi com nos avons dit, et cure la plaie tant qu’elle soit sanee;	And if you see that this cautery does not suffice to the sickness, and the patient is suffering, cauterize the middle as we have said, and cure the wound until it is healed; 
et se tu vues, aministre le cautere que nos avons dit ou chapistre de l’estraction de l’artere, avec le cautere qui ait II coutelz;	And if you see, administer the cautery that we have said in the chapter of the extraction of the artery, with the cautery that has two blades; 
et est cist cauteres millors de celui et plus aidans.	and this cautery is better than that one and more helpful.   
de la dolor des oreilles de part froidor	of the pain of the ears from cold
Quant en l’oreille vient dolor de froit, et on i a ovreit de medicines solutives et des autres cures que nos avons dit en la division, et li dolors ne se muet, adonques eschaufe cest cautere qui est apelez «poins», de coi ci est li forme:	When in the ear comes pain from cold, and one puts there opening of medicines solutives and other cures that we have said in the division, and the pains do not change, then take this cautery which is called "point," for this is the form.
Aprés pointoie tout entor l’oreille malaide, ou entor les II se la dolor tient en ambedous, et t’esloigne un poc ensus de la racine de l’oreille puis que tu as signiet le leu d’enche;	After, prick all around the ear of the sick person, or where the pain is felt in both, and move it a little above the root of the ear once you have marked the place to cut. 
et ait X poins entor chescune oreille;	and there are 10 points around each ear;  
aprés cure le leu tant qu’il soit sanez.	after curing the place until it is healthy.  
de la torture de la bouche	of the mouth's torture
Torture qui doit estre curee par cautere nen est fuers que de celles que muevent de fleume, si com nos avons dit en divisions des maladie;	Torments which must be cured by cautery are only those that move with phlegm, as we have said in the divisions of disease; 
et ne faire point de cautere as semblances que vienent de sechor et de spame de ners.	and do not make cautery to the appearances that come from dryness and  spasm of nerves.   
Quant tu cures ceste semblance de torture qui muet de fleume d’ydres et d’espurgemens de chief et de gargarisme, et ceu ne vaut, adonc covient que tu cauterizes le malaide de III cauteres:	When you cure this appearance of torment that moves with phlegm of  eyes and purges of head and gargles, and it is not worth it, then it is necessary that you cauterize the patient with 3 cauteries:
l’une en la racine de l’oreille, et l’autre un poc defuers la temple, et le tier en l’ajostement des II levres;	one at the root of the ear, and the other a point  four fingers away from the temple, and the third at the adjustment of the two lips; 
et met le cautere en la partie qui apert saine, et li fai cautere endroit le chief de l’oreille desus un poc desoz la corne dou chief, et un autre en la temple ausi longe com uns poce;	and put the cautery in the part that opens healthy, and make cautery at the top of the ear above a finger below the horn of the head, and another one in the temple as long as a finger;
et laisse le cautere tant sus que li moitiez dou keur soit arse;	and let the cautery remain there as long as the middle of the heart is burned 
et c’est li forme dou cautere:	and this is the form of the cautery:  
Et est li semblance dou cutellaire que nos avons mise devant, mais il est un poc plus subtilz et covient que li coutelz soit un poc plus gros;	And it is similar to the scalpel that we have put in front, but it is a little finer and it is necessary for the blade to be a bit thicker; 
aprés cure lou leu si com j’ai devant dit, tant qu’il soit sanez.	after healing its place as I said before, until it is healed.  
Quant apoplexie est ancieinne et tu la cures ensi com nos avons dit, et il ne profite mie, et li malaides n’ait fievre, adonques li fai IIII cauteres:	When the apoplexy is old and you cure it as we have said, and it does not benefit, and the patient does not have a fever, then I make IV cauteries:   
II sus les II cornes dou chief, et I emmi le chief, et I ou leu qui est apelez «vasselz» si com nos avons devant dit, et lou derrien cautere sus la bouche de l’estomac;	II on the II horns of the head, and I remove the head, and I put in the place that is called “vessels” as we have said before, and the last cautery on the mouth of the stomach; 
et soit curez si com nos avons dit devant.	and be cured as we have said before.  
de litargie	of lethargy
A cest maladie covient doner au malaide yeres grans et pilules mondifians le cerveil;	For this illness it is fitting to give the patient large doses and pills that make the brain swell up. 
aprés reis lou chief dou malaide tout, et li met sus l’occipite l’emplaustre de sinapi qui est escrit ou traitier des emplastres;	after the king has treated the head of the patient completely and he places on the nape of the neck the ointment of mustard which is written about or treated in the treatise of ointments. 
et c’est li maniere dou cautere:	and this is the manner of the cautery: 
si lou fai si com j’ai dit.	if you do it as I have said.  
S’il est sanez ensi, boin est;	If he is sound thus, well and good;
et s’il ne l’est, se li fai III cauteres des emmi le chief en dessendant jusc’a col, et ait d’espaice entre chescun cautere I doi de gros;	and if he is not, then make three cauteries of him in the middle of the head descending to the neck, and there should be one finger's breadth between each cautery. 
et le cure si com les autres, et se tu i vues ajoster, et li malaides est soffrans, se li fai I cautere en mileu;	and treat it like the others, and if you see it is getting worse, and the patient is suffering, then make one cautery in the middle; 
et se mestiers est, II autres sus les II cornes, et le cure tant qu’il soit sanez;	and if it is necessary, two others on the two horns, and treat it until it is sound; 
et soit li cauteres qui est apelez «olivare», si com j’ai devant dit.	and let the cautery be called "olivare," as I have said before.  
de la froidor dou chief	of the cold of the head
Il covient que li chief soit mundifiez de yeres et de ceu que nos avons devant dit;	It is necessary that the head be cleansed of herbs and what we have said before; 
aprés reis le chief dou malaide, puis li fai cautere emmi le chief et sus chescune corne, et I derrier et III sus l’espinee dou col;	After the king of the head of the sick person, then I make cautery on the head and under each horn, and in the back and III on the spine of the neck. 
et se tu en as plus mestier, et li cors est moiste et li malaides est soffrans, et li maladie est fors, se li fai IIII cauteres sus l’espinee dou dos;	And if you need more, and the body is moist and the sick person is suffering, and the illness is severe, then I make IV cauteries on the spine of the back.  
et li laisse tant que li plus dou keur soit ars, et lieve ta main;	And let him until the pus of the heart is burnt, and lift your hand. 
aprés le cure tant qu’il soit sanez, et soit li cauteres qui est apelez «olivare» que nos avons devant dit.	After curing as long as it is healed, and be the cautery that is called "olivare" that we have said before. 
de l’epilempsie	of epilepsy
Li epilentiques ne doit useir de cautere fuers que cil qui est fleumatique, et covient premier mondifier le cerveil de yeres et d’autres cures que nos avons dites en la division quant li malaides est grans et soffrans de penre medicine.	The epileptic ones should not use fire cautery except that one who is phlegmatic, and it conviene first to modify the brain of herbs and other cures that we have said in the division when the patient is great and suffers from bad medicine.
Et se c’est uns enfes qui ne lou puisse soffrir, se li fai gargarisme et mastication mondifiant le cerveil sovent avec bones viandes;	And if it's a child who can't endure it, then I make gargles and chewing modifying the brain often with good meats.
aprés li reis lou chief em mileu, et i fai I cautere selonc ce que nos avons dit devant, et I cautere sus lou vassel, et sus chescune corne;	After the king of his head in the middle, and I make I cautery according to what we have said before, and I cautery on the vessel, and on each horn. 
et se li malaides est fors et soffrans, se li fai cauteres si com j’ai dit a celui qui ait paralisie et mollification de cors, sus l’espinee dou dos et dou col, et soit li cauteres olivier selonc la maniere que j’ai dit.	and if the patient is weak and suffering, make cautery as I have said to one who has paralysis and softening of the body, on the spine of the back and neck, and let the cauteries be olive-shaped according to the manner that I have said. 
Se li malaides est enfes, se li fai I cautere subtil selonc ceste maniere:	If the patient is a child, do the cautery subtly according to this manner.
Quant par la cause de melancolie sunt les superfluitez ou les moistors corrumpues et fleume grosse, adonques lou cauterize de teils cauteres com nos avons dit a celui qui ait paralisie.	When by reason of melancholy are the superfluities or humors corrupted and phlegm thick, then one cauterizes with those cautery as we have said to him who has paralysis.
Et se par la cause de melancolie est li superfluitez declinans a melancolie, et est li cors dou malaide moistes, adonc li done a boivre chose par coi li cervelz soit mundifiez, selonc ceu qu’il est devant en la division.	And if by reason of melancholy the superfluities are declining to melancholy, and the body of the sick man is moistened, then give him to drink something by which the brain may be purified, according to that which is before in the division.
Aprés reis lou chief dou malaide;	After place the head of the patient; 
aprés fai I torteil de lin bien fait, ausi com I cercle, si le met emmi le chief;	After making a linen pad well, as well as the circle, put it within the head. 
et li malaides sié croisiez, et soit bien tenus de toutes pars;	And the patient sits crossed-legged, and be held well on all sides;  
aprés presente le linement, et vaut mues de burre de berbis ancien;	After applying the linen, take some old sheep butter and apply it. 
et lou chaufe a feu tempreement, si que li dois s’on li boute le puisse soffrir;	And heat it to a fire moderately so that if one places it on, they can suffer it;  
aprés vuide le cercle par dedens emmi le chief, et lou laisse refroidier;	After removing the circle from within the head, and let it cool. 
et fai ce a malaide chescune semaine une fois avec autre governement boin, tant qu’il soit sanez.	And do this to the patient each week once with another good government, until he is healed. 
Ou se tu vues cauterize lou en faisant poins plusors a tot le cautere.	Or if you see cauterize him by making more points all over the cautery.
Ceste maniere de cautere amoistit le cerveil igaument;	This manner of cautery soothes the brain greatly;
et puis met sus coton moilliet en burre et en graisse de geline.	and then places moistened cotton in butter and goose fat.  
de l’awe des eulz	of the awing of the eyes
Quant awe vient premierement as eulz par les signes que j’ai dit en la division, adonques encomence et done boivre au malaide chose mundifiant le chief, et le warde de toutes moistors, et lou fai suer ou bain plusors fois a jeun.	When it comes first to the eyes by the signs that I have said in the division, then begin and do drink to the patient a thing purifying the head, and keep him from all moisture, and let him sweat or bathe more times fasting.
Aprés li comande a rere son chief, et li fai cautere emmi le chief, et li fai II cauteres sus les II temples se li dessendemens de l’awe est as II eulz ensamble, ou en I se li dessendemens est en I;	After, he commands him to put his head back, and has cautery placed within the head, and has two cauteries on the two temples if the descent of the awe is to the two eyes together, or one if the descent is in one. 
et cope a tout le cautere toutes les voines et les arteres que sont desoz le keur, et soient li cautere lonc selon lou large de la temple;	And apply the entire cautery to all veins and arteries that are below the heart, and let the cautery be long according to the width of the temple. 
et te warde de decorrement de sanc, et se tu vois trop de sanc issir, si li estainche de teil pooir com tu as.	And guard against the decrease of blood, and if you see too much blood issuing, then restrain it with such power as you have.  
Et je t’enseignerai en l’estraction des arteres et a l’incision la cautele coment tu l’estencheras;	And I will teach you in the extraction of arteries and in the incision the cautery how to stop it. 
et aucune fois fait on cautere ou hatereil desoz les II os derrier.	And at no time is cautery or a hot iron applied below the two bones behind.   
dou cors des larmes	of the body of tears
Quant les larmes des eulz sont ancienes et acostumees et sont sus les voines, ou delez les arteres que sont en l’aparance dou chief defors;	When the tears of the eyes are old and accustomed and are on the veins, or beside the arteries that are in the appearance of the head outside.
et on voit que c’est des superfluitez froides fleumatiques, adonques li fai le cautere que j’ai dit en l’encomencement de l’awe dessendant as eulz:	And one sees that it is superfluous cold phlegm, then I make the cautery that I said at the beginning of the work descending to the eyes.
I cautere emmi le chief, et II cauteres sus les II temples, et II cauteres ou haiterel desoz les II os;	With cautery I burn the head, and two cauteries on the two temples, and two cauteries where hair grows under the two bones. 
et s’il i a besoigne plus, si le cauterize saigement desus le sorcil a tout I petit cautere.	And if it is needed more, cauterize carefully above the eyebrow with small cauteries.  
dou cors des larmes par dedens les eulz	Tears from within the eyes
Quant tu le medicines selonc ceu que nos avons dit en la division, et il ne profite mie, adonques done a boivre a malaide III nuis cochies;	When you medicate according to what we said in the division, and it does not benefit, then give the patient three walnuts. 
aprés li reis le chief, et li fai cautere ou mileu dou cautere olivaire;	After he has laid down his head, and you make cautery in the middle with olive oil cautery;  
et fai II cauteres dou cautere qui est apelez «clavilis» sus les II sorcis, un poc desoz les chevous;	and make II cauteries of the cautery that is called "clavilis" on the II sores, one point below the cheeks.  
et te warde de l’artere que tu ne la coper.	and guard yourself from the artery so that you do not cover it. 
Et c’est li forme dou cautere qui est apelez «clavilis»:	And this is the form of the cautery that is called "clavilis":
Quant li papiere de l’oil est mollifie de maladie et de moistor, adonques la cautarize de cest cautere qui est apelez «olivare».	When the parchment of the eye is softened by illness and moisture, then the cauterization of this cautery which is called “olivare”.
de coi ci est li forme:	of this is the form:
Et se tu vues si fai II cauteres sus les II sorcis ausi lons com li sorcilz sont;	And if you see so make II cauteries on the II sores as long as the eyebrows are;
et n’i lassiez mie la main fors que tant que li tierce partie de la papiere soit arse, selonc la maniere que j’ai dit.	and do not leave the hand except until the third part of the paper is burned, according to the manner that I have said.  
dou poil qui point l’oil	The hair that pricks the eye
Aucune fois avient que li poil des oilz sont convertit au pardedens, et poignent l’oil, et i fait on cauteres selonc II manieres:	Sometimes it happens that the hairs of the eyes are converted to the eyelids, and prick the eye, and one does cauteries according to II manners: 
c’est a savoir de feu, ou de medicine ardant.	that is to say of fire, or of burning medicine.  
Ou cautere de feu comande au malaide qu’il laisse les poilz tant qu’il soient lons et igals;	For the fire cautery, instruct the patient to let the hairs grow long and even;
et s’il le poignent a lor nassance, se li estraint les eulz qu’il ne se muevent tant qu’il naissent.	and if they prick at their base, hold the eyes steady so they do not move until they grow. 
Quant il naissent et i sont igalz, adonques met le malaide en ton sain;	When they are born and are equal, then place the patient in your healthy condition;  
aprés seigne sus la papiere des eulz une figure que soit ausi com li fuelle dou mirte, et soit li comencemens dou signe delez les poilz;	after draw on the paper of the eyes a figure that is as like as the leaf of myrtle, and let it be the beginning of the sign near the hairs; 
puis i met coton moilliet en glaire d’uef et muscillaige de persillion sus l’oil, puis eschaufe le cautere de coi ci est li forme:	then put cotton moistened in egg white and  a bit of persimmon over the eye, then heat the cautery as follows: 
Aprés cauterize sus la figure que tu as signiet poc et poc mout de fois, que li keurs soit ars lai endroit;	After that cauterize on the figure that you have signed here and there many times, so that the hairs are burned in that place. 
et li signes de la santeit de l’uevre est que tu voies la papiere retraite, et les poilz levez a la pointure de l’oil;	and the sign of the health of the work is that you see the paper retreated, and the hairs raised to the height of the eye.
adonques lieve ta main, et laisse ensi III jors, puis i met coton moilliet en burre tant que li eschaudure soit ostee;	Therefore lift your hand, and leave it so for III days, then put moistened cotton in butter until the burn is gone; 
aprés le cure d’oignement tant qu’il soit sanez.	after the ointment treatment until it is healed.  
Et se aprés ceu vienent li poilz, et li papiere est mollifie adonques rencomence le cautere sus cel leu meisme, si com tu as fait premiers;	And if after this the hairs come, and the skin is softened then begin the cautery again on that same place, as you did first;
et se li poil sont defuer, si le cauterize tant que li papiere soit levee a son leu natureil, et soit igals, et ne poignent mie li poil l’oil.	and if the hairs are cut off, cauterize them until the skin is raised to its natural place, and it be even, and do not prick the hair in the eye.  
Li cauteres de medicine ardant est que tu comandes au malaide qu’il laisse les poilz tant qu’il soient grans et igalz, puis fai de parchemin la forme de la foille de mirte;	The cautery of burning medicine is that you command the patient to let the hairs grow long and even, then make a shape of parchment like the leaf of myrtle. 
puis pren de savon fransois et de vive chalz, de chescun une .З., et broie ensamble bien;	then take French soap and quicklime, of each a third, and grind them together well; 
et le fai hastanment, si qu’il ne refroide, puis en espant sus la forme que tu es fait sicom la foille dou mirte, et met sus la papiere des eulz;	and make it hastily so that it does not cool, then spread it on the shape you have made like the leaf of myrtle, and put it over the eyes of the patient.  
et se li maladie tient en I oil soulement, si doit on ovrer en I, et se en ambedous ausi;	and if the patient holds in one eye only, then you must work in that one, and if in both eyes as well. 
et met desoz l’oil coton moilliet en abin d’uef;	and put under the eye cotton moistened in vinegar.
et li chiés dou malaide soit en ton sain et met ton doi mostrant sus la medicine, et presse I poc et lou muef toutes les fois que li malaide sent mordication de la medicine, car il sent mordication ausi com de feu.	and the shoulder of the sick person be in your healthy and put your knee showing on the medicine, and press it and its point all times that the sick person feels burning from the medicine, because he feels burning as well as fire. 
Quant tu as ceu fait longement, si oste la medicine a ton doit.	When you have done this for a long time, then remove the medicine to your place.
Et quant li mordication sera passee, si leve le leu d’awe, et rewarde se tu vois la papiere levee ausi com s’ele estoit levee par constraignement de feu ou par incision;	And when the burning will be passed, so lift the place of awe, and reward yourself if you see the parchment raised as if it had been raised by constraint of fire or by incision; 
et s’il est ensi, si est bien.	and if it is so, then it is well. 
Se ceu non, si remet encor de la medicine sus lou leu ou li medicine n’ait ovreit, tant que tes ovraiges soit igalz, et tes eulz mis a point;	If not so, so put back more of the medicine on the place where the medicine did not work, as long as your works are equal, and your eyes set to point;
puis met sus coton moilliet en burre tant que li keurs ars soit cheus, aprés cure le leu de l’oignement qui est apelez «dyafenis» et d’autre, tant qu’il soit sanez.	then put on cotton moistened in butter as long as the wound is wet, after cure the place of the ointment which is called 'diaphenis' and other, as long as it is healthy. 
Et se t’est mestier que tu te warde bien a ton ovraige par grant warde qu’il ne chiece point de la medicine as eulz.	And if it is necessary that you guard well your work with great care so that no medicine falls into the eyes.
Et se li papiere devient mole aprés, et li poil poignent en l’oil, si recomence la medicine sus celui leu qui est mollifiez de la papiere proprement, ensi com tu as fait devant;	And if the paper becomes soft afterward, and the hair pricks in the eye, then begin again the medicine on that part which is softened by the paper properly, just as you did before; 
aprés le cure tant qu’il soit sanez;	after curing it until it is healed; 
et c’est li forme de la fuelle dou mirte:	and this is the form of the leaf of the myrtle:  
Et saichés que li eul des homes sont divers en grandor et en petitece, et selonc ceu soit tes constraignemens;	And know that the eyes of men are diverse in size and smallness, and according to these be your constrictions; 
et ne soit mie reponue li droite voie a celui cui est li estude de cest art.	and let not the right way be returned to him whose study is this art.  
de la cure de fistule par cautere	of the cure of fistula by cautery
Quant tu cures fistule si com nos avons dit en divisions des maladies, et tes cures ne profitent mie, adonques covient il que tu li fais cautere selonc ceste maniere.	When you cure a fistula as we have said in the divisions of diseases, and your cures do not benefit, then it is necessary that you cauterize it according to this manner.
Comande au malaide qu’il mette son chief en ton sain;	Instruct the patient to put his head on your healthy side;
et teigne li menistres son chief entre tes mains en teil maniere qu’il ne se mueve, ne ne demoinne son chief;	and hold the head between your hands in such a manner that it does not move or tilt its head;  
aprés met coton moilliet en abin d’uef ou en jus de persillion sus l’oil;	after put moistened cotton in water of an egg or in the juice of parsley on the eye;
aprés chaufe le cautere qui est teilz:	After heating the cautery which is as follows: 
et est chevez au chief si com li forme d’une penne de vouteul, ensamble la queil soit li cautere;	and is shaped at the head like the form of a quill feather, altogether so that it is the cautery; 
se tu vues, si soit apointé des l’un chief dusc’a l’autre, et se tu vues, si soit ausi com une tente;	if you wish, it shall be pointed from one head to the other, and if you wish, it shall also be like a tent; 
mais toutevoie, cist qui est chevez vaut mues por ton ovraige.	but nonetheless, this which is shaped is more useful for your work.  
Aprés presse la fistule s’ele est overte, et en trai la porriture, et la seche;	After press the fistula if it is open, and dry out its matter 
et s’ele est close, si la oevre, et trai fuers la bowe;	and if it is closed, so the work, and extract fiercely the core.  
aprés met sus le cautere chaut forment, et tien ta main au cautere a la partie dou neif ensus de l’oil, que ta mains ne faice folie;	After put upon the hot heated cautery form, and hold your hand on the cautery at the part where it touches above the eye, so that your hands do not make a mistake.  
et met le cautere en la graisse de l’oil, et la corromp.	and place the cautery in the fat of the eye, and it corrodes. 
Se tu viens au comencement dou cautere jusc’a l’os, si serait bien.	If you come to the beginning of the cautery up to the bone, it would be good.
Se ceu non, si rencomence le cautere encor une fois, et autre se tu en as mestier, et le laisse III jors;	If this is not done, restart the cautery again once, and another if you have need of it, and leave it for 3 days.  
aprés i met sus coton moilliet en burre, et lou cure de l’oignement desiccatif tant qu’il soit sanez, et se XL jors passent qu’il ne soit sanez, si met sus medicine ague corrosive tant que li os soit descovers;	afterward put on moistened cotton in butter, and treat with the ointment of desiccation until it is healed, and if 40 days pass and it is not healed, then put on an acrid corrosive medicine until the bone is uncovered;
et lou reis selonc ceu que il venrait en son chapistre.	and treat according to what comes in this chapter.  
Et i a une maniere de cautere de fistule que aucun des anciens dirent.	And there is a way of cauterizing a fistula that none of the ancients said.
Entens a fistule, et fens le leu;	Attend a fistula, and open its place; 
aprés met en la fendure I camahan subtil de coi ci est li forme:	afterward put in the fissure one subtle camomile of which this is the form:   
et i font a la quantiteit d’une .З. de plonc;	and make it to the quantity of 1/3 of a plum ;
et tien ta main ou camahan fermement, et ne se mueve li malaides nes point, que li plons fondus ne corre a son oil;	and hold your hand or camomile firmly, and let the patient not move at all so that the melted plums do not run to his eye ;  
et covient c’on mette sus l’oil a malaide coton moilliet en abin d’uefz ou en awe:	and it is necessary to put on the eye of the patient cotton moistened in wine or ale: 
li plonc si art lou leu de fistule, et lou saine per mervillouse saniteit.	The pimple if it is at its place in a fistula, and the healthy one by miraculous healing.  
Et se li fistule est sanee per le cautere que nos avons dit, c’est boin.	And if the fistula is healed by the cautery that we have said, it is good.
Se ce non, si covient aministrer pertus au neif, et ramener la fistule au cors dou neif selonc ceu qu’il covient en som propre leu.	If this is not the case, it is necessary to administer purging to the nostril and bring the fistula back to the body of the nostril according to what is proper in its own place.
des crevaices en levres	of the openings in lips
Mout de fois avienent crevaices en levres que sont apelees «poil», et meismement en levres des enfans.	Many times there are wounds in lips which are called “hair”, and even in children’s lips.
Quant tu cures ces crevaices de ceu que nos avons dit en divisions, et li cure ne profite, adonques eschaufe I petit cautere cultellaire selonc ceste forme:	When you treat these wounds with those that we have said in the divisions, and the treatment is not beneficial, then use this small scalpel cautery according to this form.
Et le met hastanment en celles crevaices tant qu’il viegne jusc’a font;	And put it carefully in those crevices until it comes just to the fountain; 
aprés cure le leu de cerote tant qu’il soit sanez.	afterward cure the place of cauterization until it is healed.  
de l’aposteme de la goule	of the abscess of the throat
Quant apostume vient en la racine de la goule ou en l’uve, ou ou palais, ou as racines des dens, aprés fait porriture et ront et est enveillis et devient fistule;	When an abscess comes in the root of the tongue or in the cheek or palate, or at the roots of the teeth, after it has rotted and erupted and is enclosed and becomes a fistula; 
et tu le cures si com nos avons dit en divisions, et il ne profite mie:	and you cure it as we have said in divisions, and it does not benefit at all:  
adonques covient il que tu aies I cautere selonc la quantiteit de la fistule;	then it is necessary that you have the cautery according to the quantity of the fistula; 
aprés le bote ou pertus de la fistule, et tien ta main tant que li fer chaus viegne au font de li, et ou derrien leu;	after you cut or open the fistula, and hold your hand until the iron cauterizes to the bottom of it, and in the last place; 
et fai ensi une fois ou II, aprés le cure de ce que nos avons dit en cures, tant qu’il soit sanez;	and do thus once or two, after the cure of what we have said in treatments, until he is healed. 
et s’il est curez ensi, c’est boin;	and if he is healed thus, it is good;  
et se ceu non, si covient descovrir le leu et oster l’os corrumput, selonc ceu que vos le troverez en son chapistre.	and if not, then it is necessary to uncover the place and remove the corrupted bone, according to what you will find in your chapter.  
dou movement des dens	of the movement of the teeth
Quant les gencives sont mollifies par moistor et les dens muevent, et tu le cures per medicines et ceu ne vaut, adonc met le chief dou malaide en ton sain;	When the gums are softened by moisture and the teeth move, and you treat it with medicines and it is not effective, then put the head of the sick person in your hand;  
aprés eschaufe le cautere dont li forme venra ci aprés en teil maniere que tu mettes une cainne sor le dent;	after heating the cautery whose form will come here after in such a manner that you put a handle on the tooth;  
et met dedens le cautere chaut hastanment, et tien tant ta main que li malaides sente la chalor venant a la racine dou dent;	and put inside the heated cautery, and hold it so long that the patient feels the heat coming to the root of the tooth; 
aprés lieve ta main et rencomence le cautere selonc ta volenteit;	after lightly touch your hand and begin the cautery according to your will 
aprés emplisse li malaides sa bouche d’awe salee, et la teigne une houre et raiche fuers.	after fill the patient's mouth with salt water, and let it stay there for an hour and spit forcefully.  
Et en teil maniere li dens qui estoit movans si est confermez, et li gencive mollifie restrainte, et li moistors corrumpue sechie.	And in such manner the tooth that was moving is thus confirmed, and the softened gum restrained, and the moisture corrupted dry.
de la dolor des dens	of the pain of teeth
Quant dolor de dens vient por froidor, ou il i a froidor ou veir, et les cures de medicine ne valent, adonc i ait mestier de cautere selonc II manieres:	When tooth pain comes from cold, or there is cold or dampness, and the treatments of medicine are not helpful, then there is need for cauterization according to two ways: 
et cautere de burre et cautere de feu.	and cautery of butter and cautery of fire. 
Cautere de burre si est telz que tu preignes burre de vaiche, et le bout en une cuillier de fer ou d’arain;	Cauterization of butter is such that you take butter from a churn and the end in a spoon of iron or steel;  
aprés pren coton et envolope sus la pointe d’une tente, et la moille en burre bulit, et met sus le dent dolant hastanment et tien tant qu’il soit refroidiez;	after take cotton and wrap it on the point of a needle, and moisten it in melted butter, and put it on the aching tooth gently and hold it until it is cooled. 
et ensi fai sovent tant que sa vertus viegne a la racine de la dent, et se tu vues si moille laine et coton en burre froit, et met sus le dent doillant, et met sus I fer chaut tant que li feus viegne au chevement dou dent.	and thus do often until its virtue reaches the root of the tooth, and if you see so moistened wool and cotton in butter cold, put it on the aching tooth, and place a hot iron above it until the heat comes to the end of the tooth. 
Li cauteres ensamble feu si est telz que tu preignes uns cainne de fer ou d’arain, et soit grosse si que li feus ne viegne a la bouche dou malaide;	The cautery by fire is such that you take a chain of iron or steel, and it should be thick so that the flame does not come to the mouth of the sick person.  
aprés chaufe le cautere, de coi li forme venra ci aprés, et le met sus le dent et tien ta main tant que li cauteres soit refroidiez;	After heating the cautery, according to its form which will come later, and place it on the tooth and hold your hand until the cautery is cooled.  
fai ceu sovent, car li dolor sera ostee celui jor meisme ou l’endemain.	Do this often, because the pain will be removed that same day or the next. 
Et covient que li malaides emplisse sa bouche de boin burre en l’empressement de cel cautere, et puis le raiche fuer;	And it is necessary that the patient fill his mouth with good butter at the time of this cautery, and then rinse it. 
et c’est li forme dou cautere:	And this is the form of the cautery:  
Et fai cautere dou queil chief que tu voudras, et selonc ceu que tu as pooir;	And make a cautery of whatever shape you wish, and according to what you are able. 
et c’est li forme de la caine:	And this is the form of the chain: 
des scrophules	of scrofulous
Quant les scrophules sont de fleume et de moistors froides, et ne sont obeissans a digestion par medicines, adonques eschaufe le cautere cheveit de coi ci aprés vient li forme, et ait II aovertures por les fumees a issir au cautere de l’autre partie;	When the scrophules are of phlegm and cold moistures, and are not obedient to digestion by medicines, then cauterize with the fire cautery as will be described later in the form, and have it have openings for the fumes to issue from the cautery on the other side. 
et met le cautere chaut sus l’apostume une fois, ou II se mestier est, tant qu’il viegne au font de l’apostume;	And place the hot cautery on the abscess once, where it is needed, until it comes to the bottom of the abscess. 
et se li apostume est petis si met cautere selonc la quantiteit de l’apostume, et le laisse ensi III jors;	And if the abscess is small, put the cautery according to the quantity of the abscess, and leave it so for three days. 
et met sus coton moilliet em burre tant que li arsure soit ostee;	And put on moistened cotton in butter until the burn is removed. 
aprés cure le leu d’oignemens et de tentes tant qu’il soit sanez.	After care the place of ointment and tents until it is healed.
Li forme de la cainne:	The form of the dog:
Quant les moistors vainquent sus les chenals dou pormon, et meismement quant ce vient de froide complexion, adonc covient que li malaides soit voidiez premiers par medicines solutives;	When the humors dominate over the channels of the body, and also when it comes from a cold complexion, then it is necessary that the patient be first purged by dissolving medicines; 
aprés li fai cautere a la racine de la gorge, et te garde que tu ne venir mie jusc’a la gorge, et n’ardre dou keur mais c’un poc.	After you have made the cautery at the root of the throat, and keep that you do not come as far as the throat, and burn only a little bit, but of the heart
Aprés li fai I autre cautere a la jointure dou col au chief de l’espinee, et soit li cauteres qui est apelez «clavile» de coi nos avons la forme devant;	After you make another cautery at the joint of the neck to the top of the spine, and let the cautery be called "clavicle" for that is its form as we have it before;
et cure le leu si com nos avons devant dit tant qu’il soit sanez.	and cure the place as we have said before until it is healed. 
de la toust	of the boil
Quant tous et maladie de pormon sont de moistors froides, et li malaides nen ait fievre ne sechor, et est li maladie anciaine, se li fai .II cauteres sus la forcele en leus vuis;	When all and disease of the body are from cold humors, and the patient has no fever or dryness, and the disease is ancient, if you make two cautery on the fortlec in their veins; 
et I autre cautere emmi le pis entre II mameles;	and another cautery removes the lump between the two breasts; 
et soit li cauteres qui est apelez «clavile» selonc la forme qui est devant dite.	and let the cautery be called "clavile" according to the form that is before said.  
Et se tu vues, fai cautere en poignant a tot le cautere qui est apelez «poins» de coi li forme est ci devant en la maladie des oreilles;	And if you see, make cautery by pricking with the whole cautery that is called "poins" for whose form is before in the malady of the ears; 
et soient li poins jusc’a XXX, ou enqui entor.	and let the "poins" be up to XXX, or wherever it reaches.  
Aprés cure le leu selonc ceu qui est devant dit, et soit li cauteres a III rains selonc ceste forme:	After curing the place according to what is said before, and let the cautery be at III reins according to this form:
Et por ceu sont li cautere plus legier, por ceu que tu en fais III a cop.	And for this reason, the cauteries are lighter, for you make three cuts with it.
de la dislocation de l’ajutoire	of the dislocation of the shoulder
Quant li chiés de l’ajutoire est desaloiez par cause de moistor, et on le remet a leu, et il n’i puet demorer ains revient adés et desalue par petit movement qui avient, si com nos avons esproveit, adonques covient il que tu ramoinnes la dislocation premierement.	When the head of the shoulder is dislocated due to moisture, and it is reset but cannot stay in place, repeatedly dislocating with slight movement as we have experienced, then it befits you to reset the dislocation first.
Aprés soit sovinez li malaides sus son dos et sus son costeit;	Afterward soothe the patient on his back and on his ribs; 
aprés lieve le keur qui est dedens le titillite as dois de ta main senestre;	after lift the heart which is inside the little one to the two of your left hand;  
et se li jointure est desaluee dedens, si eschaufe le cautere qui a II ners douqueil ci est li forme:	and if the jointure is dislocated inside, then scald the cautery that has two nerves like this whose form is: 
et cauterize lou keur tant qu’il le perce jusc’a costeit, et venrait li fugure dou cautere ensamble IIII cauteres;	and cauterize the heart until it pierces to the rib, and comes the figure of the cautery along with four cauteries; 
et por ceu est faite cautere avec le cautere qui a III ners, por coi li figure de cauterization sunt sis cauteres;	and for this reason, a cautery is made with the cautery that has three nerves, so the figures of cauterization are six cauteries. 
et sont li nerf selonc la subtiliteit d’une tente et c’est li forme dou cautere qui a III ners:	and the nerve according to the subtlety of a tent, and this is the form of the cautery that has three nerves: 
Et aucune fois est ajostez sus ce I nerf por coi il i a VIII cauteres.	And sometimes is adjusted upon this nerve for which there are VIII cauteries.
Aprés met sus le cautere porrelz broiez avec seil;	After put the cautery over with powdered silk. 
aprés fai reposer le malaide, et ne soit meus li membres par lonc tens tant qu’il soit bien confortez.	after make rest the patient, and do not move the limbs by long time until he is well fortified.  
Et s’il est desaloiez desus, liquelz chose avient poc, adonques fait cautere sus l’epaisse dou cautere clavile, ou mout de cauteres en poignant.	And if it is dislocated upwards, which thing happens rarely, then make cautery on the thickened part of the clavicle cautery, or many cauteries by pricking.
Car li jointure est refermee, et est ostee li moistor et est sanez li malaides.	For the joint is closed, and moisture is removed, and the patient is healed.
Quant en l’estomac vienent froidures et mout de moistors tant qu’il l’estraient a sa complexion, et sont multipliet li catharre a lui, et es manieres de cures acostumees et il ne profite mie, adonc covient que li malaides soit sovinez sus son dos, et estende ses jambes et ses mains.	When in the stomach come coldness and much moisture until it becomes altered to its complexion, and many catarrhs multiply in him, and the usual methods of treatment do not help, then it is necessary that the patient be treated on his back, and extend his legs and hands.
De ceu en aprés li fai III cauteres I desoz la cuillier dou pis per la quantiteit d’un doi, a tout le cautere clavile, et II cauteres defuers les II costez tant que li figure des cauteres soit a III angles, et ait teil espaice entre l’une et l’autre qu’elles ne soient jointes ensamble quant elles giteront porriture;	Of this afterward he makes three cauteries, I under the armpit of the hip by the quantity of a die, to all the cautery clavicle, and II cauteries outside the two ribs as long as the figures of the cauteries are at III angles, and have such spacing between one another that they are not joined together when they will rot.
et soient li cautere si parfont qu’il porpreignent les II pars dou keur, et soit li figure des cauteres selonc ceste forme sens ajostement:	and let the cautery be so well-formed that it grazes the two parts of the heart, and let the shape of the cauteries be according to this form without adjustment: 
Et se tu vues cauterize d’un grant cautere enmi l’estomac selonc ceste forme;	And if you see a cautery to be made in the stomach according to this form; 
et celui qui avra paour de cest cautere, cauterize en poignant et seigne sus l’estomac i. point selonc la quantiteit que tu vues d’enche;	and he who will have fear of this cautery, cauterize by pricking and reigning upon the stomach here at a point according to the quantity that you see fit;
puis le cauterize a tot le cautere qui est apelez «poins».	then cauterize with the whole cautery which is called 'point'. 
Aprés le cure de la cure que nos avons eut devant, tant qu’il soit sanez.	After the cure of the cure we have had before, as long as it is healed.
Quant au foie vient dolor de froit et de moistor et de grosse ventositeit, tant qu’il est fuer mis de sa complexion natureil per les superfluitez;	When to the liver comes pain from cold and moisture and great flatulence, as long as it is further removed from its natural complexion due to excesses;
et li malaides est curez de ceu que nos avons dit en divisions, et il ne li profite mie, si covient que li malaides soit sovinez sus son haitereil;	and the patient is cured of those things that we have said in divisions, and it does not help him if it is necessary that the patient be treated above his head;
et signe d’enche III cauteres selonc ceste forme et ceste figure et ceste quantiteit sus lou foie, defuer les ypocondres, lai ou li coutes de l’ome vient;	and sign of this [III] cauteries according to this form and this figure and this quantity on the liver, away from the hypochondria, where the man's ribs come. 
et ait d’espaice entre chaicun cautere la groissece d’un doi;	and have of space between each cautery the thickness of a finger. 
et soient li cautere dou lonc dou cors, et ne presser mie mout ta main a tot le cautere;	and let the cauteries be long of the body, and do not press too much your hand on all the cautery.
et soit arse tant soulement li moitiez dou keur, et soit li malaides drois sus ses piez;	and let be burned only the half of the heart, and let the patient be straight on his feet; 
et s’il ne peut, si soit gisans, et estende ses jambes, et lieve ses brais;	and if he cannot, let him be lying down, and extend his legs, and raise his arms;
et c’est li forme:	and this is the form:  
Et se ta volentez est, si cauterize ces cauteres dou cutellaire, se tu es subtilz et saiges en l’art, et te warde que tu n’ardes mie tout le keur, car tu feroies sechier tout le cors;	And if your will is so, you can cauterize these cauteries of the knife, if you are subtle and wise in the art, and guard that you do not burn all the heart, for you would make the whole body dry;
et qu’il ne viegne jusc’a boueil, car li keurs est mout subtilz lai endroit, et lou saiches por voir.	And let him not come near boiling water, for the skin is very delicate there, and you can see it. 
Quant il a apostume au foie, et tu vues savoir s’il est en la char dou foie ou en la toile:	When he has an abscess in the liver, and you want to know if it is in the flesh of the liver or in the capsule: 
s’il est en la char, se sent li malaides dolor ne mie trop fort;	If it is in the flesh, the patient feels pain not too strong;
et s’il est en la toile, si sent dolor forsenee.	And if it is in the capsule, he feels a sharp pain. 
Et lors quant ceste cure desoit les mires, si covient que li malaides soit sovinez sus sa teste;	And then when this cure fails to work, it is necessary for the patient to be treated on his head;
et puis seigne d’enche le leu ou li apostumes est, et puis chaufe le cautere qui est semblans au rais, de coi ci est li forme:	and then place a poultice over the area where the abscess is, and then heat the cautery which resembles a ray, so that it looks like this form: 
Et cauterize I cautere tant que li keurs soit ars, et viegne jusc’a syphac, tant que li porreture soit toute fuers;	And cauterize the area with the cautery until the skin is burned, and it comes up to the size of a spica, so that the surrounding tissue is all gone.  
aprés la cure selonc la cure des essues tant qu’il soit sanez;	After the treatment according to the treatment of wounds until it is healed. 
et ne covient mie que de cest cautere use nuls fuers que cil qui ait estudieit longement en l’art de medicine, et par cui mains cestes maladies ont corrut aucune fois.	And it is not fitting that of this cautery use none others than those who have studied long in the art of medicine, and by whose hands these diseases have been cured any time. 
Adonques puet il hardiement ovrer, et toutevoies il me semble que mues vaut li laissier.	Therefore he can boldly work, and it seems to me always better to leave it.
dou cautere de pleuresin	For the cautery of pleurisy
Li ancien dirent que on doit faire a pleuresin cauteres de racines d’aristologe, et en teil maniere:	The ancients said that one must do cauteries with the roots of aristolochia and in such manner:  
pren une racine d’aristologe longe, la plus grant que tu poras troveir, et soit seche, et soit ausi grosse et ausi longe comme tes dois;	Take a root of aristolochia long, the largest that you will be able to find, and whether it is dry, and as thick and as long as your thumbs.  
et la moille en oile, et l’emprens au feu, et cauterize I cautere entre la forcele et lou col, et II petis cauteres un poc en dessendant en la partie qui est desoz la barbe;	and moisten it in oil, and imprint it in the fire, and cauterize with this cautery between the shoulder and the neck, and make small cauteries one by one descending in the part that is below the beard.
et II cauteres entre la quinte coste et la sisime, en declinant derrier un poc;	And make two cauteries between the fifth rib and the sixth, declining behind a little. 
et I cautere emmi le pis, et I autre sus l’estomac, et I entre II espaules, et II as II costez dou pis defuers le cautere qui est entre II espaules;	And with the cautery remove the pain, and the other on the stomach, and between the two shoulders, and the two ribs of the side where the cautery is between the shoulders. 
et ne presser mie ta main, ains fai apertement ausi com en odorant.	And do not press your hand at all, but make it open as if smelling.
