Et dirent aucun ancien que aucun home usent de cautere de feir semblant a I raseur, et l’eschaufent et le mettent entre les costes, tant qu’il vient a cel aposteme;	And they say that no one used a cautery of fire resembling a razor, and heat it and put it between the ribs, until it comes to this abscess. 
et saut fuers li dolor, si com nos avons dit en l’aposteme dou foie.	And jumps outside the pain, as we have said in the abscess of the liver.  
Mais en cestui ovraige est paour ou li malaides muert maintenant, ou fistule i vient qui ne puet estre sanee.	But in this work there is fear where the patient dies now, or a fistula comes which cannot be healed.
de la mice	of the mouse
Quant tu cures la maladie de la mice de ceu que nos avons dit as divisions des cures, et il ne profite mie, adonques i afierent III manieres de cautere que tuit sont boin.	When you treat the illness of the mouse of that which we have said as divisions of cures, and it does not benefit, then there are III ways of cautery that all are good.
Desquelz li une maniere si est que tu faices III cauteres, ou IIII, en lignant selonc la longor de la mice, selonc la figure dou cautere dou foie que nos avons dit devant;	Of which one manner is that you make three or four cauteries, lining according to the length of the mouse, according to the shape of the liver cautery that we have said before;
et n’apresser mie ta main a tout le cautere, et soit li malaides sovins sor son dos;	And do not press your hand on the whole cautery, and let the patient lie on his back; 
et une autre maniere de cautere si est que tu eschaufe le cautere qui a II ners, si com nos l’avons mostreit en la dislocation de l’espaule;	And another manner of cautery is that you heat the cautery which has II nerves, as we have shown it in the dislocation of the shoulder.  
et lieve le keur qui est endroit la mice, ou li coutes dou malaide vient devers senestre, et soit li elevations dont tu lieves le keur selonc la keur, selonc la longesce dou cors, et li cautere soient selonc la largesce dou cors.	and lift the heart which is placed in the mouse, or the cuts of the patient come from the left, and be the elevation that you lift the heart according to the heart, according to the length of the body, and the cautery be according to the width of the body.  
Aprés i boute les II ners enflamez tant que li keurs soit perciez de l’autre part, et puis trai fuers le cautere, et ensi en i avra IIII.	After it brings out the two nerves inflamed until the hearts are pierced on the other side, and then drives out the cautery, and thus there will be four. 
Et se tu vues, si cauterize a tot le cautere a III ners.	And if you see, so cauterize all the cautery to three nerves.  
Aprés le cure quant il a geteit porriture par lonc tens, et ce vaut mues que li autre des cures devant dites.	After the cure when it has gotten rot for long time, and this is worth more than the other cures before said.
de ydropisie	of dropsy
Cautere ne vaut a ydropique, fors c’a la maniere qui est apelee «asclytes».	Cauterization is not useful for dropsy, except with the method called "ascending."
Quant tu la cures selonc les manieres que nos avons dit en divisions, et ta cure ne profite mie, adonques covient il que tu li faices IIII cauteres entor la boude, et I sus l’estomac, et un sus le foie, et I sus la mice, et II derrier le dos sus l’espinee, et I endroit le pis;	When you cure it according to the manners that we have said in divisions, and your cure does not benefit, then it is necessary that you make four cauteries around the head, and one on the stomach, and one on the liver, and one on the mouse, and two behind the back on the spine, and one in place of the breast; 
et soit li cauteres bien pres de l’espés dou keur.	And let the cautery be near the side of the heart. 
Aprés laisse le cautere aovert por giter porriture lonc tens, et ne lassier mie la cure dou malaide aprés le cautere;	After let the cautery open for to ward off corruption long time, and do not leave the care of the patient after the cautery. 
et sanation se hasterait, et seront ensamble les II ententions avec l’aide de Deu.	And healing would hasten, and will be together the II intentions with the help of God. 
Li forme dou cautere por le ventre soit li clavile que nos avons devant mostreit;	The form of the cautery for the belly is the key that we have in front shows; 
et cil por le dos soit olivaire, selonc ceu qu’il est ci devant mis.	and that for the back is olive-shaped, according to those that it is here before put. 
de l’enfleure des piez	of the swelling of the feet
Quant li piez sont enflez a celui qui est ydropique, et sont plain d’awe citrine, il covient que tu cauterizes sus le dos dou piet entre l’auriculaire et l’anulaire;	When the feet are swollen in the one who is hydrophic and are full of  yellowish water, it is necessary that you cauterize on the back of the foot between the little finger and the ring finger. 
et lieve ta main avec le cautere sens torner.	and raise your hand with the cautery without turning.  
Et n’entrer mie trop em parfont, ensi sarrait fuers li awe citrine, et soit li cauteres selonc cest forme:	And do not enter too deeply with it, thus tighten outside the yellow bile, and let the cautery be according to this form.
Aprés fai sus II jambes II cauteres en chescune jambe a la pointe dou cutellaire;	After, make on each leg two cauteries at the point of the calf. 
et soit li cauteres dou lonc, l’un desoz le genoil devant et l’autre defuers, enmi la jambe;	and let the cauteries be long, one below the knee in front and the other behind, in the middle of the leg. 
et laisse les cauteres aovers longement sens curer, que li awe en isse;	and leave the cauteries open lengthwise without curing, so that the water drains out. 
aprés le cure des autres cures que nos avons dit.	after the curing of the other wounds that we have said.  
de la menoison	of the hand
Quant solution de ventre vient de froidor et de moistor, tant que li vertus retentive et digestive qui est ou stomac et en l’intestine est afleboie, et ne puet estre curez par manieres de cures;	When a flux of the belly comes from cold and moisture, so that the retentive and digestive virtues that are in the stomach and intestines are weakened, and cannot be cured by methods of healing;
et tu vois le malaide bien soffrant et de fort vertut, si fai I grant cautere sus l’estomac selonc ceu qu’il en a parleit ci devant ou cautere de l’estomac, au cautere circule;	and you see the patient suffering greatly and of great virtue, so make a great cautery on the stomach according to what has been spoken of before, or cautery of the stomach, the cautery circulates. 
et IIII cauteres entor la boude subtilz a tout I cautere clavile subtil, et II cauteres sus les hainches.	And IV cauteries around the belly subtly to all the cautery clavicle subtly, and II cauteries on the hips. 
Et se tu vois les moistors habundans et le malaide soffrant, se li fai cautere sus le poignil, et I cautere sus chaicun yle, et II petis cauteres sus l’estomac delez le grant, car li cure est profitans quant il i a bone aide.	And if you see the humors abundant and the patient suffering, make a cautery on the groin, and one cautery on each buttock, and two small cauteries on the stomach near the large, because the cure is profitable when there is good help.
de la cure des emorroydes	Of the cure of hemorrhoids
Quant les emorroydes sont ou fondement, ou une ou plusors, et sont ancienes et sont de grosses humors froides et moistes corrumpues, et sont curees si com nos avons dit en divisions, et il ne profite mie, si fai cauteres:	When the hemorrhoids are or foundation, or one or more, and are ancient and are of large cold and moist humors corrupted, and are cured as we have said in divisions, and it does not profit any, if you do cauteries: 
III sus l’espine dou dos, celi qui est tout defuers desoz almecdate poc et poc en triangulant, et I cautere desoz la boude II dois;	III on the spine of the back, that which is all outside below almecdate poc and poc in triangling, and I cautery below the belly II does. 
et se tu penses que ses estomac soit refroidiez, et li viande ne cuise, et on voit enfler la faice, adonques li faice on I grant cautere sus le stomac, si com il est devant dit, et I autre sus le foie, et I autre sus la mice a tout le cautere clavile;	and if you think that his stomach is cooled, and the meat does not cook, and one sees the face swell, then the face on I great cautery on the stomach, as it is before said, and I other on the liver, and I other on the mice to all the cautery clavicle. 
et laisse le cautere overt lonc tens.	and let the cautery remain open long time. 
Aprés cure le leu tant qu’il soit sanez.	After cure the place until it is healed.
de la charnositeit qui est nommee «thelul»	of the flesh which is called “thelul”
Quant tu copes althelul, si eschaufe le cautere qui semble I raseur, et puis le met tout embraseit sus cel althelul copeit;	When you cut flesh, carefully heat the cautery like a razor, and then place it all ablaze upon that flesh which is cut. 
et i laisse tant ta main que li cauteres viegne a la naissance de la voine, de coi li sans cort;	and leave it there as long as the cautery comes to the base of the vein, so that the blood stops;
fai ceu une fois ou II, et s’il i a mout d’althelul, si cauterize chaicun si com nos avons dit;	do this once or twice, and if there is much flesh, cauterize each as we have said;
aprés les cure d’oignemens profitans tant qu’il soient sanez;	after the cures of dressings beneficial until they are healed;
et se tu cauterizes d’un cautere grant sus alchatim, si avra plus grant aide.	and if you cauterize with a large cautery on flesh, it will have more help. 
de plaie mal curee	of poorly healed wound
Quant li malaides ne puet soffrir tailleure ne overture, que nos raconterons en son leu, si vient teil maladie que ne puet estre sanee fuer que par cautere.	When the patient cannot endure cutting or opening, which we will recount in its place, there comes a certain illness that can only be healed by cautery.
Quant a aucun vient fistule, et est enveillie et giete porriture et moistors corrumpues, si la doies prover a tot une tente subtil, et garde que tu saiches a tot la tente combien elle a de parfont.	When to any comes fistula, and it is filled and hidden rot and moist corrupted, then the does prove to at once a tent subtle, and guard that thou knowest at once the tent how much it has of length.
Aprés eschaufe le cautere qui semble I raseur, et le boute en la fistule selonc la quantiteit que li tente i est entrée, et rencomence lou cautere tant que cil cors porris et corrumpus soient ars, une fois, ou II ou III, selonc la quantiteit de som besoing;	After heat the cautery like a razor and put it in the fistula according to the quantity that the thing went into it, and reheat the cautery until that flesh which is rotten be burned, once, or twice, or three times, according to the quantity of its need; 
et te warde d’ardre lé nerf qui sunt enqui, et des grans voinnes.	and you guard against injuring nerves which are within there, and the large veins. 
se li fistule vait au cors de la vesie et a l’intestine, si te warde de ces leus, et ne faire ceu fuers que en leu charnut, et pense qu’ele n’est mie persans;	If the fistula goes to the body of the bladder and the intestine, then guard these places, and do not make those forces but in their fleshy place, and think that she is not entirely perished. 
aprés cure le leu tant qu’il soit sanez, et se li leus est saielez, et les matieres sont ostees lonc tens, adonc saiches que li leus est sanez entierement;	After the cure of the place as long as it is sound, and if the places are healed, and the matters are removed for a long time, then know that the places are completely sound. 
et se les matieres ne sont ostees, saiche que li leus est troez, et corrumpus li os au font;	And if the matters are not removed, know that the place is troubled, and corrupting the bones at the bottom; 
et ensi com un de ces que nos dirons en son leu.	and thus as one of these that we will say in its place. 
de la maladie des reins	of the disease of the kidneys
Quant dolor de froit vient as rains, et de grosse ventositeit, et ne prent talant de femme, adonc covient il que tu li fais cautere sus les rains d’une part et d’autre au cautere clavile que nos avons devant dit;	When pain from cold comes to the kidneys, and of great windiness, and they do not take a tablet from women, then it is necessary that you make a cautery on the loins on one side and the other with the cautery clamp that we have said before.
et se nos le cauterizons em mileu, si avra III cauteres en ligne, et se feront plus grant aide.	And if we cauterize it in the middle, it will have three cauteries in a line, and it will be more helpful.  
de la vessie	of the bladder
Quant li vessie est mole et foible de froit et de moistor, si que li malaides retient l’urine, adonc li fai cautere en la partie defuers sus la vessie, la ou encomencent li poil dou poignil, et I a destre et I a senestre, et soit chescuns cauteres si lons com li nous d’un poce;	When the bladder is soft and weak from cold and moisture, so that the patient holds back urine, then I make a cautery in the outer part above the bladder, where the hairs of the pubic region begin, on the right and on the left, and each cautery should be as long as the width of a fist.  
et li fais I cautere defuers le dos, ou II se tu en as besoing;	And I make the cautery outwards towards the back, where it is needed. 
et soit li cauteres clavile selon la forme devant dite.	And let the cautery be made according to the shape mentioned before. 
de la marris	of the marsh
Quant li marrix est froide et moiste, et ne laisse mie por ceu a concevoir, et les flors sont corrumpues et lor termines tarde;	When the uterus is cold and moist, and does not allow for conception, and the flowers are corrupted and their ends are late;
et quant elles vienent, si sent grant dolor:	And when they come, there is great pain: 
adonques covient il c’on li faice III cauteres entor la boude, si com nos avons dit ou cautere de la vessie, et II cauteres defuers le dos;	therefore it is necessary that one make III cauteries around the head, as we have said or cautery of the bladder, and II cauteries behind the back 
et soit li cauteres clavile, si com nos avons dit.	and let the cauteries be cauterized, as we have said.  
de la hainche	of the hip
Quant les moistors viscouses dessendent a la boiste de la hainche, et por ceste cause si se muet de son leu, et li signes est que li cuisse est plus longe que li autre quant on le mesure ensamble;	When the viscous moisture descends to the hip joint, and for this reason it moves from its place, and the sign is that the thigh is longer than the other when measured together.
et est trovez li leus dou departement vuis, si covient que tu cauterizes le malaide sus la boiste de la hainche a I cautere semblant au cercle, et seigne devant le leu entor la boiste si com elle torne, si que li boiste soit dedens le cercle;	and it is found the location of the viscus department, so it is necessary that you cauterize the patient on the hip joint with a cautery resembling a circle, and sign in front of the place around the hip as it turns, so that the hip be within the circle;
et si soit li cauteres telz com cil dont on a cauterizeit le stomac.	and let the cauteries be such as those with which one has cauterized the stomach.  
Et se cist cauteres ne t’est presens, se li fai III cauteres de l’olivaire grans, et soit li cauteres ausi parfont com tous li keurs;	And if this cautery is not present to you, make III cauteries of the olive large, and let the cauteries be as deep as all the others; 
et le cure tant qu’il soit sanez.	and cure it until it is healed.  
de la dolor de la hainche	of the pain of the hip
Quant dolor vient en la boiste de la hainche, et c’est de froidor et de moistor, et li malaides est curez de ceu que nos avons dit en la division et li cure ne vaut, et li maladie est anciene:	When pain comes in the hip joint, and it is from cold and moisture, and the patient is cured of those things we have said in the division and the cure does not work, and the disease is old: 
adonc covient il que tu purges le malaide des grosses humors de pilules fetides, ou autres pilules bones semblans.	then it behoves you to purge the patient of gross humors with foul pills, or other good-looking pills.  
Aprés li fai cautere;	After that, make a cautery;
et li maniere dou cautere si est selonc II manieres:	and the manner of the cautery is according to II manners: 
c’est a savoir ensamble medicines ardans, et cautere de feu.	that is to say, together with burning medicines, and fire cautery.
Cautere de feu si est selonc mout de manieres, desquelz li uns est telz:	Fire cautery is according to many ways, some of which are such: 
que tu cauterize sus la boiste de la hainche III cauteres triangulalz selonc ceste forme, et i fai bone profunditeit et grant, et ait entre chaicun cautere d’espaice la groissece d’un doi, et soit li cauteres olivaire;	that you cauterize on the prominence of the hip III triangular cauteries according to this form, and make good depth and wide, and have between each cautery space the size of a finger, and let the cauteries be olive-shaped;  
aucune fois fait on cautere en mileu sus lou chief de la hainche, por coi il en i a IIII selonc ceste forme:	At times one does cauterize in the middle on the top of the hip, for which there are IIII according to this form: 
Et se tu vues, si le cauterize au cautere dou cercle que nos avons devant dit en la dislocation de la hainche;	And if you see, so cauterize with the cautery of the circle that we have before said in the dislocation of the hip;
mais fai en teil maniere que li cercles conteigne toute la hainche, et tous li espés dou keur soit ars.	But make in such manner that the circles contain the whole hip, and all the spaces of the groin be seared. 
Et c’est li maniere c’on fait en sciatique, quant li dolor tient en la hainche, et ne parvient mie jusc’a la cuisse ne jusc’a la jambe.	And this is the manner one does for sciatica, when the pain holds in the hip, and does not reach to the thigh nor to the leg.
Et s’ele vient jusc’a la cuisse et la jambe, se li fai II cauteres lai ou li malaides dit que li dolor li tient, et I cautere desus la cheville IIII dois, a la partie senestre un poc;	And if it comes just to the thigh and leg, so you make II cauteries there where the patient says that the pain holds him, and I cautery above the ankle IIII fingers, to the left part one finger;
et soit li cauteres cutellaire, et soit arse li espesseté dou keur;	And let the cautery be a knife, and let the thickness of the heart be burned.  
et se li malaides sent que li dolor s’estende jusc’a dois dou piet ou pres d’enqui, se le cauterize la ou il sent la dolor III poins ou IIII au cautere qui est apelez «poins».	And if the patient feels that the pain extends to two feet or nearby, cauterize where he feels the pain three or four times with a cautery called "points." 
Et se mestiers est, se li en fai plus;	And if it is necessary, if he makes more.  
et se il seit que li dolor soit desoz le genoil vers la cuisse, se li fais cautere au cautere cutellaire ou circulaire, et te done bien garde en tous tes cauteres que tu n’i lassier mie tant le cautere que tu brules les ners et les grans arteres, et que tu ne faices au malaide plus grant nuisance et contraction.	And if it seems that the pain is below the knee towards the thigh, then make a cauterization with a knife or circular cautery, and be well guarded in all your cauterizations that you do not leave the cautery in so long that you burn the nerves and large arteries, and that you do not cause the patient more discomfort and contraction.
Et je meisme ai veus plusors qui ont fait cautere sus la cheville dou piet, et li lasserent tant que li jambe fut toute enflee, et li piez ausi, et fut perciez et corrumpus toz li piez.	And I myself have seen many who have made cautery on the ankle of the foot, and they left them until the leg was all swollen, and the foot too, and it was pierced and corrupted throughout the foot.
Aprés une solution de ventre dont il ot la mort.	After a stomach solution of which he had death.
Et se li dolors est en II parties ensamble, fai cautere en l’une et en l’autre, selonc ceste maniere.	And if the pain is in two parts together, make cautery in one and in the other, according to this manner.
Et li saige dirent en la cautere de la hainche, de coi ci est li maniere, fai I tel fer et soit au chief ausi gros com uns nauvillon de dacte, ou un poc moins, et soit par entrechetres et soit des l’un entrechetres jusc’a l’autre d’espaice la quantiteit d’un nou de poce;	And the sage say in cauterization of the hip, because this is how it is done, make one like a nail and be at the head as thick as a thimble, or a little less, and be by entrechetses and from one entrechetres to the other with a space the quantity of a finger's joint; 
et soient li entrechetres aovers de II pars, et soient aussi comme noez, et i ait I mainche de fer bien fait;	And let the pliers be over two parts, and also be like nuts, and there be the iron forceps well made; 
et c’est li forme:	And this is the shape:  
Et soit eschaufez tant qu’il soit toz rouges et giete senteles, et puis le mette on sus la boiste de la hainche malaide, et soit tornez sus lou sain costeit;	And be heated until it is all red and glowing hot, and then put it on the bone of the sick hip, and be turned upon the healthy side;  
et lou cauterize une fois I cautere reont et lou laisse III jors;	And cauterize once the cautery is red-hot and let it three days; 
et puis fai emplaustre de burre, et laisse la plaie aoverte lonc tens;	And then make a plaster of butter, and leave the wound uncovered for a long time; 
aprés la cure d’oignement tant qu’il soit sanez.	after the ointment cure until it is healed. 
Albucasim dit que nos usons poc de cest cautere por la paor de son regart, et se voions poc qui en usent;	Albucasim says that we should use this cautery little because of its danger, and few see who use it; 
et toutevoie ceu est des boins cauteres, qui le puet soffrir, et lai ou il s’afiert.	and nonetheless these are good cauteries, which those who can suffer it, and where it applies to.  
Li cauteres de medicine ardant si est que tu faices I estrument a entrechetres en coi dessende li marge de la porte, et soit d’arain ou de fer a une paroit longe, et en la hautece ait II nous, et ait entre chaicun la quantiteit de la groissece d’un doi;	The cautery of medicine burning is that you make the instrument between tweezers in which descends the margin of the door, and be of iron or of an appearance long, and in the height have two, and each one the quantity of the size of a coin.  
et soient overt defuer et desus, et se joignent ensamble selonc ceste forme:	And be open below and above, and they join together according to this form: 
Aprés met sus la boiste de la hainche au malaide gisant sor suin costeit sain, et apresse ta main mout sus la boiste de la hainche;	After put on the boil of the hip on the patient lying on his healthy side, and after your hand over on the boil of the hip. 
aprés giete entre les II cercles de l’awe chaude qui soit chaufee au feu I poc, et li laisse une houre dou tens, et soffre li malaides la chalor et l’arsure de li.	After cast between the two circles of the hot fire which is heated to the fire, and let him for an hour of ten, and suffers the patient the heat and the burn of it.
Car il i trueve mordication ausi com de feu;	For there he finds healing as well as fire; 
et quant li mordications iert passee, se lieve ta main avec l’estrument et leve la hainche d’awe douce, et laisse ensi III jors, et met sus burre tant que ceu qui est noir de l’eschaudure soit osteit;	And when the healing is passed, lift your hand with the instrument and lift the hip of soft wax, and leave thus for three days, and put on butter as much as that which is black from the burn is removed.
et lou laisse III jors que porriture en istrait;	and let him stay III days while rot draws out of it 
et ceu serait li derriene aide aprés le cure d’oignemens tant qu’il soit sanez.	and this would be the last aid after the care of healing until he is healed.  
Et se li dolor s’est estendue jusc’a la cuisse ou jusc’a la jambe, se li fai I estrument que teigne awe selonc ceu que tu as fait en la hainche igaument;	And if the pain has spread to the thigh or to the leg, then you make the instrument that holds it taut according to what you have done in the hip ligament. 
et c’est li maniere de l’awe chaude, et je l’ai escripte ou traitier de la rectification de medicine.	and this is the manner of the hot awe, and I have written it or treated of the rectification of medicine.  
Pren alcali et chaulz vive, autant de l’une com de l’autre, et les broie ensamble, et les met en I nuef pot.	Take alkali and quicklime, as much of each as the other, and grind them together, and put them in a new pot.
ou il ait I petit pertuis defuer se que li pointe d’un raisor i puisse entreir;	where there is a small hole from fire so that the point of a razor may enter in it; 
et met desor celui pot I autre pot bien plombeit, et met sus alcali et chalz et awe douce sus, tant qu’il en i ait I doi desus les poudres cant tu l’avras bien preingte a ta main;	and put on top one pot or the other well sealed, and put on top alkali and heat and sweet awe, until there is a thickness of it as much as the powders that you have well taken in your hand.
et le laisse ensi tant qu’il en dessende awe ague et chiece ou pot plombeit, puis pren toute cele awe, et la giete sus chalz et sus alcali si com devant.	and let him do so until it descends like a fever and chills or as much as it pleases, then take all this matter and place it on coals and on alkali as before. 
Et lors si sera mout ague et est aministree en mou d’ovraiges de medicine et en cauteres d’autres membres.	And then if there will be much fever, and is administered in many works of medicine and cauteries of other members. 
Car elle fait auteil oevre com feus, et si a autres medicines dont on cauterize bien la hainche ensi com tesisie et miel anacardi et chalz avec savon, toutes ces choses mellees ensamble.	For it does this work like fire, and with other medicines which are well cauterized the hip in this way, such as honey, terebinthine, and coals with soap, all these things mixed together.  
Et Galiens nos raconte une cure dont uns hons fut curez de la dolor de la hainche et de la voine sciatique, et lou loe mout, et dit que on n’i fist autre cure, et qu’il en fut sanez a une soule fois quant on ot fait ceste cure, et il se fut baigniez si com il l’enseigne ci aprés.	And the Galicians tell us of a cure of which a man was cured of pain in the hip and sciatic vein, and low back, and said that no other cure was made, and that he was healed at one time when this cure was made, and he was bathed as he teaches afterward.
Et dist en teil maniere que tu preignes dou litargire vert fres et sec, et le broie mout avec I poc de graisse, et met sus la hainche et sus la cuisse et sus la jambe ou la dolor tient, et la lie;	And say in this manner that you prick a little bit of green and dry litharge, and grind it well with a pinch of grease, and put it on the hip and thigh and leg where the pain is held, and cover it.
et li laisse III houres et par la quantiteit que li malaides ne sente plus l’arsure.	and let him remain for three hours and by the quantity that the patient no longer feels the burning. 
Et puis le fai entrer ou bain tant que li cors li soit un poc arousez, et lou fai entrer ou lit, et li dolor s’en ira toute et sera sanez.	And then let him enter into a bath until the body is a little aroused, and let him enter into bed, and the pain will go away entirely and be cured.
Et saiches que nuls ne doit user de cautere de telz medicines, se ceu n’est aprés l’evacuation de cors.	And know that no one should use fire cautery with such medicines unless after evacuation of the body.
Et Dyascorides dist que quant li voine sciatique est cauterizee de fiens de chievre, si i aide mout;	And Dioscorides says that when the sciatic vein is cauterized with goat's iron, it helps a lot. 
et doit estre fais li cauteres en teil maniere.	and it must be done the cautery in this manner.  
Prenez lainne et la beurez d’oile vielz, et metez sus la fossete qui est entre le pouce dou piez et l’autre qui est apelez foscile.	Take flax and soak it in old oil, and put it on the hollow which is between the thumb and the foot and the other called fossile.
Aprés pren fiens de chievre sec, et l’empren a feu tant qu’il soit charbons, et lou met sus la laine, et le laisse tant qu’il soit estains;	After take iron of goat dry, and grip it in fire until it is coals, and put it on the wool, and let it until it is stains. 
et refai encor ensi, et ne cesser de faire ensi tant que tu penses par sens qu’il viegne jusc’a la hainche, et que li dolor soit cessee;	and redo again like this, and do not cease to do so until you think by sense that it comes up to the hip, and that the pain is ceased. 
et cist manieres de cautere est apelez «cautere de chievre».	And this manner of cautery is called "cautery of goat". 
de la dolor dou dos	of the pain of the back
Quant dolor vient au dos, ou par cheoir ou de percussion ou par trop grant evacuation, ou par semblans de matiere espandue froide, a nule de ces semblances ne vaut cauteres, fuer que a celi qui vient de infusion de froide matiere.	When pain comes to the back, whether by falling or percussion or by excessive bloodletting, or by any kind of cold matter spread, none of these appearances are worth cauterization, except for that which comes from the infusion of cold matter.
Il covient c’aprés ceu que li malaides est voidiez de pilules fetides ou d’autres semblans, que on li faice sus lou dos, lai ou li dolor tient, trois lignes signies d’enche, et en chescune ligne V cauteres ou plus selonc la vertut et la quantiteit que li malaides puet soffrir;	It is necessary after this that the patient be free of fetid pills or similar things, that one makes on his back, where the pain holds, three lines marked with ink, and in each line 5 cauteries or more according to the virtue and quantity that the patient can suffer;  
et soit fait li cauteres selonc le cautere qui est apelez «poins»;	and let the cauteries be made according to the cautery which is called "point"; 
et se tu vues, fai III cauteres ou IIII au cautere clavile moien selonc ceste forme:	and if you see, make III or IV cauteries with the middle clavicle cautery according to this form:
Maintes fois vient ceste maladie as petis enfans, et li signes de l’encomencement si est qu’il ont estroite alainne quant il se lievent, et paor;	Many times this illness comes to little children, and the signs of the beginning are that they have a narrow throat when they lie down, and fear;
et tu trueves en la derriene espinee dou dos et en nous l’apparance qui vient sus les autres espinees.	And you find in the last spine of the back and in us its appearance which comes above the other spines.  
Quant tu vois ceu et tu le vues curer, si le cauterize au cautere de celcle selonc ceste forme.	When you see this and you want to cure it, cauterize it with the cautery of this kind according to this form.
Si que li cautere porpreigne chescune partie de l’espinee egaument.	So that the cautery touches each part of the spine evenly.
Et se tu vues, si cauterize entor l’espinee au cautere poignant II lignes ou III, et soient li poins pres l’uns de l’autre.	And if you see, then cauterize around the spine with the cautery prick two lines or three, and let the points be near each other.
Aprés cure le leu tant qu’il soit sanez selonc ceu que nos avons dit, et warde que tu n’amenistrer cautere en gilbositeit qui soit en spame de nerf.	After curing the wound until it is healed according to what we have said, and beware that you do not apply a cautery in a place which is in the nerve's sheath.
de la dolor des jointes	of the pain of the joints
Quant dolor de jointes sunt de moistors que sont espandues a chaicun membre dou cors, et quant dolor vient em piez, que li mire apelent «podagre» proprement, et quant elle est de froide cause et cures de medicines ne la puent curer, si est curez par cauteres en teil maniere:	When pain in the joints comes from moistures that are spread to each limb of the body, and when pain comes in feet, which they call gout properly, and when it is from a cold cause and cures of medicines cannot heal it, then it is healed by cauteries in this manner: 
fai li mout de cauteres entor la jointure dou piet, et soit li cauteres olivaire selonc ceste forme:	Make the mouth of cauteries around the joint of the foot, and let the cauteries be olive-shaped according to this form: 
Et s’il i a besoigne que tu poignes sus la faice dou piet, se li fai cautere a tot le cautere c’on claime «point».	And if it is necessary that you prick upon the face of the foot, then make cautery to the whole cautery as one calls 'point'.
Et se les dolors viegnent jusc’a genous et as autres jointures, et ceu avient maintes fois, se li fai cautere sus chaicun genoil III cauteres ou IIII de chescunne partie, a tout le cautere olivaire;	And if the pains come up to the knees and other joints, and this happens many times, then on each knee make three or four cauteries on each side, with all olive-shaped cautery. 
et se tu as mestier de plus, si en fai plus, mais n’i tenir mie ta main fuers que tant que li espés dou keur soit ars.	And if you need more, then make more, but don't hold your hand farther than until the tip of the cautery is burned.  
Et se les dolors dessendent jusc’a genoil et au dos, se li aministre le cautere que nos avons dit en son chapistre.	And if the pains descend to the knee and the back, administer the cautery as we have said in our chapter.
Et se les dolors sunt as mains, si fai poins entor le foscile II lignes;	And if the pains are in the hands, so make points around the socket two lines; 
et s’il remaint point de dolor as dois, si fai poins sus chescune jointe et sus lou poil de la main;	and if there remains no pain in the two, so make points on each joint and on the hair of the hand; 
et se les dolors vienent jusc’as coutes ou jusc’as espaules, si cauterize chescune partie, et fai boin governement au malaide et penre medicines.	and if the pains come to the elbows or to the shoulders, so cauterize each part, and make good governance to the patient and prescribe medicines. 
Car se tu li fais boin governement et tu purges fleume, si sera saneis a l’aide de Deu.	For if you give him good governance and purge phlegm, he will be healed with the help of God.
de la routure dou syfac	of the rupture of the hip
Quant routure vient en angres, et li bouelz dessendent as coions et c’est novelement, si covient que quant tu lou vues curer, qu’il ne menjuce mie celui jor;	When a rupture comes in the arms, and the bones descend to the armpits and it is new, so it is necessary that when you see to cure it, that he does not move it that day;
et qu’il use choses qui laichent lou ventre, si que li fiens dessende de son ventre;	and that he uses things which loosen the belly, so that the pain descends from his belly; 
aprés le fai seoir sus son dos entre tes mains, et li comande qu’il teigne son alaine tant que li boueil soient repairiet, et les ramoinne a tes dois, et seigne d’enche desoz la routure sus l’os dou poignil, et a tout un signe que soit semblans a la moitiet d’un cercle a desus dou cors;	afterwards he makes him sit on his back between your hands, and commands him to hold his arm as long as the bones are repaired, and rearranges them in his arms, and  signs of an incision below the rupture on the bone of the elbow, and a whole sign that is similar to half a circle above the body; 
puis eschaufe le cautere de coi ci est li forme:	then heats up the cautery as this shape is: 
tant qu’il soit blans et qu’il giete senteles.	as long as it is white and it feels tender
Puis ramoine les bouels a lor leu;	Then reset the bones in their place.  
et li ministres teigne sa main sus qu’il ne retornent arrier;	and the ministers hold his hand so that they do not return backwards. 
et oevre bien les cuisses au malaide, et met desoz lui I cussin et I serjant sus les cuisses, et I autre sus lou pis qui li teigne les mains;	and work well the thighs on the patient, and put underneath him the cushion and the sergeant on the thighs, and the other one on his hips which holds his hands.  
puis met le cautere sus lou signe a tout ta main, et lou tien droit et lou tien tant que tu ateignes l’os, et se tu ne l’ateins la premiere fois, si le rencomence encor une autre tant que tu viegnes jusc’a l’os;	then put the cautery on the sign with your whole hand, and hold it straight and hold it until you reach the bone, and if you don't reach it the first time, do it again another time until you come to the bone.
et te warde subtilment que li boueil ne saille quant tu fais lou cautere;	and carefully guard so that the boil does not burst when you do the cautery; 
que tu ne le brulasses;	that you do not burn it;  
et que par ceu li malaides ne muere, ou autre malz.	and that through this the patient does not die, or other harm. 
Et saiches que quant tu ne viens jusc’a l’os au cautere, tes ovraiges ne vaut rien.	And know that when you do not come close to the bone with the cautery, your works are worth nothing.
Et covient que li cauteres des enfans soit subtilz selonc la mesure d’ous, et des grans gens aussi grans selonc lor mesure;	And it is necessary that the cauteries of children be subtle according to the measure of them, and of great people also large according to their measure; 
aprés III jors cure lou leu dou cautere de burre tant que li eschaudure soit ostee;	after three days, treat the place of the cautery with butter until the burning is removed;  
aprés le cure d’autres oignemens tant qu’il soit sanez, et gise li malaides XL jors sus son dos tant que li plaie soit bien soudee;	after the cure of other ointments as long as it is healed, and lie the patient forty days on his back until the wound is well joined together;   
et covient que ses norrissemens soit lassatis longement, si que li boueil ne saillent quant il se preigdra d’aler en chambres.	and it is necessary that his dressings be loosened for a long time, so that the boils do not burst when he tries to go into rooms. 
Et aprés XL jors, quant il se voudra lever, se li amenistre une faixe bien faite, et la porse XL autres jors;	And after forty days, when he wants to stand up, a well-made splint is given him, and it is worn for another forty days. 
et ait boin repos, qu’il se travaille poc et se warde de trop grant repletion de boivre et de mengier, et de trop haut braire;	And have good rest, that he does not work too much and be careful of excessive filling of drinking and eating, and of too high a braise. 
et quant il fait cest enseignement si est sanez entierement.	And if he follows this instruction, he will be fully healed.  
Et je dirai ci aprés la cure de taillier en son chapistre.	And I will say here afterwards the cure of tailoring in its chapter.
de la routure dou ventre	of the rupture of the belly
Quant routures vienent en autres ventres et sont connisans, et tu vues qu’elles ne croissent plus, se li fai I cautere dou cautere reont selonc sa quantiteit, et soit ars li tiers dou keur;	When ruptures come in other bellies and are known, and you see that they do not grow anymore, you make the cautery of cauterization according to its quantity, and a third of the heart.  
aprés le cure selonc ceu que nos avons dit;	After the cure according to what we have said; 
et aucun des anciens ont dit c’on le doit cauterizer au cautere a III angles selonc ceste forme:	and none of the ancients said that it should be cauterized with a three-angled cautery according to this form:  
mais signe premier le leu d’enche et fai une ligne per la largesce desus la routure, et une autre defuers, et main ta main emmi a tout le cautere clavile.	but first sign the place of incision and make a line across the width above the break, and another below, and hold your hand over the entire fire cautery clavicle.
Mais li premiers cauteres est plus legiers et muedres.	But the first cauteries are lighter and more mobile.
de dolor anciene en aucun membre	of old pain in any limb
Quant dolor vient en aucun membre, ou de cheoir ou de ferir, et cele dolor tient lonc tens, et li cure de medicine n’i vaut, adonc covient qu’il soit cauterizeis au cautere qui est apelez «poins», et soit li cauteres selonc la longesce dou membre et la petitece et sa foibleteit et sa vertut et sa location de torcions et de sa dolor.	When pain comes in any limb, whether from a fall or blow, and this pain lasts for a long time, and the treatment of medicine does not help, then it is necessary that it be cauterized with the cautery called "poins", and let the cauteries be according to the length of the limb and its smallness and its weakness and its virtue and its location of twists and its pain.
s’il est sanez dou premier cautere, c’est bien;	If he is healed by the first cautery, that's good.
se ceu nom, recomence I autre cautere sus celui, car teilz costume est qu’il se doit muer au membre que li est prochiens, por coi il covient que tu faices les cauteres tant que li malaides soit saneis.	If this name, begin again the cautery on that one, for such is the custom that it must grow on the limb that is near, therefore you must make the cauteries as long as the patient is healing.  
de meselerie	of mixing
Li meseil sont aidiet aucune fois par cautere par grant aide, et meismement li maladie que vient de la putrefaction de fleume et de melancolie.	The month of May is aided sometimes by fire cautery with great help, and also the sickness that comes from the putrefaction of phlegm and melancholy.
Cant tu la vues cauterizer, pren warde se li maladie est au comencement, et s’ele est curee selonc ceu que nos avons dit en la division, et ne dessent ne ne demoure, et tu doutes que li corruption ne porpreigne tout le malaide, adonques li fai V cauteres sus lou chief:	If you can see that cautery, take care if the patient is at the beginning, and if she is healed according to what we have said in the division, and do not send or stay, and you doubt that corruption does not spread throughout the patient, then make V cauteries on his head: 
I emmi le chief a nouf, et l’autre vers lou front a la fin des chevous;	I place the head at nine, and the other towards the forehead at the end of the hairs;
et II sus les II cornes, et I derrierre sus le haiterel;	and II on the II horns, and I behind on the hairline; 
et i laise tant ta main que li cauteres viegne jusc’a l’os, et tant que les escorces en issent fors si que les vapors des grosses humors s’en puissent issir;	and let your hand so that the cautery comes up to the bone, and as long as the scorches issue out so that the vapors of the thick humors can issue forth; 
et le cauterize sus la mice selonc ce qu’il est devant.	and cauterize on the mouse according to what it is before. 
Et se li meselerie est partout esparse;	And if the flesh is spread everywhere;  
et elle pert manifestement, si covient que tu lou cauterizes de ces cauteres que nos avons dit ou chief, et I cautere en som lou neis, et II cauteres sus l’espinee dou col, et VI cauteres sus l’espinee dou dos, et I grant sus la crupie et I autre delez, et II sus les II espaules;	and it is clearly lost, then it is necessary that you cauterize it with these cauteries that we have said or chief, and I cautery on its neck, and II cautery on the spine of the neck, and VI cautery on the spine of the back, and I great on the crupie and the other below, and II on the two shoulders; 
et II sus les coutes, et II sus les tendrons dou pis, et I sus chascune jointe des mains et des piez, et sus les fosses des mains;	and II on the cuts, and II on the tendons of the leg, and I on each joint of the hands and feet, and on the hollows of the hands;  
et te warde des ners que sunt sus lou derrien calcant, que tu ne les bruler;	and guard against the nerves that are on the last bone, that you do not burn them; 
et aucune fois fait om cautere sus l’os dou poignil, et I autre sus l’os de l’estomac, et I autre sus lou foie.	and never has anyone made a cautery on the bone of the finger, and I other on the bone of the stomach, and I other on the liver. 
Et saiches que quant plus i fais de cautere, plus li fais d’aide, et mues li profite;	And know that when more fire cautery is done, it does more help, and moves it to profit. 
et saiches que li malaides ne sent point de dolor au cautere si com li sain le sentent, por ce que li cors est ja toz corrumpus.	And know that the patient feels no pain from the cautery as much as the healthy person feels it, because the body is already completely corrupted. 
Et covient ke li cautere soient grant et petit selonc les membres et les jointures, selonc ceu que vos lou troverez en manieres des fers.	And it is necessary that the cauteries be large and small according to the limbs and joints, according to what you will find in the ways of irons.
Aprés cure lou leu de farine de veces avec miel et autres cures tant qu’il soit saneis.	After cure the place with flour of chickpeas with honey and other cures until it is healed.
Quant enfleure vient en aucun membre et est curee par medicines et oiles et emplastres, et il n’est mie sanez, adonques li fai cauteres sus le membre selonc la grandour et la petitece dou membre;	When swelling comes in any limb and is cured by medicines and oils and plasters, and it is not healed, then I make cautery on the limb according to the size and smallness of the limb. 
et soit li cauteres un poc entrans en l’espés dou keur;	And let the cautery be a point entering into the thickness of the flesh.
puis le cure d’oignemens tant qu’il soit sanez.	Then cure with ointments until it is healed. 
Et aucune fois fait on cautere et a la main et au piet et au dos, a l’issue dou nerf que muet le membre, et ensi si est ostee li enfleure;	And at times one makes cautery to the hand and foot and back, at the end of the nerve that numbs the limb, and thus the swelling is removed. 
et toutevoie ne s’en entremette nuls s’il n’est conoissans des membres et des issues des ners movans lou cors.	And nevertheless, let no one interfere unless he is knowledgeable about the members and the exit points of nerves moving the body. 
de albaras	of albaster
Quant li maladie qui est apelee «albaras» est enveillie, et li engien de medicine n’i valent rien, adonques le cauterize d’un cautere un poc parfont, selonc la quantiteit de l’espés dou keur, tant que li blenchour soit ostee, et soit muee sa color;	When the illness called "albaras" is present, and the means of medicine are useless, then cauterize with a cautery a small spot, according to the quantity of the hardness of the heart, until the whiteness is removed, and its color changes.  
puis le cure de farine de veces et de lentilles avec oile roset et foilles de plantain, et sanc de colon et sanc d’alondre, de chescun une partie;	then treat with flour of chickpeas and lentils with rose oil and plantain leaves, and blood of colon and blood of alondine, of each one part; 
et soit mellez tout ensamble, et soit liiez d’un drapel, et soit aers au leu tant qu’il soit sanez.	and mix everything together, and bind it with a cloth, and apply it to the place until it is healed. 
li cure de chancre par cautere	The cure of a chancre by cautery
Quant chancre vient au comencement, et tu lou vues arrester, si le cauterize au cautere qui semble I cercle, tout entor au tour dou chancre.	When an ulcer comes at the beginning, and you see it to be arrested, cauterize it with a cautery that seems like a circle, all around the perimeter of the ulcer.
Et toutevoie li saige dirent que on faice cautere ausi au mileu dou chancre;	And nevertheless, the sages say that one should cauterize also in the middle of the ulcer;
et toutevoie ceu ne me semble mie boin, car je redous que il ne soit ulcerez et corrumpus, et je l’ai ja veut avenir aucune fois;	and nevertheless these do not seem good to me, because I fear that it may become ulcerated and corrupted, and I have never wanted this to happen before. 
et plus droituriere chose est qu’il soit cauteriés entor, au cautere qui est apelez «circule», si com nos avons dit en mout de cauteres.	and a more skillful thing is that it be cauterized with the cautery called "circle," as we have said among many cauteries. 
de l’enfleure qui ne puet meurer	of the swelling which cannot move
Quant aucuns ait une maladie qui est apelee «adubelati», et elle tarde de meurer ou por la superfluiteit qu’ele fait ou por l’eaige dou malaide quant il est decrepites (c’est a dire trop vielz) et il a poc de sanc, ou por lou tens;	When someone has an ailment called "adubelati," and it delays in dying either because of the superfluity it produces or because of the blood of the patient when he is decrepit (that is to say too old) and has little blood, or because of the tension; 
et tu la vues haster de meurer:	and you see it hasten to die:
adonques le cauterize entor de mout de petis cauteres en poignant;	then cauterize it around with many small cauteries in pricking. 
aprés le laisse ensi.	afterwards leave it so.
Car elle se hastera de meureir.	For she will hasten to die.
Et se tu la vues percier a tout le cautere, si chaufe le cautere de coi ci est li forme:	And if you see it necessary to perform the whole cautery, then heat the cautery with this form:
Et met ta main en mileu de cele maladie qui est apellee «adubelati» tant que li cauteres ait perciet lou keur, et soit telz li cauteres que li malaides lou sente defuers en teil maniere que li cours de la porriture soit alegis.	And put your hand in the middle of the illness that is called “adubelati” until the cautery has pierced the heart, and let the cautery be such that the patient feels it burning in such a way that the course of the rot is alleviated.
Aprés le cure tant qu’il soit sanez parfaitement.	After the cure as long as it is perfectly healed.
li cure dou feu par fer	The cure of fire by iron
Une autre maniere de maladie i a qui est apelee «corrodens», et n’est autre chose que une mengeson de membre, car ele menjut les membres ausi com li feus les leignes seches.	One other way of sickness there is called 'corrodens', and it is nothing else than a gnawing of the limb, because it wastes the limbs as if the lines were dried up.
Se tu vois ceste maladie en leu qui puisse soffrir cautere ensamble feu, adonques eschaufe les cauteres clavile mout petit et grant, selonc ceu qu’il covient au leu ou li maladie est;	If you see this illness in a place where it can endure cauterization with fire all at once, then sharpen the cautery, small and large, according to what is fitting for the place where the illness is;
aprés le cauterize de toutes pars tant que tu erraiche toute la corruption, et nen remaigne rien de li, que tout ceu qui est corrumpus ne soit osteit.	After the cautery of all parts as long as you reach all the corruption, and nothing remains of it, that all that is corrupted be removed.  
Et puis le laisse III jors, et met sus les leus cauterizez soffre broiet avec oile tant que les eschaudures dou feu soient ostees, et toute li corruption.	And then let him be for III days, and put over the cauterized places softened broth with oil until the scabs of fire are removed, and all the corruption.
Aprés lou cure d’oignemens engendrans char.	After the cure of suppurations causing flesh.
Et se tu vois aprés III jors que chars saine ne naisse, c’est boin;	And if you see after three days that healthy flesh does not grow, it is good. 
et se ceu non, si rencomence le cautere sus ceu qui est demoreit des leus corrumpus.	And if this is not the case, begin the cautery again on that which remains corrupted.  
Et ceste mengeson est aucune fois esteit curee de medicine ague en leu de cautere de feu;	And this malady has never been cured by medicine alone instead of fire cautery; 
mais toutevoie cautere de feu est de plus grant aide, et j’ai ja dit la cure de la medicine ague en la division:	But nonetheless, fire cautery is of greater help, and I have already said the cure of medicinal herbs in the division:
pren la quant tu en as mestier.	Take it when you need it. 
des porrelz qui vienent as piez	of the sprouts which come to the feet
Mout de fois avient que as piez par defuers naist une maladie qui est apelee «clos» selonc nostre entencion, et est une grosse chose fautree qui blece lou piet.	Many times it happens that the feet by fire give birth to a sickness which is called “closed” according to our understanding, and it is a large thing fouled which blunts the foot.
Et li cauteres de ceste maladie si est selonc II manieres.	And the cautery for this malady is according to 2 manners.
C’est a savoir cautere de feu, et cautere d’aigue chaude.	This is to know fire cautery, and cautery of hot water.
Cautere de feu si est que tu eschaufe I cautere cheveit ausi com est une penne de vouteul, et soit fait de boin fer a la mesure qu’il puisse porpenre le clou de toutes pars, et qu’il i ait subtilz marges;	Fire cautery is that you heat the iron cautery as it is a vulture's feather, and it should be made of good iron to the measure that it can reach the nail in all parts, and that it has subtle margins;
aprés le met tout chaut sus lou clou, et torne ta main tot entor le clou tant qu’il viegne au font dou clou;	After place it all hot upon the nail, and turn your hand all around the nail until it comes to the bottom of the nail. 
et lou laisse ensi III jors tant qu’il encomence giter porriture;	And let it thus for III days until it begins to get rot;  
puis li fai un emplaustre de malves savaiges broiies avec seil, et laisse l’emplaustre sus toute la nuit, et li clous cherra et sera desracinez de ses racines.	Then make it an ointment of wild mallows bruised with oil, and leave the ointment upon all night, and the nail will fall and be uprooted from its roots. 
Puis cure le leu d’oignement enjanrant char tant qu’il soit sanez.	Then cure the place with ointment closing flesh until it is healed.
Et s’il sont convertit par defuers lou cors, et maintes fois avient et en mains et em piez, si covient que tu i amenistres cautere d’aigue chaude;	And if they are converted by fire the body, and many times happen in hands and feet, then it is necessary that you bring them a cautery of hot water;
et est en teil maniere:	and is in such manner: 
pren une cainne d’arain ou de fer, ou une penne de vouteul, et met sus lou clou et l’althelul, c’est asavoir porrelz verrues;	Take a cannon of iron or steel, or a feather of vulture, and put upon the nail and the althelul, that is to say corns, warts;
et met la cainne sus si qu’ele porpreigne tout entor, puis i met un poc d’awe chaude, et retien bien ta main, et presse ta main en tornant si que li marge de la cainne viegne a la racine dou clou, et puisse trover l’aigue chaude voie parfonde jusc’a la racine;	and put the cannon upon it so that it pricks all around, then put a drop of hot oil, and hold your hand well, and press your hand turning so that the edge of the cannon comes to the root of the nail, and can find the hot oil going deep until the root;
et soffre li malaides un poc la mordication de l’aigue chaude une houre;	and lets the patient suffer a little the sting of hot water an hour; 
puis le laisse ensi, et il se derracinera tous a tout ses racines.	then lets him so, and it will dislodge itself from all its roots.  
Ensi fai un aprés autre, tant que tu esraiches toz ces qui sont au cors, puis les cure des oignemens qui engenrent char.	Thus do one after another, until you have scraped all those that are on the body, then cure the wounds that engender flesh.
li cure dou trembler	The cure of trembling
Quant aucuns tremble de froidor de ners, ou de fievre quartaine ou d’autre, si covient que tu li faices IIII cauteres ou IV sus l’espinee dou dos, I cautere entre chescune espinee;	When some shiver from cold, or from quartan fever, or another, it is necessary that you make him four cauteries or four on the spine of his back, one cautery between each vertebra.
et I cautere ou pez, et I sus l’estomac au cautere olivaire;	and one cautery or weight, and one on the stomach at the olive cautery; 
si laissera lou trembler, et se hastera li santez de la maladie froide.	so letting him tremble, and will hasten his health from the cold disease.
des pustules puans	of pimples painful
Aucune fois apperent par defuers le cors bathes, ou pustules puans, que vienent de grosses matieres corrumpues.	At no time appear by fires the bathed body, or puss-filled pustules, that come from large corrupted materials.
si covient au premier quant eles apperent que on faice cautere sus chescun chief de la pustule:	it is necessary at first when they appear that one makes a cautery on each head of the pustule:
un cautere subtil de fust de mirte, de coi li pointe soit emprise au feu, ou de racine de aristologe longe, ou au cautere lenticulaire.	a subtle cautery of myrtle stick, so that its point is seized by fire, or of long birthwort root, or the lentil cautery.
Et aucune fois les cauterize on au comencement quant il aperent, selonc ceste maniere, et il ne puent croistre des enqui en avant, mais est desrompue li superfluitez dont il vienent, et sont sanez;	And sometimes when they appear at the beginning, they are cauterized in this manner, and they cannot grow back from then on, but the superfluities that come from them are removed, and they are healed. 
mais il covient que ceu soit fait aprés l’evacuation de sanc.	But it is necessary that this be done after the evacuation of blood.  
quant li artere est copee	when the artery is cut
Maintes fois avient grans decorremens de sanc de l’artere qui est copee a la plaie que vient au pardefuers, ou a l’incision de l’aposteme, ou au cautere dou membre, et as semblans choses;	Many times great hemorrhages of blood occur from the artery that is cut at the wound which comes to the outside, or in the incision of an abscess, or in the cauterization of the limb, and similar things.
et est mout grief chose d’estenchier.	And it is a very grave thing to prolong.  
Et toutevoie quant ceu avient a aucun, si te haste de mettre ton doi indice sus la plaie de la voinne, et l’estrain mout tant que li sans soit apaisiez desoz ton doi, et que goute n’en isse plus;	And yet when this happens to anyone, hasten to place your index finger on the wound of the vein, and restrain it very much until the bleeding is appeased beneath your finger, and no more drops issue.
puis met au feu les cauteres olivaire plusors petis et grans tant qu’il soient tuit rouge;	then put on the fire olive cautery more small and large as they are all red; 
puis empren I, ou grant ou petit selonc la plaie et lou leu en coi li artere est route, et met le cautere sus cele voine ou tu tiens ton doi, et tien le cautere tant sus que li sans soit restainchiez.	then take it [the cautery], whether large or small according to the wound and its place where the artery is cut, and put the cautery on that vein where you hold your hand, and hold the cautery as long as the blood is stopped. 
Et s’il saut fuers quant tu lieves ton doi desus la voinne, et li cauteres estint, si pren hastivement I autre des cauteres qui sont au feu.	And if it jumps out when you lift your arm above the vein, and the cautery is extinguished, then take hastily another cautery from the fire.
Et ne cesser de faire ceu l’un aprés l’autre tant que li sans soit estenchiez;	And do not cease to make those one after another until the bleeding is stopped.  
et warde que tu n’ardes lou nerf qui est delez, et que autre malice ne viegne sus lou malaide;	and guard that you do not burn the nerve which is nearby, and that no other harm comes to the patient. 
et saiches que quant sans decourt de l’artere, c’on ne lou puet mie bien restenchier meismement quant li artere est grans, se ceu n’est par une des IIII manieres que nos avons dit:	And know that when without cutting of the artery, one cannot well stitch it even when the artery is large, unless by one of the four ways that we have said: 
ou par cautere, ou par extraction quant ele n’est mie traite, ou par fort liement de fil, ou par medicines mises sus qui ont pooir de restenchier sanc;	or by cautery, or by extraction when it is not treated, or by strong tying of thread, or by medicines put on that have power to stitch blood. 
et soit liee et estrainte avennament.	And be bound and strained well.  
Qui i amenistrera restenchement de liier estroitement de drapelz ou de metre choses ardans sus, ou autres semblans choses, se n’i profite se poc non.	Who will bring it tight with bandages or by placing hot things on it, or other similar things, if it does not benefit it a little.
Et se ce avient a aucun et il n’ait mie mire ne medicine present, si doit mettre son doi indice sus la plaie de la voinne si com nos avons dit, et bien estrendre tant qu’il soit restenchiez desus la plaie et desus la voinne;	And if this happens to anyone and there is no medicine present, then one must put his two index fingers on the wound of the vein as we have said, and well strain until it is stitched above the wound and above the vein.
et ne remuer lou doit, mais lou moille d’awe froide sovent que soit mout froide tant que li sans soit congelez et engrossiez et restenchiez;	and he must not move them, but often moisten them with cold water that is very cold until the blood is congealed and thickened and stitched. 
et faice des enqui en avant ceu dont il a mestier de cauteres et de medicines.	And make inquiries beforehand of those who need cautery and medicines. 
Ci encomence li secons livre des cures de taille	Here begins the second book of the cures of the knife
Nos vos avons dit ou premier chapistre toute maladie en coi il covient cautere de feu, ou de medicine ardans, et les oquisons et les causes et les estrumens et les formes des cauteres;	We have told you in the first chapter all illnesses where it is necessary to use fire cautery, or hot medicines, and their origins and causes and instruments and forms of the cauteries; 
et ai mis celui chapistre des lou chief jusc’a piez, et je irai en cest chapistre par celi meisme voie por ceu c’on trueve plus legierement ceu c’on voura.	And we have placed this chapter from the head down to the feet, and in this chapter I will follow the same way for those things that are found more easily for those who want them.  
Et ainsois que je encomence ceu, il covient, chier fil, que vos aprenez que en cest chapistre a plus de peril et de paor que ou premier des cauteres, et por ceu il covient plus grant cautele.	And thus as I begin these, it is necessary, dear child, that you learn that in this chapter there is more danger and fear than in the first of cauteries, and for that reason greater caution is needed.
Car en l’ovraige de cest chapistre avient maintes fois evacuation de sanc a l’ovrir la voinne, et a l’incision sus aposteme, et as cures des plaies, et a l’estraction des saiettes, et a l’incision sus la piere, et les semblans choses;	For in the work of this chapter there is often the evacuation of blood when opening a vein, and incising an abscess, and in the treatment of wounds, and in the extraction of arrows, and in cutting into stones, and similar things; 
ou il a doutance et paor, et en vient li mors a plusors.	where there is doubt and fear, and many die.  
Et je vos amoneste que vos n’entreprenez folie.	And I warn you that you do not undertake folly.
Car mout de manieres de gens vienent en cures.	For many kinds of people come to cures.
si vienent de telz qui s’aïrent si avec lor maladie qu’il muerent legierement por la forsenerie qu’il trueve de sa maladie, et de la grandour de son malice;	If they come from such ones who have suffered so much with their sickness that they die easily because of the famine they find in their illness, and because of the greatness of their wickedness. 
et de ces doit on avoir paor.	And from these one should have fear.  
Et de ces i a qui te done son sens, et dit:	And of these there is one who gives you his meaning, and says: 
«atendez, je sui garis»;	Wait, I am healed"; 
et li maladie est despitouse.	and the sickness is spiteful.  
Il ne covient mie que vos vos consentez a ces qui vienent a vos qui ont ceste maniere, mais mettez plus grant cusanson en vostre honor qu’en vostre covoitise, et n’ovrez mie folement mais saigement de ceu dont vos estes certain, et dont vos poez avoir pris et los;	It is not fitting that you consent to those who come to you who have this manner, but put more emphasis on your honor than on your greed, and do not open yourself fully but wisely to those of whom you are certain, and from whom you can take and profit.
et usez de pronostication et de indication en cures de vos malaides a coi salus soit convertie;	and use prognostication and indication in the treatment of your patients so that health may be restored. 
et ceu vos aidera a aquester bone renommee, et gloire, et memoire de loenge.	And this will help you to acquire good reputation, and glory, and lasting memory.  
Tres chier fil, Nostres Sires vos doint boin entendement et droiture, et se vos vuelle espireir de la sainte inspiration de sa main, amen.	Three cheers, our Lords give you good understanding and straightness, and if you wish to be inspired by the holy inspiration of his hand, amen.
Or je vos ai ordeneit cest chapistre en devisant par chapistres, selonc ceu qu’il est devant ou chapistre des cauteres, que je vos ai deviseit des le chief jusc’a piez, por ceu que vos trovez plus legierement ceu dont vos avrez mestier.	Or I have ordered this chapter to you by chapters, according to what is before the chapter of cauteries, that I have devised from the head to the feet, for those who find it easier.
dou chief plein d’aigue	The head full of water
Saiches que ceste maladie vient mout de fois as enfans a l’enfanter, et quant li baille estraint trop fort le chief de l’enfant;	Know that this sickness comes often to children at birth, and when the midwife pulls too hard on the head of the child; 
et aucune fois vient ceu de cause reponue que on ne seit.	and sometimes it comes from a reason unknown.  
Et je ne vis onques ceste maladie fuers qu’en enfans, et a toz ces que j’ai veus se hastait li mors;	And I have never seen this sickness outside of children, and in all those that I have seen it hastened death; 
et por ceu me semble qu’il me vaut mues lassier l’ovraige en teilz cures.	and for this reason it seems to me that I should leave the work in such cures.  
Et je vis I enfant de coi li chiés estoit plains d’aigue, et li chief engroissoit chescun jor tant qu’il ne lou pooit sostenir;	And I saw a child whose head was full of water, and it grew each day until he could not bear it; 
et crut tant li moistor qu’il fut mors, et ceste moistor si est assemblee desoz l’os sus lou syphac, entre lou keur et l’os;	and the water grew so much that he died, and this water is assembled under the bone above the spine, between the heart and the bone; 
et li ovraiges si est telz se li moistor est entre lou keur et l’os, et li apostemes est petis, que tu fendes emmi lou chief une fendure large;	and the works are such if moisture is between the heart and bone, and the abscess is small, that you split in between the chest a wide slit; 
et soit ausi longe com II nous, tant que li mostor corre;	and let it also be as long as we II, while the moisture runs;  
et vez ci la forme dou spatumile:	and see here the shape of the spatula: 
Se li moistor est plus creue, et li aposteme soit plus grans, si fai II fendures en maniere d’une croix, selonc ceste forme:	If the moisture is more abundant, and the abscess is larger, then make incisions in the form of a cross, according to this shape:
Et se li moistor est desoz l’os, et li signes que tu vois les commissures dou chief overtes de chescune partie, et li aigue saut fuer quant tu la presses de ta main au dedens, et ceu ne t’est mie reponut:	And if the moisture is below the bone, and the signs that you see are the incisions of the chest open from each side, and the liquid jumps out when you press it with your hand inward, and this does not return to you:
si covient que tu fendes enmi lou chief III fendures selonc ceste maniere:	then it is necessary that you split in the chest III incisions according to this manner: 
Et aprés l’incision estrai la moistor toute fuers.	And after the incision remove the moisture all outside.
Aprés estraint les fendures de drapelz et de poudres, et i met vin et oile, et laisse ensi jusc’a cinquieme jor;	Afterward, restrain the incisions with cloth and powders, and put in wine and oil, and leave thus until the fifth day;
puis le deslie, et cure la plaie par tentes et par oignemens, et laisse estraindre le chief egaument, et done mengier au malaide viande seche de poc de moistor tant que li membre soit confortez et sanez.	Then loosen it, and cure the wound with bandages and ointments, and let the principal bandage be strained, and then feed the patient dry meat of little moisture until the limb is fortified and healed. 
Et une autre maniere d’incision est que tu regardes ou apert li grandor de l’aposteme, et li assemblé de l’aigue;	And another way of incision is that you look where opens the greatness of the abscess, and the assembly of the liquid; 
car aucune fois est elle devant;	for no times is it in front;
aucune fois derrier;	no times behind;
aucune fois en destre;	No time in the right;  
et aucune fois en senestre.	and no time on the left. 
Taille donques lai ou li aposteme apert, et l’emplissement de l’aigue, et lou fent selonc ce que tu en as le pooir;	Therefore take it where the abscess is open, and the filling of the water, and make it according to what you are able.  
et warde que tu ne coper l’artere;	and guard that you do not cut the artery; 
et veigne flun de sanc, si que li malaides muere dou decorrement de sanc et de l’evacuation de moistor.	And vein blood, so that the patient dies from the loss of blood and the evacuation of moisture.  
de reume	of a summary
Quant il avient a aucun une maladie qui est apelee «catarre» as eulz ou au pis, et li maladie est anciainne, et li cure de medicine ne profite mie, adonques li derraine cure si est li cauteres avec ceu c’on li copera les II arteres.	When it happens to someone a sickness which is called “catarre” in the eyes or in the breast, and the sickness is old, and the cure of medicine does not help at all, then the last cure that is done is cauterization with those which one covers the II arteries.
Il covient donques, cant tu les vues coper, que li malaides faice rere son chief;	Therefore it is fitting, since you are about to cut them, that the patient turns his head back; 
aprés li frotte lou leu d’un drapel aspre tant que les arteres aperent, puis estraingne li malaides son col a tout I drapel;	after he rubs the place with a rough cloth until the arteries are open, then restrain the patient's neck to all the cloth.
puis regarde ou li voine bait, et li leus de l’une et de l’autre sont aprés les oreilles, et poc sont reponues;	then look where the vein beats, and the veins of one and the other are after the ears, and they are then returned. 
puis signe les leus d’enche, puis cope l’une et l’autre d’un spatumile agut de II pars, tant que li taille veigne jusc’a l’os, et ceu soit par lou large dou chief.	Then sign the places of the joints, then cut one and the other with a sharp spatula from II parts, as long as the flesh comes to the bone, and that it be by the wide part of the head. 
Et se tu vues, boute le spatumile desoz l’artere et la cope au desus, en taillant ausi com II dois au traver.	And if you see, put the spatula under the artery and the cup above, cutting as I do across.
Et quant li voinne est copee, si saut li sans en haut continuelment fuers.	And when the vein is cut, the blood leaps out continuously upwards.
Et se li artere n’apert au sentir, si covient que tu mesures la quantiteit de l’espaice de III dois, puis seigne d’enche et fent jusc’a l’os;	And if the artery does not open to the feeling, then it is necessary that you measure the quantity of the space of III digits, then sign it and go until the bone. 
et ceu qu’il covient dou sanc mettre fuers si est VI c/, et par aventure un poc plus ou moins, selonc ce que li malaides puet soffrir, et la repletion de l’artere;	And that which is necessary of blood to put out is VI c/, and perhaps a little more or less, according to what the patient can suffer, and the filling of the artery;
puis regarde la plaie:	then look at the wound:
s’il remaint sus l’os point dou syphac, si le cope que apostemes chaus n’i veigne, puis estrain la plaie et lie, et la cure d’oignement tant qu’ele soit sanee.	If it remains on the bone without a bit of syphac, then cut it so that an abscess does not come, then strain the wound and bind it, and the cure of ointment as long as it is healed.
de emigrainne	of migraine
Quant emigrainne anciaine vient, et catarre agut, por les moistors des larmes et les chalors en temples et sode anciene forsenee et semblans choses, et il est medicinez par manieres de cures de medicine et tout ceu ne li profite mie, si estraions les arteres des temples et lou cauterizons, si com nos avons conteit.	When ancient migraine comes and acute catarrh, for the moistors of tears and the heats in temples and old forsenee and similar things, and it is medicated by manners of cures of medicine and all that does not help it, if we drain the arteries of the temples and cauterize them, as we have recounted.
Et li maniere de l’estraction d’elles si est que li malaides faice rere les poilz de ses temples, et entende a l’artere qui apert en la temple, car elle apert bien par son batement, et est poc reponue fuers que en aucuns homes qui sont trop froit;	And the manner of their extraction is that the patient makes his hair rear up from his temples, and listens to the artery which opens in the temple, for it opens well by its beating, and is poorly returned outwards than in some men who are too cold; 
et s’elle est reponue, si estraigne son col li malaides d’aucuns drapelz, puis frote le leu d’aucun aspre drap, et arose le leu d’aigue chaude tant que li artere apere manifestement;	And if it is returned, then the patient's neck is restrained with some cloths, then the place is rubbed with some rough cloth, and the place is raised with hot water until the artery opens manifestly; 
puis pren le spatumile de coi ci est li forme:	Then take the spatula of which this is the form;
puis escorche le cuir legierement tant que tu veignes a l’artere, puis la trai en haut as pinceures, et la depart bien des toiles que sont desoz li de chescune partie;	then scrape the skin lightly until you come to the artery, then treat it upwards with pinches, and separate it well from the webs that are under from each part; 
et se li artere est subtilz, si la torne a la pointe de l’uncine, puis la cope de celle partie selonc la quantiteit des II chiés.	And if the artery is subtle, then it is turned to the point of the instrument, then it is cut from that part according to the quantity of the two heads. 
Car s’elle n’est copee, si ne saut mie li sans dou tout en tout.	For if it is not cut, it will not jump the veins at all.
Et trai dou sanc des VI c/, jusc’a III;	And treat with blood from VI to III;  
et se li artere est grans, si covient que tu la lies en II leus d’un fil double fort de soie, que porriture n’i veigne devant le soudement de la plaie, et veigne decorremens de sanc;	and if the artery is large, it is necessary that you tie it in II places with a strong double thread of silk so that rot does not come before the healing of the wound and bleeding comes.  
puis cope la superfluiteit qui est entre les II liiens en celle houre meisme, et puis, se tu vues, si lou cauterize dou cautere cutellaire jusc’a l’os tant que li chiés soient copez;	then cut the excess that is between the two ties in the same hour, and then, if you see fit, cauterize with the cuticular cautery up to the bone as long as the extremities are cut; 
et c’est li muedre oevre, se li malaides n’a fievre et il est de chaude complexion.	and this is the best work, if the patient does not have a fever and he is of a warm complexion.  
Car li cauteres est aide por finir les moistors:	For cautery helps to finish the dampness: 
por ceu est il de plus grant aide as moistors.	for that is of greater help against dampnesses.   
Ou il covient por l’estraction des arteres que om emplisse lou leu de viel coton et mette on sus tentes bien faites;	Where it is necessary for the extraction of arteries that one fills the place with old cotton and puts a good tent on top; 
et quant on les desliera, si soit curez de medicines seches que font naistre char, et de tentes, tant qu’il soit sanez;	And when they are untied, so it is cared for with dry medicines that cause flesh to grow, and bandages, until it is healed.  
et se sans cort de l’artere tant dis com tu i oevres, si te haste dou coper par cautere, ou tu emple lou leu de vitriole et l’estrain a ta main que li sans soit estainchiez;	And if the artery is without cord as you work it, then hurry to cover by cautery, or you employ the place of vitriol and strain it with your hand that the bleeding be stopped. 
et se tu n’as ceu present, si met sor le leu ton doit tant que li sans soit congelez, et arose le leu d’aigue froide tant que li sans cesse, et soit estraint si com il covient;	And if you lack these things present, then put on the place your thumb until the bleeding is stopped, and raise the place with cold water as long as the bleeding ceases, and be restrained as it is fitting.  
et ceu qui est muedre et plus legier en l’estraction de l’artere est que tu cauterizes la voinne de cest cautere trenchant de II pars, mais li trenchant soient bien espés por warder plus longement lor chalor.	And that which is more to be done and lighter in the extraction of the artery is that you cauterize the vein with this cautery trenching on two parts, but the trenches should be well spaced in order to keep their heat for longer. 
Car quant li estrumens est trop tenves, si tient moins sa chalor.	For when the instrument is too stiff, it holds less heat.
Et doit avoir entre les II coutelz I doit de gros d’espaice, et puis quant tu as signiet d’enche les II leus, et tu mes lou fer ardant sus tant qu’il viegne jusc’a l’os, et cope la voinne en II leus;	And it must have between the two knives one doit of wide space, and then when you have signed their two places, and you put the burning iron upon it until it comes to the bone, and cut the vein in two places.  
et soient esloigniet entre les II chiés car il n’est mie soudez de cest cautere dou tout en tout;	And be separated between the two shoulders because it is not well healed of this cautery at all or in any way. 
et c’est li forme dou cautere:	And this is the shape of the cautery: 
des larmes	tears
