Quant les larmes des eulz sont dessendans des voinnes que sont sus lou test dou chief de fuer, et il ne profite mie cure de medicine c’on i faice, et tu vois la faice dou malaide enrougir, et sent ou front ambulation si com de fremis;	When the tears of the eyes are flowing down from the veins that are on the forehead above the head, and it does not benefit medicine at all if one applies it, and you see the face of the patient becoming entangled, and feel on his forehead a walk like a tremor; 
et sui oil sont tenve et moiste si que li poil des papieres sont cheut, et sont eschaufees les papieres, et escorchies de l’ardor des larmes, si ait mestier de ceste cure.	And where the skin is thick and moist so that the hair of the temples falls out, and the temples are dry, and scorched by the heat of the tears, this treatment is necessary. 
Et l’apelerent li ancien «cure contuse», et est que tu faices a rere au malaide qui a ceste maladie les poilz qu’il ait ou front, puis li fai III fendures ou front igalment selonc la longesce dou front;	And they called it in the old days "contused cure," and is that you do to the patient who has this sickness the hairs that he have on his forehead, then make three cuts on his forehead evenly according to the length of the forehead. 
et soit l’une des fendures ausi com II doi tout emmi lou front en avalant aval jusc’a neif, et les autres II as II costelz par desus les papieres, et te garde de l’incision des arteres que sont as II costez par desus les papieres;	and let one of the cuts be as two should all remove the forehead down to the root, and the other two as two on top of the cheekbones, and keep yourself from the incision of the arteries that are the two on top of the cheekbones. 
et aloigne ta main de la continuation des II mandibules, et soit chescune plaie la quantiteit de III dois au traver joins;	and move your hand away from the continuation of the two jawbones, and let each wound the quantity of three be on the cross joints.
et aies apparillie une piece d’esponge et mout de drapelz ses por essuer lou sanc, puis boute le spatumile agut de II pars de coi ci est li forme:	and have prepared a piece of sponge and plenty of cloths to wipe the blood, then put the spatula sharp from two parts where this is the shape.
des l’incision qui est dever la temple jusc’a la seconde incision;	From the incision which is behind the temple to the second incision. 
et escorche tout le keur qui est entre les II fendures a tot lou syfac qui est sus l’os, puis fai autreteil des la moiene incision jusc’a l’autre seconde, et puis estrai fuer cest spatumile.	And scrape all the core which is between the two fissures to all the syfas that are on the bone, then make another part from the middle incision up to the other second, and then extract further this spatula. 
si boute en la premiere fendure l’estrument qui est apelez «cultellaire», et est tresbien trenchans d’une part, et d’autre part est souef, ne mie trenchans, et c’est li forme:	If in the first incision you put the instrument called "cultellaire," and it is very sharp on one side, and on the other side is blunt, not sharp, and this is its form:
Et met le costeit taillant vers la char aerse au keur, et lou costeit souef vers l’os, et lou boute tant qu’il veigne a la moiene fendure.	And put the rib cutting towards the flesh to the heart, and the rib bottom toward the bone, and the point until it comes to the middle joint.
Et cope toz les vasselz que dessendent dou chief as eulz tant que l’incision soit continue jusc’a ceu qui apert dou keur, et puis autreteil fai en la moiene fendure jusc’a l’autre defuer;	And cut all the vessels that descend from the head to the eyes as long as the incision is continuous until it reaches those who open the heart, and then another part make in the middle furrow until the other side. 
et puis estrai dou sanc igalment, et espresse lou leu por le sanc pris;	And then withdraw blood evenly, and press the wound to stop the bleeding. 
puis met en chescune fendure une tente de viel coton, et met sus drapelz moilliez en vin et en oile et en aisil, et garde que apostemes chaus n’i veigne;	Then place a tent of old cotton in each incision, and put cloths moistened in wine, oil, and asphalt above them, and keep that an abscess does not come.  
et au tier jor deslie lou liien, et i amenistre grant planteit d’aigue tede, puis lou cure d’oignement basilicon avec oile roset, et d’autres cures dont on cure plaies, tant qu’il soit sanez.	And on the third day untie the bandage, and then administer a great quantity of tepid water, then apply ointment of basil with rose oil, and other ointments used to treat wounds, until it is healed. 
dou reume des eulz	of the closing of the eyes
Quant a aucun vienent catarre agut acostumeement, et tu vois les eulz tenves et petis, et afoiblir la veue, et les papieres brulees;	When someone comes down with a sharp catarrh, and you see the eyes swollen and small, and the vision weakened, and the whites of the eyes burned; 
et li poil chieent, et ou chief en parfont a dolor ague, et li malaides esternue;	and hair falls out, and where it is touched they feel sharp pain, and the patient sneezes.
adonques saiches par ces accidens que celles matieres et cil catharre ne vient fuer que de maintes voines, et li muedre cure que i est, si est ceste.	Then know by these signs that those materials and this catarrh come from many veins, and the best remedy for it is as follows.
Et est que tu comande au malaide a rere son front, puis fai une grant fendure emmi lou front, et une autre dou large I poc.	And it is that you command the patient to raise their forehead, then make a great cut in between the brow, and another one wide in the cheekbone.
Et comence des la fendure de la temple senestre a la temple destre, et soit li incision jusc’a l’os;	And begins from the slit of the left temple to the right temple, and let the incision be up to the bone; 
et esloigne ta main des ners des temples que muevent au mengier;	and keep your hand away from the nerves of the temples that move when eating; 
et quant li os est descovers, si essue tout le sanc a une esponge, et puis desevre entre les II levres de la fendure et i met coton viel, et tentes de lin;	and when the bone is uncovered, wipe all the blood with a sponge, and then sew between the two lips of the slit and put old cotton there, and linen bandages;
puis lie desus drapelz moilliez en vin et en oile, et te garde d’aposteme chaut;	then bind above with cloths softened in wine and oil, and guard against a hot abscess;  
quant il est ostez, si covient que tu frottes l’os tant que chars i comence a naistre, puis le cure de choses exiccatives, que font enjanrer char.	when it is removed, then you must rub the bone until flesh begins to grow, then treat with drying things that make flesh come together. 
En teil maniere:	In this manner: 
pren II parties de flor de froment, et de colofoine IIII parties, et en fai emplaustre;	Take two parts of wheat flower and four parts of colophony, and make a plaster;
et l’aministre en ces plaies por enjanrer char per tout.	and administer it on these wounds to bring flesh together throughout. 
de l’estoupement des oreilles	of the stopping up of the ears
Tout ceu que chiet ens oreilles est une des IIII choses:	Everything that falls into the ears is one of four things:
ou grains, ou beste, ou piere de mine ou semblans chose si com fer;	or grains, or beast, or stone, or similar thing like iron; 
ou semence, si com jaisses, feves, pois;	or seeds, such as lentils, beans, peas;
ou chose defluans si com aigue et aisilz et semblans choses.	or flowing things such as water and oil and similar things. 
Quant il chiet en l’oreille piere ou autre maniere de chose que ne s’ajoste mie a l’oreille, ne ne croist en l’oreille, si met l’oreille au solel.	When it falls into the ear stone or any other kind of thing that does not join with the ear, nor grows in the ear, put the ear to the sun.
Se tu vois la piere, si distille aucun poc d’oile violet ou oile de sisament, puis i amenistre extraction;	If you see a stone, if it distills any drop of violet oil or sesame oil, then administer extraction. 
et lou fai esternuer de condisi, et li estoupe les narines quant li esternuemens vient, et met entor l’oreille pieces de drapelz ou laine;	And make him sneeze with condiment, and stuff his nostrils when the sneezing comes, and place around the ear pieces of cloth or wool; 
et estent l’oreille au desus.	and hold the ear upwards.  
Mout de fois vient fuer par ceste cure;	Often a fever comes with this cure;   
et s’elle ne vient fuer, se li amenistre extraction as pinceures subtilz, de coi ci est li forme:	And if it does not come forcefully, administer an extraction with subtle pinches, for this is the form:  
S’elle saut fuer as pinceures, c’est boin;	If it jumps forth forcefully from the pinches, that is good;  
se ceu non, si amenistre extraction a l’oncine subtil de petite doubleure;	if those do not, administer extraction to the edge with a small fold. 
et s’elle ne saut par ceu, si fai une caine d’arain et boute lou chief de la cainne ou pertuis de l’oreille fort, et estoupe ceu qui est entor la cainne de cire mole si que li vens n’i puisse entrer avec la cainne;	and if it does not jump by those, make a tube of reed and insert the head of the tube or orifice of the ear forcefully, and stuff that which is around the tube with soft wax so that the wind cannot enter with the tube.  
puis le trai fuer forment, car mout de fois vient fuer si com nos avons dit;	Then the treatment must be formed, because many times it comes as we have said.  
et s’elle ne vient fuer en teil maniere, si prent glut de coi en prent les oisiaus, et met en som aucun estrument qui soit a point por ceu faire, et met un poc de coton entor;	And if it does not come to treatment in such manner, then take glut of this and pluck the feathers, and put it into some instrument which is pointed for this purpose, and put a piece of cotton around it; 
puis presse le glut sus la piere ou quel chose que ce soit, et trai fuer.	Then press the glut upon the stone or whatever else it may be, and treat as before.  
Et s’elle ne saut fuer de toutes ces choses que nos avons dit, si te haste de fendre l’oreille ainsois que aposteme chalz i veigne, et spasme;	And if it does not come to treatment from all these things that we have said, then hasten to split the ear in such a way that a pus-filled abscess comes out, and spasms.   
et li maniere de la fendure si est que tu faices premier sainier lou malaide de la cephalique, et estrai dou sanc selonc la mesure de sa vertu, puis fai seoir lou malaide entre tes mains et li torne l’oreille au desus, et fent une petite fendure en la racine de l’oreille a la graisse ou leu dependant;	And the manner of splitting it is that you first make the patient healthy from the head, and extract blood according to the measure of his virtue, then make the patient sit between your hands and turn the ear upwards, and make a small split in the root of the ear to the fat or where it depends;
et soit li fendure ausi com une lune, tant que tu viegnes a la piere, puis l’oste selonc ton pooir, et la suce hastanment a ta bouche;	and let the cut be like a moon, as long as you come to the stone, then the bone according to your strength, and suck it gently with your mouth; 
et la cure tant qu’il soit sanez.	and treat it until it is healed. 
Et se c’est grains qui est ens et il enfle, si aministre extraction;	And if it's grains that are inside and it swells, then administer an extraction;  
et si’il ne puet issir, si amenistre I spatumile tenve subtil selonc ceste forme:	and if it cannot be issued, then administer a spatula gentle according to this form: 
et amenistre incision de celui grain.	and administer an incision to that grain.
Mais ne faire mie ceu quant tu penses que li grains est moistes por la moistor de l’oreille, tant que tu en aies fait maintes pieces;	But do not do this when you think that the grain is moist due to the moisture of the ear, until you have made many pieces. 
puis l’estrai as pinceures subtilz et au succier, si com nos avons dit, si que li estractions soit aligie.	then extract with fine pincers and by suction, as we have said, so that the extraction be aligned.  
En l’aigue donques que chiet en l’oreille covient que li malaides use d’esternuement de condisi premiers, et ample l’oreille de viel coton.	In the earache therefore that falls in the ear it is necessary that the patient uses a first external of condiment, and opens the ear with old cotton.
Et soit gisans sus celle oreille meisme ou li aigue est.	And lie lying on that same ear where the water is.
s’elle saut fuer per ceu, c’est boin.	If it has leaped forward because of this, it is good.
se ceu non, si prent maintes pieres selonc li longesce de ton doit tenves et legieres, et les eschaufe un poc au feu;	if this is not the case, then take many stones according to the length of your finger, thin and light, and warm them a little in the fire.
et em mette li malaides une ou pertus de son oreille, et saille sus i. de ses piez d’autre part, et fiere d’une autre piere sus la piere qui est en l’oreille;	and he puts in the patient one of pierced from his ear, and it is raised up on those legs of other side, and fire of another stone upon the stone which is in the ear. 
et ne cesse de faire ceu de piere em piere tant que li aigue isse toute fuer, et ensi saut elle toute fuer;	and does not cease to do that of stone on stone until the water comes out all force, and then it jumps all force; 
et se tu vues, si prent I jonc, et boute l’un des chiés en l’oreille, et l’autre chief emprent de feu tant que li plus dou jonc soit ars;	and if you see this, then take reed, and put one end in the ear, and the other end take fire until the most soft part of the reed is burned. 
puis refai autreteil d’autres jons tant que li aigue isse toute, si com nos avons dit en la piere.	then redo the other piece with other reeds until the water comes out all, as we have said in the stone.  
En l’estraction de la beste, s’elle est de petit cors, si com puce et semblans chose, cure la si com nos avons dit en la division;	In the extraction of the beast, if it is of small body, as flea and similar thing, cure it as we have said in the division; 
mais s’elle est de grant cors c’on la puisse sentir, si amenistre extraction de pinceures;	but if it is of large body so that one can feel it, then administer extraction with forceps; 
et c’est li chose plus legiere a oster qui soit en l’oreille.	and this is the thing lightest to remove which is in the ear. 
En l’estraction des vers enjanrez as oreilles, quant tu lou cures si com nos avons dit en la division et ou traitier des distillations, et li cure ne profite mie, si covient que tu regardes l’oreille au soleil:	In the extraction of worms, cleanse the ears, when you treat them as we have said in the division and where we treated distillations, and if the treatment does not help, then it is necessary that you look at the ear to the sun.  
s’il i apert nulz vers, si les trai as pinceures subtilz, et s’il n’aperent, si prent la cainne de coi ci est li forme:	if there appear any worms, then treat them with subtle pincers, and if they do not appear, then take the cage of which this is the form: 
Et soit estroite desoz et large desus.	And it should be narrow below and wide above.
Et boute lou plus subtil chief en l’oreille selonc la quantiteit de la soffrance dou malaide, puis succe forment a tot la caine;	And put the most subtle head into the ear according to the quantity of the suffering of the sick person, then succeed in forming all the cage: 
fai ceu sovent tant que tuit li ver issent.	do this often as many times as all the worms exit.  
Et s’il n’obeissent a issir, si estoupe entor la cainne de coton si com j’ai dit en la piere;	And if they do not obey to come out, then stuff around the cage with cotton as I have said in the stone;
et s’il ne saillent fuer si com nos avons dit, si aministre distillations que li ancien ont esprovees en l’ocision des vers, et tu les troveras ou traitier des distillations;	and if they do not sprout forth as we have said, then administer distillations that the ancients have proven in the killing of worms, and you will find them or treat with distillations 
et si distille tes oiles et tes medicines en l’oreille a tout cest estrument, de coi ci est li forme si com tu vois:	and if you distill your oils and your medicines into the ear to all this instrument, for this is the form as you see:  
Et soit d’argent ou d’arain estrois desoz a I petis pertuis, et desus overs por distiller;	And whether of silver or of iron be cut out at the small opening, and above over to distill; 
et por presser dedens la distillation a I estrument d’arain bien fait por ceu, et se tu vues pren I raseur et envoloupe entor la pointe avenanment coton;	and to press inside the distillation to the instrument of iron well made for this purpose, and if you see take the razor and wrap around the tip carefully cotton;
puis i giete ton oile ou ton jus, et ceu que tu vues de tes medicines en la cainne, et li caine soit en l’oreille;	then throw your oil or your juice, and what you see of your medicines in the channel, and the channel be in the ear; 
puis boute dedens lou raseur a tout lou coton, et presse ta main tempreement tant que li oile soit distilleit ou chevement de l’oreille;	then put inside the razor all the cotton, and press your hand temperately until the oil is distilled or at the end of the ear;
et lou sente li malaides dedens, et soit li distillations I poc eschaufee au feu ainsois c’on la distille en l’oreille;	And he feels it inside the patient, and if the distillation is a little too hot from the fire then one puts it in the ear. 
et garde qu’elle ne soit trop froide, car li medicine ne seroit mie si bone.	And keep it from being too cold, for the medicine would not be so good.  
de l’estoupement des oreilles	of the stopping up of the ears
Aucun enfant naissent qui n’ont nul pertus ens oreilles;	No child is born without a hole in their ears; 
et ceste meisme chose avient as homes par estoupement de plaie, ou de char nee dedens l’oreille, et cist estoupemens vient aucune fois em parfont en l’oreille, si c’on ne lou puet veoir;	And this same thing happens to people by a swelling of wound, or a boil formed inside the ear, and these swellings come sometimes from within the ear, if one cannot see them.  
et aucune fois avient I poc defuer lou pertus, et lou voit om bien.	And sometimes it happens that there is a little bit of pus coming out of the hole, and one sees it well. 
Celle donques que vient em parfont, si c’on ne la puet veoir, est de grief sanation em plusors dispositions, et en cele c’on voit covient que tu mettes l’oreille dou malaide au soleil;	That one which comes from within, if one cannot see it, is of grievous healing in more cases, and in this one sees that you must put the ear of the sick person to the sun. 
et regarde dedens:	and look inside: 
se tu vois l’opilation apparent, si la oevre a tot cest spatumile de coi ci est li forme:	if you see the  apparent opening, if the work has completely this spatula of what it is the form: 
Et soit agus et trenchans devant et derrier tout plain, si qu’il ne blece l’oreille;	And be smooth and notched in front and behind all plane, so that it does not  bleed the ear;
se li opilation est de char nee ou cors de l’oreille, si la tien as pinceures subtilz, et la cope legierement, tant que celle chars soit toute ostee.	if the opening is of flesh or the  flesh of the ear, if the hold with subtle pincers, and the cut lightly, until that flesh is completely removed. 
Et se li opilations est em parfont en l’oreille, si pren I raseur subtil legier et l’eschaufe un petit au feu, puis li met ou cors de l’oreille.	And if the operation is done in the ear, then take a fine and light razor and heat it slightly at the fire, then put it on the body of the ear.
Se tu sens l’opilation dont li malaides sent grieteit a l’oïr, perce legierement, et garde que tu ne grever les ners de l’oreille;	If you feel the opening that the patient feels great pain in the ear, pierce lightly, and keep that you do not wound the nerves of the ear;
puis met en l’oreille une tente selonc la largesce dou pertus, et la moille en l’oignement egyptien.	then put in the ear a tent according to the width of the hole, and moisten it with the Egyptian ointment. 
Fai ceu aucun jor tant que li plaie soit soudee, ou tu pren une tente et la moille en aigue rose, et poudre sus vitriole broiet;	Do this until no day until the wound is healed, or you take a tent and moisten it in red wine, and powder on crushed vitriol;
et se tu vois enflee l’oreille, si couvient que tu traies la tente et remue une autre tente moillie en cerote qui soit fait d’oile roset et de cire, tant que li enfleure soit ostee;	and if you see the ear swollen, it is necessary that you draw the tent and move another tent moistened in a cerate which is made of rose oil and wax, until the swelling is removed. 
puis le cure tant qu’il soit sanez.	then cure it until it is healed.  
Et se decorremens de sanc vient, si plonge une esponge et drapelz en aigue froide, et le met sus l’oreille, et use d’autres cures qui oste lou decorrement de sanc qui sont ou traitier des destillations.	And if bleeding occurs, then dip a sponge and cloth in cold water, and put it on the ear, and use other treatments that stop bleeding which are or treated with distillations.
de la char des papieres	of the skin of paper
Cist althelul que vienent em papieres des eulz quant ils sont moiste et sont sec, si covient que tu les estendes de tenailles et de pinceures, et le cope d’un spatumile de ses racines;	This ailment that comes in papers of the eyes when they are moist and dry, if it is necessary that you extend them with tweezers and pincers, and the scope of a spatula from its roots; 
puis met sor le leu vitriole broiet.	then put on the place powdered vitriol.  
Et se sans en decort, si le cauterize dou cautere lenticulaire subtil, et li cauterizeir aprés l’incision vaut mues;	And if without it does not decorticate, then cauterize it with the subtle lentil cautery, and the cauterizer after the incision worths moves.   
et maintes fois repairent, cant aucune chose demoure de lor racines;	and many times repaire, since no thing remains of their roots; 
et quant elles sont cauterizees par feu, si sont arses celles racines et ne revienent mie.	and when they are cauterized by fire, then those roots are burned and do not return at all.  
de la gresle	of the ankle
Maintes fois vienent em papieres des eulz unes choses que semblent gresle en sa forme et en sa duresce, et por ceu est ceste maladie apelee «grandine», et est une assemblee de moistor grosse en la papiere desus et desoz;	Many times come in papers the eyes some things that seem broken in their form and in their hardness, and for this reason this illness is called "hailstorm," and it is an assembly of moisture large in the paper above and below. 
li ovraiges est telz:	The works are such: 
pren warde se li grandine se muet d’une part et d’autre, et c’est legiere chose a savoir;	Take ward if the hailstone moves on one side and another, and it is a light thing to know; 
fent la donques dou large, puis l’escorche de chescune partie legierement, puis la prent as pinceures, et la cope.	Make then the opening wide, then the peel from each side lightly, then take it with the pliers, and cut it. 
se tu ne la pues coper sens percier un poc la papiere, si ne grieve rien au malaide;	If you cannot cut it without piercing a bit of the paper, it does not harm the patient;
et se li fendure est grans, si l’assemble a une costure, et la cure tant qu’ele soit sanee;	And if the tear is large, so assemble it with a suture, and cure it until it is healed. 
et s’elle est petite, si n’i faire point de force, car li oignemens la restoure tantost et enjanre char.	And if it is small, do not make force, for the natural healing restores it quickly and prevents scar. 
Et se li grandine est dessendans au dedens de l’oreille vers la partie desus, si enverse la papiere, et estent la grandine a unes pinceures, et la cope et presse d’une part et d’autre;	And if the hailstone is descending into the ear towards the upper part, then turn the paper over, and hold the hailstone with tweezers, and the cup and press from one side and the other. 
et se li papiere est esloignie par l’incision, ce ne grieve rien;	and if the paper is moved by the incision, it does not matter;  
et quant li grandine est copee, si leive l’oil d’aigue salee, et cure le leu de ceu qui enjanre char tant que li malaides soit sanez.	and when the hailstone is cut, let the salty water eye remain, and care for the place of what generates flesh until the patient is healed. 
de la graisse des eulz	of the fat of the eyes
Exinach est une graisse qui est enjanree en toiles des papieres desus, et ce avient plus as enfans c’a nules gens, et grieve mout a lor eulz, et li vienent li catharre as matinees, et ne pueent regardeir la lumiere dou soleil por ceu que les larmes se hastent a lor eulz;	Exinach is a grease that is generated in the papers above the eye, and it happens more to children than adults, and it grieves their eyes much, and they come to have a cold at the mornings, and cannot see the light of the sun because the tears hasten to their eyes;  
et por ceu se couchent il sor lor faices adés, et dorment sus, et sont lor papieres desoz lor sorcilz moistes que li enfleure et li apparance ont covert de l’exinach qui apert en l’oil.	and for this they lie on their faces down, and sleep like that, and are their papers below their eyebrows moist so that the swelling and the appearance have covered with exinach which opens in the eye.  
Et quant tu presses lou leu a tes dois et sent l’exirnach entr’ous.	And when you press the place to your two hands and feel the snapping between them.
Et li maniere de l’ovraige si est que li malaides mette son chief en ton sain;	And the manner of the work is that the patient puts his head on your breast. 
et puis pren I drapeil de lin, et appareille une tente em maniere d’un cercle selonc la quantiteit que conteigne exirnach de chescune partie, puis le met sus li;	and then take the linen cloth, and prepare a tent in the manner of a circle according to the quantity that contains each part, then place it on him.  
et presse a tes dois d’une part et d’autre, si que li exirnach soit assemblez emmi le cercle;	and press with your two hands on one side and the other, so that the parts are assembled within the circle. 
puis fent em mileu de la moistor au spatumile trenchant une fendure dou large, et ne soit mie plus grans que li plaie c’on fait a la sainie de voinne;	then make in the middle of the moisture with a sharp spatula a fissure as wide, and no larger than the wound one makes at the vein.  
et fent le cuir em parfont tant que tu veignes a l’exirnach;	and make the skin apart until you reach the parts. 
et em plusors dispositions vient exirnach de la fendure, selonc la forme d’une piece de graisse blainche.	And in more than one disposition comes the parts from the fissure, according to the form of a piece of white fat.   
Estrai la donques a tout une piece de drap charpit entre tes dois au defuer, et torne ta main a destre et a senestre tant qu’il soit espars;	Extract therefore with a whole piece of cloth between your hands outwards, and turn your hand right and left until it is spread. 
et garde que tu n’ajoster en la fendure, que tu ne viegnes a tout le spatumile jusc’a l’oil, que tu ne le bleces.	And guard that you do not add to the fissure, than you come to all the spatula until the eye, than you it bleach. 
Et se li exirnach n’apert en l’encomencement de la fendure, si acroi un poc la fendure legierement tant qu’il apere;	And if the exinar does not open at the beginning of the fissure, so sharpen the fissure lightly until it opens. 
puis l’estrai si com nos avons dit, puis moille drapelz en aisil et en aigue, et met sus le leu, et estrain de bendelz.	then extract it as we have said, then moisten bandages in ash and water, and put on the place, and strap with bands. 
Et si a de tels homes qui broient seil et mettent sus por corrompre cele moistor qui est demoree.	And if there are such men who grind herbs and put them on to corrupt the moisture which is lingering.
Puis le cure tant qu’il soit sanez.	Then cure until it is healed.
Et s’il vient au leu aposteme chaut, si lou cure d’emplaustres assouajant tant qu’il soit sanez.	And if an abscess comes to the place hot, then its treatment with plasters soothing until it is healed.
des poilz des papieres	of hairs of the papers
Quant em papieres naissent poilz ajostez autre que li naturez, et sont enveillit, si nuisent as eulz, et font venir manieres de maladies si com larmes acostumees et mollifications des papieres et albugine, tant que c’est cause de la destruction des eulz;	When hairs grow in papers  altered other than the natural ones, and are inflamed, then they harm the eyes, and bring forth manners of diseases as habitual tears and softening of the papers and albuginea, as long as this is the cause of the destruction of the eyes; 
et est li cure selonc IIII manieres:	and there is the cure according to IV manners:  
ou par cautere ensamble feu, ou par medicine ague selonc ceu qu’il est devant ou chapistre de cautere, et est fais ou par incision et costure ou par caines, selonc ceu que je dirai.	or by cautery with assembled fire, or by medicine hot according to what is before or chapter of cautery, and it is done or by incision and suture or by caines, according to what I will say. 
Il covient que tu mettes lou chief dou malaide en ton sain, puis torne la papiere de l’oil a ta main senestre;	It is necessary that you put the head of the patient on your healthy side, then turn the paper of the eye to your left hand.  
s’elle est convertie, c’est boin;	If it is converted, it is good; 
se ceu non, si i boute une aguille a tout I fil desus;	if not, then you put a needle to all the thread above;  
et soit ce delez la marge de la papiere ou li poil naissent delez ces poilz, et trai I fil au desus a tout la papiere, et la torne au raseur;	and whether it is near the edge of the paper or where the hairs grow next to these hairs, and you pull the thread upwards to the whole paper, and turn it to the razor;
puis fent en la partie desoz la papiere, desoz les poilz ajostez, a tout le spatumile copant, des le grant larmier jusc’au petit;	then make in the part below the paper, below the hairs adjusted, to all the spatula scraping, from the large tear to the small; 
puis estrai I fil, et met desoz la papiere une petite tente de couton et de drapeil, puis seigne sus la papiere une figure d’enche, si com la fuelle de mirte, et toutevoie il covient que li figure soit selonc la quantiteit que tu vues eslever la papiere qui est devisez a toz.	then extract the thread, and put under the paper a small tent of cotton and cloth, then place on top of the paper a figure of an arch, like the leaf of myrtle, and nevertheless it is necessary that the figure be according to the quantity that you see to raise the paper which is divided to all. 
Et si a teil qui a mestier c’on cope grant quantiteit de la papiere selonc ceu que li papiere est mollifie;	And if it is necessary for someone who needs, cut a large quantity of paper according to how the paper is softened; 
puis fent a tout le spatumile sus les II lignes que tu as signiet, et comence des lou grant larmier jusc’a petit;	then make on all the spatula across the two lines that you have marked, and begin with wide tears up to small ones; 
et soit li une des fendures pres des poilz naturez en la groissece d’un raiz, puis boute l’oncine en l’un des II angles dou keur, puis l’escorche toute;	and let one of the tears be near the natural hairs in the thickness of a root, then put the blade in one of the two angles of the heart, then peel it all; 
puis assemble les II levres a une costure d’une aguille a tout I fil de laine subtil, et essue le sanc, et fai aerdre la superfluiteit des filz sus les II sorcilz a tout aucunes choses gluans, se tu vues faire ce;	then assemble the two lips with a stitch of a needle to all the thread of fine wool, and wipe the blood, and make air holes the surplus of threads on the two eyebrows to nothing sticky, if you want to do this; 
et se ce non, si n’en aies cure, puis laisse la costure et les filz jusc’a III jors ou IIII;	and if not, if you don't care, then leave the stitch and the threads until three days or four; 
puis cure la plaie sens costure de choses sechans et constrignans, car li papiere se relive au soudement de la plaie et l’assemblement de li, mais li costure est muedre (si com dirent li ancien), et c’est ovraiges sens paor;	then cure the wound without stitching with dry and constricting things, because the parchment comes alive to the suturing of the wound and the assembly of it, but the stitches are moved (as they say the ancients), and this work without fear. 
et si a une autre maniere:	and if in another manner:  
et est que tu seignes la papiere d’une figure qui soit ausi com li fuelle de mirte, si com nos avons conteit, a III oncines desevrez selonc la forme qui est ci:	and it is that you sign the parchment with a figure that is like the leaf of myrtle, as we have recounted, at three inches wide according to the shape which is here: 
puis cope ceu qui sormonte as petites forces igalment selonc la forme qui est ci:	then treat those who are sore with little force equally according to the form which is here:
Et se tu n’as pooir de tenir les tenailles, et li chose n’est mie igalz, si prent une aguille ou il ait I fil, et la boute emmi la figure;	And if you cannot hold the pliers, and the thing is not equal, then take a needle or one that has thread, and insert it into the figure. 
et boute I autre fil delez lou grant larmier, et lou secont fil delez lou petit, et assemble entre tes dois les filz igalment;	and insert another thread next to the large tear, and the second thread next to the small one, and assemble between your two threads evenly. 
puis lieve ta main igalment, et lieve tout le cuir sus coi tu as signiet, si com nos avons conteit, puis assemble les II levres de la plaie par costure, et le cure tant qu’il soit sanez;	Then gently lift your hand evenly, and lift all the skin over where you have marked it, as we have recounted, then join together the two edges of the wound with stitching, and cure it until it is healed. 
et se aposteme vient a ton incision, si l’apaise de cerote et de semblans oignement assouajans;	And if an abscess comes to your incision, soothe it with cerate and similar soothing ointments;  
et aucune fois avient que li poil de la papiere sont convertit:	And sometimes it happens that the hair of the paper is converted: 
si covient que tu uses ceu que nos avons dit de l’incision;	then you should use what we have said about incision;
mais li costure en l’une et en l’autre est plus artificialz.	but the stitching in one and the other is more artificial. 
Li cure des caines si est selonc ceste forme:	The cure of bites is according to this form:
et est que tu convertisses la papiere et la fent dedens selonc ceu que j’ai dit, et puis fai II caines par art, et II liiens subtilz ausi lonc com li papiere et li largesce dou spatumile est;	and that you convert the paper and the lint inside according to what I have said, and then make two bites by art, and two subtle threads as long as the paper and the breadth of the spatula are.  
et cope as II chiés de II pars ou tu tiens les filz;	and grip as II shoulder of II parts where you hold the arms 
puis assemble l’un et l’autre subtilment sus ceu que sormonte de la papiere de l’oil, et estrain les II cainnes des II parties forment;	then assemble one and the other subtly upon that which surmounts of the paper of the eye, and hold the II legs of the II parts forming; 
et le laisse ensi aucuns jors, et li cuir qui iert estrainte morra et nercira et porrira, tant qu’il cherra par lui.	and leave it so for some days, and the skin which is strained will die and shrivel and draw together, until it shrinks by itself. 
S’il tarde, si le cope a unes forces, puis le cure tant qu’il soit sanez;	If it delays, if you seize it with some force, then treat it until it is healed;
et quant li plaie iert soudee, et si ert levee li papiere, et ne poindront plus li poil;	and when the wound is sewn, and if it has been lifted the paper, and they will not prick anymore the hairs;
et c’est li forme des II cainnes que tu feras selonc ceste figure, et selonc ceste quantiteit de lonc et de large:	and this is the form of the two bones that you will make according to this figure, and according to this quantity of long and wide.  
li ovraiges est telz que tu preignes une aguille subtil, et i boute I fil de soie souef et subtil;	The works are such that you prick a fine needle, and it puts the silk thread fine and subtle. 
puis assemble les chiés et noe l’un et l’autre subtilment, et soit li longesce des filz une palme de lonc;	then assemble the bones and knot one and the other subtly, and let the length of the threads be a palm long. 
puis ordene en la chasse I autre fil subtil de soie briément, et noe les chief dou fil;	then order in the chase the other silk thread slightly, and knot the heads of the thread.
puis mette li malaides son chief en ton sain;	then put the patient's head in your hand. 
et soit delez lou soleil si que li ovraiges soit declairiez, car c’est uns ovraiges subtilz et menus, puis boute l’aguille a tout la chasse en la racine dou poil ajosteit, et la fai percier en la papiere hastanment tant que tu la traies desus lou poil natureil;	and be facing the sun so that the works are clear, for it is a subtle and fine work, then put the needle at all the chase in the root of the hair placed, and make it pierce into the paper carefully until you draw it above the natural hair.
puis estrai le poil jusque sus la chasse, et boute en la chasse celui poil, s’il en i a I ou II ou III ou plusors;	Then pull the hair up to the root, and put that hair into the wound if there is one or two or three or more; 
puis estrai ta main tant que li poilz veigne fuers a tout la chasse en la papiere avec lou poil natureil.	Then pull out your hand as long as the hairs come out of the entire wound in the paper with the natural hair.  
Et se li chasse est traite et li poilz ne vient fuer avec li, si trairas la chasse au desoz a tout le fil que tu i as ordeneit, tant que li chasse veigne fuer dou pertus desus et que tu la voies par la vision de l’oil;	And if the wound is treated and the hairs do not come out with it, then you will pull out the wound down to all the thread that you have ordered, until the wound comes out through the opening above and that you see it by the sight of the eye;
adonques si trairas la chasse et le fil, et clo l’oil et lou laisse clo II jors ou III, tant que li poil s’aerde en son leu et naisse li char sus;	Then you will pull out the wound and the thread, and close the eye and leave it closed for two or three days, until the hair hardens in its place and flesh grows above; 
et se li poilz est petis, si acompaigne I poil lonc des chevoulz naturez, et soit alevez avec celui ou tu le laisse, tant qu’il soit eslongiez et puis le lieve.	And if the hairs are small, you accompany one long hair of the natural ones, and whether it is raised with that one or you leave it, as long as it is elongated and then lift it.
de la porriture de l’oil	of the rot of the eye
Quant ceste maladie qui est apelee «aleacrati» ou li porriture vient en l’oil, si en i a de II manieres:	When this sickness which is called "aleacrati" or the rotting comes into the eye, there are two ways of it. 
l’une natureil, et l’autre innatureil.	one natural, and the other unnatural.  
Et avient par soudement de plaie, ou de tailleure ou de cautere, et par semblans choses.	And it happens by a sudden blow from a wound or incision or cautery, and by similar things.
Et li maniere de l’ovraige en li est que tu fendes celle soudure, et dessevre les levres de li, et met dedens tentes de lin, et la lie tant qu’elle soit sanee;	And the manner of the work in it is that you cut open that sore, and separate the lips of it, and put inside it lint, and bind it until it is healed. 
et ne covient mie que tu uses en la cure de li de choses que sechent et restraignent.	And it is not fitting that you use in its cure things that dry and constrict.  
Car se tu fais ceu, si revient li maladie pire que li premiere;	Because if you do those things, the sickness comes back worse than the first. 
mais i oevre de choses amollissans, si com fenugreic;	but use softening things, such as fennel.  
et l’arose d’aigue ou altee et semence de lin soient cuites, et oignemens dyaquilon fondut en aucun des oiles, et i envoloupe une tente, et le cure de ceu.	and the root of water or aloe and linseed are cooked, and the oil of diaquillone melted in any oil, and it envelops a lint, and cures it with those things.  
Et li tresors de ta cure si est que tu te dones en garde qu’ele ne soude mie selonc la forme qu’elle fut devant;	And the treasures of your cure is that you take care that it does not join together according to the form that it was before. 
et cist ovraiges que nos avons dit nen est fuers que adresemens de ceste maladie, qu’elle ne reviegne selonc la forme qu’elle fut devant.	And this work that we have said is nothing but the treatments of this malady, that it does not return according to the form that it was before. 
de la char qui vient en l’oil	of the shard which comes in the eye
Ceste maladie que est desoz qui vraiement est apelee «axacrati», et est naturelz et accidens.	This illness which is dislocation is truly called "axacrati", and is both natural and accidental.
Li accidens vient de plaie et de fendure et de cautere et de choses semblans;	The accidents come from wounds and cuts and cauteries and similar things; 
et li voie de l’ovraige en li si est que tu preignes un aguille, en coi il ait I fil double, et la fiche en la char, et li fai percier des le senestre larmier tant c’a destre, si que li filz veigne en II chiés de la char;	and the way of the work in it is that you prick a needle, in which it has double thread, and you put it into the skin, and make it pierce from the left eye to the right, so that the threads come in two shoulders of the skin; 
puis estent la char au desus a tout l’aguille, et la cope a I spatumile large.	then hold the skin above the whole needle, and the end at the spatula wide.  
Et se li figure de la papiere revient selonc ceu qu’il covient, c’est boin;	And if the figure of the paper returns according to what is required, it is good;
se ceu non, si pren I raseur et le met en la fendure, et torne la papiere, et fent II fendures ou costeit dedens la papiere;	If this is not so, then take a razor and put it in the split, and turn the paper, and make two splits where the cost is inside the paper. 
et soient li chiés des II fendures des II angles de l’incision que tu as copeit, et soit fais uns angles si que quant elles sont assemblees, que li figure soit ausi com li figure d’une lettre qui a non «I griesche»;	And let the heads of the two slits be at the two angles of the incision that you have made, and make them so angled that when they are assembled, the figure is like the figure of a letter which has no "italic" ;
puis oste celle char, selonc la quantiteit que ses costez est agus desoz, de ceu qui enseut la papiere, puis ajoste les II parties desevrees, et les cout d’un fil de lainne;	Then remove that cartilage, according to the quantity that its costs are below, from those which follow the paper, then join the two detached parts, and sew them with a thread of wool;
puis lou cure de ceu que nos avons dit des medicines mollifians, et de tentes, tant qu’il soit sanez.	Then care for it as we have said of softening medicines and bandages, until it is healed. 
Et se li maladie vient de fendure ou de costure ou de cautere, si covient que tu fendes une fendure plainne desoz les poilz des papieres, et selonc ceu qui est ci devant;	And if the illness comes from a split or suture or cautery, then it is necessary that you make a flat split below the hairs of the papers, and according to what has been said before;
puis desevre entre les II leivres d’une tente, si com j’ai dit;	Then carefully between the two leaves of a tent, as I have said. 
et doit on faire l’ovraige selonc la forme de la maladie, car elle est mout diverse en forme, et li saiges maistres appareille engien de tout som pooir coment il faice revenir la figure a sa forme natureil;	And one must make the work according to the form of the illness, because it is very diverse in form, and the wise masters prepare everything of all their power how they make return the figure to its natural form; 
et li malaides meisme, selonc ceu qu’il i covient d’ovraige et d’estrumens em plusors dispositions.	And the patient himself, according to what it is necessary of work and instruments in many dispositions. 
dou soudement de la papiere	of the pressing of the paper
Quant ceste soudure avient a mains homes en teil maniere que li papiere desus est sodee avec le blanc de l’oil, et ne puet movoir ne faire ses ovraiges naturez, si covient donques que tu i boutes la pointe d’un raseur desoz la papiere, et la lieve en haut;	When this soldering happens to a man's hands in such a manner that the paper above is soldered with the white of the eye, and cannot move nor do its natural works, then it is necessary that you put the point of a razor underneath the paper, and lift it upwards; 
et l’estent as pinceures, tant que tu copes ceu qui est aert au spatumile subtil, qui ne soit mie trop agus ne trop trenchans, si que li malaides ne puisse soffrir que li spatumile trop agus ne blecent l’oil;	And the extent as pinches, until you cut what is attached to the spatula subtle, which should not be too blunt nor too sharp, so that the patient cannot suffer that the spatula be too blunt nor pierce the eye; 
et soit ton incision, dont tu escorche celle assemblee, legierement, si que li papiere reviegne selonc sa forme natureil;	And let your incision, where you have peeled together the assembly, be light, so that the paper returns to its natural form; 
et est sanee toute celle assemblee, et font aucune fois en l’oil aigue salee, et le leve d’aigue douce, et de coliere;	And let the entire assembly be healed, and never use saltwater in the eye, but clear water, and of barley-water.
puis met entre la papiere et l’oil une tente de lin, et met sus l’oil laine moillie en abun d’uef;	Then place between the paper and the eye a tent of linen, and put on top of the eye wool moistened in an egg white; 
et aprés le tier jor use dou coliere et des choses soudans tant qu’il soit sanez.	And after the third day use barley-water and similar things until it is healed.  
de l’ungle de l’oil	of the angle of the eye
Saiches que li ungle est selonc II manieres:	Know that the nail is according to two manners:
elle est nervouse et semblans a I dur syfac, et une autre qui n’est mie nervouse, mais est semblans a blainche moistor congelee, que quant on la touche de fer et on la cuide panre as pinceures, si ne puet om;	One is nervous and similar to hard styrax, and another which is not at all nervous, but is similar to white moisture frozen, that when one touches it with iron and cauterizes it in pincers, one cannot. 
et l’une et l’autre semblance encomence devers le grant larmier, et croist poc et poc tant qu’ele cuevre toute la veue et toute la lumiere et le movement de l’oil.	and both of those appearances begin toward the great tear, and cross point by point until it covers all the sight and all the light and the movement of the eye. 
Et li maniere de l’incision si est que li malaides mette son chief en ton sain, puis li oevre les eulz;	And the manner of the incision is that the patient puts his head in your hand, then he opens his eyes;  
et lieve la papiere a ta main, puis coil l’ungle as pinceures de petite doubleure, et l’estent au desus;	and lifts the paper with your hand, then while you hold it with the pincers of small folds and pull it upwards;   
puis pren une aguille, et i met I poil de cheval, ou de vaiche, ou de buef, et I fil fort;	then take a needle, and put on its thread the hair of horse, or of calf, or of ox, and a strong thread; 
et double la pointe de l’aguille un poc et la fiche emmi l’ungle, et la perce a tout l’aguille, et lie l’ungle d’un fil et l’estent au desus, et escorche a tout lou poil le costeit de l’ungle qui enseut la prunele et la soie au poil jusc’au chief, puis cope lou remanant en la racine dou larmier a tout lou spatumile subtil et as petites forces, et laisse la char natureil ou larmier, si que par l’incision ne veigne li cors des larmes acostumeement;	and double the point of the needle a bit and put it in the fold, and pierce it with the whole needle, and tie the fold with a thread and pull it upwards, and scrape all the hair along the edge of the fold that follows the wrinkle and the silk to the hair until the head, then cut the remaining part at the root of the tear towards the entire spatula with small forces, and leave the natural flesh or tear, so that by the incision does not come the body of tears as usual; 
et aucune fois s’estent li ungle a l’oncine soulement, et au fil, si com nos avons dit;	and sometimes the finger is stuck to the bone alone, and on the string, as we have said. 
puis l’escorche on a tout le spatumile souef de coi ci est li forme:	then the scraping has the whole spatula shape of which this is the form: 
Et garde que li spatumile ne touche la toile charnue et la rompe, et que li prunele ne soit percie;	And guard that the spatula does not touch the fleshy cloth and break it, and that the needle is not pierced.  
et aprés l’incision giete en l’oil un poc de seil broiet, et dou coliere fait de litargire, et le laisse jusc’a l’autre jor;	and after the incision put in the eye a bit of ground silk, and of the collar made of litharge, and leave it until the next day.  
puis le cure de ceu qu’il i covient tant qu’il soit sanez.	then cure of those that are necessary until it is healed. 
Et se li ungle n’est mie nervouse, et tu ne pues bouter l’aguille, et li uncines n’i puet entrer, maintes fois est curee ceste semblance d’ungle de medicines;	And if the fingernail is not nervous, and you cannot put the needle, and the pincers cannot enter, many times this kind of fingernail is cured with medicines.
et naissent sicom j’ai conteit en la division, et se tu la vues coper, si oevre l’oil dou malaide, et pren le spatumile legier poc agut selonc ceste forme:	and they grow as I have recounted in the division, and if you see it covered, then work the eye of the patient, and take the spatula lightly pointed according to this form:
Et reis l’ungle desus subtilment, et se tu vois qu’elle amenuise point et li rasion i apresse, si distille de ta bouche en l’oil coliere fait de litargire et dou coliere rouge et seil broiet, et estoupe l’oil jusc’a l’autre jor;	And lift the eye gently, and if you see that it does not diminish and its root is urgent, so distill from your mouth into the colic eye made of litargire and the red colic and seal broited, and stop the eye until the other day. 
puis rencomence l’autre ovraige selonc ceste meisme oevre, tant qu’elle soit toute ostee.	then begin the other work according to this same work, until it is entirely removed.  
Se aucune chose ne t’est contraire en l’oil, si com aposteme chaus, adonques la lait, et cure premier l’aposteme chaut tant qu’il soit sanez, puis rencomence l’ovraige si com devant, tant qu’il soit sanez.	If nothing is contrary to you in the eye, such as a boil, then treat the boil first and cure it well until it is healed, then begin the work again as before, until it is healed.
Et se li apparance de la chair dou larmier nuit en l’oil par grant nuisement, si la sospent a l’oncine, et en cope une partie et non mie tot, que cors de larmes n’i viegne;	And if the appearance of the flesh of the tear harms the eye by great nuisance, so suspend it to the oncine, and cut off a part and not half all, that body of tears does not come. 
puis distille en l’oil coliere rouge qui est fais de litargire.	then distill into the colic eye red which is made of litargire.  
de la char qui naist sus la prunelle	of the flesh which rises upon the pupil
Es eulz d’aucuns homes naist aucune fois char rouge, et cuevre la prunele et restraint sus les papieres et les torne au defuer, et semble une rose de balauste;	The eyes of some men are born no times red, and cover the prunella and restrain upon the papers and turn them to the fire, and seem a rose of baluster. 
et li ovraiges si est que li malaides mette son chief en ton sain, puis li oevre les eulz, et coil toute celle char as uncines convenaubles a ceu, et la sostien a la force;	and the work of this is that the patient puts their head in your healthy hand, then opens the eyes and coils all that flesh with appropriate incisions to it, and sustains with strength. 
puis cope la premiere char, et vai tout copant au raseur jusc’a la fin, et te garde que tu ne bleces l’oil a l’ovraige;	then cut the first flesh, and go on cutting to the razor until the end, and be careful that you do not wound the eye during the work; 
et soit li incision dou spatumile que nos avons dit en l’incision de l’ungle et as petites forces de coi on oste lou sebel, si com li forme aprés cest chapistre lou demostre;	and let the incision be of the spatula that we have said in the incision of the angle and to the small forces by which one removes the seb, as the form after this chapter demonstrates;
et quant li incision est acomplie et ostee toute li char, si emple l’oil de seil broiet ou tu i distille coliere rouge et semblans medicines corrosives, et met sus l’oil defuer coton avec abin d’uef, si qu’il soit asseurez d’aposteme chaut;	and when the incision is complete and all the flesh has been removed, then use the oil of wool ground or distill with red mercury and similar corrosive medicines, and place on top of the eye cotton with a bit of yolk, so that it be assured of hot pus; 
et s’il i demore rien, et li sans chaus te sormonte, et tu doutes aposteme chaut, si laisse l’oil et cure l’aposteme de choses apaisant aposteme chaut;	and if it remains there, and the skin of the wound swells, and you doubt an abscess hot, leave the eye and treat the abscess with soothing things for a hot abscess. 
puis revien a ton ovraige tant qu’il soit sanez, et ensi fai cant chars est ajostee en l’oil par ceste semblance.	then return to your work as long as it is sound, and thus do when the char is attached in the eye by this appearance. 
Mais toutevoie il covient que tu aliges la cure de chescun oil foible de la voie natureil;	But nonetheless it is necessary that you align the treatment of each weak eye of the natural path;
et de la voie accident, en ovraige de fer;	and of the accidental path, in the work of iron. 
et ne bouter mie ta main en aucun de ces ovraiges tant que tu voies que cist membres soit soffrans celui ovraige.	and do not put your hand into any of these works until you see that this member is suffering from the work.  
des voines des eulz	of the veins of the eyes
Sebel sont voinnes rouges que sont covertes sus l’oil, et tolent a la veue son ovraige et afoiblissent l’oil toz jors.	Bloody veins are visible that are covered over the eye, and they take away from its work and weaken the eye all days.
Mestier est donques au premier que tu regardes se li oil, en coi sebel est, est fors, et n’i a autre maladie fuers que lou sebel;	It is therefore necessary first that you look at the eye, in what it is, and where it is, and there is no other sickness except for the uvula.
adonques le coil en teil maniere:	then the coil in this manner: 
comande au malaide qu’il mette son chief en ton sain, puis sospent celles voines a tout l’oncine selonc sa sapience, et soit li oncines subtilz double selonc ceste forme:	instruct the patient to place his head on your hand, then suspend those veins at the entire body according to his knowledge, and let the incisions be subtle double according to this form 
Et soient dui oncine par degrez en I cors selonc ceste forme:	And they shall be two ounces by degrees in the body according to this form:
puis c’on coil as forces celles voinnes subtilment, et essue lou sanc houre aprés autre, tant que tu voies removoir celles voines fuers de l’oil;	then one coils those veins subtly, and wipes the blood hour after another, until you see removing those veins away from the eye 
et garde que tu ne blecier l’oil as pointes des spatumiles, et fai cest ovraige a houre de midi devant lou soleil, et soies mout fervans en ton ovraige si que tu ne copes fuer que celles voinnes;	and guard that you do not pierce the eye at the points of the spatulas, and make this work at the hour of midday in front of the sun, and be very fervent in your work so that you do not cut further than those veins 
et quant tu avras ce fait, si distille en l’oil coliere vert et rouge por corrumpre ceu qui est demorez dou sebel.	and when you will have done this, if distill in the eye colic green and red to corrupt those who are remaining from the blood 
Et se tu n’as pooir de coillir tout ceu en celle houre, si fai emplastre sus l’oil de choses apaisans la dolor des eulz, et le laisse aucuns jors tant que li dolors soit apaisie et soit asseurez d’aposteme chaut, puis rencomence selonc ceste maniere qui est devant tant qu’il soit sanez;	And if you cannot collect all of it in that hour, then make a plaster on the eye of things soothing the pain of the eyes, and leave it for some days until the pain is appeased and the abscess is assured hot, then begin again according to this manner which is before as long as it is healed;
et c’est li forme des forces:	and this is the form of the forces: 
de la fistule de l’oil	of the fistula of the eye
Li mire si nomment «arissati» fistule:	The wound that is named “arissati” fistula:  
quant tu la cures per cautere et par medicine ague ardant selonc ceu que j’ai devant dit, et elle n’est mie sanee, si est engien en li que tu fendes sus l’aposteme, lai ou il doit meurer, et trai toute la moistor que i est, tant que li os soit descovers.	when you treat it with cautery and with burning hot medicine according to what I have said before, and if it is not healed, then there is something in it that you should cut into the abscess where it must die, and remove all the moisture that is there, until the bone is uncovered.  
Et quant li os iert descovers, et tu verras la corruption et la noiror, si la reis a tout l’estrument de coi ci est li forme;	And when the bone is uncovered, and you see the corruption and the blackness, then there is all the instrument of what this form is: 
et est apelez «aspre chief», et soit fait de feir inde a I chief reont, et soit pointoiez si com une lime si com il est en la presente forme:	and it is called "aspre chief," and it is made of iron into the shape of a hook, and it is pointed like a file as it is in this present form:
Et met sus lou leu de l’os corrumput, puis le torne entre tes dois, et presse ta main un poc tant que tu saiches que celle corruption est rese;	And place it on the place of the corrupt bone, then turn it between your two hands, and press your hand a little until you know that that corruption is removed; 
et fai ceu aucune fois, puis restoure lou leu de medicines exiccatives.	and do this several times, then return to their place with drying medicines. 
se li leus est soudez, et char i naist, et li cors de la bowe est soudez, et remaint ensi XL jors, et il ne renovele et n’est mie apostemez, et accidens mavais n’i vient, saiches qu’il est sanez;	If the bones are joined, and flesh grows, and the body of the bow is joined, and remains so for 40 days, and it does not renew or become infected again, and a bad accident does not happen, know that it is healed. 
se ceu non, si n’i a autre engien que de ramener la fistule au pertus dou neif selonc ceste forme:	If this is not the case, if there is no other way than to bring the fistula back to the entrance according to this form: 
et est que tu descuevre de l’os la seconde fois par fer, et par medicines agues, et quant il iert descovers si prent I foret selonc ceste forme, et soit li chiés de fer a III angles, et li fust soit atenuis jusc’a chief si com tu vois ci:	And it is that you uncover the bone for the second time with iron and sharp medicines, and when it is uncovered take the forest according to this form, and let the head of the iron be at 3 angles, and the fist be thinned out to the top as you see here:  
puis le met sus l’os delez lou larmier, et esloigne ta main de l’oil I poc, puis torne a tot le foret tant qu’il perce l’os et le sent li malaides par ceu que li vens en ist s’il tient sa main sus son neif;	Then put it on the bone below the tear duct, and move your hand away from the eye a little, then turn the entire forest until it pierces the bone and the patient feels it through this as if he holds his hand on his nose.  
et pues restoure lou leu de medicines seches, si com je t’ai ensigniet, et quant li char naist et endurcist li leus, si vait li matiere au neif;	And after you restore its place with dry medicines, as I have taught you, and when the flesh has risen and hardened the joints, then it goes to the nerve;  
si est plus legiere chose au malaide.	it is a lighter thing for the patient. 
de l’issue de l’oil	Of the issue of the eye
Quant li eulz apert fuer dou tout en tout, et il ne vient point de destorbier au nef, ne amenuisement, si covient que tu lies lou malaide;	When the eyes are open from all of it and they do not come to disturb the nerve or lessen, then you must tie up the patient; 
puis le saine, puis li met ventouses ou haterel sens ferir por succier, puis met sus l’oil I liien fait d’acaice et de aloe et d’encens et de sarcocolle, et puis estrain l’oil, et l’emplaustre sus de bendes et de drapelz;	then heal it, then place the patient on leeches or a heater without injuring him to suck out blood, then put on the eye ointment made of acacia and aloe and incense and sarcocolla, and then strain the eye, and bandage it with bandages and cloths;
et li maniere des drapelz si est que tu preignes drapelz assez molz, et double chescun en IIII, et puis met l’un sus l’autre selonc la quantiteit que li eulz en ait mestier;	and the manner of the bandages is that you take soft bandages and double each one into four, and then put one on top of the other according to the quantity that the eye needs; 
puis l’estrain par desus d’un bendeil dur forment, et rencomence les ventouses por succier sens ferir;	Then restrain it from above with a hard band, and reapply the suction cups to draw without injuring.  
puis oste les ventouses et laisse l’oil estraint jor et nuit, et se li liiens amolist, si covient que tu l’estraignes mout;	Then remove the suction cups and leave the eye restrained day and night, and if the ligaments soften, it is necessary that you restrain it much. 
puis oste lou liien aprés le jor et la nut, et se tu vois l’oil repairier, c’est boin;	Then remove the bandage after a day and night, and if you see the eye repairing, it is good;
se ce non;	If not; 
si rencomence l’emplaustre et les drapelz et lou liien et les ventouses tant qu’il soit sanez.	If he starts the  bandaging and dressings and linen and suction cups as long as it is healed. 
dou derrompement de toile uvee	of the derangement of web woven
Quant disruptions vient en la toile uvee, puis apert, et vient fuer des papieres si com I grain de resins, et est espoantauble a veoir;	When disruption comes in the woven cloth, then open, and comes out like papers as if grain of resin, and is expectable to see. 
adonques se tu la vues coper, li ovraiges est telz que tu boutes une aguille en la racine des la partie desoz jusc’a celi desus, puis boute une autre aguille ou il ait I fil double des la partie dou larmier;	then if you see it covered, the work is such that you thrust a needle into the root of the lower part up to the top, then thrust another needle where there is the double thread of the part of the tear. 
et la fai percier, et laisse la premiere aguille selonc la disposition;	and make it pierce, and leave the first needle according to the arrangement.
puis cope lou leu dou fil double et lie une partie de l’uve entor, et l’estraint bien, puis estrai l’aguille et met sus l’oil lainne moillie en abun d’uef;	then cut the place of the double thread and tie one part of the grape around, and restrain it well, then remove the needle and put on top the eye half-silk in an abundance of egg. 
et le laisse tant que li filz chiece avec l’uve, puis cure l’oil de choses confortans tant que li plaie soit sanee;	and let it be until the threads come off with the grape, then cure the eye with comforting things as long as the wound is healed. 
et aucune fois li plaie est restrainte par l’uve chescune part d’un cercle de drap, tant qu’elle soit sanee.	And at times the wound is restrained by a cloth circle on each side until it is healed. 
Et se li eulz done grant apparance, si le perce au spatumile subtil qui viegne em parfont de l’oil, et corre la moistor albuginé et dessende li eulz, et entre ens tantost;	And if the eyes show great appearance, pierce them with a subtle spatula which comes in from the eye, and correct the whitish moisture and bring down the eyes, and insert it into the meantime. 
puis l’estrai tant qu’il soit sanez.	Then extract it until it is healed.  
de la bowe de l’oil	of the bowl of the eye
Ceste maladie qui est apelee «alcunnati» nen est fuers que bowe qui est assemblee en l’oil, semblant a aigue dessendant, et ce n’est mie aigue;	This disease which is called "alcunnati"  is nothing but a web which is assembled in the eye, seeming like water descending, and it is not water. 
et li maniere de l’apparance de l’ovraige si est que tu faices seoir lou malaide sus I siege appareilliet et droit, puis prent le chief entre tes mains de II pars, et lou muef tant que tu voies la bowe venir au desus a tes eulz;	And the manner of the appearance of the work is that you make the patient sit on a prepared and straight seat, then take the head between your hands in two parts, and move it until you see the web coming up to your eyes.  
puis soit ens fichie, et ne dessende et soit descombree li lumiere, et voie li malaides les choses si com il soloit;	Then it is sewn together, and does not descend, and let the light be removed from it, and the patient sees things as he desired. 
et s’elle ne dessent desoz, saiches que c’est aigue, et se li dessendemens de la bowe n’est appareilliez si com nos avons dit.	And if it does not descend below, know that it is acute, and if the descent of the bowel is not apparent as we have said. 
si fai seoir lou malaide entre tes mains, puis prent le spatumile subtil et fent sus la toile cornee I poc par la continuation de la conjunctive avec la toile cornee et la corone, tant que li bowe isse;	If you make the patient sit between your hands, then take a subtle spatula and feel on the cornea above the point where the conjunctiva continues with the cornea and the crown, as long as the bowel issues. 
et quant elle ert issue, si distille en l’oil aigue chaude mellee a miel, ou aigue ou fenugreic est boillis et miel, puis soit curee d’autre cure tant qu’elle soit sanee.	And when it is out, distill in the hot water mixed with honey, or water where fennel is boiled and honey, then be cured with another cure until it is healed. 
des aigues de l’oil	of the eyes
Nos avons jai les semblances des aigues en la division, et ceu qu’il covient por percier;	We have shown the likenesses of waters in the division, and those that are fitting to consider.  
si en oevre selonc la santeit.	if in work according to health. 
Il covient que tu faices seoir lou malaide entre tes mains croisiet, fuers de la lumiere por le soleil, et li lie l’oil sain et estreint mout fort;	It is fitting that you make the patient sit between your hands crossed, away from the sun's light, and tie the healthy eye and hold it very tightly. 
puis met la papiere de l’oil a ta main senestre se li eulz est senestres, ou a ta main destre se li eulz est destres;	Then put the paper of the eye to your left hand if the eyes are left, or to your right hand if the eyes are right.
puis prent en ta main destre, se li eulz est senestres, l’estrument qui est apelez «almagda», ou a ta main senestre, se li eulz est destre;	Then take in your right hand, if the eyes are left, the instrument that is called "almagda," or in your left hand, if the eyes are right.
puis met la pointe de l’estrument delez la corone par la groissece d’un rait en celle blenchor de l’oil a la partie dou menor larmier, puis boute l’estrument qui est apelez «almagda» vertuousement, et trestorne ta main tant qu’il perce en la blenchor de l’oil, et sente que almagda viegne a la chose vuide;	Then put the point of the instrument near the crown by the width of a finger in that white part of the eye to the side of the less tear duct, then thrust the instrument which is called "almagda" virtuously, and retract your hand until it pierces into the white part of the eye, and feel that almagda comes to the empty thing; 
et covient que li mesure de la voie almagda soit au parfont de la mesure des l’espaice qui est des la prunele jusc’a la fin de la noirour;	And it is necessary that the measure of the way almagda be at the point of the measure of the space which is from the pupil to the end of the black;  
et c’est li corone de l’oil;	and this is the crown of the eye; 
si verras l’os en celle papiere por la clarteit de la toile cornee, et pues met l’estrument jusc’a leu ou li aigue est, puis l’espresse desoz une voie aprés autre.	if you see the bone in that paper for the clarity of the cornea, and then put the instrument until where the water is, then express it below one way after another.  
se li aigue dessent maintenant, si voit li malaides devant lui et l’estrument en son oil.	If the water descends now, the patient sees before him and the instrument in his eye.
Aprés repose I petit, et se li aigue remonte la seconde voie, met la fuer avec l’estrument, et quant elle est ens fichie et ele ne monte, si estrai almagda legierement en tornoiant ta main poc et poc;	After rest the little, and if the water rises the second way, put the force with the instrument, and when it is once fixed and it does not rise, then extract almagda lightly by turning your hand poco a poco.   
et puis remette en aigue un poc de seil gemme, et leive de ceu l’oil dedens.	and then put back in sharp a bit of silk thread, and remove from it the oil inside.  
Puis met par defuer l’oil estoupes ou lainne moillie en oile roset et en abun d’uef, et lie avec l’oil sain.	Then put by way of defense the eye plugged with a cloth or felt moistened in rose oil and honey, and tie it with the healthy eye.
Nos, et cil qui sont de nostre tens, mettons sus comin broiet avec abun d’uef.	We, and those who are of our time, put on top a common broth with abundance of egg.
Et se almagda n’i puet entrer en l’oil par sa duresce, car il i a de teilz homes qui ont trop durs les eulz, si covient que tu preignes l’estrument qui est apelez «alberit», de coi ci est li forme:	And if the almagda cannot enter into the eye because of its hardness, for there are some men who have very hard eyes, so it is necessary that you prick the instrument which is called "alberit", for this is its form:
Et perce donques la conjunctive soulement, et n’aler mie trop em parfont, mais fai I leu subtil, puis i boute almagda, si com nos avons dit;	And pierce then only the conjunctiva, and do not go too deep into it, but make it subtle, then put in almond, as we have said.   
et au complissement de l’uevre appareille au malaide I dorteur avenant, en coi il dorme sus son dos en I leu tenebrous;	And at the completion of the work, equip the patient with the sleeping mat beforehand, in which he sleeps on his back in a dark place.   
et soit deveez de toz movemens, et preigne legieres viandes, et ne mueve son chief ne a destre ne a senestre, et soit liiez selonc sa disposition jusc’a tier jor;	and be free from all movements, and eat light foods, and do not move his head neither to the right nor to the left, and be bound according to his disposition until the third day. 
puis le deslie en cele maison meisme tenebrouse, et esprueve sa veue, et lou fai veoir aucunes choses, et puis li remet lou lien jusc’a septime jor;	Then untie him in that same dark house, and observe his vision, and let him see some things, and then put the bandage back on until the seventh day.
et ne covient mie que tu faices ceu en l’oure de la cure ou aprés l’incision maintenant, mais il covient que tu aliges ceu, por ceu que li aigue monte hastanment.	And it is not right that you do these things in the hour of the cure or after the incision now, but it is necessary that you bandage them because the water rises quickly.  
se apostemes chaus vient, que tu desliies l’oil devant le septime jor, et l’adrece de ceu qui assouaige aposteme;	When an abscess comes, that you unbind the eye before the seventh day, and the address of those who soothe abscesses. 
et quant il est apaisiez, si deslie la veue et met sus sa faice I orilliet por covrir aucun jor, et soit adés en celle maison tenebrouse.	And when it is appeased, then unbind the eye and put on its face a little border to cover for any day, and let it be in that dark house. 
Et puis isse de la maison poc et poc, et se convertisse en ses cas;	And then from the house a little bit here and a little bit there, and let itself turn in its case; 
et saiches que nulz deciples ne se doit entremettre en cest cas.	And know that none of the disciples should interfere in this matter. 
Et uns vint a nos qui estoit de la Yrach, qui nos dist que en som pais faisoit om almagda perciet, a coi on succe l’aigue, mais toutevoie je n’en vis onques nul en nostre terre, ne je ne lou lis onques en livres des anciens;	And one came to us who was from the Yrach, who told us that in his country they made almond cake by which one sucks the water, but nevertheless I have never seen any in our land, nor have I ever read it in books of the ancients; 
et par aventure c’est une novele chose.	and perhaps it is a new thing.   
Et ce sont les semblances des formes de almagda, por ceu que cil qui ne les conoit les voie;	And these are the resemblances of the forms of the almond, for those who do not know them see them. 
et soient d’arain proprement:	and be properly of a kind of wood:  
Et soient li chief d’aus de ceste meisme subtiliteit, et li derriene en III angles ague.	And let the head of each of this same subtlety, and the last in three angles acute.
de la char sor le neis	of the bone on the birth
Aucune fois naissent ou neis chars ajostees diverses, de coi il i a aucunes qui semblent scorpions a mout de piez;	At times they are born or grow askew and diverse, for which reason some seem like scorpions with many legs;  
et si i a de telz ou il ait char enchancree de fuxe color, et si a char souef de bone color.	and if there are such ones where they have bark split of bad color, and if the wood has a good color beneath it. 
En celle donques de ces chars qui est souef, et ne mie enchancree, covient que tu faices seoir lou malaide entre tes mains encontre lou soleil;	In that one, then, of these branches which is sound and not split, it behooves you to make the patient sit between your hands against the sun; 
et oevre ses narines, et giete l’oncine a celles chars, et les trai fuers;	and open his nostrils, and place the herb on those branches, and they will be pulled out. 
pues cope ceu que tu em pues sostenir au spatumile subtil agut d’une part, tant que tu saiches que celle char est toute ostee.	Then take what you are able to hold on the fine sharp point of a knife as long as you know that that branch is completely removed.  
Et s’il en remaint aucune chose c’on ne puisse coper, si l’ovrez a tout I des estrumens subtil legierement, si qu’il n’i demoure rien;	And if any thing remains which one cannot cover, then open it all with the most subtle instruments lightly, so that nothing remains there. 
et se sans te sormonte, ou aposteme chaus, si lou secort si com il covient;	And if without a swelling or abscess chaws, if its short as it should be;  
et se c’est apostemes malignes, si te haste et lou cauterize tant que li sans soit estainchiez et soient ostees toutes les chars, puis giete ou neis aisil et aigue ou vin.	And if it is malignant abscess, then hasten and cauterize it until the pus is exuded and all the char are removed, then pour  water or wine there. 
Se li neis oevre, et moistors en vient jusc’a palais, saiches qu’il est sanez;	If the wound works, and moisture comes up to the palate, know that it is healed; 
et se moistors ne perce si com il covient, saiches qu’il i a char nee en l’os desus, a coi li estrumens ne vient mie por taillier:	And if the moisture does not penetrate as it should, know that there is raw flesh on the bone above, which is why the instruments do not come to cut;
adonques covient il que tu i boutes I fil de lin un poc gros, et soit noez de mains nous, et ait entre chescun nout d’espaice I doit ou moins;	Therefore it is necessary that you put in a thread of linen somewhat thick, and be knotted by hands of ours, and have between each knot the space of an inch or less;
et mette li malaides lou chiés dou fil en son neif a som pooir, et traie en odorant tant qu’il viegne par lou neif dedens la bouche;	and puts the patient's shoulder down into its socket with his hand, and pulls in smelling until it comes through the nostril inside the mouth; 
et maintes fois font ensi li enfant as escoles, et c’est legiere chose a celui qui le vuet faire;	and many times do children so at school, and it is an easy thing to him who wants to do it;  
puis tien le chief qui vient par lou neif a une main, et l’autre chief qui vient par la bouche a l’autre main, et saiche l’un aprés l’autre en soiant as nous qui sont ou fil.	then hold the head that comes through the nostril with one hand, and the other head that comes through the mouth with the other hand, and pull one after the other carefully as we who are or thread. 
Fai ceu tant que tu saiches que li nout ont corrompue celle char, puis trai lou filz, essue le sanc, et moille lou fil en oignement egiptien, et le remet derechief au neis si com devant;	Do this until you know that the nostril has corrupted that flesh, then pull the thread, wipe the blood, and moisten the thread in Egyptian ointment, and put it back straight into the nostril as before;
fai ceu III jors ou plus, tant que li oignemens corrode tout ceu qui est demorez de char;	do this III days or more, until the ointment corrodes all that is remained of flesh;
et puis met ou neis une caine de plonc aucuns jors tant qu’il soit sanez, et s’il a mestier de medicines sechans, si en use;	And then put on his new bandage until it is healed, and if he needs drying medicines, use them. 
et c’est li forme de l’estrument por purgier lou chief, a coi on distille les oiles et les medicines ou neis:	And this is the form of the instrument for purging the head, by which we distill the oils and medicines therein:
