Et soit d’argent ou d’arain, semblant a une lampe overte, si com une cainne, et li conduis ausi;	And let it be of silver or copper, resembling an open lamp, like a bowl, and its conductors also: 
et se tu vues, si fai une cainne close, et soit li estrumens plains por espurgier lou chief;	and if you wish, make a closed bowl, and let the instruments be full for purging the head; 
et ait I mainche au chief por lou tenir quant on chaufe l’oile ou aucune liquor.	and have a handle at the top to hold it when one heats the oil or any liquor.
de la char sor le neis	of the bone on the birth
Maintes fois naist au chief dou neis une maladie qui est apelee «telul», et croist et devient grans adés, tant qu’il est vis chose au regarder;	Many times a disease is born in the head called "telul," and it grows and becomes very large, so that it is a visible thing to look at; 
et por ceu covient que tu lou copes au comencement, et l’oste tout fuer, puis met sor leu lou cautere ou la medicine ardant;	and for this it behooves you to cut it at the beginning, and remove all of it, then put on its place the cautery or the burning medicine; 
et s’on le tarde a coper tant qu’il soit grans, si pren warde s’il est durs, de fuxe color, de povre sens:	and if one delays to cover it until it is large, then take heed if it is hard, of dusky color, of poor sense: 
si ne lou touchier mie de fer car c’est uns apostemes enchancrez, car quant on le cope aucune fois, si en vient grant malice au malaide;	If it isn't touched with iron for it is a festering abscess, because when one covers it at any time, there comes great harm to the patient; 
et se li apostemes est de soef touchement, non mie de fuxe color, et tu vois c’on le puisse tout coper, si vuide le malaide et lou cope sens paor, et cure le leu de choses sechans et restraignans.	and if the abscess is of soft touch, not of dusky color, and you see that one can fully cover it, then empty the patient and cover it without fear, and cure the place with drying and constricting things. 
quant li neis est copez et cosus	When the nose is cut and sewn
Saiches que quant solutions de continuation vient en une de ces cartillagines ovraiges, i profite poc, fuer que en aucuns homes.	Know that when a solution of continuation comes in one of these works cartilages, it profits little, because in some men.
Il covient donques cant ceu avient a aucun, si regarde se li plaie est fresche a tout son sanc;	It is therefore necessary that when this happens to anyone, one sees if the wound is fresh with all its blood;
et adonques ajoste les II levres a une costure, puis le cure tant qu’il soit sanez;	and then adjust the two lips with a suture, and treat it until it is healed;
et se les levres sont ja desevrees d’une part et d’autre, si covient que tu escorches toutes les parties de lor keur tant qu’elles sainent, puis assemble les II levres a une costure, et l’estraint, et poudre sus poudre de sanc de dragon, et encens broiet;	and if the lips are already separated on one side and the other, then you must scrape all parts of their core until they bleed, then assemble the two lips with a suture, and restrain them, and powder upon powder of dragon's blood, and incense ground. 
et met sus les poudres une piece d’emplaustre de fort ou d’autre emplaustre soudant, et le laisse tant qu’il chiece par lui, puis le cure d’oignement tant qu’il soit sanez.	and put on the powders a piece of plaster of strong or other soldering plaster, and leave it until it falls off by itself, then cure it with ointment until it is healed. 
Li maniere de la costure si est que tu assembles la solution:	The manner of the suture is that you assemble the solution:  
ou par aguilles, si com nos avons dit en la costure dou ventre;	or with needles, as we have said in the stitching of the belly;
ou par fil, si com je le t’ai fait savoir.	or by thread, as I have told you.  
des apostemes des levres	of abscesses of the lips
A mains homes avient dedens les levres aposteme dur, semblans a grains de veces, et menor et plus grant;	Sometimes in the lips, men have abscesses hard, like grains of rice, and smaller and larger;
adonques couvient que tu tornes les levres, et fendes sus chescun nout, et le prent as pinceures et le cope en chescune partie;	Therefore it is necessary that you turn the lips, and cut above each nostril, and take them with tweezers and cut them in each part. 
puis emple lou leu aprés l’incision de vitriole broiet, tant que li sans soit estainchiez;	then apply the place after incision of powdered vitriol, until the blood is stained; 
et puis lou leive d’aisil, et cure lou leu de choses seches tant qu’il soit sanez.	and then leave it and cure the wound with dry things until it is healed.  
de la char des gencives	of the flesh of the gums
Maintes fois naist sus les gencives char ajostee, que li ancien apelent «albulus»;	Many times on the gums grows flesh that is attached, which the ancients call "albulus"; 
si covient que tu la sostienes as tenailles, et la cope a sa racine, et laisse corre la bowe ou le sanc;	so it is necessary that you hold it with tweezers and cut it at its root, and leave the bleeding to stop;
puis met sor le leu vitriole broiet, ou autres poudres restraignans et desiccatives;	then put on the wound powdered vitriol, or other astringent and drying powders; 
et se celle char revient aprés l’incision, et maintes fois avient, si la cope la seconde fois, et la cauterize:	and if that flesh returns after the incision, which often happens, cut it a second time and cauterize it;
si ne revient mie aprés le cautere;	If it does not return after the cautery; 
et ce sont les formes des estrumens por coper.	and these are the forms of the instruments for covering.  
des sordens	of deafness
Aucunes fois sont assemblees au chief des dens, dedens la bouche entre les gencives, escorces qui sont laides et aspres;	Sometimes they are assembled at the top of the teeth, inside the mouth between the gums, scabs that are ugly and rough. 
et aucune fois sont li dent noir et citrin et vers, tant que li corruption vient a la gencive, et sont li dent puant;	And sometimes the teeth are black and yellowish and putrid, as long as the corruption comes to the gum, and the teeth are foul-smelling.
si covient que tu faices seoir lou malaide entre tes mains, et ses chiés soit en ton saint, et reis les dens ou les escorces aperent, tant qu’il n’i demore rien;	So it is necessary that you make the patient sit between your hands, and his shoulders be in your arms, and raise the teeth or scabs as they appear, until nothing remains. 
et ensi fai de la noiror et de la verdor, et de la jaunice et des autres taiches, tant qu’elles soient mondees;	And thus do of the blackness and yellowing, and jaundice and other blemishes, as long as they are seen.
et s’on oste ceu que i est a la premiere rasion, c’est boin;	and if one removes those that are at the first reason, it is good; 
se ceu non, si rencomence a rere le secont jor et lou tier, tant que tu aies tout reis;	If it is not so, begin again on the second day and the third, until you have all healed.  
et saiches que li dent ont mestier de diverses formes d’estrumens por reire, selonc ceu que li oevre lou demoustre, por ceu que li raseur dont on reit defuer les dens ont autres formes que cil dont on reit entre les dens;	And know that teeth need various tools for extraction, according to what the work demonstrates, because the rasp with which one removes teeth outside have other forms than those with which one removes between the teeth. 
et cestes formes et autres soient avec toi appareillies.	And these forms and others be equipped with you.  
Il covient quant tu cures lou dent de sa dolor que tu tardes dou traire tant com tu pues, car ce ne doit om mie faire;	It is necessary when treating the tooth for pain that you take a while to draw (it) as much as you can because one must not do otherwise; 
car c’est une substance mout haute jusc’a donc c’on n’ait point d’excusation dou raier.	because it is a very high substance until then, we have no excuse to scrape.   
Adonques quant li malaides est constrains dou traire, si covient que tu soies certains dou dent doillant.	Therefore when the patient is constrained to endure pain, it is necessary that you are certain about the tooth aching.
Maintes fois desoit li dolor lou malaide, et cuide qu’elle soit ou dent saint, et fait traire le boin dent;	Many times the patient needs the pain, and thinks it is the good tooth, and draws (it) out. 
et toutevoie ne se depart mie li dolor per ceu, tant que li malvais estrais, car nos l’avons ja veut faire a ces sainors;	And nevertheless the pain does not depart because of that, as long as the evil is present, because we have already seen it happen to our elders.  
et quant tu es bien certains dou dent doillant, si covient que tu escorches entor lou dent a tout i. spatumile fort por warder la gencive de toutes pars;	and when you are well certain of the tooth aching, it befits that you scrape around the tooth on all sides with a spatula strong to protect the gum from all parts; 
puis le mues a tes dois ou as tenailles subtilz au premier poc et poc, tant qu’il soit bien eslochiés, puis i afferme bien les tenailles;	then bring it to your pliers or very fine forceps at the first notch and notch, until it is well spread apart, then firmly secure the pliers. 
et soit li chiés dou malaide en ton saint entre tes genous, et lou tien bien si qu’il ne se mueve.	and let the patient's shoulder be in your holy between your knees, and hold it well so that it does not move. 
Aprés estrai lou dent droitement sens brisier, et s’il ne saut fuer, si prent aucun de ces estrumens et le boute dedens de chescune part legierement, et lou remuef si com tu as fait premier.	After you have pulled the tooth straight without breaking it, and if it does not come out, take one of these instruments and push it gently inside from each side, and move it as you did at first.
Et se li dens est perciez et mengiez, si covient que tu l’emplisses de drapelz, lai ou li pertus sont;	And if the bone is pierced and broken, then you must fill it with bandages where the perforations are; 
et si l’estraint subtilment as tenailles, que il ne brise a l’estraindre;	and gently restrain it with pliers so that it does not break when restraining.
et covient mout saigement ovrer entor la gencive por deschaucier lou dent.	and it is necessary to work very skillfully around the gum to loosen the tooth. 
Et te done bien en warde que tu ne le brises, et en remaigne une partie, et reveigne au malaide par la malice de la racine plus grans dolors de la premiere.	And therefore take good care that you do not break it, and remain a part of it, and return to the patient through the wickedness of the root greater pains than the first.
Et te warde que tu ne faices mie ensi com font li ignorant sainor, qui par lor haste et par lor hardiesce brisent aucune fois le charreit, et n’i amenistrent mie ceu que nos avons conteit;	And beware that you do not act as the ignorant healers do, who by their haste and boldness sometimes break the jawbone and bring no one to what we have recounted. 
mais font venir aucune fois par l’oquison de ceu grant maladie por les racines que i demorent, ou por lou charreit qu’il brisent, si com nos avons sovent veut;	but bring forth at times by the opening of these great illnesses due to the roots that remain, or because of the jawbone they break, as we have often seen.
et quant li dens est trais, si lavez lou leu de vin ou d’aisil et de seil;	and when the tooth is pulled, wash its place with wine or oil and salt; 
et se decorremens de sanc i vient, que sovent avient, si emple lou leu de vitriole broiet;	and if bleeding occurs, which often happens, apply ground vitriol to the place; 
et se ceu ne vaut, si le cauterize.	and if that does not help, cauterize it.  
Les formes des estrumens, a coi om muet les dens premier, soient a longes pointes et a gros mainches, qu’il ne doublent mie quant tu trairas le dent;	The shapes of the instruments, to which one pulls teeth first, should be with long points and thick handles, so that they do not double when you pull the tooth;
et ce sont les formes:	and these are the shapes: 
Et soient de gros membres si qu’il ne ploient mie au traire, et soient de fer inde bien fait, et soient dentez por mues tenir.	And let them be thick members so that they do not bend when pulled, and let them be of well-made iron, and let them be toothed to hold the parts.
de la racine des dens	of the root of the teeth
Quant li racine demoure au traire, si covient que tu mettes sor le leu coton moilliet em burre I jor ou II, tant que li leus soit amolis, pues i boute les tenailles qui sont apelees «algefri», de coi li chiés semblet bec de soigne;	When the root remains after pulling, it is necessary that you put on the place moistened cotton in butter every day or two, as long as the area softens, then use the pliers called "algefri," because the jaw resembles a beak of attention; 
et soient dedens faites ausi com une lime et c’est li forme:	and be made inside like a file, and that is the shape:
Et se les racines ne vuellent issir a tout ces tenailles, si covient que tu descuevre la char tot entor la racine, et i met l’estrument qui est apelez «althali», c’est a savoir palainche, de coi ci est li forme:	And if the roots do not want to issue with all these pincers, then it is necessary that you uncover the flesh around the root, and put there the instrument which is called "althali", that is to say, a spatula, because of this is its form.
Et soit fors et gros si qu’il ne brise mie, et se li racine saut par ceu, c’est boin;	And be strong and thick so that it does not break, and if its root jumps out of those, it is good. 
se ceu non, si t’aide de toz les estrumens, de coi les formes vienent ci aprés:	If these are not there, with the help of all your instruments, as their forms come after here: 
Et si s’aide on de cest estrument qui ait II rains, de coi ci est li forme:	And if one helps oneself with this instrument which has II reins, of this is the form:
et d’autres ferremens qui sont devant en la rasion des dens, et de cest estrument qui semble unes grans tenailles, dont ci est li forme:	and other instruments which are in front in the order of teeth, and of this instrument which resembles great pliers, whose form is here:
Et soit cist estrumens fors qu’il ne puisse brisier, et saiches que mout d’estrumens de dens sont;	And let this instrument be strong so that it cannot break, and know that many instruments of teeth are;
et ausi d’autres estrumens, qui ne sont mie contez;	and also other instruments, which are not counted. 
et li saiges maistres subtilz trueve par soi meisme son estrument, selonc ceu que ses ovraiges et li maladie li demoustre, car il i a de teilz maladies ou li ancien n’enseignerent point d’estrument por la diversiteit d’au;s et s’om brise point dou charreit ou des autres os, ou il porrit, si i cerche as estrumens qu’il i covient, que je t’ai dit, et t’aide des gestes, de coi ci est li forme:	and the wise masters subtle find by themselves their instrument according to what their works and the illness demonstrate to them, for there are such illnesses where the old ones do not teach any instrument because of the diversity of others, and if one does not break the bone or other bones, or where it may occur, then he searches for the instruments that he needs, which I have told you, and help with the gestures, as what is here is the form. 
Et soient gros et bien tenant por tenir l’os, qu’il n’eschaipe, mais le puisse tenir et oster;	And let them be large and well-fitting to hold the bone so that it does not escape, but can hold and remove it. 
et puis restoure lou leu de medicines convenant a ceu, et s’il ait en l’os porriture, et elle est petite, si la reis a tout cest estrument:	And then restore the place with suitable medicines for them, and if there is in the bone rot, and it is small, then the king has all these instruments: 
Quant li dent apperent ne mie selonc lou cors natureil, et li forme est laide, et meismement en femmes puceles, si covient que tu saiches se li dens est neis aprés lou dent, et n’est mie en droit leu, et on ne lou puet soier ne limer:	When the tooth appears not according to the natural body, and the form is ugly, and even in virgin women, then you should know if the tooth is born after the tooth, and is not in its right place, and it cannot be filed or trimmed: 
adonques lou raie;	then the edge;  
et s’il est aers avec lou dent, si prent cest estrument dont ci est li forme, et est semblans a I petit bec, et soit de fer inde agut en som:	And if it is near with the tooth, then take this instrument whose shape is here, and resembles a small beak, and be of sharpened iron at its summit: 
Et lou cope poc et poc em mains jors por la duresce dou dent, et por ceu que tu ne mueves les autres, et s’il est apparans c’on le puisse limer, si lou lime d’une teil lime com ci est li forme:	And the cope a little and little with hands for the hardness of the tooth, and because you do not move the others, and if it appears that it can be filed, then file it with a tool like this is its form.
et est ausi com li lime de coi on fait les aguilles;	and is also like the file with which one makes needles;  
et en lime lou dent poc et poc em mains jors legierement, si qu’il ne se mueve tant qu’il chiece;	and with a file smooth the tooth little by little in hands gently, so that it doesn't move until it falls;  
puis la plaine en la fin a tout aucun raseur, et se li dens est trop trenchans et il blece la lengue, si covient limer l’aspreteit tant qu’il soit igalz, si qu’il ne blece la lengue ne ne corrompe la parole.	then smooth it in the end with no scraper, and if the tooth is too sharp and it pricks the tongue, then file the sharpness until it's equal, so that it doesn't prick the tongue nor corrupt speech.  
quant li dent lochent	when the tooth loosens
Quant li dent devant lochent, ou par percussion ou par cheoir, et li malaides ne puet presser sus ceu qu’il menjue qu’il ne chient, et tu les as curez de medicines restrignans, et ceu ne vaut;	When the tooth before loosens, either by percussion or by falling, and the patient cannot press on it so that he doesn't bite, and you have cured them with medicine restraining, and these don't work; 
si les covient restraindre d’un fil d’or, car li filz d’argent devient vert et porrit, mais li ors ne se mue onques;	then it is necessary to restrain it with a gold thread, because the silver threads become green and corrupt, but gold never changes. 
et soit li filz moiens ne trop gros ne trop menus, selonc la quantiteit de l’espaice entre les dens;	and let the thread be moderate neither too thick nor too thin, according to the quantity of space between the teeth;
et se tu vues adrecier les dens, si pren lou fil et lou boute double entre les II dens sains, puis met les chiés entre les dens meus, s’il en i a I ou plusors, tant que tu veignes saigement jusc’au dent sain d’autre part;	and if you see the teeth being crowded together, take the thread and the double end between the two healthy teeth, then put the head between the teeth yours, if there are one or more, until you come skillfully to the healthy tooth on the other side; 
puis rencomence la coverture jusc’a la partie ou tu encomensas, et estrains ta main subtilment et saigement, tant qu’il ne se mueve point;	then begin again the covering until the part where you started, and strain your hand subtly and skillfully, so that it does not move at all; 
et soit ta lieeure a la racine dou dent si qu’il ne puist eschaper.	and let your ligature be at the root of the tooth so that it cannot escape.  
Puis cope les chiés dou fil a unes tenailles, et les assemble, et les repont entre le dent sain, et le met ensi qu’il ne blece la lengue;	Then cut the head of the thread with pliers, and assemble them, and put them between the healthy tooth, and place it so that it does not touch the tongue;
et puis le laisse ensi estroit tant com il puet demorer, et s’il deslie, ou li filz ront, si l’estraint d’un autre fil;	and then leave it as tight as it can remain, and if it unties, or the threads break, so strain it with another thread; 
si demorrait et servira ensi tout son tens, et c’est li forme des dens et li figure de l’adrecement des II dens sains, et des II meus, si com tu vois:	If it remained and would serve thus all its length, and this is the form of the teeth and the figure of the placement of the II healthy teeth, and the II mine, as you see: 
Et quant li dent chiet, si lou remet on en son leu, de fres en fres, si com nos avons dit;	And when the tooth falls out, if one puts it back in its place, from fresh to fresh, as we have said.  
et ne s’en entremette mie qui n’est saiges et soffrans, et aucune fois fait on la forme d’un dent d’os de vaiche, et lou met on au leu ou li defaute est, et l’estraint on si com nos avons dit, et demore et sert ensi lonc tens.	and no one intervenes who is not wise and suffering, and never once does one make the form of a tooth from bone of calf, and one puts it in the place where the deficiency is, and one restrains it as we have said, and it remains and serves thus for a long time. 
de coper lou liien de la lengue	To cover the vein of the tongue
Aucune fois est cist liiens qui vient desoz la lengue ou naturez, que on naist ensi;	Never once is this ligament that comes from under the tongue or nature, that one is born thus;  
ou par accident de plaie soudee;	or by accident of a wound joined; 
et li ovraiges est telz que tu oevre la bouche dou malaide, et ait sa teste en ton sain, et li lieve la lengue;	and the work is such that you open the mouth of the patient, and have his head in your hands, and lift the tongue.
puis cope lou liien nervous dou large, tant que li lengue soit desloie de son tenement, et se il i a duresce ou nout, et c’est de soudement de plaie, si i boute l’uncine et cope dou large celui liement;	then cut the nerve cord wide, as long as the tongue is dislocated from its place, and if there is stiffness or knot, and that is due to a wound, then put the probe and cut wide that nerve. 
et garde que li fendure ne soit mie trop em parfont, por l’artere qui est desoz;	and keep that incision not too deep, for the artery which is underneath;  
et quant tu as fait, si leve le leu d’aigue rose et d’aisil, ou d’aigue froide, puis met desoz la lengue une tente de lin;	and when you have done that, then lift the place with a rose and white, or with cold water, then put underneath the tongue a tent of linen; 
et la teigne li malaides chescune nuit, que li leus ne puisse soder.	and bind the patient every night so that the place cannot close up.  
Et se decorremens de sanc vient, si met sor le leu vitriole broiet;	And if bleeding occurs, put on the place powdered vitriol; 
et se li sans te vaint, si le cauterize au cautere lentiginout, qui est boin a ceu;	and if the bleeding does not stop, then cauterize it with the lentil cautery, which is good for this.  
puis le cure d’autre cure tant qu’il soit sanez,	Then the cure of other cures until he is healed. 
et se tu lou vois de fusse color ou noir ou dur, si que li malaides ne lou sent, si n’i touchier point, car c’est chancre;	And if you see it with a black or hard color, so that the patient does not feel it, do not touch it, for it is an ulcer. 
et s’il est declinans a blenchor, et il i a moistor, si i giete l’oncine, et lou fent d’un spatumile subtil, et lou delivre d’une part et d’autre;	And if it is turning white and there is moisture, lay the ointment on it, and apply it with a small spatula, and deliver it from one side and the other. 
et se li sans te vaint a ton ovraige, si met sus vitriole broiet tant qu’il soit estainchiez, puis revien a ton ovraige tant que tu traies tout fuer;	And if the patient refuses to comply with your work, put on crushed vitriol until it is whitened, then return to your work as long as you draw out all the pus. 
puis leve lou leu d’aisil et de seil, et le cure d’autres cures tant qu’il soit sanez.	Then raise the level of ash and earth, and treat it with other remedies until it is healed. 
des apostemes de la gorge	of the abscesses of the throat
Aucune fois vient dedens la gorge boces qui sont apelees «godath», et les apele on proprement les II amandres, et quant tu les cures, si com nos avons dit en la division, et elles ne sont sanees, si pren garde:	Sometimes comes from within the throat growths called "godaths," and they are properly called the two almonds. And when you treat them, as we have said in the division, and they are not healed, then be careful: 
se c’est apostemes dur de petit sens et de fusse color, si ne lou touchier mie de fer.	If it is abscesses hard of small size and red colored, do not touch it with iron. 
Et s’il est rouges et li racine est grosse, si ne lou touchier mie de fer, ausi por lou decorrement de sanc;	And if it is red and the root is thick, do not touch it with iron, also for the discharge of blood. 
mais lou laisse tant qu’il soit meur, et adonques tu lou partiras, ou il rompirait par soi;	But let it be until it is ripe, and then you will part it, where it would break by itself;
et s’il est de blainche color reont, et li racine est subtilz, si aies apareilliet l’estrument por coper, mais regarde premierement se li apostemes chalz repose et est apaisiez.	And if it is of white color and the root is subtle, have the instrument prepared to cut, but first look whether the abscess is warm and calmed.
Adonques fai seoir lou malaide devant lou soleil, et ses chiés soit en ton sain, et li oevre la bouche et lou preigne li serjans entre ses mains, et presse la lengue desoz a tout l’estrument, de coi ci est li forme;	Then make the patient sit facing the sun, and his shoulders be on your healthy side, and he open his mouth and you put the instruments between his hands, and press the tongue down with all the instrument.
et soit d’argent ou d’arain subtil ausi com uns coutelz:	And it is of silver or thin iron as a knife: 
Cant tu presses la lengue a tout cest estrument, et tu vois l’aposteme, si pren l’oncine et lou fiche en l’amandre, et la trai fuer au desus plus que tu pues;	Since you are pressing the tongue to all this instrument, and you see the abscess, then take the needle and put it in the middle, and draw it upward more than you can. 
et trai aucune chose des toiles avec, puis la cope a l’estrument, de coi ci est li forme, que semble unes forces;	and do nothing with the cloths, then cover with the instrument from this is the form, that seems like forces; 
et toutevoie li chief sont corbé, et l’un endroit l’autre, et sont molt agut, et est fait de fer inde ou d’andainne:	and nevertheless the head are curved, and one place the other, and are very sharp, and is made of iron or steel;
Et se tu n’as cest estrument present, si lou cope as tenailles, de coi ci est li forme:	And if you do not have this instrument present, use tongs for this is its form:
Et soit trenchans d’une part, et d’autre part nom;	And be sharp on one side, and blunt on the other. 
et quant tu as copeit l’une des amandres, si cope l’autre selonc cele meisme maniere, et aprés l’incision gargarize li malaides aigue chaude, et aigue et aisil, et se decorremens de sanc avient, si gargarize li malaides aigue, ou escorces de pomes grenates soient cuites, ou fuelles de mirte, et semblans choses, tant que li sans soit estainchiez;	and when you have cut one of the abscesses, then cut the other according to the same manner, and after the incision gargle the patient with hot water, and vinegar, and thus. And if a discharge of blood happens, then gargle the patient with water, or juices of pomegranates boiled, or myrtle leaves, and similar things, until the bleeding stops; 
puis lou cure tant qu’il soit sanez;	then cure it until it is healthy; 
et aucune fois naissent en la gorge autres apostemes que les II amandres, si les cope donques ensi com les II amandres igament.	And no other abscesses ever arise in the throat other than the two tonsils, so cut them thus as the two tonsils are. 
Et je medicinai une femme d’un aposteme que li estoit neis dedens la gorge, c’est a savoir I aposteme de petit sens;	And I treated a woman for an abscess that was growing inside her throat, namely the small abscess; 
et avoit jai bien pres close toute la gorge, si que li femme ne pooit expirer por le conduit qui estoit estoupez, et ne pooit ne mengier ne boivre, et fust morte s’elle demorast ensi I jor ou II.	and I had closed the entire throat very tightly, so that the woman could not expire through the airway which was blocked, and she could neither eat nor drink, and she would have died if she remained like this for a day or two. 
Et li apostemes estoit jai si montez qu’il avoit fuer mis II rains par les II pertuis dou neis.	And the abscess was so high raised that it had to have been put II reigns by the II openings of the two.
Je hastai donques tantost, et fichai en l’un I oncine, puis lou traï fuers, et en traï grant porcion de bowe;	I hastened therefore, and placed one finger in the throat, then pushing out through it, and pulling out a large portion of the bowel;
puis refis autreteil en l’autre pertus dou neis, et li ovrai la bouche et li pressai la lengue;	then I put the other end into the other opening where it was lodged, and opened the mouth and pressed down on the tongue; 
aprés fichai l’oncine en ces apostemes, et en copai une partie, et n’en issit fuers que un poc de sanc;	after he opened the abscess and cut into one part, and there came out only a little blood 
et ensi fut destoupez li conduis de la gorge la femme, et comensa maintenant a boivre aigue et puis vin, et ne cessai de taillier de cel aposteme par lonc tens;	and thus the woman's throat was unblocked and now she began to drink water and then wine, and did not stop cutting into that abscess for a long time
et li apostemes recroissoit adés, et remplissoit lou leu que je avoie vuidiet, tant qu’il refut mout gros;	and the abscess grew back again, filling up the space that I had emptied, until it became very large
adonques je l’engignai et lou cauterizai dedens la gorge:	then I grasped it and cauterized it inside the throat 
ensi demora sens croistre;	and then it stopped growing.  
et me partis de ces parties, et ne soi que Deus fist de li aprés moi.	and I left those parts, and only God knows what happened to her after me. 
de l’uve	of the grape
Quant reume dessent a l’uve, et elle est enflee et elle est longe, si est apelee «perpendiculaire»;	When the stem returns to the grape and it is swollen and long, that is called "perpendicular
et s’elle est desoz grosse et reonde, si est apelee «uve».	and if it is small and round, it is called "grape". 
Quant elle est curee si com nos avons dit en la division, et li cure ne profite mie, et tu vois que li chaus apostemes est apaisiez, et elle est subtilz, si covient que tu la copes;	When it is cured as we have said in the division, and the treatment does not benefit, and you see that the pus-filled abscess is appeased, and it is subtle, then it behooves you to cut it. 
et celle qui est reonde assemblee et n’est mie longe;	and that which is rounded assembled and is not long;  
et elle est sanguine ou de fusse color ou noire, si covient que tu eschues l’incision de li.	and it is bloody or of a rust color or black, then it behooves you to widen the incision of it. 
Car il i a grant peril sus lou malaide.	For there is great peril for the patient.
Il covient donques, quant tu la vois, selonc la maniere que j’ai dit, de sa blenchor et de sa longesce, que tu faices seoir le malaide devant lou soleil, et li presse la lengue a l’estrument dont nos avons fait la remembrance ci devant;	Therefore, when you see it, according to the manner that I have said, of its whiteness and its length, that you make the patient sit before the sun, and press the tongue to the instrument about which we have made mention earlier; 
puis fiche l’oncine en l’uve, et la trai desoz, et la cope a I des II estrumens que j’ai dit en l’incision des II amandres.	then place the needle in the eye, and treat it with this, and cut it at the two instruments that I have said in the incision of the two almonds. 
Et covient que tu ne coper mie fuer que la superfluiteit qui est outre le termine natureil;	And it is necessary that you do not cut more than the superfluity which is beyond the natural term;  
car se tu en copes plus, si grieves a la voix, et a la parolle;	because if you cut more, so it harms to the voice and to speech; 
et aprés l’incision, use de ceu que nos avons dit en l’incision des II amandres, et le cure tant qu’elle soit sanee.	and after the incision, use of those that we have said in the incision of the two almonds, and cure it as long as it is healed.  
Et se li malaides a paor dou coper, si covient que tu i use d’engien a la cauterization de li sens paor.	And if the patient is afraid to have it cut, then you must use something to lessen the fear of cutting.
Et li maniere dou cautere si est aigue ague.	And the manner of the cautery is sharp acute.
Et est que li malaides mette son chief en ton sain, et puis li presse la lengue a l’estrument que nos avons dit ou chapistre de cautere, et confis avec aigue vive chaus, si qu’elle ne soit mie trop espesse ne trop clere;	And it is that the patient puts his head in your hand, and then presses the tongue to the instrument that we have said in the chapter of cautery, and confides with boiling water cloth, so that it is neither too thick nor too clear;  
et en emple le chevement de cest estrument, de coi ci est li forme:	and in employing the end of this instrument, from which this form is: 
Et ait ou chief une cheveure ou om met la medecine, si com li chevemens d’une cuillier, et met l’estrument a tout la medicine sus l’uve;	And have on the head a tuft where one puts the medicine, as the end of a spoon, and put the instrument to all the medicine on the grape; 
et li malaides soit gisans sus son costeit, si que li salive et li muscillaige corre de sa bouche de la medicine dedens, si qu’ele ne dessende a la gorge, et lou blece;	and the patient lies on his side so that the saliva and the mucus flow from his mouth outside, so that it does not go down to the throat, and into the chest. 
puis tien ta main a tout la medicine et la presse sus l’uve, la quantiteit de la moitiet d’une houre, tant que tu la vois nercie et li mordications de la medicine soit apaisie;	then hold your hand over the whole medicine and press on the eye, for the quantity of half an hour, until you see it soften and the bites of the medicine be calmed. 
et se tu vues, pren coton et l’envoloupe sus aucun estrument, et moille lou coton en la medicine, et boute l’estrument a tout le couton en la cainne desus, tant que li coton s’aerde sus l’uve;	and if you see it, take cotton and wrap it around some instrument, and moisten the cotton with the medicine, and put the instrument with all the cotton in the canal of the eye, until the cotton rests on the eye. 
et fai ceu sovent, tant que li cauteres soit parfais, puis la laisse elle seche, et chiet aprés IIII jors ou V.	and do this often, until the cautery is perfect, then let it dry, and after IV or V days. 
Et se tu as mestier de rencomencier lou cautere de la medicine, si le rencomence, et aprés le cautere l’essue entor l’uve, de couton embut em burre, et mundifie ceu qui est entor de la medicine;	And if you have need to begin the cautery of the medicine again, then begin it again, and after the cautery wipe around the eye, with cotton dipped in butter, and purify that which is around the medicine.
et soit arosez d’aigue froide, et soit curez de gargarismes tant qu’il soit sanez.	and be washed with cold water, and be treated with gargles until it is healed. 
Ceste cure est plus save de l’incision, ne que li cautere;	This cure is safer than incision, nor the cautery;
s’elle est curee de fumigation selonc ceste maniere, pren calament et ysope et origanum et rue et camomille et avronne et semblans herbes, et les assemble toutes ou aucunes d’eles en I pot, et i met aisil, et fai bullir;	If it is treated by fumigation according to this manner, take wormwood and hyssop and oregano and rue and chamomile and savory and similar herbs, and put them all or any of them in a pot, and put water in it, and boil.
et li potz soit bien gluez de fort terre, et enmi le pot ait I estrument cheveit selonc ceste maniere:	and the pot should be well sealed with strong earth, and within the pot have the instrument heated according to this manner: 
Et soit d’argent ou d’arain, et soit li uns des chiés boutez en la bouche dou malaide tant que li vapor monte a l’uve par la caine, tant que li uve soit mortifie;	And it should be of silver or iron, and one end of the piece put into the mouth of the sick person until the vapor rises to the eye through the nose, until the eye is dead. 
aprés lou rencomence sovent, tant que li uve seche, et garde que tu ne faices ceu au comencement de l’avenement de l’aposteme chaut, car plusors choses i avienent;	Afterwards it should be repeated often until the eye dries, and guard that you do not do this at the beginning of the coming of the hot abscess, for many things happen. 
et ne faire mie ceu fuer que a la declination d’aposteme chaut.	and do not make any of these cures except at the decline of an abscess hot. 
Et se cist estrument n’est presens, si pren une caine et met dedens lou chief une craiffe d’uef, si que li bouche au malaide n’ait mie trop chaut;	And if this instrument is not present, then take a dog and put inside its head a bit of egg, so that the mouth of the patient does not become too hot. 
car li craiffe d’uef ne lait mie la vapor grever la bouche, et c’est bone cure ensamble salut.	for the yolk of egg does not let the vapor bother the mouth, and this is a good cure altogether healthy.  
Maintes fois s’aert a la gorge os ou espinee de poisson, ou aucune chose;	Many times it has been put in the throat bones or spine of fish, or any other thing; 
si covient donc que tu traies ceu que tu pues veoir, et li presse la lengue au soleil a tout l’estrument, si que tu voies mues la chose;	so it is necessary that you pull out what you can see, and press the tongue to the sun with all the instrument, so that you see the thing move; 
et ceu que ne t’apert mie et est reponus en la gorge, covient que tu faices vomir le malaide ainsois que li viande soit cuite en l’estomac;	and that which does not open for you and is put back in the throat, it is necessary that you make the patient vomit so that the meat may be cooked in the stomach; 
par aventure si istra li chose aerse par le vomissement;	perhaps if this thing were expelled by vomiting; 
ou li malaides englutisse une piece d’esponge, ou une piece de navel, ou une racine de laitue, ou I morceil de pain sec;	or the patient swallows a piece of sponge, or a piece of cloth, or a root of lettuce, or a morsel of dry bread;  
et lie a l’esponge I fil, et puis la transglutisse;	and tie to the sponge the thread, and then swallow it; 
et quant elle venra au leu, si s’aerdra, et puis trairas fuer;	and when it comes to its place, it will harden, and then you will draw it out;   
et s’elle ne vient fuer de ceu que nos avons dit, si pren I estrument de plonc selonc ceste forme:	and if it does not come out as we have said, then take the instrument of wood according to this form: 
Et soit li estrumens corbés au chief si qu’il puist plus legierement entrer en la gorge, et ait le chief en haut leveit;	And let the instrument be curved at the head so that it may more easily enter into the throat, and have the head raised high;  
et warde que tu ne touchier l’epiglote, que li tous ne li viegne, ne ne bouter mie l’os dedens;	And guard that you do not touch the epiglottis, lest it come alive, nor push bone inside.  
et mues vaut que li malaides i boute l’estrument, por ceu qu’il seit mues ou li chose est aerse;	And move it so that the patient puts the instrument in, because he must know if the thing is eased or not. 
si la boute aval, ou il la traie fuer a tout l’estrument igalment, tant qu’elle soit fuer.	If he pushes down, or he pulls it hard with all the instrument evenly, until it is hard. 
de la sansue de la gorge	Of the throat cutting
Aucune fois est medicinee li sansue, si com j’ai dit en la division, par la cure de medicines;	At no time is the bloodletting medicinal, as I have said in the division, by means of medications;
et quant ceu ne profite mie, adonques regarde en la gorge dou malaide au soleil, puis que tu li presses la lengue a l’estrument que je t’ai dit.	and when this does not help, then look in the throat of the patient to the sun, then that you press his tongue with the instrument that I have told you. 
Et se tu vois la sansue, si la trai a tout I petit uncine, ou as tenailles subtilz que valent a ceu.	And if you see the wound, treat it with all small instruments, or subtle tweezers that are fit for this purpose.
Et se ceu ne vaut, si pren une caine chevee, et la boute en la gorge dou malaide, puis boute ou chevement de la caine I fer chaut, et fai ce sovent.	And if this does not work, then take a horsehair and put it in the throat of the patient, then put the end of the horsehair into the fire hot, and do this often.
Et se teigne li malaides d’aigue toute jor.	And the patient remains with a fever every day.
puis pren plein I voirre d’aigue froide, et oevre la bouche, et la giete ens sens englutir, et la mueve a sa main sovent;	Then take full a cup of cold water, and open his mouth, and let him pour it into his throat without swallowing, and move it with your hand often;
et si tost com li sansue sent l’aigue, si chiet.	and as soon as the wounded person feels the water, he falls. 
Et s’elle ne chiet si com nos avons dit, si subfumige lou malaide d’asefetide, a l’estrument que j’ai dit en la fumigation de l’uve;	And if he does not fall as we have said, then smoke the patient with asafoetida, using the instrument that I mentioned in the smoking of the grape; 
fai ceu maintes fois, car elle cherra sens targier.	do this many times, for it will fall without resisting. 
Et li maniere de la fumigation si est que tu preignes I pot ou il ait charbons vis, et soit li pos covert d’un coverseil perciet en mileu, et en celui pertus soit li chiés de l’estrument;	And the manner of the smoking is that you take a pot or it has live coals inside, and let the pot be covered with a pierced cloth in the middle, and in that pierce the head of the instrument;
puis i giete ta fumigation, et li malaides mette lou chief de la cainne en sa bouche, et cloie la bouche, si que li fumee n’en isse mie, mais viegne jusc’a la sansue;	then throw your smoke in it, and the patient puts the head of the cane in his mouth, and closes his mouth so that the smoke does not come out, but comes until the wound; 
et la sansue cherra maintenant, et s’elle ne chiet, si rencomence la fumigation par maintes fois;	and the wound will now fall, and if it doesn't fall, then begin the smoking again many times.
et soffre li malaides soif, et menjuce choses salees et als, et ne boive point d’aigue;	and suffers the patient thirst, and eats salty and bitter things, and drinks no water. 
et adonques li iert mestier qu’elle isse fuer par cest governement.	And therefore it is necessary that she be cured by this governance.  
Et li forme de l’estrument a coi on trait la sansue, si est, quant on la puet veoir, semblans a tenailles corbés por mues entrer en la gorge;	And the form of the instrument with which one treats bleeding is like, when one can see it, tongs curved to enter into the throat.
et ait semblance au bec de soigne, et i ait asperiteit de lime, si que ceu qu’elle prent, elle ne puet lassier;	and has the appearance of a bird's beak, and it has sharpness of lime so that what it takes it cannot leave. 
et vez ci la forme:	And see here the form:  
li chapistres des apostemes	The chapter of abscesses
Mout de semblances d’aposteme sont, selonc ceu que li remembrance vient ci aprés d’un et d’autre en cest livre, et sont diver en perforation et en taille;	Many things similar to abscesses are, according to those that the memory comes after here from one and the other in this book, and they differ in perforation and size. 
et c’est en II manieres dont l’une est en sa semblance meisme, et de ceu qu’il tient moistor.	and it is in two manners of which one is in its very same appearance, and from that which it holds moisture.  
Et li seconde maniere si est por les leus ou il sont au cors.	And the second manner is for the eyes where they are on the body.
car li apostemes dou chief est autres que cil dou fondement, et li apostemes dou leu charnut est autres que cil qui vient en jointures, et chescuns ait son jugement en l’uevre.	for the abscesses of the head are other than those of the base, and the abscesses of the fleshy part are other than those that come in joints, and each has its judgment in the work.
Et si a apostemes c’on ne doit mie percier, tant que li bowe est meure selonc son acomplissement;	And if to abscesses one must not pierce until the boil is mature according to its accomplishment. 
et si a de telz qu’il covient percier quant il sont crut, et ne meurent mie selonc lor acomplissement, si com aposteme qui sont delez jointures.	And if there are of such kind that it is necessary to pierce when they are ripe and do not die according to their accomplishment, such as abscesses near joints. 
Car quant apostemes vient delez jointures, et on le laisse tant qu’il est porris entor, par aventure si sont corrumput li liien et li nerf de la jointure, par coi ce est cause de contraction en celui membre.	For when abscesses come near joints, and it is left as long as it is rotten and swollen, by chance the tendons and nerves of the joint are corrupted, which is the cause of contraction in that limb.
Ou li aposteme est delez lou membre principel, et se tu tardes la perforation tant qu’il soit meurez, si nuira au membre principeil;	Or the abscess is near the principal limb, and if you delay piercing until it is ripe, it will harm the principal limb. 
ou il est delez lou fondement, si le perce on ainsois qu’il soit meurs;	Or if it is near the foundation, pierce it then if it is ripe.  
et ne covient mie que tu perces aposteme crut sens digestion acomplie, fuers que celui qui est delez lou fondement, qu’il ne porrisse em parfont, et soit alongiez dedens, et i viegne fistule;	And it is not fitting that you pierce an abscess before complete digestion has occurred, except for the one that is below its base, so that it does not push out and become longer within, and a fistula comes from it. 
et ne puisse saner en grant termine.	and not be able to heal in a great term.  
Et covient que tu saiches l’oure de la perforation de l’aposteme qui est meur selonc l’acomplissement, et c’est quant li dolor est apaisie, et li departemens de la fievre, et l’amenuisement de la dolor et de la roujor, et dou debatement et de l’aguisement dou chief de l’aposteme, et les autres signes;	And it is necessary that you know the time of perforation of the abscess which is done according to its accomplishment, and this is when the pain has subsided, and the fever departs, and the lessening of the pain and redness, and the softening and healing of the head of the abscess, and the other signs; 
et covient que tu faices seoir la perforation ou plus dependant leu de l’aposteme, et la ou il apert mues;	And it is necessary that you make the perforation where more dependent the base of the abscess, and where it opens with pus; 
et soit li perforation dou lonc dou cors, et se li apostemes est as mains ou as piez, ou en jointures et au ners et as arteres, et en toz leus igalz ou il n’a point de ploieure.	and be the perforation of the long side of the body, and if the abscess is in the hands or feet, or in joints and nerves and arteries, and in all their equal parts where there is no folding.  
En ces que ploient, par selonc celui membre.	In these that are dislocated, according to which limb.
Et quant apostemes est en leu charnut, si vaut mues que tu laisses la perforation tant qu’il soit confermez en digestion acomplie, si com nos avons dit.	And when an abscess is in a fleshy place, it is worth while that you let the perforation remain until it is confirmed in complete digestion, as we have said.
Car se tu lou perces devant ceu, si iert alongiez li cors dou venim de lui, et est plains de mout d’ordure;	For if you pierce it before these, then the body of the worm will be lengthened, and it is full of much filth. 
et par aventure endurcissent les levres et li parfondetez de lui.	And by chance they harden the lips and deepen them.  
Et si a aucun aposteme que sont perciet selonc le large dou cors, selonc ceu que li membres en ait mestier.	And if to any abscess that is perceived according to the width of the body, according to what the members have need.
Et covient que tu amenistres em petis apostemes, petis pertus;	And it is necessary that you bring in small pustules, small openings; 
et en grans apostemes, grans pertus, et maintes fendures selonc la semblance de la grandor de l’aposteme;	and in large pustules, large openings, and many incisions according to the appearance of the size of the abscess; 
et si a de tels apostemes ou il covient chever lou keur, et coper;	and if it has such abscesses where it is necessary to cut the heart, and cover; 
quant il est jai devenus ausi com I drapelz, et est amortis, si covient faire ausi com on fait as bubes:	when it becomes like a shroud, and is dead, then it is necessary to do the same as with boils; 
et si a de telz que sont fendut en III angles, et si a de telz dont on cope ausi com la fuelle de mirte, si com apostemes des angres;	and if it has such that are cut in three angles, and if it has such that one covers like the leaf of myrtle, as abscesses of the angles; 
et si a de telz ou on fait une reonde taille, et autres tailles et semblant copeure.	And if there are such or one makes a round cut, and other cuts and seeming cuts. 
Cil qui n’ont point de chief, si com aposteme souef superficial, il covient que tu lou perces plainnement;	Those who have no chief, like a superficial abscess, it is necessary that you pierce it fully;  
et covient quant li apostemes est gros, et il a coillit grant bowe, et tu lou perces, si ne traire mie toute la bowe en celle houre, mais en trai une partie;	And it is necessary when the abscess is large and has collected a great amount of pus, and you pierce it, if you do not drain all the pus in that hour, but drain a part;  
puis estoupe l’aposteme jusc’a l’autre jor, puis en trai aucune chose derechief;	then stop the abscess until the next day, then drain nothing from it; 
fai ceu par maintes fois de greit en greit, tant que li bowe isse toute;	do this many times little by little, until all the pus is gone;  
meismement se li malaides est de foible vertut, ou femme portans, ou petis enfes, ou viez hons decrepites.	Likewise if the patient is of weak strength, or a woman carrying, or a young child, or an old man decrepit. 
Car li esperis tressaut aucune fois avec l’issue de la bowe, que par aventure muert li malaides, et tu ne t’en persois.	For the spirit sometimes trembles with the issue of the bowels, that perchance the patient dies, and you do not lose yourself.
Eschuez donques cest chapistre par grant cautele, et quant tu as perciet ton aposteme, si essue la plaie, et regarde se li plaie de l’aposteme est petite;	Therefore, avoid this chapter with great care, and when you have pierced your abscess, then wipe the wound, and see if the wound of the abscess is small;  
et se c’est une tailleure plainne, si amenistre tentes de lin ou de viez coton;	and if it is a plain incision, apply tents of linen or old cotton; 
et se c’est uns grans apostemes, et il i a mout de pertus, si covient que tu boutes en chescun une tente si qu’ele viegne l’une contre l’autre;	and if it is a large abscess, and there are many openings, then you must put a tent in each one so that they come against each other; 
et se tu as copeit en l’aposteme une partie dou cuir, et tu l’as cheveit entor, si covient que tu l’emplisses de viel couton ou de rasure de dras de lin sens moistor, et le lie jusc’au tier jor;	and if you have cut into the abscess a piece of skin and stitched it back together, then you must fill it with old cotton or lint from flax cloth without moisture, and bind it until the third day; 
puis l’oste, et le cure d’oignement tant qu’il soit sanez.	then the abscess will heal, and treat it with ointment until it is healed.  
Et se decorremens de sanc avient a ton ovraige, si amenistre aigue froide et aisil, et moille I drapeil, et met sor le leu decorrant par maintes fois.	And if bleeding occurs in your work, then administer cold water and ice, and moisten the cloth, and put it on the bleeding area many times.
Et se li decorremens de sanc persevere, se i amenistre governement et cure, et les poudres que j’ai dit em mains leus en cest livre, et se c’est ou tens d’iver, et li leus ou li apostemes est est mout nervous, si couvient que tu mettes sus tentes et drapelz moilliez en vin et en oile chaut;	And if the bleeding persists, administer treatment and care, and the powders that I have mentioned in this book. And if it is during winter, and the place where the abscess or wound is is very sensitive, then you must put moist tents and cloths soaked in wine and hot oil on top; 
et se c’est en esteit, et li leus est charnus, si covient que tu mes sus drapelz moilliez en aigue et en oile, ou en vin et en oile froit, jusc’au tier jor, si com nos avons dit;	And if it is in this state, and the limbs are fleshy, then it behooves you to put upon them soft cloths soaked in water and oil, or in wine and cold oil, until the third day, as we have said. 
et puis deslie l’aposteme et l’essue et le cure, si com il covient, tant qu’il soit sanez.	And then untie the abscess and wipe it and treat it as is proper, until it is healed.  
Et ceu covient il conoistre universement en cures des apostemes:	And this it behooves to know universally in the treatment of abscesses: 
or vos ai dit coment on doit aler avant as cures des apostemes, et vez ci le chapistre.	as I have told you how one should proceed before treating abscesses, and here is this chapter.  
des soros	Of sores
Ou keur dou chief vienent petis apostemes, et sont manieres de nous que sont en toiles, ausi com li josier d’une geline, et mout en i a de semblances.	When the heart of the head comes little abscesses, and are manners of ours that are in webs, just like the braiding of a tunic, and there are many resemblances.
Il en i a de gras et de telz ou il a moistor ausi com poulz;	There are some that are fatty and such as those which have moisture also like poultices; 
et si a de telz qui sont dur et pierous au taillier, et n’i a point de doutance se li artere n’i fait contraire.	and there are some that are hard and stony in shape, and there is no doubt if the artery does not oppose it. 
Et li ovraiges de la taille si est que tu esprueve a tout I estrument qui est apelez «entromissoire», de coi li forme vient ci aprés, quel chose il contient.	And the works of the waist are that you experience to all instrument which is called "entromissoire", from what the form comes after, what thing it contains.
Car s’il contient moistor, si lou fent par desus dou lonc.	For if it contains moisture, then lift it up by the long end.
Et quant li moistor est vuidie, si escorche sens rien laissier la peil qui contient celle moistor, car il revient adés quant on i laisse rien;	And when the moisture is drained, then scrape it without leaving the skin which contains that moisture, for it returns as soon as one leaves it so; 
puis plonge coton en oignement egiptien, s’il est presens;	Then dip cotton in Egyptian ointment, if it is present; 
se ceu non, en aigue et en seil, et en emple la plaie, et la laisse jusc’a l’autre jor;	If not, in water and salt, and apply it to the wound, and leave it until the next day; 
et ceu corront ceu qui est demorez dou nit.	And remove that which is left over of the ointment.  
Et pues rencomence lou coton, si com devant, le second jor, et lou tier, tant que tu saiches bien qu’il ne demoure point dou nit;	And then begin again with the cotton, as before, on the second day, and the third, until you know for sure that there is no more ointment left;
puis cure la plaie d’oignement a ceu convenauble, tant qu’il soit sanez.	then treat the wound with suitable ointment until it is healed.  
Et se li apostemes tient I nout gras, si le cope selonc ceste forme, dou lonc;	And if the abscess holds in its fat, then cut it according to this form, of length;
et i giete tes oncines, et l’escorche de toutes pars, et met toute ta cure de traire fuer la cotte ou il gist;	and you dig out the pus, and its skin from all parts, and put all your care into drawing out the core where it lies;
et se li artere te fait contraire, si fai ceu que je t’ai dit aprés.	And if the artery works against you, then do what I have told you afterwards. 
Et ausi fai de l’aposteme s’il est pierous, et dou taillier et dou curer si com je t’ai dit.	And also do for an abscess if it is foul, and how to cut and cure as I have told you.
Et li taille sus l’aposteme pierous et le moiste, si est plus legiere, car il sont de poc de sanc.	And the boil on the abscess festering and moist, it is lighter because they are of little blood.
Et si a aucuns de ces apostemes ou chief ou il n’a point de moistor, et de ces fut I apostemes que je copai ou chief d’une vielle femme;	And if to some of these abscesses or heads where there is no moisture, and of these old abscesses that I scraped or head of an old woman; 
et trovai l’aposteme ausi com une piere xourde, aspre et blainche, et ne pooit brisier;	and found the abscess as a hard stone, rough and white, and could not break; 
et s’on en eust ferut aucun, on li eust ausi bien fait plaie com d’une piere.	And if one had made none of them, one would have done as well a wound as from a stone. 
En autres apostemes venans ou chief, fuer que ces qui vienent as chief des enfans et as racines des oreilles, li overture si soit toz jors au plus dependant leu, por mues issir la bowe;	In other abscesses coming or chief,  for that which come to the head of children and to the roots of the ears, let the opening be always towards the most dependent place, in order to drain better. 
et les cure si com il covient.	And the cure as is proper.
des scrophules	of scrofulous
Maintes fois avienent cist aposteme au col, et desoz les asseles, et ens angres, et aucune fois vienent autre part ou cors, et sont mout, et sont enjanrees l’une avec l’autre.	Many times these abscesses happen in the neck, and under the armpits, and in the groin, and sometimes they come elsewhere on the body, and are bad, and are intertwined with each other.
Et chescune scrophule est proprement dedens sa cote, si com li nout et li aposteme dou chief, si com nos avons dit;	And each scrofulous [affliction] is properly inside its part, like the boils and abscesses of the head, as we have said;  
et les semblances de ces scrophules sont maintes.	and the resemblances of these scrophulous [afflictions] are many. 
Il i a de teles que contienent moistor, et si a de malignes qui ne vuellent obeir a santeit.	There are some who contain moisture, and there are some who do not want to obey health.
en celle donques que tu vois de bone disposition au tochier, et est semblans a la color dou cors, et muet de chescune part et n’est mie aerse as ners dou col ne a l’artere ne au conduit, et n’est mie parfonde;	In that one therefore that you see of good disposition to the touch, and resembles the color of the body, and moves in each part and is not at all averse to the nerves of the neck nor to the artery nor to the conduit, and is not too deep;
si covient que tu la copes par desus, et l’escorche de chescune partie, et estent les II levres dou keur as oncines, se tu en as mestier, si com nos avons dit en apostemes dou chief;	so it is necessary that you cut it from above and the skin of each part, and extend the two lips of the heart like incisions, if you need it, as we have said in abscesses of the head. 
et la trai poc et poc, et soies seur que tu ne coper lou nerf ne la voine, et ne soit mie li spatumile agus ne trenchans, que li mains n’eschaipe, et ne voise trop avant, que tu ne coper mie ceu que tu ne dois.	and the probe and probe, and be sure that you do not cut the nerve nor the vein, and do not be the spatula or trowel, so that the hands escape, and do not look too far ahead, lest you cut what you should not. 
Et se tu copes la voinne ou l’artere, et ceu ne te laisse ovrer, si met en la plaie vitriole broiet, ou aucunes poudres que restainchent sanc, et estraint la plaie;	And if you cut the vein or artery, and it does not let you work, then put in the wound powdered vitriol, or any powders that restrain blood, and tighten the wound.  
et la laisse tant que li apostemes soit apaisiez, et soit amollie li plaie, et encomence a porrir.	and leave it until the abscess is appeased, and the wound is softened, and begins to heal. 
Et quant li sans est estainchiez, si revien a ton ovraige, tant que tu l’acomplisses;	And when the hand is stained, return to your work, until you have completed it; 
puis quier a ton doit indice s’il i demoure nules petites scrophules, si les cope et les munde.	then if there remain any small pustules on your index finger, cut them and remove them.  
Et s’il a en la racine de la scrophule voinne grant, si ne covient mie que tu copes celle scrophule en sa racine, mais la lie d’un fil double fort, et la laisse cheoir par li, sens nuisement;	And if there is a large vein at the base of the pustule, it is not necessary to cut the pustule at its root, but tie it with a strong double thread and let it hang, without causing pain.  
puis emple la plaie de viel coton plongiet en oignement egiptien, puis la cure.	then apply the wound with old cotton soaked in Egyptian ointment, then dress it. 
Et se tu copes toute la scrophule, si covient que tu assembles les II levres de la plaie, et les cout maintenant, puis qu’il n’i a point demoreit de superfluiteit por la grandor de la scrophule.	And if you cut the whole scrophula, it is necessary that you assemble the two lips of the wound, and sew them now, since there is no remaining superfluity for the size of the scrophula.
si covient que tu entendes a coper la racine de li, et traire fuer, et la cout si com nos avons dit.	So it is necessary that you understand to cover the root of it, and milk forth, and the count as we have said.
Celles scrophules que tienent superfluiteit, perce lai ou il apert meure;	Those pustules that hold too much fluid, pierce them where they appear to be ripe;
et la perce ensi com celle devant dite, en dependant, puis i amenistre tentes avec oignement et semblans choses, si qu’elle corrompe ceu qui est demorez de la corruption;	and pierce them as described before, depending on the location, then administer poultices with ointment and similar things so that it corrupts what remains of the corruption.
et quant li plaie est bien mundee, si la cure d’oignement enjanrant char, tant qu’il soit sanez.	and when the wound is well cleaned, apply ointment to prevent flesh, until it is healed. 
de squinance	of squinting
Li ancien dirent et parlerent de la tailleure de la gorge;	The ancients said and spoke of cutting the throat;  
mais je ne vis onques en nostre terre qui la feist, et c’est li escripture de lor parole.	but I have never seen it done in our land, and that is the writing of their words. 
A ces qui ont squinance, il covient que li fendure de la gorge qui est apelee «epiglote» soit eschuee;	For those who have squinting, it is necessary that the cut in the throat called "epiglottis" be removed; 
et c’on ne faice aide par ceu, por ceu que toutes les voines et li pormon dou malaide sont a ces qui ont aposteme chaut en la bouche, ou en la gorge ou en II amandres.	and one does not help with this, because all the veins and arteries of the patient are hot to those who have an abscess in the mouth, or in the throat or in the almonds. 
Quant li maladie est en la chenal dou pormon, il covient coper l’epiglote por fuir la perdition qui vient de l’estranglement.	When the patient is in the channel of the throat, it is necessary to cover the epiglottis to avoid the danger that comes from strangulation.
Il covient donques, quant nos volons fendre l’epiglote, que nos le fendons desoz III cercles ou IIII une petite fendure dou travers, entre les II cercles ou par la quantiteit de la fendure dou syfac, ne mie en la cartillaige;	Therefore, when we want to cut the epiglottis, it is necessary that we cut it below three circles or four a small incision across, between the two circles or by the quantity of the incision of the stylet, not in the cartilage;
et cil leus si est covenaubles a la section de l’epiglote qu’il n’i a point de char, et li vasseil sont lonc d’enqui.	And those [parts] are so suitable to the section of the epiglottis that there is no flesh, and the vessels are long in length.  
Et se li maistres est paourous, si covient qu’il estende le cuir de la gorge a tout l’oncine, puis fende lou keur tant qu’il viegne a la cheneil;	And if the master is fearful, then it is necessary that he stretch the skin of the throat to the entire circumference, then cleave [it] as far as it comes to the channel; 
et eschue les vasselz de sanc, se tu vois aucune chose, et puis cope lou syfac, si com nos avons dit;	and avoid the vessels of blood, if you see nothing, and then cut the sifac, as we have said; 
et est demostrez par la section dou fleume de la cheneil ki saut fuer par le leu qui est rompus, et par la defaute de la voix;	and is demonstrated by the section of the phlegm of the channel which jumps out of place which is broken, and by the lack of voice; 
et laisse la plaie overte une piece.	and leave the wound open a bit.  
Et quant li houre est passee de coi on doute l’estranglement, assemble les II levres de la plaie dou keur, et la cout toute soule sens la cartillaige;	And when the hour has passed of which one doubts the strangulation, assemble the two lips of the wound of the heart, and sew them together alone except for the cartilage. 
puis aministre medicines qui font naistre char, tant qu’il soit sanez.	then administer medicines that make flesh grow, until it is healed.   
Albucasim dist c’on ne faice ce jusc’a tant que li gorge est toute estoupee, et li malaides est jugiez a mort, et li defaut li alaine.	Albucasim says one does not do this until the throat is completely swollen and the patient is judged to be dead, and the fault lies with the wing.
Adonques cope on l’epiglote por ceu que li malaides ne puet alener, et il respire par la plaie, et ensi est gardez de mort;	Then cut open the epiglottis for those who cannot breathe, and they breathe through the wound, and thus are kept from death; 
et por ce commanderent li anciain a laissier la plaie overte tant que li malice de la maladie soit passee, et elle est passee en III jors ou en IIII Et adonques il comanderent a coudre la plaie et curer, tant qu’elle fut curee;	and for this, the elders command to leave the wound open until the evil of the illness has passed, and it passes in three days or four, and then they command to sew up the wound and heal it, until it was healed.
et je vos dirai ceu que je vis.	and I shall tell you what I have seen. 
Je vis que une damoisele prist I coutel, et le ficha en sa gorge, et copa partie des chenelz dou pormon;	I saw that a young lady took the knife, and thrust it into her throat, and cut part of the channels of the peritoneum. 
et je fui apelez por li curer, et la trovai ausi com morte.	and I was called by her to cure her, and found her as dead.  
Je descovris la plaie, et trovai le sanc qui en estoit issus, et soi bien qu’elle n’avoit mie copeit voine ne conduit fuer que la gorge, et li vens issoit fuer par la plaie.	I discovered the wound, and found the blood that had come from it, and I see well that it had not struck a vein nor led further than the throat, and the veins were coming out through the wound.
Je me hastai, et cousi la plaie, et la curai tant qu’elle fut sanee;	I hastened, and sewed up the wound, and cured it until it was healed; 
et n’avint a la damoisele fuer qu’elle fut roge de voix, et revint aprés a sa disposition;	and the young lady did not have any further problem, except that she had a hoarse voice, and returned afterwards to her disposition; 
por ceu di je que en la tailleure de l’epiglote n’ait mie paour.	for this reason I say that in the cutting of the epiglottis there is no fear.   
de la grosse gorge	of the large throat
Cist apostemes est apelez «hernie de gorge», et est uns grans apostemes en color d’une jaisse, et est molt en femmes;	This abscess is called "a hernia in the throat," and it is a large abscess in the color of a bruise, and it is very common in women;
et est selonc II manieres:	and it exists according to two manners:
naturez, et accidens;	Natures, and accidents; 
ou natureil n’a point d’engien.	Or nature has no engine. 
Et li accidens est selonc II manieres, de coi l’une est semblans a gras nous, et li autre maniere est semblans a aposteme qui vient de nous d’artere;	And the accident is in two ways, of which one is like pus to us, and the other manner is like an abscess that comes from our artery; 
et il i ait paour, et ne covient mie ovrer de feir fuers que en celi qui est petite, et le prueve et cerche a tout l’intromissoire:	And there is fear in it, and it does not behoove to work fiercely except in this one that is small, and proves and searches the entire introduction:
se tu le trueves ausi com I nout gras, et ne pent a nulle voine, si le cope, si com on cope les nous, et le trai a tout sa coife, s’il en i a point;	If you find it like our pus, and cannot to any vein, if you cut it, as one cuts the pus, and the track to its entire tip, if there is any. 
et encerche bien tot, et le cure si com il covient, tant qu’il soit sanez parfaitement.	And surround it well soon, and cure it as it behoves, until it is perfectly healed.
des nous	of us
Maintes manieres de nous sont, dont je dirai toutes les semblances;	Many manners of pus are, which I will say all the appearances;
et or covient que je die toute la difference qui est entre nout et issue.	And now it is necessary for me to say all the difference which is between us and dislocation. 
Je dis que issue est chalors et fievre tenans, tant que li ebulicions est passee, et est acomplie li porriture;	I say that a dislocation is sometimes accompanied by fever and inflammation as long as the boiling (or inflammation) has not passed, and putrefaction has come to completion. 
adonques repose li fievre et li chalor.	Therefore rest the fever and heat. 
Avec lou nout n’a ne chalor ne fievre ne dolor, et contient I syfac, qui est ses propres sac et est selonc la color dou cors, et encomence ausi com une jaisse, et devient gros;	With the sprain there is neither heat nor fever nor pain, and it contains a swelling, which is its own bag and is according to the color of the body, and begins like a bruise, and becomes large.
et sont selonc II semblances, ou grais, ou moiste, et mout de color sont si com j’ai dit en la division.	And there are according to its appearances, whether it is thick or moist, and of many colors as I have said in the division.
Il covient, quant tu viens a la cure dou nout, que tu esprueves et l’enquier premierement a tout l’estrument qui est apelez «entromissoire», selonc ce que sa forme venra ou chapistre qui est aprés.	It is necessary when you come to the cure of the new, that you try and inquire first to all the instrument which is called « entromissoire », according to what its form will come or chapter which is afterwards.
Et li maniere de l’inquisicion des apostemes des nous est que tu preignes ou plus moiste leu que tu trueves en l’aposteme, et torne tes dois poc et poc, tant que tu saiches que li estrumens ait perciet le keur, puis que ce soit selonc la grandor de l’aposteme;	And the manner of incision of an abscess from a sprain is that you prick or more moist place than you find in the abscess, and turn your two points (of the instrument) and points, until you know that the instrument has pierced the core, then let it be according to the size of the abscess;
puis estrai l’entromissoire, et pren garde en ceu que saut fuer.	then extract the intromitter, and take heed of those who leap. 
Se moistor corrans cort, queil color elle ait, si le fent si com j’ai dit des autres apostemes;	If moisture runs short, whatever color it is, treat it as I have said of other abscesses.  
et se aprés l’entromissoire nen vient moistor, saiches qu’il est gras, si le fent donques en croix, et le prent as pinceures, et l’escorche legierement de chescune part et warde la cotte ou il gist que tu la traies saine avec le nout;	and if after the intromitter no moisture comes, know that it is fatty, so treat it with a cross and take it with forceps, and lightly scrape each side and ward the cloth where it lies so you can draw it out healthy with the needle.  
et se tu ne la pues traire saine, si la trai par pieces si qu’il n’i demoure rien.	and if you cannot draw it out healthy, then draw it out piece by piece so that nothing remains. 
Car s’il i demoure rien, si revient li nous par maintes fois;	For if anything remains, it will return to us many times.  
et s’il en demore un poc, et li sans te grieve, si emple la plaie d’aucunes poudres corrosives agues, et estraint la plaie, et met sus choses apaisans aposteme chaut, et le cure d’autres cures tant qu’il soit sanez;	and if some remains and it does not grieve you, then apply to the wound some sharp corrosive powders, and drain the wound, and put on soothing things above, an abscess hot, and treat it with other cures until it is healed.
et se li nous est grans, si cout les II levres de la plaie, et le cure de ceu qui enjanre char.	and if it is large for us, then we sew the two lips of the wound, and treat with those who create flesh. 
et se li voine batans t’est contraire ou autre si te haste et emple le leu de vitriole broiet, et lou laisse liiet II jors ou III, tant que li plaie porrisse, et repose li ebulicion dou sanc;	and if the vein is pulsating for you contrary or otherwise hasten and apply the place of crushed vitriol, and leave it for two days or three, as long as the wound suppurates, and rest the boiling of blood. 
puis revien au coper ceu que i est demoreit dou nout.	then return to covering what is remaining from within.  
Vez ci les formes des estrumens entromissoires, et sont de III manieres:	See here the forms of the introduction instruments, and there are in three ways: 
grans et moien et petit;	large and medium and small;
et s’en i a III quarrez qui sont apelez «albaret», et I qui est apelez «breb», et s’en i a de III manieres:	and there are three squares which are called "albaret", and one which is called "breb", and there are in three ways:
grant, moien, et petit, por encerchier les apostemes de fistule;	large, medium, and small, to surround the abscesses of fistula;
et sont ausi com les aguilles dont on cout les sorceles, et sont d’arain citrin, ou de fer, ou d’argent, et mues valent cil qui sont jaune, et sont plus esprovez de plonc noir por encerchier les corbeures de fistule;	And they are also like the needles that one sews with sorcerers, and they are of citrine iron or silver, and the yellow ones are more valuable, and they are more proven from black lead to encircle the curves of fistulas.  
et sont de III manieres:	And they are in three ways: 
grans, moiens, et petis, selonc la quantiteit de la largesce des pertus.	large, medium, and small, according to the quantity of the width of the perforations. 
Les formes des oncines sont de mout de semblances, si com tu vois ci:	The shapes of the probes are of many resemblances, as you see here:  
grans, moiens, et petis;	large, medium, and small;
et si a oncines qui ont II corbeures de III manieres ausi;	and there are probes that have two curves in three ways also; 
et si a oncines qui ont III corbeures, et sont ausi de III manieres;	and there are probes that have three curves, and they are also in three ways; 
et si a oncines qui ont II corbeures, et oncines d’une corbeure soulement, et sont de III manieres;	and there are probes that have two curves, and probes of one curve only, and they are in three ways; 
et tuit cist sont necessaire en lor leu.	and all of these are necessary in their place.  
Li chief de ces a coi on fent sont trenchant, et de telz i a qui ne taillent mie fuer que d’une part, dont on escorche les nous, por ceu c’on ne cope la voine ne le nerf;	The chief of these things that one does is cutting, and there are some which do not cut more than from one side, because we skin them, for this reason one does not cut the vein or the nerve. 
et de ces intromissoires sont les alemeles reponues en mainches, si que li malaide ne s’en persoivent a l’overture des apostemes;	And of these introducers are the probes put into handles, so that the patient does not feel them at the opening of abscesses.  
et sont de III manieres:	and there are three ways. 
grant, petit, et moien, si com tu vois;	large, small, and medium, as you see.   
et n’en use on mie fuer que en leu charnut, si com jambes, et bras, et mameles, et as angres, et en semblans leus;	and one does not use them more than in fleshy places, such as legs, and arms, and breasts, and flanks, and similar places.   
et aucune fois fait on I autre estrument petit, semblant a escorces de fistices, selonc ceste forme, a coi on estainche sanc:	and at no time is the other instrument small, seeming to scrapes of fistulas, according to this form, which one drains blood. 
et le met on aucune fois au leu qui saine a copement des voines, et as arteres, et aucune fois reont selonc ceste grant forme:	and put it once in its place which is wholesome to cutting of veins, and arteries, and never again according to this great form:
Aucune fois enflent les mameles d’aucuns homes quant cil encomencent estre corrumput, tant qu’eles semblent mameles de feme;	At times the breasts of some men swell when they begin to rot, until they seem like women's breasts.  
et demorent laides et enflees, et qui les vuet curer, si le covient soier selonc ceste forme des ceste ligne .b. jusques a .g.:	and remain disfigured and swollen, and whoever wants to cure them, must follow this form from line .b. to .g.:  
puis escorche la graisse, et emple la plaie de medicine enjanrant char, puis assemble les II levres de la plaie a costure, et la cure tant qu’ele soit sanee;	then scrape the fat, and apply medicine to the wound,  healing flesh, then join the two sides of the wound with stitching, and treat it until it is healed. 
et se li mamele cline aval, et est amolie por sa grandor si com il avient as femmes, si la fent en II costelz desus, par II semblans fendures;	and if the breast leans down and softens due to its size, as it happens with women, then make two incisions above it. 
de coi l’une soit tenans a l’autre a la fin de l’une et de l’autre, si que li plus grans ligne conteigne la menor selonc ceste forme, des ceste ligne .b. jusc’a la ligne .g.;	so that one hangs from the other at the end of each, so that the larger piece contains the smaller, according to this form, from line .b. to line .g.
