puis escorche le cuir qui est entre les II levres, et oste la graisse, et i amenistre ceu que nos avons dit de costure et de poudres, et ceu qui est necessaire en la cure, tant qu’il soit sanez;	Then scrape the skin that is between the two lips, and remove the fat, and administer there what we have said of stitching and powders, and what is necessary in the cure, until it is healed. 
et s’il n’est sanez, ou li incision n’est mie toute faite, por ceu que li malaides ne vuet reposer, ou por le decorrement de sanc, si covient que tu emplisses la plaie de coton moilliet en oignement corrosif;	And if it is not healed, or the incision is not entirely made, for that the patient does not want to rest, or for the loss of blood, then you must fill the wound with cotton moistened in corrosive ointment; 
et le laisse tant qu’il menjuce le remenant et la graisse, puis le cure tant qu’il soit saneis.	and let it stay until it dries the remaining and the fat, then cure it until it is healed.  
des apostemes des asselles	of abscesses of the armpits
Cist apostemes que vienent desoz les asseles sont manieres de scrophules dures ou il ait cotes, et s’en i a que contienent moistor.	These abscesses that come from under the arms are kinds of hard scrofulas which have edges, and some contain moisture.
Cil donques qui contienent moistor covient qu’il soient copez selonc ceste forme, des la ligne .b. jusc’a la ligne .g.:	Therefore those who contain moisture should be cut according to this form, from the line .b. to the line .g..
Et quant toute li bowe qui est en l’aposteme est vuidie, si emple la plaie de viel coton, et la laisse jusc’a l’autre jor, puis oste tout le coton, et cure d’oignement avenant a ceu tant qu’il soit sanez.	And when all the matter that is in the abscess is emptied, put the wound with old cotton, and leave it until the next day, then remove all the cotton, and care with ointment after this as long as it is healing.
Et se li apostemes est de semblances de scrophules, si le fent si com nos avons dit en fendures des scrophules, et se li plaie rent bowe, si amenistre cautere si com nos avons dit devant.	And if the abscess is of the appearance of scrofulas, then cut it as we have said for incisions into scrofulas, and if the wound is bowed inward, then administer cautery as we have said before.
de la routure de l’artere	Of the rupture of the artery
Quant li artere est route, et li cuir est soudez qui est sus, si en vient maintes fois apostemes, et tout aussi avient il a la voine enflee et aposteme;	When the artery is severed, and the skin above is seared shut, then abscesses often arise, and it also happens to the swollen vein and abscess.
et si le conoist on ensi quant c’est por l’artere, si est li apostemes lons em parfont;	and if he knows this is for the artery, then let the abscesses grow long. 
et quant tu le sens a tes dois, si sens I estraignement;	and when you feel it in your hands, it feels like constriction; 
et quant c’est por la voine, si est reons defuer aparans;	and when it is for the vein, then it appears red and hot.  
et c’est folie de coper cest aposteme, et meismement quant il est desoz les asseles et as angres et ou col et em mout d’autres leus, et est mout grans.	and it is folly to cover this abscess, and even when it is under the armpits and at the neck and in many other places, and is very large. 
Il covient donques eschuir la cure de fer, et celui qui est a chief covient eschuir ausi, et en celui qui est d’enfleure d’artere fent par desus le cuir dou lonc;	Therefore it is necessary to abandon the treatment of iron, and whoever is at the head should also abandon it, and in those who are swollen with artery felt through the long skin; 
puis oevre la taille as oncines, et depart bellement l’artere des toiles, tant qu’ele soit descoverte;	then work the incision carefully, and depart beautifully the artery from the tissues, until it is uncovered;  
puis boute desoz li une aguille, et la fai percier jusc’a l’autre costeit, et estraint l’artere d’un fil double en II leus, selonc ceu que je t’ai ensigniet en l’estraction des II arteres qui sont en temples;	then put under it a needle, and make it pierce until the other side, and extract the artery with a double thread in II leagues, according to what I have taught you in the extraction of the II arteries that are in the temples; 
puis point le leu qui est entre les II liens d’un intromissoire tant que li sans en isse qui i est, et soit deliiez li aposteme;	Then point the place which is between the two joints of an intromissoire until the pus that is there, and be careful of the abscess. 
puis amenistre la cure que enjanre bowe, tant que li liien chient;	Then administer the cure that engenders bowel, as long as the ligament hangs; 
puis cure ceu d’oignement avenant a ceu, tant qu’il soit sanez;	Then cure those of ointment coming to these, as long as they are healed.
et se li apostemes est por la taille de la voinne, si covient que tu teignes a ta main ceu que tu pues de l’aposteme a tout le cuir, puis boute l’aguille desoz le leu que tu tiens a ta main, et la fai percier, et i ait I fil double, si que tu le trais de l’autre costeit;	And if the abscess is for the size of the vein, then it is necessary that you tie with your hand those that you can of the abscess to all the skin, then push the needle under the place that you hold in your hand, and let it pierce, and let it have a double thread, so that you draw it from the other side;
puis lie l’aposteme, si com je t’ai dit, ou liien de l’une de II pars as II chiés dou fil;	Then tie the abscess, as I have told you, or the ligament of one of the two parts as the two ends of the thread; 
et se tu doutes que li filz n’isse fuer, si i reboute une autre aguille a tout I fil desoz tout l’aposteme a l’incision de la premiere aguille, et estraint les filz en IIII leus;	And if you doubt that the needle isn't far enough, reinsert another needle through all of the pus below the incision of the first needle, and hold the threads back in four places. 
puis cope l’aposteme tant que li superfluitez en isse, puis cope la superfluiteit dou keur et laisse ceu qui est liiez;	Then cut the abscess until all of the excess comes out, then cut away the superfluity from the core and leave what is attached. 
puis met sus I drapeil moilliet en vin et en oile, puis li amenistre cures de tentes et d’oignemens tant qu’il soit sanez.	Then put a moist cloth soaked in wine and oil on top, then administer care with tents and ointments until it is healed. 
des apostemes des ners	of abscesses of the nerves
Ausi com aposteme vienent en l’artere et en la voine, vienent aposteme as ners quant il sont ferut, ou par trop grant travail, et semblans choses.	As abscesses come in the artery and in the vein, abscesses come to the nerves when they are burned or by too much work, and similar things.
Et ceu avient plus sovent as adjutoires et as dois et en toz leus ou il ait jointures, et c’est I grief apostemes, et sa color semble la color dou cors, et est em plusors dispositions sens dolor;	And this happens more often at the shoulders and hips and in all places where there are joints, and it is a painful abscess, and its color resembles the color of the body, and it is in many positions without pain;
et quant on l’estraint forment, si sent li malaides dolor, et n’est mie em parfont dou cors, mais desoz lou keur;	And when it is restrained firmly, the patient feels pain, and it is not in proportion to the body, but below the core;
et muet bien de toutes pars, et ne va ne avant ne arrier, ne desoz ne desus, et celui qui est en jointures ne covient mie coper par fer:	And keep it still from all sides, and do not go forward or backward, neither sideways nor up and down, and the one that is in joints should not be covered by iron. 
par aventure i vanroit contraction;	For fear it might contract.  
et cil qui est ou chief ou ou front, fent le cuir au spatumile.	And the one that is on the head or forehead, make the skin into a pad. 
Se li apostemes est petis, si le tien a unes tenailles, et le cope en sa racine;	If the abscess is small, then hold it with tweezers and cut it at its root; 
et s’il est grans, si le sospent a l’oncine, et l’escorche, puis l’oste et assemble la plaie a la costure, et lou cure tant qu’il soit sanez.	And if it is large, then suspend it with a sling, and lance it, then drain it and stitch the wound together, and treat it until it is healed. 
des grosses boces pendans	of large bladders hanging
Aucune fois avient en ventres et ne mie autre part thelul, et est une maladie qui est apelee «funge» par la semblance d’aus, et est li racine subtilz, et li chiez gros;	Sometimes there appears in the belly and nowhere else a tumor, and it is a disease that is called "fungus" because of its appearance as such, and is the root subtle, and the head large;
et en i a de petis et de mout grans;	And there are some small and some very large. 
et je vis I home qui en avoit II ou ventre qui estoient plus semblans a funges que ai autre chose, et n’i avoit point de difference, et estoient blanc, et avoient menue racine, et estoient jai fendut, et en corroit adés moistor.	and I saw the man who had II in his belly which were more like mushrooms than anything else, and there was no difference, and they were white, and they had small roots, and they were slightly split, and pus oozed from them 
Je les copai et trovai en l’un XVIII onces pesant, et en l’autre VI З., et li ovraiges en l’incision si est que tu regardes se li malaides est moistes, et li color de l’artelul est blainche et moiste et de subtil racine;	I cut them open and found in one XVIII ounces weighing, and in the other VI III., and the work in the incision is that you look if the patient is moist, and the color of the vessel is white and moist and of subtle root; 
si le cope au spatumile large, et soient en ta presence li cautere au feu.	if it's cut with a broad spatula, and be in your presence the fire cautery.  
Car au taillier vient maintes fois trop grans decorremens de sanc, et se li sans te vaint, si te haste donques dou cauterizer;	Because at the incision often comes many large hemorrhages of blood, and if the bleeding does not stop, then hasten to cauterize. 
et se tu vois le malaide espoanteit et paourous de l’incision dou fer, si prent I fil de plonc bien fait, et en lie l’artelul si com nos avons dit, et le laisse II jors;	and if you see the patient is frightened and afraid of the incision of iron, then take a thread of wool well made, and tie the vessel as we have said, and leave it for II days;
et puis le restraint, et ne cesser d’estraindre lou fil de plonc tant qu’il cope l’artelul, et chiece par lui sens travail;	and then restrain it, and do not cease to restrain the thread of lead until it heals the articulation, and it will be healed by it without work. 
et se les racines sont grosses, si a paour au coper meismement por le ventre, mais tu em pues bien coper la moitiet, puis le cauterize qu’il ne reviegne;	and if the roots are thick, if there is fear to cauterize even for the belly, but you may well cauterize half of it, then cauterize it so that it does not return.  
puis cure la plaie, et garde que tu ne coper le thelul qui est de fuxe color et de povre sens et de lait regart.	Then cure the wound, and guard that you do not cauterize the thread that is of dark color and poor sense and milky appearance. 
Car c’est uns apostemes enchancrez, et je venrai a la cure de chancre ci aprés.	For this is an abscess encrusted, and I will come to the cure of ulcers after.
quant li boude ist fuer	when the head is carried
Se li apparance de la boude vient par cautere de plaie ou de fendure de syfac, et est sus le ventre et en ist aucuns des bouez, si com il avient en autres routures, ou de sanc qui cort de voines ou d’arteres selonc ceu qui est devant, ou de ventositeit;	If the appearance of the boil comes from cautery of a wound or fissure of the body, and is on the belly and in some of the boils, as it happens in other ruptures, or of blood which flows from veins or arteries according to what is before, or of wind;
et se c’est par la routure dou syfac et par l’issue dou bouel, si est li color de l’aposteme semblans a la color dou cors, et est legiere chose sens dolor, et apert de diverse issue.	and if it is by the rupture of the body and by the issue of the boil, then the color of the abscess is similar to the color of the body, and it is a light thing without pain, and opens with diverse issue.  
Et se c’est por l’issue de l’intestine, adonques est il plus divers, et quant on le presse a ses dois si se repont, et puis revient, et par aventure si est sarrez, et agrandist mout a l’entree dou bain et por fort travail.	And if it is for the issue of the intestine, then it is more diverse, and when one presses it to its sides it returns, and then returns again, and perhaps it is seized, and enlarges greatly at the entrance of the bath and for heavy work.
Et se c’est por moistor, c’est legiere chose, et apert bien quant tu le presses a ta main, ne ne constraint mie;	And if it is due to moisture, it is a light thing, and open well when you press it with your hand, do not constrain it at all;  
et se c’est por sanc, si apert par ces signes li apostemes gros et dur, et est fichiez selonc une quantiteit;	and if it is for blood, then open by these signs the abscess thick and hard, and is filled according to a quantity;  
et se c’est por ventositeit, si est souef au tochier, et li ovraiges si est que tu regarde se li apparance est por le sanc de l’artere, ou de la voine, ou ventositeit.	and if it is for windiness, then it is puffed by touching, and the work is that you look if its appearance is for the blood of the artery, or of the vein, or windiness.  
Si covient que tu laisses la cure.	So you must leave the cure.
Car il en a doutance et paor, si com je t’ai dit ou chapistre des apostemes, por l’artere et por la voine.	For there is doubt and fear in it, as I have said to you in the chapter of abscesses, for the artery and for the vein.
Et se li apparance est por l’intestine ou lou boueil, si covient que tu comandes au malaide qu’il teigne son alaine, et soit estendus tout drois, puis seigne d’enche tout entor la boude;	And if its appearance is for the intestine or the bile, then you must command the patient to hold his arm, and be outstretched straight, then feel all around the belly;  
puis le comande a gesir sovin entre tes mains, puis va entor le leu que tu as signiet a tout le spatumile, puis estent la moitiet de l’aposteme au desus a tout le grant uncine;	then command him to move his bowels between your hands, then go around the place that you have marked with all the spatula, then extend half of the abscess above to the whole great one-inch.
puis le lie entor d’un fil fort, ou d’une corde de fort soie fermement, et soit li nous dou liien assolz;	then tie it around with a strong thread, or a strong silk cord firmly, and let the two ends be tied together.
puis oevre la moitiet de l’aposteme estendut sus le liien, et i boute ton doit indice, et quier l’intestine;	Then work on the half of the abscess extending over the linen, and put your index finger in it, and probe the interior. 
se tu le trueves pris dou liien, si le deslie, et boute l’intestine au defuer dou ventre;	If you find it stuck to the linen, untie it, and bring the interior out of the depth of the belly; 
et se tu trueves le boueil, si le prent a l’oncine, et en cope la superfluiteit;	And if you find it boiled, take it with the pincers, and cut off the excess.  
et se li artere te fait contraire, ou li voine, si vai belement entor, puis revien a ton ovraige et pren II aguilles, et i boute II fors filz, et boute les II aguilles entor ceu que tu as fait en crois que tu feis percier;	And if the artery opposes you, or the vein, then go beautifully around, then return to your work and take two needles, and put two threads through them, and insert the two needles back into what you have done in crosswise so that you make it pierce. 
puis estrain l’aposteme en IIII leus sus les aguilles, et se tu vues, oste les aguilles, et laisse lou leu tant qu’il porrisse, et chiece li char morte par soi;	Then strain the abscess in four leagues on the needles, and if you see it, remove the needles, and leave them there as long as it purges, and let the dead flesh fall off by itself.  
ou tu la cope quant elle iert subtiliie et porrie, puis le cure de ceu qu’il covient, et cheve l’aposteme si com nos avons dit;	or you cut it when it is subtle and soft, then the care of it as is proper, and cover the abscess as we have said. 
et estrai le sanc ou la moistor que tu trueves, puis cure le leu de ceu qu’il couvient, et soude le leu.	and extract the blood or moisture that you find, then cure the place as is proper, and bind the place. 
dou chancre	of the ulcer
Nos avons dit en la division les semblances de chancre, et coment on i doit ovrer par medicines, et coment on doit eschuer la cure de fer;	We have said in the division the appearances of sores, and how one must work them by medicines, and how one must avoid the cure of iron; 
et disons le chancre enjanreit en la marris, et grant cautele a en la cure, et dirent li ancien que quant chancres est en leu ou on le puet raier si com chancre qui est em mameles, et en la cuixe, et en semblans leus, et le doit tout oster quant il est en l’encomencement;	and we say that a sore  begins in the marshes, and great caution is needed in its cure, and ancients said when a sore is in a place where one can scrape it like sores which are on the nipples, and in the groin, and in similar places, and one must remove it entirely when it is in the beginning; 
et quant il est grans et anciens, si ne covient mie que tu l’aproches, car je n’en poi onques nul saner;	and when it is large and old, it is not fitting that you approach it, for I can never heal any of them. 
ne nulz n’en sana onques devant moi.	no one has ever cured them before me. 
Et li ovraiges, quant il est en leu ou on le puet oster, si com nos avons dit, est que tu purge aucune fois le malaide de cole noire;	And the work, when it is in place where one can remove it, as we have said, is that you purge the patient of black blood at any time. 
puis le fai sainier s’il ait manifeste repletion, puis afaite le malaide I boin leu por faire l’ovraige;	then make him bleed if he has a manifest repletion, then put the patient in good condition to do the work; 
puis giete tes oncines ou chancre, et le cheve de toutes pars, et l’oste de toutes pars sens rien laissier;	then throw your incisions or ulcers and the hair from all parts and the bone from all parts without leaving anything.  
et laisse corre le sanc tout fuer, et espreint bien le leu a ta main ou a aucune chose, et se li decorremens de sanc te fait contraire de l’incision de l’artere ou de la voine, si le cauterize tant que li sans soit estainchiez;	and let the blood flow completely, and press well the place with your hand or any thing, and if the bleeding contrary to the incision of the artery or vein, cauterize it until the bleeding is stopped. 
puis le cure d’autre cure tant qu’il soit sanez.	then treat it with other cures until it is healed.  
de ydropisie	of dropsy
Nos avons jai dit en la division les semblances d’idropisie, et en queil maniere li assemblee de l’aigue est faite, et les signes de chescune semblance, et la cure qui est faite par medicines, et cele qui est curee par fer:	We have said in the division the similarities of dropsy, and how the assembly of water is made, and the signs of each similarity, and the cure which is made by medicines, and that which is cured by iron.  
si est eclites soulement;	It is struck alone; 
et ne doit on touchier de fer en ces II semblances:	and one should not touch iron in these two resemblances: 
c’est a savoir, tympanites et yposarche, car c’est mortelz chose;	that is to say, tympanites and hypoarche, for it is a mortal thing;  
donques quant tu medicines ceste semblance de ydropisie qui est apelee «eclites» de medicines, et li cure ne profite, si regarde se li malaides est foibles, ou s’il ait autre maladie que ydropisie, si com toust et solution de ventre et semblans choses;	Therefore when you medicate this semblance of dropsy which is called "eclights" and the cure does not profit, see if the patient is weak, or if he has another illness besides dropsy, such as gout and diarrhea and similar things;
si n’i touchier de fer, car il i a doutance;	if you do not touch iron, for there is doubt; 
et se tu vois le malaide de fort vertut, et il n’a autre maladie que ydropisie soulement, et il n’est mie trop jones ne trop vielz, si dois ensi ovrer:	and if you see the patient of strong virtue, and he has no other illness besides dropsy alone, and he is neither too young nor too old, then you must thus operate: 
lieve le malaide droit sus tes mains, et li ministres presse le ventre em boutant l’aigue a la plus basse partie dou pis, puis pren le spatumile espinous selonc ceste forme:	Lift the patient straight on your hands, and the assistants press the belly pushing the water to the lowest part of the basin, then take the spatula spine according to this form: 
Et soit trenchans de II pars.	And shall be sharp of II parts.
a pointe, et toutevoie ne soit mie si entrans qu’il puist venir jusc’a l’intestine quant on le fiche ens, et ne le puist blecier;	To a point, and nevertheless, it should not be so deep that it can come to the intestine when one inserts it, and one cannot bleed it. 
puis regarde se li ydropisie est enjanree devers les intestines:	Then look if hydropisie is formed towards the intestines:  
si covient que tu fendes ensus de la boude III dois droit desoz sus lou poignil;	If it is appropriate, that you cut in below the hip bone, three fingers to the right of the hip; 
et se li ydropisie est por la maladie dou foie, si soit ta fendure au senestre de la boude III dois;	And if hydropisie is due to the disease of the liver, then the incision should be made on the left side of the hip bone, three fingers. 
et se c’est por la miuce, si soit a destre, et ne covient mie que li malaides gise sus la fendure que les superfluitez ne corrent a celui foible leu;	And if it is due to the spleen, then it should be on the right, and it is not appropriate that the patient lie on the incision so that the superfluities do not run to the weak place. 
puis perce tout le cuir a l’estrument, et le boute, et lieve ta main a tout le spatumile entre le cuir et le syfac ausi com en escorchant a la quantiteit d’une ungle ou enqui entor;	Then pierce the whole skin with the instrument, and it will burst, and lift your hand all over the spatula between the skin and the fascia as much as in scraping to the quantity of a fingernail or less. 
puis perce lou syfac tant que li spatumile viegne au leu vuit, et c’est li leus de l’aigue, puis le trai fuer, et i boute cest estrument de coi ci est li forme:	then pierce the shaft as long as the spatula reaches its eighth place, and this is the level of the water, then remove the blade, and put this instrument in which is the shape: 
Et est semblans a une caine d’argent subtil, et est d’arain ou d’archaut legier, et a en la partie desoz I petit pertus;	And it resembles a silver chain that is subtle, and it is of iron or light steel, and on the lower part, there is a small hole. 
et ou costeit d’une part, III pertus;	and where it costs from one side, III pierced.  
et II d’autre part, et I d’autre;	and II on the other side, and I on the other; 
et est li chiés tailliez si com une penne, et c’est li forme de l’incision dont li escrivains taille la penne:	and the head is cut like a feather, and this is the shape of the incision with which the writers cut the feather: 
au chief desus est li alemele, si que quant li estrumens vient a l’aigue, si dessent maintenant sus l’estrument;	at the top is the  alemele, so that when the instruments come to the point, it descends now on the instrument; 
vuide la donques la moitiet ou la tierce part, car se tu en vuides plus qu’il ne covient en celle houre, par aventure si muert li malaides por la resolution de son esperit de l’arme, ou il chiet paumez, ou il aproche a la mort;	empty the half or the third part, because if you empty more than it is proper in that hour, by adventure the patient dies for the resolution of his spirit from the weapon, or he falls faint, or he approaches death; 
mais en vuide selonc la quantiteit de sa vertut, et selonc ceu que les dispositions de la vertut dou malaide signifient, et ses poulz;	but empty according to the quantity of his virtue, and according to what the dispositions of the virtue of the patient signify, and his pulses; 
puis trai l’estrument et retien l’aigue, et elle est retenue maintenant por le keur qui estoupe le pertus qui est sus le syfac, de coi j’ai parleit, que tu perces selonc ceste maniere;	Then treat the instrument and hold the point, and it is now held by the heart that stops the opening which is on the surface, for this reason I have spoken, that you pierce in this manner. 
puis rencomence l’estrument l’autre jor, se tu vois le malaide soffrant ceu, et trai de l’aigue une petite quantiteit;	Then begin the instrument again another day, if you see the patient suffering these, and treat the point a small quantity. 
fai ce aucun jor, et te garde de foloier tant qu’il ni demore mais c’un poc d’aigue.	Do this every day, and keep from probing until there remains but a little point of fluid.
Et se tu doutes sus le malaide, et tu i lais mout d’aigue, si le cure de la sepulture ou sablon chaut, et par mout sueir ou bain et au soleil, et se teigne de boivre;	And if you doubt about the patient, and you let too much fluid out, so cure him with  earth or hot sand, and by much sweat or bath and in the sun, and have him drink.
et le cure de medicines desiccatives tant qu’il soit sanez, et cauterize sus l’estomac et sus lou foie et sus l’esplen aprés l’estraction de l’aigue, si com j’ai dit devant.	And cure him with drying medicines until he is healthy, and cauterize on the stomach and on the liver and on the spleen after the extraction of the fluid, as I have said before. 
de l’estopement de la verge	Of the stoppage of the penis
Aucune fois naissent enfant qui n’ont point de pertus en la verge, ou li pertus est petis, ou il n’est mie en son leu.	At times children are born who have no opening in the penis, or the opening is small, or it is not in its place.
Si le covient tantost qu’il n’aist percier a tout I spatumile molt subtil selonc ceste forme:	If it is necessary, then he must see to every little detail very carefully according to this form:
puis met ou pertus I clo subtil de plonc, et le lie et le tien ensi III jors ou IIII et quant il vuet faire urine, si soit ostez li clos, et faice urine, et puis li remet;	Then put in the hole a small plug of lead, and tie it and keep it so for three or four days, and when he wishes to urinate, remove the plug, and make water, and then put it back. 
et par aventure nen i couvient point, car li urine qui vient fuer ne lou laisse close.	And perhaps it does not work because the urine coming out does not allow it to be closed.  
Cil de cui li pertus est petis, si est medicinez dou clo de plonc, si com nos avons dit, si s’eslargera.	He whose hole is small, if he is medicated with the clove of plantain, as we have said, it will widen.
Cil qui n’ont mie le pertus en lor leu sont bleciet, car aucun naissent qui ont le pertus au chief de la verge, por coi il ne puient pissier avant s’il ne lievent lor verge en haut;	Those who do not have the urethra in its place are blue because none are born with the urethra at the head of the penis, so they cannot urinate before lifting their penis upwards.
et ne pueent enjanrer por ceu que li matiere ne puet venir jusc’a la marris, et c’est une male maladie.	And cannot ejaculate because the material cannot come to the mouth, and this is a bad illness.  
Et li maniere de l’ovraige si est que li malaides gise sovin sus son dos, puies estent le chief de la verge et le cope ausi com la taille d’une penne, si ke li pertus chiece em mileu, si com il covient;	And the way to operate is that the patient lies flat on his back, then they extend the head of the penis and the scrotum as if it were a feather, so that the urethra falls in the middle, as it should;
et te garde de decorrement de sanc qui i vient maintes fois, et s’il avient, si l’estainche de ceu qui estainche sanc, et cure la plaie tant qu’il soit sanez.	And guard yourself from the flow of blood that comes many times, and if it happens, with the stanch of those who stanch blood, and cure the wound until it is healed. 
des pustules de la verge	of the blisters of the penis
Maintes fois vienent cist albathe en la verge, et est une apparance de char laide;	Many times this albata comes in the region, and is a disfiguring appearance of flesh;  
et en i a malignes et non malignes;	And there are malignant and non-malignant ones; 
si covient que tu les preignes a I oncine subtil, et les cope et munde toutes, puis met sus coton moilliet en oignement egiptien;	So it is necessary that you prick them with the sharpest needle and cut and cleanse all of them, then put upon it moistened cotton in Egyptian ointment. 
puis le cure d’oignement diafinicon tant qu’il soit sanez.	Then cure it with Diaphicon ointment until it is healed.  
Et se li albathe est maligne, de pute color et depuant, si covient que tu i amenistres cautere.	And if the boil is malignant, of bad color and pus, then you must apply a cautery to it.
Quant tu l’as copeit, et se li albathe est en som la verge, et en ait partie dedens la peil et partie defuer, si covient que tu oste l’albathe qui est dedens premier;	When you have cut it open, and if the albata is in some part within the penis and part outside, then it is necessary that you remove the albata that is inside first; 
et quant il est soudez, si le cure defuer.	and when it is united, care for it well. 
Car quant tu le cures ensamble, si n’est mie asseurez li chiez de la verge qu’il ne soit perciez, et vient noiror et corruption en son la verge et ou coion;	For when you cure it together, make sure the head of the shaft is not pierced, and blackening and corruption come in its shaft and groin. 
si covient chever tout ceu qui est noir et corrumput, puis lie sus l’emplaustre de miel et de farine qui soit fait d’escorce de poumes grenates et de veces, puis le cure d’autres cures tant qu’il soit sanez.	so it is necessary to remove everything that is black and corrupt, then cover it with a plaster of honey and flour made from the bark of pomegranates and veils, then cure it with other dressings until it is healed.  
Et se decorremens de sanc vient, si amenistre le cautere lunaire selonc ceste forme:	And if bleeding occurs, administer the lunar cautery according to this form:
Li cauteres si aide as II dispositions ensamble:	The cauteries help with two kinds of positions together: 
c’est asavoir, au decorrement de sanc, et a la corruption;	that is to say, in the reduction of blood and against corruption.  
et se li chiés de la verge est corrumpus et retrais, si covient que tu boutes ou conduit de la verge une cainne de plonc, et pisse li malaides parmi;	and if the head of the shaft is corrupt and withdrawn, it is necessary that you place a chain of plank in the shaft and let the patient urinate among them.
et quant li pelz iert aerse au chief de la verge qui avient a ces qui n’ont mie esteit circoncis, ou il avient por plaie ou por aposteme, si covient donques que tu l’escorches a I estrument cheveit, tant que li liiens soit desliiez, et soit delivrez li chiez de la verge de toutes pars;	and when the skin is irritated at the head of the stick which happens to those who have not been circumcised, or there is a wound or an abscess, then it is necessary that you scrape it with the instrument until the tendons are loosened, and the head of the penis is delivered from all sides; 
et se c’est grief chose de deviser ceu, si covient que tu l’escorches a I spatumile aucun poc dou chief de la verge et de la peil;	and if it is a difficult thing to discuss these, then it is necessary that you scrape it with the spatula any pox on the head of the penis and the skin; 
puis dessevre belement entre II, et i met I subtil drapeil de lin moilliet an aigue froide, qu’il n’aerse derechief.	then carefully separate them, and put between them the fine linen cloth moistened in cold water, so that it does not irritate;
de la circoncision	Of circumcision
Circoncision n’est mie desliemens de continuation si com les autres plaies;	Circumcision is not a wound of continuity like the others; 
toutevoie quant nos faison ceste oevre de nostre volenteit, et proprement as enfans, si est mestier que nos faisiens la millor oevre, et la plus legiere a salut.	nevertheless, when we do this work of our will, and properly to the children, then it is necessary that we make the best work, and the lightest for salvation. 
Je dis que li ancien ne dirent mie la circoncision de lor enfans, car il n’en usent mie en lor loi, et n’en avons mais que ceu que nos avons aquis par experiment.	I say that the ancients did not say the circumcision of their children, because they do not use it in their law, and we have no more than what we have acquired by experience.
Car j’ai veut la plus grant partie des maistres et des sainors qui faisoient circumcision entor I dal, et as forces, et a tout une novacule;	For I have wanted the most part of the masters and the healers who did circumcision around the Dal, and to all strength, and a whole scalpel; 
si fuioit li keurs car il i a II toiles, et par aventure si cope on celi desus et demore celle desoz.	if it was the shears because there are two of them, and by chance if one cuts above and remains below. 
Or la recovient coper, et est li dolor double, et a la mundification qui est dou dal n’est mie asseuree li pointe dou membre;	or it is necessary to cut again, and the pain is double, and at the purification which is the Dal is not assured the tip of the member;
et a la mundification de l’ungle par aventure eschaipe li fer, et corront l’uevre, et maintes fois naissent ensi qu’il n’ont mestier de mundification et je l’ai veut.	and at the purification of the angle by chance escapes the iron, and the work runs, and many times they are born as if they do not need purification and I have wanted it. 
De la mondification qui est faite as forces a tout le liien de fil ai je troveit la bonteit de l’experiment, car les forces taillent justement ausi bien desus com desoz.	Of the modification that is made by force to all the linen thread I have found the goodness of the experiment, for the forces cut equally well above and below.
Car quant tu presses ta main, si tailles igalment en I tout soul tens;	For when you press your hand, so equally in all soul tension;
mais que li filz soit bien estrois entor lou cuir;	but that the child be well stretched around the skin;
et soit li maniere dou premier ovraige si est que tu faices penser l’enfant, s’il entent, que tu ne li fais fuer que liier le fil entor la verge tant soulement, et pues le fai esjoir en toutes les manieres que tu pues;	and be the manner of the first work that you make the child think, if he understands, that you only force him to tie the thread around the penis and then let him rejoice in all ways that you can;
puis le fai ester entre tes mains tout droit, et repont les forces entre tes mains ou desoz tes piez que li enfes ne les voie, ne aucun des estrumens;	Then make it be between your hands straight, and bring back the forces between your hands or beneath your feet that the child does not see them, nor any of the instruments.  
puis boute ta main a la verge et souffle ou keur, et la trai en haut tant que li chiés de la verge soit ens;	Then put your hand to the shaft and blow where the heart is, and pull it up as long as the head of the shaft is within. 
puis la mundifie bien de l’ordure qui i est assemblee, puis lie le leu signiet d’un fil double, puis la lie desoz I poc a I autre liien;	Then purify it well of the filth that is assembled there, then tie the place with a double thread, then tie it below one point and the other to the other.  
et la tien as II dois par la seconde lieeure au pouchet et au doit indice, et cope entre les II liiens, puis lieve le keur desus hastanment et trai le chief de la verge;	and hold it as II does by the second loop to the pocket and to the index finger, and cut between the two loops, then lift the heart upwards carefully and pull the head of the shaft. 
puis laisse corre le sanc poc et poc, car c’est li muedres;	Then let blood flow drop by drop, for that is the measure.   
et met poudre sus et sus la poudre I drapeil glueit d’un moieuf d’uef cuit destempreit d’aigue rose, confit avec oile roset boin et fres, et lou laisse sus jusc’a l’autre jor, et le cure d’autre cure tant qu’il soit sanez.	and put powder on and on the powder the drape is glued with a yolk of an egg cooked tempered with rose water, mixed with good and fresh rose oil, and let it remain until the next day, and heal it with another healing as long as it is healthy.   
Li forme des forces a la mundification si est ceste:	The form of the forces at the purification is this: 
li dui chiés soient tenves et soient trenchans, et soient li chiés ausi grant com li mainche igalment:	the two arms should be straight and sharp, and the arms as large as the hand equally.  
li error de la mundification si est quant li keurs dedens fuit a l’incision;	The error of purification is when the kernels inside are at the incision. 
donques il covient que tu l’estendes a ton ungle, ainsois que li leus faice aposteme;	Therefore it behooves you to extend it to your fingernail, so that the lesions make an abscess; 
et le cope igalment, et se tu ne lou pues tenir a ton ungle, si le tien as tenailles, et puis le cope.	and cover it equally, and if you cannot hold it on your fingernail, then hold it with tweezers, and then cover it. 
Et s’il trespassent III jors, et ceu qui est desoz la verge est enflez, si le laisse tant que li apostemes chaus soit apaisiez, et l’escorche legierement;	And if they pierce for III days, and that which is below the rod is swollen, leave it until the abscess has calmed and slightly peel it. 
si le cope si com tu pues mues, et te garde de la partie de la verge, ce ne li nuira niant.	then cover it as you can, and keep from the part of the rod, it will harm it nothing.  
Cure donques le leu de choses soudans plaie de poudre, que nos avons dit ou traitier des poudres, et s’on cope dou keur outre mesure, et il va au desus, si ne nuira point;	Therefore cure the place with things softly wound a wound of powder, that we have said or treated of powders, and if one cuts too much, and it goes upward, it will not hurt. 
cure le donques, si com nos avons dit, tant qu’il soit sanez.	Cure therefore, as we have said, until it is healed.  
dou retenement de l’urine	holding back of urine
Li retenue de l’urine si est d’opilation de piere, ou de sanc congeleit, ou de bowe, ou de char nee, ou de semblans choses, que nos avons dit en la division;	The retention of urine is from an obstacle in the stone, or blood clotted, or a bowel, or fatty substance, or similar things, that we have said in the division.  
et se li urine n’est desliie , et tu vois estre la retenue por la piere qui est jai ou col de la vessie, si covient que li malaides soit corbés sus ses genoulz;	And if the urine is not discharged, and you see that the retention is from the stone which is in the bladder or neck of the bladder, then it befits that the patient be bent upon his knees. 
et li soient mis li piez sor le dos, et estende son ventre de la partie desus lou dos, et restraigne li malaides s’alainne tant com il puet;	And let his feet be placed on his back, and stretch his belly from the upper part to his back, and restrain the patient's legs as much as he can.  
et adonques est constrains li colz de la vessie a l’expression de la piere au desus, por coi li urine est desliie e;	and therefore it constrains the neck of the bladder to the expression of the stone above, for which the urine is released. 
et s’elle ne vient, si com nos avons dit, et li malaides sent grant dolor, si covient que tu i aministres extraction a tout l’estrument qui est apelez «siringue», de coi ci est li forme:	and if it does not come, as we have said, and the patient feels great pain, then you must administer to him extraction with all the instrument that is called "syringe", for this is its form:  
et soit d’argent subtilz legiere chevee, si com li penne d’un oiseil;	and be of silver, finely wrought and light, like the feather of a bird; 
et soit li caine d’une palme de lonc et demie, et soit subtilz au chief.	and be the shaft a palm long and a half, and be finely wrought at the head.  
Et li maniere de l’issue de l’urine si est que tu pren I fil double, et lie au chief I poc de laine ou de couton, et boute le chief dou fil dedens la siringue;	And the manner of the urine's discharge is that you take a double thread, and tie to the head one piece of wool or cotton, and put the end of the thread inside the syringe;
et cope la superfluiteit de la lainne et le boute jusc’au chief de la siringue, puis oint la siringue d’oile ou de burre et d’aubin d’uef, et fai seoir le malaide sus I siege, et li arose la vessie et la verge d’oile moiste et d’oile d’olive et d’aigue tede;	and cut the superfluity of the wool and bring it up to the head of the syringe, then anoint the syringe with oil or butter and rue leaf, and make the patient sit on the seat, and raise the bladder and penis with moist oil and olive oil and warm water;  
puis met legierement la siringue en la verge, tant qu’elle viegne a la racine de la verge, puis double la verge desus devers la boude;	then gently put the syringe on the penis, until it reaches the root of the penis, then fold the penis above towards the bud; 
puis boute la siringue avant jusc’a la vessie, et la sente li malaides venir jusc’a la chose vuide, et ceu n’est mie fait selonc cest ordre fuer que por ceu que li conduis ou elle vait est tors;	then push the syringe forward to the bladder, and feel the patient's feeling coming up to the empty thing, and this is not done according to this order except for those who lead or where it goes is twisted;  
puis estent le fil a tout la laine poc et poc, et li urine en suit la laine, puis l’estrai fuer, et fai corre l’urine;	then stretch the thread all over the wool and pull it, and the urine follows the wool, then remove it, and make sure the urine is correct; 
et rencomence la siringue tant que li vessie soit vuidie, et soit aligiez li malaides.	And restart the syringe until the bladder is emptied, and the patient is aligned. 
des maladies de la vessie	of bladder ailments
Quant escorcheures ou sanc vient en la vessie, ou porriture i est assemblee, et tu i vues distiller aigues et medicines, si fai a tout l’estrument qui est apellé «clepsedre», et c’est li forme:	When sores or blood come in the bladder, or rot is assembled there, and you see them distilling sharp waters and medicines, do as to all the instrument that is called “clepsedre,” and this is its form:
Elle est close, et si a III pertus:	It is closed, and if to the III perts:  
II d’une part, et I d’autre, si com tu vois;	II on one side, and I on the other, as you see; 
et li leus chevez par coi li medicine cort soit telz qu’il estoupe bien la verge sens adition, si c’on em puisse traire la moistor, et bouter quant mestier est;	and the eyes cover because by this the medication is such that it stops well the member without addition, if one can draw out the moisture and push when necessary; 
et quant tu vues giter tes medicines en la vessie, met le chief dou keusteur en la moistor, et trai au traiant qui est ens;	and when you see fitting your medicines in the bladder, put the chief of the catheter into the moisture, and pull with the pulling which is inside; 
si trairas la moistor au kesteur, et puis reboute fort le traiant ens;	if you draw the moisture to the catheter, and then push firmly back the pulling inside;
si entrera li moistors ens, et venra a la vessie maintenant, si que li malaides la sentira;	if the moisture will enter inside, and come to the bladder now, so that the patient will feel it; 
et c’est li forme dou clistere subtil dont on clisterize la vessie:	and this is the form of the subtle clyster with which one cleanses the bladder:   
si est ci:	If it is here: 
Et est d’argent ou d’archaut, et est li chiés plus haut;	And is of silver or of arch-wood, and is the head higher. 
et desoz a I sein ou li liiens chiet;	and below to the breast where the bones fall;  
puis pren une vessie de mouton et i met la moistor dont tu vues clisterizer la vessie, puis la lie entre les II seins forment d’un boin fil double, et chaufe I poc celle moistor sus le feu;	then take a sheep bladder and put the moisture that you see to be used for enemas in it, then tie it between the two breasts with a good doubled thread, and heat that moisture on fire; 
puis boute le chief dou clistere en la verge, puis estrain ta main sus la vessie a tout la moistor avenanment, tant que li malaides sente que celle moistor est jai venue a la vessie;	then put the head of the enema into the rectum, then strain your hand on the bladder to all the moisture coming out, until the patient feels that that moisture has come to the bladder; 
et se tu n’as la vessie, si pren une piece de parchemin, et en fai I cercle, et le perce rondement entor;	and if you do not have a bladder, then take a piece of parchment, and make it into a circle, and pierce it roundly through;
puis boute I fil fort en ces pertus, puis assemble le cercle si com on assemble I dal, et met dedens ceu que tu vues d’oile et de moistor et d’aigue, et le lie en l’estrument;	then put a strong thread through these perforations, then assemble the circle as one assembles a hoop, and put inside it what you want of oil and moisture and water, and tie it in the instrument; 
et fai si com tu as fait de la vessie, de presser a ta main tant que li moistor veigne a la vessie.	and do as you have done of the bladder, to press with your hand until the moisture comes to the bladder. 
de la piere	of the stone
Nos avons jai dit en la division les manieres de piere, et l’estraction ensamble medicines;	We have said in the division the manners of stone, and the extraction together with medicines; 
et ai dit la difference entre la piere enjanree as rains, et toz les signes, et en queil piere on doit ovrer de taille;	and we have said the difference between the stone engendered as rain, and all the signs, and in what stone one must work of cutting; 
et en la vessie, et en la verge;	and in the bladder, and in the penis; 
et je le vos dirai apertement et briément.	and I will tell it to you clearly and briefly.  
Je dis que li piere qui est enjanree en la vessie si avient plus sovent as enfans, et c’est signe que li aigue saut de la vessie semblans a aigue en sa subtiliteit;	I say that the stone which is engendered in the bladder so often happens to children, and it is a sign that the water leaps from the bladder seeming like water in its subtlety; 
et i apert harene, et graite li malaides sa verge, et li pent maintes fois, et puis enroidist;	and it appears hareng [unclear], and grieves the patient his penis, and it hurts him many times, and then becomes red; 
et a mout de ces saut li fondemens;	and to many of these jumps the foundations. 
et est legiere li sanation des enfans jusqu’il ont IIII ans, et est mout grief en viellars, et est as jones moiene, a ces qui sont entre jonesce et viellece;	and it is light healing in children until they have four years, and it is very grievous in old people, and it is as moderate, to those who are between youth and old age; 
et est li cure plus legiere de ces qui ont la piere grans, que de ces qui l’ont petite.	and the cure is lighter for those who have large stones than for those who have small ones. 
Et quant nos venons a la cure, si couvient premier mundifier le malaide per clistere, por traire tout le fiens qui est as intestines.	And when we come to the cure, it is necessary first to purify the patient by clyster, in order to draw out all the phlegm that is in the intestines.
Car il encombre aucune fois a querir la piere.	For it often hinders seeking the stone.
Puis prenez le malaide par les piez, et lou deboutez et movez au desoz, si que li piere dessende au parfont de la vessie, et saille aucune fois dou leu haut;	Then take the patient by the feet, and loosen and move them downwards so that the stone descends to the bottom of the bladder, and comes out sometimes from its high place; 
puis le fai seoir entre tes mains appareilliet, et ses mains soient desoz ses cuisses, si que li vessie soit toute declinans aval;	then make him sit between your hands apported, and his hands be under his thighs so that the bladder be entirely declining down;
puis la quier et la touche dedens;	then press and touch inside; 
se tu sens la piere en l’espaice, si te haste maintenant de taillier sus la piere.	if you feel the stone in the space, then hasten now to cut above the stone. 
Et s’elle ne chiet au touchier dou tout, si moille ton doi indice d’oile de la main senestre, se li malaides est enfes, ou ton doi moien, se li malaides est jovencelz acomplis;	And if it does not fall upon touching at all, then moisten your index finger with oil from the left hand, if the patient is a child, or your middle finger, if the patient is an adult.  
et le boute en son fondement, et quier la piere, et quant tu la sens a ton doi, si l’amoine au col de la vessie;	And put it in its base, and seize the stone, and when you feel it with your right hand, then move it to the bladder neck. 
puis presse sus a ton doi, et la boute au defuer lai ou tu vues taillier.	Then press upon your right, and put it out to the outside where you wish to cut. 
Et comande au ministre qu’il presse la vessie a sa main, et li comande qu’il estende a sa main destre les coions en haut, et a sa main senestre oste le cuir qui est desoz les coions en la partie ou on fait la taille;	And command the minister that he presses the bladder with his hand, and command him to extend with his right hand the testicles upwards, and with his left hand remove the skin which is under the testicles in the part where one makes the incision. 
puis i boute le spatumile copant, de coi ce est li forme:	Then put the spatula cuttingly, of which this is the form:  
Et fent entre ceu qui est entre les coions et le fondement, ne mie em mileu mais au costeit de la naige senestre;	And make between those who are between the testicles and the base, neither in the middle but at the side of the left hip. 
et soit drois sus la piere, et tes dois soit adés ou fondement, et soit li taille dou traver si qu’ele soit large par defuer, et dedens estroite, selonc la quantiteit de la piere, ne mie trop grans;	and be straight on the stone, and your thighs should be even or foundation, and let the hips be wide outside so that it is wide from the outside and narrow inside, according to the quantity of the stone, not too big; 
par aventure la presse si li dois qui est ou fondement, qu’elle saut fuer sens travail;	by adventure the press if the thighs which are or foundation, that she leap be without work;  
et saiches qu’il i a teil piere ou il a angles, et marges:	and know that there is such stone where it has angles, and margins: 
si est griés a issir;	if it is grated to issue;
et si a teil qui est souez, semblans a une glant, et reonde, dont li issue est legiere.	and if there is such which is smooth, seeming like a gland, and round, whose issue is light. 
A celi donques ou il a angles et marge, fai la taille plus grant;	To this one therefore where it has angles and margins, make the hips larger;
et s’elle ne saut, si covient que tu estraignes sus as tenailles qui sont ausi com une lime au chief, por mues estraindre la piere si qu’elle n’eschaipe;	and if it does not come out, it is necessary that you extract it with tongs which are like a file at the head, so as to tighten the stone so that it does not escape. 
ou tu boute desoz li I estrument subtil corbé au chief;	or you insert underneath it the subtle curved instrument at the head.  
et se tu ne la pues engignier ensi, si eslarge I poc lou pertus, et se li sans decort, si l’estrainche de vitriole;	and if you cannot engage it this way, then enlarge the hole and if the stone is covered, strain with vitriol.   
et s’il i a plus d’une piere, si boute premier la plus grant au col de la vessie, puis cope sus, puis le trai fuer, et les petites aprés s’il en i a plusors.	and if there is more than one stone, first insert the largest one at the neck of the bladder, then cut on top, and then remove it with the instruments, and the smaller ones afterwards if there are more. 
Et s’elle est mout grans, si la covient soier, et faire plus grant plaie.	And if it is very large, it must be cauterized, and make a larger wound.
Car II choses avienent au malaide:	For these things happen to the patient:
ou il muert, ou li urine vient adés par lai que li leus ne puet souder;	either he dies, or the urine comes back through the place where the lesion cannot be sutured.  
mais toutevoie t’efforce dou traire, ou dou debrisier as tenailles, tant que tu la traies par pieces;	But nonetheless, you must try to remove it, or break it up with the tongs, as long as you remove it in pieces.
et quant tu as acomplit ton oevre, si emple la plaie d’encens et d’aloe et de sanc de dragon, et l’estraint, et met par sus I drapeil moilliet en oile et en vin, ou en oile et en aigue rose et aigue froide, por apaisier l’aposteme chaut;	And when you have completed your work, then apply to the wound incense and aloe and dragon's blood, and hold it, and put on top a soft cloth in oil and wine, or in oil and rose water and cold water, to soothe the hot abscess.  
puis resovine le malaide sus son col, et ne desliier lou lien jusc’au tier jor.	Then rest the patient on their neck, and do not loosen the bandage until the third day. 
Et quant tu le desliies, si arose mout bien lou leu d’oile et d’aigue, puis le cure d’oignement dyafinicon et d’oignement basilicon, tant qu’il soit sanez.	And when you set it, so well raised its place with oil and water, then the cure of ointment diaphicon and ointment basilcon, until it be healed.
Et se apostemes chaus vient en la plaie et corrosions, et congelemens de sanc en la vessie, et soit par ceu retenue li urine, qui est conue en teil maniere que sans saut avec l’urine:	And if an abscess comes in the wound and corrosion, and blood clotting in the bladder, and due to this the urine is held back, which is known in such a manner that without jumping with the urine: 
boutes donques ton doi en la plaie, et estrai celui sanc, car s’il i remaint, si corront la vessie, et la porrit;	Therefore drain your wound well and extract that blood, because if it remains, then the bladder will corrode and be spoiled.
puis leve la plaie d’aigue et d’aisil et de seil, et li aide en toutes les manieres que tu seis, tant qu’il soit sanez;	Then wash the wound with water and ash and salt, and help him in all the ways that you know, until he is healed. 
et covient que toutes les oures que tu le cures, que tu li lie les II cuisses, et assemble les medicines sus le leu.	And it is necessary that all the hours that you cure him, that you bind his two thighs, and apply the medicines on the place. 
Et se li piere est petite, et ele est ou conduit de la verge, et fichie ens, et li urine ne puet issir;	And if the stone is small, and it is or carried by the penis, and fixed in there, and the urine cannot flow out; 
si le cure de ceu que je dis ainsois, que tu lou tailles maintes fois, est on escusez de la taille per ceste cure.	if you cure it of what I say thus, that you cut it many times, and one excuses the cutting of the stone by this cure. 
Je ai ja ce proveit ensi.	I have already proven this thus.
Pren I foret de fer selonc ceste forme et soit a III angles fichiees en I tison:	Take I a piece of iron according to this form and let it be three-angled shaped in one stick.
puis pren I fil et lou lie entor la verge desoz la piere, si qu’ele ne puist venir arrier en la vessie;	then take a thread and tie it around the penis below the stone, so that it cannot come back into the bladder.
puis boute le foret en la verge legierement, tant qu’il viegne a la piere;	then put the borer into the penis gently, until it reaches the stone. 
et torne le foret a ta main en la piere poc et poc, tant que tu puisses percier la piere d’autre part;	and turn the borer in your hand on the stone peck and peck, until you can feel the stone from the other side. 
si venra tantost li urine, puis presse ta main sus ceu qui est demorez de la piere qui est dedens la verge.	if the urine comes then press your hand on what remains of the stone which is inside the penis.  
Si est tantost brisie, et saut fuer avec l’urine, et est garis li malaides;	It is then immediately broken, and jumps out with urine, and the patient heals. 
et se tu ne pues ce faire por aucune chose qui le deffent, si lie I fil desoz la piere et I autre desus, puis fent la verge endroit la piere entre les II liiens, puis l’estrai fuer, et deslie lou liien, et mundifie lou sanc congeleit qui est en la plaie;	And if you cannot do this for any reason that prevents it, then tie one thread under the stone and the other above, then make the stick in the right place in the stone between the two threads, then pull it out forcefully, and untie the threads, and cleanse the congealed blood that is in the wound; 
et le cure tant qu’il soit sanez.	And care for it until it is healed.  
de la piere des femmes	of the stone of women
Poc avient que piere soit enjanree en femmes, et s’il avient aucune fois, si est li cure grief, et est deffendut por III choses:	There happens that stones are embedded in women, and if it happens once, the cure is grievous, and it is forbidden for three things: 
l’une est que per aventure li femme est vierge;	One is that perchance the woman is a virgin;  
et li seconde est c’on ne puet trover femme bien saichant qui se descuevre as mires, meismement quant elle est caste.	And the second is that one cannot find a well-knowing woman who will reveal her privates, even when she is chaste. 
Et li tierce maniere si est que par aventure on ne puet trover femme bien saichant en cest art de mains;	And the third manner is that perchance one cannot find a woman well-knowing in this art of hands;  
et li quarte maniere si est que li piere de la femme si est plus em parfont que li piere de l’ome, por coi il i couvient faire plus parfonde taille, et grant paour i a. Et se necessitez semont a ceu, si covient que tu preignes une mieresse bien sachant, et a poines la trueve on, et se tu n’en trueves, point si quier I caste mire subtil;	and the fourth manner is that the stone of the woman is more embedded than the stone of the man, so it is necessary to make a deeper incision, and great fear there is. And if necessity demands this, then you must take a wise midwife, and put the truth on her, and if you cannot find one, point no matter; I cast mire subtle. 
et li presente une baile bien saige en la vie des femmes, ou une femme qui saiche une partie de l’art, et li comande qu’ele faice ceu que tu li comandes de l’inquisicion de la piere;	and present her a wise woman in the life of women, or a woman who knows part of the art, and command her to do what you command her about the incision of the stone. 
et regarde mout bien se li femme est vierge:	and look very well if the woman is a virgin: 
adonques li covient bouter son doit ou fondement et querir la piere;	then it is necessary to put her foot or foundation and seek the stone.
et s’ele la trueve, si la constraigne desoz son doit, et li recomande qu’elle boute son doit ou con la malaide, et quiere et presse sa main senestre sus la vessie forment.	and if she finds it, she confines her under her foot, and recommends to her that she put her foot or on the sick woman, and seeks and presses her left hand on the bladder forming.  
S’elle la trueve, si covient qu’elle la mueve de greit en greit des l’entree de la vessie jusque desoz, tant qu’elle viegne a la racine de la cuisse;	If she finds it, then it is necessary that she move it from great to great from the entrance of the bladder to below, until it comes to the root of the thigh;  
puis cope sus la piere en la racine de la cuisse encontre le mileu dou con, lai ou il est mues apparilliet, et sent la piere en celle partie;	then cut above the stone at the root of the thigh against the middle of the cone, where it is moved appeared, and feel the stone in that part; 
et ne mueve son doi desus la piere ou desoz, et soit li taille au premier petite;	and do not move his two above the stone or below, and let the tail be at first small;  
puis boute lou rait en la taille, se tu sens la piere si acroi la plaie tant que li piere puisse issir fuer, et saiches que maintes manieres de pieres sont:	then push the root into the tail, if you feel the stone so close to the wound as long as the stone can come out further, and know that many kinds of stones are: 
c’est a savoir, petites et grans et aspres et souez, longes et reondes, et qui ont rains.	that is to say, small and large and rough and smooth, long and round, and which have veins.  
si saiches les semblances por savoir l’issue.	If you know the likenesses to know the outcome.
Et se li sans te vaint, si met au leu vitriole broiet, et li tien une houre tant que li sans soit estainchiez;	And if the stone does not come out, then put powdered vitriol, and hold it for an hour until the wound is stained; 
puis revien a ton ovraige, tant que li piere soit fuer, et aies des estrumens que je t’ai dit en l’estraction de la piere as homes por toi aidier en ton oevre;	Then return to your work, as long as the stone remains, and have the instruments that I told you about in the extraction of stones for men to aid you in your work; 
et se li sans te vaint, et c’est de l’artere qui est copee, si met la poudre sus le leu et l’estrain de tentes et de bendelz, et ne rencomencier plus ceu, et laisse la piere et ne la traire mie, que par aventure morroit li malaide;	And if the artery does not stop bleeding, and it is from the artery that is cut, then place the powder on the wound and strain with bandages, and do not begin again those actions, and leave the stone and do not milk it, lest the patient die by chance;
puis cure la plaie.	Then treat the wound. 
Et quant li chalor dou sanc est apaisie, et li leus porrist, si revien a ton ovraige, tant que li piere soit fuer.	And when the heat of the blood is appeased, and the eyes are closed, then return to your work, as long as the stone is firm.
de hernie carnouse	of fleshy hernia
Ramice aquouse n’est autre chose que assemblee de moistor ou blanc syfac, qui est desoz lou keur des coions, que contient l’uef;	Ramic aquouse is nothing else but a gathering of moisture or white substance found in the yolk of the eggs. 
et est apelez «syfac», et aucune fois est proprement en la toile de l’uef, si c’on cuide que ce soit I autre oef;	and it is called "syfac," and sometimes it is properly in the membrane of the egg, if one believes that it is another egg.  
et c’est li cuir dou coion entre lou blanc syfac que nos avons dit;	And it is the skin of the yolk between the white syfac that we have said; 
et ceu n’avient se poc non.	and this did not happen at all. 
Et li generation de cest ramice si est de foibleteit que vient as coions, et est espandue celle matiere.	And the generation of this root is of weakness that comes to the testicles, and that matter is spread.
Et aucune fois si vient de percussion sus les coions, et ceste moistor si a maintes colors:	And never if it comes from percussion on the joints, and this moisture has many colors:  
ou c’est color declinans a jaunice, ou c’est sans rouge, ou noir, ou aquous blans, et ce avient plus;	or it is yellowing in color, or it is red, or black, or white and watery, and this happens more: 
et ce sont li signe de conoistre ceste assemblee, car s’elle est ou blanc syfac que nos avons dit, si est li apostemes reons, I poc lonc si com li figure d’un oef, et n’apert mie li coions, car il a moistor tout entor.	and these are the signs of knowing this assembly, because if it is white as we have said, then the abscess is ripe, and it appears long like the shape of an egg, and does not open the joints because it has moisture all around.
Et s’il a moistor en la propre toile, si est li apostemes reons avec une partie de l’uef, et por ceu pense on que c’est uns autres oef;	And if it has moisture in its own cloth, the abscess is covered with a piece of the egg, and for this reason they think that it is another egg; 
et se li moistor est entre le cuir des coions et le blanc syfac, si le sent om bien;	And if the moisture is between the skin of the scrotum and the white tunic, then one feels it well; 
donques quant tu vues savoir la color de la moistor, si esprueve a tout l’intromissoire quarreit, de coi li forme est ci devant.	Therefore when you want to know the color of the moisture, carefully probe the entire intro-mittor, because its form is as described above. 
Selonc ceu donques qui vient aprés l’intromissoire, juge de ceu qui est dedens.	According to what then comes after the introducer, judge of what is inside.
Et quant nos la curons par fer, si covient que li malaides soit sainiez selonc som pooir et la repletion de son cors;	And when we cure it with iron, it is necessary that the patient be healthy according to our power and the fullness of his body; 
puis le sovine sus son dos, sus une chose un poc haute, et met desoz lui mout de drapelz;	then he lies on his back, on a thing slightly high, and puts under him many cloths; 
puis sié sus sa senestre, et comande au ministre qu’il sié a destre, et estende la verge a l’un des II costelz dou keur des coions;	then he sits on his left, and commands the minister to sit on his right, and extend the instrument to one of the two ribs near the scrotum; 
puis pren le spatumile leit, et cope le cuir des coions parmi leu dou lonc jusque delez lou poignil, et soit ta fendure toute droite en devisant le cuir des coions jusc’a syfac blanc, et l’escorche subtilment selonc tom pooir;	Then take the spatula, and cut the skin of the head among their length until near the point of the elbow, and let your cut be straight when separating the skin of the head up to the white part, and gently peel it according to your power.  
puis perce lou syfac plain d’aigue a I large pertus, et estrai toute l’aigue, et puis met tes oncines, et estent lou syfac amont;	Then pierce the white part with water to the wide hole, and extract all the water, and then put your bandages, and cover the white part. 
et ne touchier le keur des coions, mais que le syfac soulement;	And do not touch the skin of the head, but only the white part; 
cope tout ou par pieces meismement le costeit de lui subtil, que se tu ne le copes bien saigement, si revenra li aigue;	Cut all or in parts evenly the edge of it subtly, that if you do not cut it wisely, the water will return. 
et se l’uef saut fuer a ton oevre, si le ramoinne en son leu quant tu avras acomplit l’uevre dou syfac;	And if the egg sac were in your work, then reset it in its place when you have completed the work of the white part. 
puis assemble les II leivres dou keur des coions a une costure, puis le cure si com les autres plaies, tant qu’il soit sanez.	Then join the two books of the heart to one seam, then treat it like other wounds, until it is healed. 
Et se tu trueves l’uef corromput d’autre maladie, si covient que tu lies les vasselz que sont suspensoire, en doutant le decorrement de sanc;	And if you find the egg corrupted by another disease, then it is necessary that you tie the vessels that are suspended, suspecting the flow of blood. 
puis cope le coion a tout le suspensoire, et estrai l’uef, et le cure si com nos avons dit.	Then cut the testicle to all the suspender, and extract the egg, and treat it as we have said. 
Et se aigue est assemblee en II parties ensamble, saiches que ce sont II ramices;	And if the water is assembled in two parts together, know that they are two branches;  
si cope l’autre partie si com tu as fait la premiere igalment, puis essue lou sanc, et met en la plaie lainne moillie en oile roset;	so cut the other part in the same way as you did the first one, then wipe away the blood, and put in the wound linen soaked in rose oil; 
et met defuer autre laine moillie en vin et en oile, et met sus les II coions, et met desus drapelz doublés, et le lie sus a tout le liien qui est selonc ceste forme:	and put more wool soaked in wine and oil on top, and place the two cushions on top, and put doubled cloth above it, and tie it up over the whole linen according to this form: 
Puis pren II drapelz, et les emple de laine charpie selonc ceste semblance et soient assemblez par cousture en la gorle des braies, et li uns des chiés preigne sus le fondement jusc’au dos, et li autres a la partie dou poignil;	Then take two cloths, and use wool padding according to this appearance and be assembled by stitching at the waist of the breeches, and one of the arms reaches over the foundation up to the back, and the other to the armpit part; 
et li autre dui chief sus les II angres, et soit toute assemblee li restreinture en la boucle dou braier;	and the other two sides over the two angles, and let the whole restraint be assembled at the waist of the breeches;  
et aucune fois est medicinee ceste ramice de cautere en leu de taille de fer, et est que tu preignes I cautere cultellaire subtil, et cope le cuir des coions, et soit eschaufez si com nos avons dit, si que li syfac blanc que contient l’aigue est descovers;	And at no time is this ramice of fire cautery a medicine in the place of an iron one, and it is that you take the cautery with a thin knife, and cut the skin of the cushions, and let it be heated as we have said, so that the white syfac which contains the water is exposed;  
si pren lou cautere selonc ceste forme, et perce celui syfac as oncines, et l’escorche a cest subtil cautere chaut:	If you take the cautery according to this form, and pierce it in the manner as shown, and the eschar to this subtle cautery hot.  
Et lou cope en toutes les manieres que tu pues, tant que tu esraiches tout;	And the cut in all ways that you can, until you have removed everything.  
et garde que li feus ne touche l’uef;	And guard that the fire does not touch the eye;  
et saiches que ceste oevre est plus salve;	And know that this work is more helpful; 
et mues gardans de decorrement de sanc, et muedres que li ovraiges de taille;	And moving guards from the bloodletting and moves that the works of size;  
et se nulle chose te fait contraire, ou aposteme chaus ou decorremens de sanc ou autre chose, si cure ce qui te fait contraire, selonc ceu qui est devant dit.	And if no thing makes you contrary, or abscess heals or bloodletting or another thing, so cure that which makes you contrary, according to what is said before. 
Et se li malaides est paourous, et ne vuet atendre cest ovraige por son horribleteit, si amenistre perforation, si com je te di, et est que quant tu es bien certains par les significations que nos avons dit que ramice aquouse est lai, si fai seoir le malaide sus I siege leveit;	And if the patient is fearful, and does not want to endure this work for its horror, so administer perforation as I tell you, and it is that when you are well certain by the significations that we have said that watery root is there, so make the patient sit upon the raised seat; 
pues perce l’aposteme an la partie desoz a tout le spatumile large, et met la perforation dou lonc dou cors;	Then pierce the abscess at the part below to all the spatula wide, and put the perforation through the long of the body; 
et soit larges li pertus, si que toute li aigue corre fuer;	and let the openings be wide, so that all the water runs out. 
puis met coton sus le leu, et le lie, et laisse por corre le remenant de l’aigue, puis le cure tant que li plaie soit sanee;	then put cotton on the spot, and bind it, and let the remaining water run out, then treat it until the wound is healed.  
et se li blainche toile ne laisse issir l’aigue en la bouche de la plaie, si covient que tu i boutes une penne ou l’estrument dont on trait l’aigue des ydropiques, de coi li forme est ci devant;	and if the white cloth does not allow the water to flow out of the mouth of the wound, then you should pour into it a pipe or the instrument used for draining the water from hydrophics, whose shape is described earlier; 
et eslarge I poc la plaie, et saiches que li aigue revient, et est assemblee aprés VI mois ou enqui entor, et quant elle est assemblee si com devant, et ensi passera li malaides ses jors.	and enlarge the opening of the wound, and know that the water returns, and it is assembled after six months or until then, and when it is assembled like before, and thus the patient will pass his days.  
de l’aposteme des coions	of the abscess of the genitals
Saiches que en la section de ceste ramice a paor em plusors dispositions, por coi il me semble que mues vaut c’on la laisse;	Know that in the section of this branch there is fear in many situations, for which I think it is better to leave it.
et je vos dirai l’ovraige et les semblances de l’aposteme.	and I will tell you the work and the appearances of the abscess. 
Je dis donques que maint aposteme vienent ou cors, et meismement as coions;	I say therefore that many abscesses come to the body, and also to the genitals; 
et c’est par mout de cas.	and this is by many causes.  
C’est a savoir par superfluiteit aigre et ague, qui est espandue as coions, ou de percussion;	That is to say by excess of sour and hot humors which are spread to the genitals, or from blows; 
et est li color de l’aposteme selonc la color dou cors;	and the color of the abscess is according to the color of the body;
et ne trueve point de dolor, et est aposteme grief;	and does not find pain, and is a grievous abscess;
et par aventure est uns apostemes griés paourous et pierous, et de fuxe color, et aucune fois vient de nout d’artere, ou d’enfleure de voine.	and by adventure are some grievous abscesses pale and bloody, and of a dark color, and sometimes comes from the outside of an artery, or from the swelling of a vein.
Quant c’est par nout d’artere, si est conus par la disposition d’aposteme chaut, quant tu la presses a tes dois;	When it is from an artery, then it is known by the arrangement of the hot abscess when you press it with your fingers;
et ne covient mie que tu i touches.	and you should not touch it at all. 
Cil qui est fais d’enfleure de voine est conus par sa disposition a l’expression dou touchement des dois, et puet om bien faire la taille sus ceste semblance, et sus les autres chars;	He who is made of the swelling of the vein is known by his disposition to the feeling of the fingers, and one can well do the incision on this semblance, and on the other parts. 
et est que tu cope lou keur des coions, puis estent l’uef en haut, et le trai fuer dou blanc syfac, et delivre lou suspensoire de toutes pars de l’uef.	and is that you cut the root of the cones, then being the egg on top, and the trail from the white this way, and deliver the suspension from all sides of the egg.  
Se li uef est ja sodez avec ces chars nees, si covient donques que tu traies l’uef, et lou cope;	If the egg is already soldered with these newly formed parts, then it is necessary that you pull out the egg, and cut it.  
et s’il est aers au syfac, ou en ceu qui est dedens les vasselz, si covient que tu delivre toute celle tenve, et la cope reondement.	and if it is in the way of the white, or what is inside the vessels, then it is necessary that you deliver all that vein, and cut it roundly.   
Et se li naissance de la char est ou leu derrier, si covient que tu la copes toute, et estrai l’uef, si com nous avons dit.	And if the birth of the cartilage is or its rear, then it is necessary that you cut it all, and extract the egg, as we have said.
Et quant tes ovraiges est acomplis, si emple la plaie de laine moillie en oile roset et en vin, puis le cure d’autres cures tant qu’il soit sanez.	And when your works are accomplished, then use the wound of wool moistened in rose oil and wine, then care for it with other cares until it is healed.
de l’aposteme des coions	of the abscess of the genitals
Cis est uns apostemes envoloupez d’un envoloupement semblant a I borjon, avec le mollifiement des coions, et se muet li malaides griement quant il vait;	This is an abscess enveloped in an envelope resembling the yolk, with the softening of the cones, and the patient moves badly when he goes.  
et li cure de ceste maladie si est bien pres ausi paourouse com ceste ci devant, et toutevoie nos vos dirons l’ovraige de li, selonc ceu que li ancien firent.	and the cure of this disease is as perilous as the one before, and nevertheless we will tell you the work of it, according to what the ancients did. 
Il covient que tu faices seoir lou malaide sus I siege aleveit, puis li boute le suspensoire des coions aval a tes dois, a tout le vasseil qui sont prochien a la verge, et les teigne li maistres, et les estende forment;	It is necessary that you make the patient sit on an elevated seat, then put the suspensory of the genitals down to your two hands, over all the vessels which are near the penis, and hold them tight, and stretch them. 
puis cope au spatumile trenchant large dou traver endroit les vasselz, tant qu’il soient descovert, et puis escorche de chescune part, si com nos avons dit en l’estraction des arteres qui sont en temples;	then cut with the sharp spatula through the middle of the vessels, until they are exposed, and then scrape from each side, as we have said in the extraction of the arteries which are in the temples;
puis i fiche une aguille ou il ait I fil double, et le lie au premier leu ou li vis est venue, et le lie derechief a l’autre chief;	then insert an awl where there is the double thread, and tie it at the first place where the vein came from, and tie it straight to the other end; 
puis les cope em mileu droitement, selonc la longesce dou cors, et en trai les moistors corrumpues;	then cut them in the middle directly, according to the length of the body, and remove the corrupted moisture;
puis cure la plaie si com les autres ou on enjanre bowe, si que aucun vassel chiecent que norrissent l’un des coions;	then cure the wound like the others where one avoids bowing, so that no vessel spills which nourishes one of the corners; 
car par ceu n’i vient point de mal, et se a toz les vasselz vient vis, si covient traire les coions a tout les vasselz;	for by these there comes no harm, and if all the vessels come alive, it is necessary to drain the corners of all the vessels; 
si que li oes ne perde son norrissement por l’incision des vasselz, et sechent et ne se puient aidier.	so that the eye does not lose its nourishment due to the incision of the vessels, and dries up and cannot be aided. 
de la routure dou syfac	of the rupture of the hip
