Li avenemens de ceste ramice si est par la section que vient ou syfac, ou l’estension sus le ventre en la partie des angres, por coi li intestine dessendent de celle routure a l’un des coions;	The happenings of this ramic are thus by the section that comes or is placed there, or by the extension on the belly in the area of the angles, for which the intestines descend from that rupture to one of the corners; 
et ceste routure est ou dou syfac, ou de l’estension de li, et vienent ces II manieres de mout de causes:	and this rupture is either where the section is, or from the extension of it, and these two ways of much cause:
ou de percussion, ou de saut, ou de braire, ou de levement de grief faix, et par semblans choses;	or of percussion, or of jump, or of wrestling, or of lifting heavy loads, and similar things.  
et li signes quant c’est de l’estension dou syfac, si est qu’il avient poc et poc, en lonc tens, et ne vient mie soudainnement;	and the signs when it is of extension of the staff, if they have pock and pock, in long time, and come not suddenly.  
et est li apostemes igalz jusque vers le parfont, por ceu que li syfac apresse l’intestine.	and are the abscesses even until towards the middle, because the pus comes forward quickly with the intestines. 
Et li signes est quant c’est de la section dou syfac, qu’elle fait venir a l’encomencement dolor soudaine, et est li apostemes divers apparans, desoz le cuir pres, et c’est por l’issue de l’intestine et le cors au defuer dou syfac.	And the signs are when it is of the section of the skin, that it brings at the beginning a sudden pain, and there are diverse appearances of abscesses, under the skin near, and this is for the issue of the intestine and the body to the outside of the skin.
Et aucune fois dessent li cirbes avec l’intestine, et est retenus enqui, et fait grant dolor soffrir au malaide, meismement quant il est pressez.	And sometimes the intestines are drawn into the wound, and are held in there, and cause great pain to suffer the patient, even when it is pressed.
Et en ces cures de fer a paor, por coi il s’en covient eschuir.	And in these cures of iron there is fear, for which it behoves one to shun.
Et li maniere de l’ovraige si est que tu comande ou malaide qu’il ramoine l’intestine a sa main au dedens en la plaie, s’il i puet rentreir;	And the manner of the operation is that you command the patient to bring the intestine into its place with his hand within the wound, if it can enter. 
puis soit sovinez sus son col. entre tes mains, et lieve les cuixes;	then be supported on its neck between your hands, and lift the hips; 
puis estent le keur au desus, et cope tout le cuir des coions dou lonc;	then extend the heart upward, and cut all the skin of the groin long;  
puis boute dedens les leivres de la taille uncines selonc ceu que tu en as mestier por ovrir la plaie, et soit telz que li oes em puist issir;	then put inside the folds of the waist splints according to what you need to open the wound, and such that the pus may issue forth.
puis escorche lou syfac que est desoz lou cuir des coions, tant que li blans syfac dur soit descovers de toutes pars;	then scrape the pus that is beneath the skin of the groin, until the white pus is uncovered on all sides;
puis boute ton doi indice en ceu qui enseut lou coion, en ceu qui est entre lou blanc syfac qui est desoz lou cuir de l’uef, et entre lou secont syfac, et depart ceu qui est derrier l’uef, et entre lou secont syfac;	then put your two index fingers into that which follows the groin, where it is between the white pus that is beneath the skin of the buttock and between the second pus, and depart what is behind the buttock and between the second pus;
et pues muef a la main destre dedens lou keur des coions, et estent lou blanc syfac en haut a ta main senestre, et lieve l’uef a tout lou syfac devers la taille;	and then move the hand to the right inside the heart of the coins, and are white siyac in high to your left hand, and lift the egg to all the siyac towards the waist; 
et comande au ministre qu’il estende l’uef en haut, et deslie ceu qui est aers derrier le liement;	and command the minister that he extend the egg on high, and untie those who are behind the binding; 
et quier a tes dois s’il a point de l’intestine envoloupeit ou blanc syfac dur, et se tu en trueves aucune chose, si le boute au ventre desoz;	and  ask at his two if he has any intestine enveloped or white siyac hard, and if you find nothing of that kind, put it in the belly below;
puis pren une aguille ou il ait I gros fil fait de X filz, et la boute en la derriere partie dou syfac, qui est aprés lou cuir des coions;	then take a needle which has the thick thread made of X threads, and put it in the rear part of the siyac, which is after the skin of the coins; 
aprés la taille, puis cope les chiés qui apperent des filz, tant qu’il i ait IIII filz;	after the waist, then cut the hairs that appear from the threads, as long as there are four threads; 
puis les assemble l’un sus l’autre en maniere de croix, et en lie lou syfac, dont nos avons dit qui est desoz lou cuir des coions, d’un fort liien de II pars;	then assemble them one on top of the other in the manner of a cross, and bind the siyac, which we have said is below the skin of the coins, with a strong binding of two parts; 
puis envoloupe les chiés des filz, et les lie forment de II pars, si que nuls des vasselz que les norrissent ne puissent entrer en ous, que aposteme chaus n’i viegne;	then wrap the shoulders with threads, and tie them together from two parts, so that none of the vessels which nourish them can enter within, except that an abscess may not come there. 
et met derechief le liien selonc le premier liien lonc II dois de celui, et aprés ces II liiens laisse dou syfac qui est desoz lou keur des coions le grant d’un doi;	and put the thread directly according to the first thread long two of that one, and after these two threads leave the said space which is below the heart of the bones the large one of a finger. 
et aprés tout l’autre selonc la rondesce que li euf porte;	and after all the other according to the roundness that the egg bears.  
puis cope en la partie qui est desoz le cuir des coions, tant qui li sans corre, et li bowe, si com nos avons dit ci devant;	then cut in the part which is below the skin of the bones, as much as the sinew and the bone, as we have said before.  
puis amenistre laine moillie en oile, et met em plaies, et i amenistre le liien que nos avons dit.	then administer wool moistened in oil, and put it in the wounds, and there administer the thread that we have said. 
Et aucune fois est cauterizez li blans syfac que nos avons dit, aprés l’incision, par doutance de decorrement de sanc.	And sometimes is cauterized the whites as we have said, after the incision, out of fear of a decrease in blood.
Car ce avient maintes fois, et laisse le liien tant qu’il chiece per lui;	For this happens many times, and leave the thread as long as it dries by itself;
et s’il tarde au cheoir, si soit arosez d’aigue chaude, et met sus ceu que nos avons dit, tant qu’il chiece;	and if he delays in healing, so it is to be raised with hot water, and put upon that which we have said, until it heals. 
puis cure la plaie d’autre cure, tant qu’il soit sanez parfaitement.	then cure the wound with other cures, until it is perfectly healed.  
de hernie carnouse	of fleshy hernia
En ceste ramice ne vis je onques nul qui osast faire la cure par fer.	In this branch I have never seen anyone who dared to perform the cure with iron.
Et li ancien dirent qu’ele est faite si com li ramice qui est ensamble la vis, en teil maniere que tu lie les vasselz, aprés la taille sus ous legierement au desoz;	And the ancients said that it is made like the branch which is assembled with the vein, in such a manner that you tie the vessels, after the cut above or lightly below. 
puis cope em mi, et cure l’aposteme de ceu qui oevre, tant que li vasselz chient;	then cut it in half, and treat the abscess with those who operate, as long as the vessels bleed;  
et le cure si com nos avons dit, tant qu’il soit sanez.	and treat it as we have said, until it is healed. 
Aucune fois vient routure ens angres, si com nos avons dit, et apert li leus;	Sometimes a rupture comes in the groin, like we have said, and opens them;  
et ne dessent nulz des intestines as coions, et s’il en i dessent, c’est poc, et repaire toutes houres;	and do not send any of the intestines into the groin, and if any come out, it is bad, and repair immediately;   
et toutevoie s’il demoure trop en cest point, si croit li plaie ou syphac, tant que li intestine dessent;	And nevertheless if it remains too long in this point, it believes the wound or syph, as far as the intestines descend. 
et ceu avient par l’estension dou syfac qui est as angres, si com nos avons dit, car il est estendus, puis est mollifiez et enflez li leus et apert;	And this happens by the extension of the syph which is at the angles, as we have said, because it is extended, then it softens and swells its parts and opens.  
et li cure si est par cautere, si com nos avons devant dit;	And the cure for this is by cautery, as we have said before.  
et aucune fois est curee par fer en ceste maniere:	And at no time is it cured by iron in this manner: 
et est que li malaides gise sovin sus son dos entre tes mains, puis cope le leu de la routure enfleit dou large selonc la quantiteit de III dois;	And it is that the patient lies supine on his back between your hands, then cut the place of the rupture enflamed outward according to the quantity of three fingers; 
et puis estrai le syfac qui est desoz le cuir que l’ensuet, puis pren lou rait et lou met sor le leu apparant dou syfac;	and then extract the  suface which is beneath the skin that it follows, then take the rait and place it on the apparent place of the suface; 
et lou presse au parfont dou ventre, puis cout les II leus apparans dou syfac sus lou chief dou rait, et cout l’un et l’autre;	and press it at the end of the belly, then sew the two apparent places of the suface on the head of the rait, and sew the one and the other; 
puis estrai le chief dou rait, et ne coper point dou syfac ne n’estendre l’uef n’autre chose, si com je t’ai fait savoir en la cure de la ramice des intestines;	then extract the head of the rait, and do not cut the suface or extend the one nor another thing, as I have made you know in the cure of the root of the intestines; 
puis le cure par la cure des plaies.	then the cure by the treatment of wounds. 
Et quant tu copes les filz, si le mundefie et cure la plaie, tant qu’elle soit sanee.	And when you cut the threads, if it is defaced and care for the wound, until it is healed.
Li syfac est constrains, et n’a point d’apparance en la routure, et li cauteres est muedres en cest leu, et plus prochiens a salut.	The suture is constrained, and has no appearance in the rupture, and the cautery is moved in this place, and closer to salvation.
de l’amollissement dou cuir des coions	of softening of the skin of the genitals
Maintes fois est amollis li cuirs des coions en aucuns homes, por ceu que les chars que sont dedens sont mollifiees, et est lait a veoir;	Many times the skin of the testicles is softened in some men, because the contents within are softened, and it is made to be seen. 
et est mestier, quant on le vuet curer, c’on faice gesir lou malaide sus son dos, et li cope le cuir qui est mollifiez sus le cuir natureil;	and it is necessary, when one wants to cure it, that one makes the patient lie on his back, and he cuts the skin that is softened on the natural skin; 
puis assemble les II levres a une costure, et se tu vues, cout premier la superfluiteit dou cuir mollifiiez a III costures ou IIII fermement;	then join the two edges with a suture, and if you see it, first sew the excess of the softened skin to three or four firmly;
puis cope entre les costures, et lou cure si com les autres plaies, tant qu’il soit sanez, et chient li fil.	then cut between the sutures, and treat the wound like other wounds, until it is healed, and remove the thread. 
dou chastrement	Through chastisement
Saiches que chastremens est escomeniez en nostre loi, et por ceu il me plairoit que je n’en parlasse mie en cest livre;	Know that this chapter is commonplace in our law, and for this reason I would like that I do not speak of it in this book; 
et n’est necessaires fuer que por II manieres:	and there are necessary for two manners: 
dont l’une est que li mires en saiche respondre quant on li demandera, et en saiche la cure;	one of which is that the patient in their own words answer when they are asked, and by themselves seek treatment;
et li autre, por ceu que nos avons sovent mestier de chastrement d’aucunes bestes por nos aidier, si com de bouc et de mouton et de chait et d’autres bestes.	and the other, because we often need to fasten certain animals to help us, such as goats and sheep and oxen and other animals. 
Je dis donques que chastremens est fais selonc II manieres:	Therefore I say that fastening is done in two ways:
ou par atraction, ou par fendure.	either by attraction, or by fenestration. 
En celle que nos faisons par attraction, faisons nos seoir la beste en aigue chaude, tant que li coion soient mollifiez et pendant;	In the one we do by attraction, we make the animal sit in hot water, until the hooves are softened and pliable; 
puis les preing a ta main, tant qu’il soient remis et que tu ne les sentes plus.	then grasping them with your hand, until they are placed back and you no longer feel them.  
Du chastrement de taille:	Of the size fastening:
covient que tu teignes la beste, et li presse le cuir des coions a ta main senestre, puis lie le suspensoire, et cope sus chescun oef a I cop, quant tu les avras bien escorchiez;	it is fitting that you hold the animal, and press the leather of the hooves with your left hand, then tie the suspender, and cut above each hoof at the joint, when you have well scraped them;
et i laisse aucun poc dou syfac et lou subtil syfac qui est sor les vasselz;	And I let none prick of the Syriac and the subtle Syriac which is on the vessels; 
et ceste maniere de chastrement est muedre que cele qui est faite par attraction, por ceu que a l’atraction demoure par aventure aucune chose des coions, par coi li beste desire luxure;	And this manner of chastisement is more effective than the one done by attraction, because in attraction perhaps nothing remains of the parts, by which the beast desires lust; 
puis cure la plaie tant qu’ele soit sanee.	then care for the wound until it is healed.  
des hermofrodites	Of the hermaphrodites
Hermofrodie est selonc II manieres as homes:	Hermaphroditism is according to II manners as men: 
l’une si est que entre les II coions apert ausi com li figure de la nature d’une femme, ou il ait poil, et aucunes fois en cort li urine.	one if it is that between the two sexes appears also as the figure of a woman's nature, or it has hair, and sometimes in court the urine.
Et li autre maniere si est en femmes, et ait sus lou poignil ausi com une verge et II coions.	And the other manner is so in women, and about the nipple as well as a staff and they copulate.
Et li cure de l’ome et de la fame si est que tu copes les chars ajostees toutes, et les cure si com autres plaies;	And the care of the man and the woman is that you cut all the joined parts, and treat them like other wounds;  
en la seconde maniere, des homes dont li urine saut par lou cuir des coions, si n’a point de cure.	in the second manner, men whose urine comes out through the skin of the genitals, there is no cure.
de la tentigene	of the tenting
Tentigene est une chars ajostee sus la partie natureil, tant qu’elle est trop laide a veoir;	A pimple is a lump attached on the natural part, so much it is ugly to see 
et aucunes femmes l’ont ausi grant com une main, et c’est li cure.	And some women have them as large as a hand, and that is their cure.  
Il covient que tu teignes la superfluiteit de la tentigene a ta main ou as oncines, et la cope legierement;	It is necessary that you squeeze the surplus of the pimple onto your hand or a cloth, and apply it lightly; 
et n’aler mie trop em parfont, que decorremens de sanc n’i viegne, puis le cure d’autre cure tant qu’il soit sanez;	and do not squeeze too hard so that bleeding does not come out, then the cure of another cure until it is healed. 
et a une autre char que naist a la bouche de la marris, et l’emple, et par aventure saut fuer, et est selonc la semblance d’une kowe, et por ceu l’apelerent li ancien «maladie kowee».	And to another lump that is born at the mouth of the groin, and the employee, and by chance if it was hurt, and is according to the resemblance of a cow, and for this reason they called it in old times “cow disease”. 
Si covient que tu la copes, si com nos avons dit la tentigene, et la cure tant qu’elle soit sanee.	If it is necessary that you cover it, as we have said the tendon, and the care until it is healed.
de erratique	of erratic
Erratique si est quant li nature de la femme n’est mie percie, ou li pertus est petis;	 Erratic if is when the nature of the woman is not perceived, or the hole is small.  
et est naturez par naissance, ou accidens par maladie que venue i est;	And is natural by birth, or accident by disease that comes from it. 
ou c’est par char ajostee, ou dou syfac subtil ou espés, et est fais em parfont en la marris, ou en costez, ou desoz, ou que soit;	Or it is by the charm of the joint, or by the subtle or thick sinew, and is done from within in the joints, or in the ribs, or underneath, or wherever it may be. 
et deffent le concevoir, et l’enfantement, et par aventure les flors a avoir;	And prevents conception, and childbirth, and by adventure the flowers to have.
et li connoissance de ceu si est par le regart de la baile.	And knowledge of these is by the regard of the bailiff. 
Se li estoupemens est prochiens apparans, si quier a tes dois ou au rait.	If the stop is near appearing, then to the two or to the rail.
S’il est dou syfac subtil, et il est prochiens as II leivres, si te haste, et la ront ensi:	If it is subtle sinew, and it is near to the two books, then hast thou, and do thus:
met tes II dois indices ensamble, et li femme soit sus son dos, espandues ses jambes;	Place your two index fingers together, and have the woman lie on her back, legs spread.  
puis estent les II leivres forment, tant que li subtilz syfac soit rons, et soit overs li estoupemens;	Then form the two leaves, as long as the subtle one is rounded, and the stupefaction be over. 
puis pren laine, et la moille en oile, et la met sus le leu, et gise li femme a home chescun jor, si qu’il ne puist souder.	Then take wool, and moisten it in oil, and put it on the place, and have the woman lie down at home every day, so that she cannot move.   
Et se li syfac est dur et espés, si covient que tu lou copes au spatumile semblant a foille de mirte.	And if the sty is hard and thick, then it is necessary that you cut it with a spatula seeming like a myrtle leaf.
Se li estoupemens est de char nee, si la sospent a l’oncine et la cope;	If the stupefaction is of flesh origin, then suspend it with the string and cut it;
et aies les medicines estainchans sanc, si com acaice, sanc de dragon, encens, ensamble abun d’uef;	and have the medicines that stanch blood, such as acaice, dragon's blood, incense, and a mixture of egg. 
puis amenistre une caine de plonc large, si que li plaie ne puisse souder;	Then administer a band of broad cloth so that the wound cannot close;
et ensi soit longement, et li amenistre une tente de lin sec;	and thus it should remain long, and administer to her a tent of dry linen.  
puis soit curez d’autres cures tant qu’il soit sanez.	then let other cures be done until he is healed. 
Et quant en la marris vient char nee, si la covient coper selonc ceste maniere, se ce n’est apostemes enchancrez.	And when in the marsh comes new clay, then it should be covered in this manner, if it is not abscesses suppurating.
Car a l’aposteme enchancreit qui est en la marris, ne doit on touchier de feir.	For an abscess that is in the flesh one must not touch with fire.
des emorroides	of hemorrhoids
Emorroydes sont overtures de voines dont sans cort acostumeement, et quant les emorroydes sont vielles si devienent thelul;	Hemorrhoids are openings of veins that without court customarily, and when hemorrhoids are old they become tuberous. 
et nos avons jai dit en la division les semblances d’aus, et les signes, et je dirai ci celles qui resoivent curation.	and we have said in the division the resemblances of those, and the signs, and I will say here those which resolve cure. 
Je di que les emorroides et li thelul, quant il sont em parfont en la marris, et il n’aperent au sentir, si n’est mie li cure par fer.	I say that hemorrhoids and the boils, when they are brought in the marsh, and they do not appear to the touch, unless it is cured by iron.
Cil qui sont a la bouche de la marris, c’on puet sentir, sont cil c’on puet curer.	Those who are at the mouth of the marsh, one can feel them, those who can be healed.
Il covient donques que tu mettes la femme en une maison froide, puis estent l’altelul as tenailles, et le cope en ses racines, puis poudre sus medicines restraignans sanc, si com acaice et sanc de dragon et encens, et semblans choses;	Therefore it behooves you to place the woman in a cold house, then being the tuberous as tongs, and the cope at its roots, then powder on restraining medicines of blood, such as acaice and dragon's blood and incense, and similar things.
puis boute ses piez a la paroit une houre, puis la met en aigue froide;	then plunge her feet to the air an hour, then put her in cold water; 
et se decorremens de sanc i vient, si la fai seoir en une decoction de sumac et d’escorce de pomes grenates et de gales et de semblans choses, et puis pren farine d’orge, et la confis avec miel et aisil, et en fai I emplaustre sus son dos.	and if decorremens of blood comes, then let her sit in a decoction of sumac and bark of pomegranates and galena and similar things, and then take flour of barley, and the confit with honey and aisil, and make an emplastrum on her back. 
Et se il estainche, c’est boin.	And if it stays put, it is good.
Se ceu non, se li fai aerdre ventouses au dos et as mameles sens ferir;	If this does not work, apply suction cups to the back and breasts without striking. 
puis pren lainne, et la moille en jus de plantain ou en jus d’aglentier avec vin viel, et fai aerdre au leu.	Then take linen, and soak it in juice of plantain or in elderberry juice with old wine, and apply it to the place.  
Et quant li aposteme repose, si cure lou leu d’oignement tant qu’il soit sanez;	And when the abscess rests, care for the place with ointment until it is healed. 
et celle qui est apelee «albathir» est rouge, et est semblans a I chief aspre, si le covient coper si com j’ai dit le thelul;	And that one which is called "albathir" is red and similar to the bitter root, so it should be covered as I have said before. 
et puis lou cure tant qu’il soit sanez.	And then care for it until it is healed.  
des apostemes de la marris	of the abscesses of the marsh
Maintes manieres d’aposteme vienent en la marris, si com chancre et aposteme pierous et herpes et estiomenes et fistules et emorroides et aposteme chaut, et plusors autres maladies que j’ai dit en la division.	Many ways of abscess come in the flesh, such as cancer and festering abscess and herpes and boils and fistulas and hemorrhoids and hot abscess, and more other diseases that I have said in the division.
Il covient donques que je die en cest traitier l’aposteme chaut qui vient en la marris, qui n’est mie des apostemes que coillent bowe;	Therefore, I must say in this treatise about the hot abscess that comes in the marshes, which is not like the abscesses that are covered with a boil;
et se tu vues savoir l’ovraige de fer, si regarde se li apostemes est agus en l’encomencement de sa venue, et plain de chalor et de fievre, et s’il devient rouge se tu le pues veoir.	and if you want to know the work of iron, look at whether the abscess is angry at the beginning of its coming, and full of heat and fever, and if it becomes red if you can see it.
Adonques ne te haster mie de percier, mais lou fais meurer tant que li dolor soit apaisie;	Therefore do not hasten to pierce, but let him suffer as long as the pain is appeased. 
et puis fai seoir lou malaide sus I siege, et ait II petis sieges ou il se cline, et apoie sus son dos et assemble ses piez as parties defuer la jambe;	And then make the patient sit on a seat, and let him have small seats where he leans, and support his back and bring together his feet to the parts outside the leg; 
et soient ses cuixes espandues, et mette ses braz desoz ses genous, et les lie bien d’un boin liien;	And let his thighs be spread apart, and place his arms under his knees, and bind them well with a good linen band;
puis succe li baille devers lou destre costeit, et i amenistre l’estrument dont on oevre la bouche de la marris, de coi ci aprés vient li forme;	then he brings the tail towards the right side, and there administers the instrument with which one operates the mouth of the channel, so that afterwards comes the form.  
et covient que quant tu i vues amenistrer cest estrument, que tu fiches le rait premier ens por savoir la parfondeté de la marris, si que ceu qui entre ens de l’estrument n’i viegne plus em parfont qu’il ne doit, et qu’il ne blece la malaide;	and it is necessary that when you see him administering this instrument, that you first put in the tail so as to know the depth of the channel, so that what goes into the instrument does not go deeper than it should, and that it does not injure the patient; 
et se li estrumens est plus grans, si covient covrir la parfondesce de la marris de drapelz, si que li estrumens ne li grieve;	and if the instrument is larger, then it is necessary to cover the depth of the channel with cloths so that the instrument does not harm him;
et covient qu’il mette le cornet de l’estrument au desus, et qu’il teigne l’estrument.	and it is necessary that he put the cone of the instrument on top, and that he holds the instrument. 
Et quant li apostemes apert, et on lou fent a la main mol, si le covient coper au chief, au spatumile leit;	And when the abscess opens, and one makes it with a soft hand, then it is necessary to cover it at the head, with the spatula clean. 
et quant li bowe est vuidie, si covient que tu mettes en la plaie tentes moillies en oile roset, ou en oile vert sec;	and when the wound is emptied, it is necessary that you put in the wound damp lint in rose oil, or in green dry oil; 
et met la tente fuer de la plaie au parfont de la marris, et met par defuer sus la marris et sus le poignil lainne nette moillie en aigue ou malves soient cuites;	and place the lint away from the wound to the edge of the margin, and place outside over the margin and on the knife-sharp clean damp lint in water or mullein be cooked; 
puis le cure aprés II jors d’oignement avenant a ceu, tant qu’il soit sanez;	then cure after two days of oiling preceding these, as long as it is healed;
et aucune fois leve on la marris et la plaie par clistere d’aigue et de miel, et puis d’aigue ou racines de lis et aristologe longe soient cuites;	and no time raise the margin and the wound by enema of water and honey, and then water or roots of lilies and long aristolochia be cooked;
puis reveigne a l’oignement.	then return to oiling. 
Et se li plaie est reponue en la marris, si covient que tu te gardes de cuire de fer, mais cure la si com nos avons dit en la division.	And if the wound is put back in the flesh, then you must guard yourself from cauterizing with iron, but treat it as we have said in the division.
de l’enfantement	of the birth
Mestier est premier a la baile qu’elle conoisse la figure de l’enfantement natureil, et li signes si est quant tu vois la femme apresser aval, et desire odorer l’ar:	It is first necessary for the midwife to know the figure of natural childbirth, and the signs are when you see the woman pressing down, and desiring to smell the air;
adonques se haste li enfes de fuer issir;	therefore the child must hastily be moved by force  
adonc saiches que cil enfantemens est selonc la figure natureil, et est li issue soz son chief, et li secondine avec lui;	therefore know that this childbirth is according to the natural form, and is below his head, and the second with him. 
et quant tu vois ces signes, si covient presser legierement son ventre, si que li enfes isse tost;	and when you see these signs, it is necessary to gently press on his belly so that the child comes out quickly. 
car quant il dessent sus son chief, si ist li secondine avec lui, et est mondee li marris de ses superfluitez par bone mundification;	because when he descends with his head, the second follows him, and is cleansed of its superfluities by good purification. 
et cist qui vient autrement ne vient mie naturelment.	and this one that comes otherwise does not come naturally. 
Car il vient aucune fois sus ses piez, et vient fuer li cors ou li chiés, et les mains, ou il vient sus son ventre, ou sovin, et est convertis par aventure sor son col, et par autres figures malvaises;	Because it comes never with his feet, and comes by force on the body or the shoulder, or the hands, or it comes on his belly, or groin, and is turned by chance on its neck, and by other bad figures. 
si est mestier a la baile qu’elle soit saige et subtilz en ces choses, et se warse d’error et de decevement, et je vos mostrerai toutes les figures coment on li doit aidier.	so it is necessary for the midwife to be wise and skillful in these things, and to guard against error and deception, and I will show you all the figures how one must help them. 
Se li enfes vient sus son chief par issue natureil, et li femme enfante griement, et li vertus de li est foible, si la fai seoir sus une selle, ou les femmes la tienent;	If the child comes onto its head by natural birth, and the woman gives birth with difficulty, and the strength of the one giving birth is weak, then make her sit on a saddle, or have women hold her. 
et arose sa nature d’oile ou fenugreic soit cuit, et puis boute li baile entre ses dois le petit spatumile dont ci est li forme:	and bring its natural oil or fennel to be boiled, and then put the bail between its thighs with the small spatula whose shape is here: 
et fende la secondine, et cope a son ungle tant que li moistors qui est ens corre fuers;	and split the secondine, and cut at its fingernail as long as the moisture which is within corrects;
et preint lou ventre de la femme tant que li enfes dessende, et s’il ne dessent, si covient clisterizer la femme de muscillaige de fenugrec avec oile de sisament;	and take the belly of the woman as long as the child descends, and if it does not descend, then you must administer an enema to the woman with flaxseed mucilage and sesame oil. 
puis la fai preindre et esternuer de condisi, et tien sa bouche et son neis une houre:	Then make her sneeze and cough, and hold her mouth and nose for an hour;
si istra maintenant l’enfes.	then now extract the child. 
Et se les II mains issent fuer, si covient que tu les ramoinne legierement poc et poc;	And if the two hands are dislocated, then it is necessary that you reset them lightly here and there. 
et s’elles n’i puent entrer, si met la femme sus I siege, et li lieve les piés en haut;	and if they cannot enter, then put the woman on the chair, and raise her feet up.  
puis deboute le siege sus terre, et teigne on la femme, qu’elle ne chiece au deboutement;	then tip the chair over to the ground, and hold the woman so that she does not fall during the tipping; 
et se li mains n’i puet entrer, et li enfes muert, si li cope les mains au couteil qui est ci devant mis, et estrai l’enfant, et ramoine igalment.	and if the hands cannot enter, and the child dies, then cut off the hands at the elbow which was placed before, and extract the child, and reset it equally.  
de l’issue de l’enfant sus ses piés	of the issue of the child on its feet
Quant li enfes vient sus ses piez, si lou covient bouter en haut;	When the child comes onto its feet, then it is necessary to push upwards. 
et puis le torne poc et poc, tant qu’il soit igalz;	and then turn it here and there, until it is equalized;  
puis preigne I des piez et l’estende poc et poc.	then grab its feet and extend them here and there. 
Cant il saut jusc’as cuixes, si la comande a preindre, et la fai esternuer de condisi;	When it jumps up to the hips, then command to grasp, and make it sneeze with condition;   
si saut fuer, se Deus vuet.	If it will be so, God willing. 
Et s’il n’ist fuer si com nos avons dit, si le torne poc et poc, tant qu’il soit selonc la figure natureil.	And if it is not as we have said, turn it back and forth, until it is according to the natural shape.
Car adonques ist il legierement.	Therefore, there must be treated lightly.
Et s’il ne vient fuer si com nos avons, dit si pren muscillaige de altee, et oile de sisament, et gomme fondue, et broie tout en I mortier;	And if it does not come as we have seen, say that you take mullein of the herb, and sesame oil, and melted gum, and grind all in a mortar; 
et met sus la nature de la femme dedens et defuer cest oignement, puis la fai seoir en aigue tede jusque desoz les costelz;	and put it on the woman's body inside and outward this ointment, then make her sit in hot water up to below the ribs; 
et quant elle est moillifie desoz, se li fai I coliere de mirre, et li met desoz, et li laisse une houre;	and when she is softened below, say that you make her a collar of frankincense, and put it under, and leave it for an hour; 
puis la fai seoir sus I siege, puis la fai esternuer et estraint sa bouche et son neis, et li preint le ventre legierement, car li enfes saut maintenant.	then make her sit on the stool, then make her sneeze and strain her mouth and nose, and take her belly lightly, for the child is now coming out.
de l’issue de l’enfant sus ses genous	of the issue of the child on his knees
Quant li enfes vient en ceste forme, si i mette li baile ses mains poc et poc;	When the child comes in this form, you put your hands on the child, patting it, patting it; 
puis soit sovinee sus son col, et li pendent li piez aval, et soit gisans sor I lit;	Then let him be laid on his back, and let his feet hang down, and let him lie on the bed.  
et plie ses mains poc et poc, et puis li preint les mains sus lou ventre, et li oste les cussins desoz, tant qu’elle soit appareillie aval;	And bend his hands palm to palm, and then take his hands above his belly, and remove the cushions from under him, until she is prepared downwards;  
et se li enfes ne saut, si pren ses piez et li muef forment, puis li muef lou ventre amont, puis i boute tes mains;	And if the child does not jump, take his feet and move them forcefully, then move his belly upwards, then push with your hands;  
et ewe l’enfant poc et poc;	and poke the child here and there; 
et comande a la femme qu’elle se preigne tant que li enfes isse.	And instruct the woman to shave herself until the child is born. 
de l’issue de l’enfant qui vient dou large une main pendant	of the issue of the child who comes out by a wide hand during
I covient engignier a ramener la main:	It is necessary to devise a way to bring back the hand: 
s’on ne la puet ramener, si fai lever la femme, et aler;	If it cannot be brought back, have the woman get up and leave;  
s’elle ne puet aler, si la fai gesir sus I lit, et li deboute les jambes forment;	If she cannot leave, have her lie on the bed and uncross her legs. 
puis amenistre lou muscillaige que j’ai conteit;	Then administer the concoction that I have recounted;   
et s’elle n’enfante, si la fai seoir sus I siege, puis estudie au rameneir la main;	And if she does not give birth, have her sit on the stool, then study how to bring back the hand. 
et ewe l’enfant selonc la figure natureil, et la fai esternuer, et li comande qu’elle se preigne tant que li enfes isse fuer.	And guide the child according to its natural form, and have her sneeze, and instruct her to shave herself until the child is born.  
de l’issue de l’enfant sus son col, et ait espandues ses mains, et sa faice tornee devers lou dos sa mere	Of the issue of the child on its neck, and have spread its hands, and its face turned toward the back of its mother
I covient que li baile teigne sa main, puis le torne poc et poc, et l’ewe legierement;	It is necessary that the midwife hold her hand, then poke it gently here and there,   
et quant il est igalz, si met sus la nature muscillaige de altee et oile, si com nos avons dit, puis li comande qu’elle se mueve poc et poc;	And when it is even, place on the nature of flesh, a little bit of oil, as we have said, then command her to move a little bit at a time. 
et quant tu avras ce fait, si la fai seoir sus I siege, et li comande k’elle se preigne;	And when you have done this, make her sit on the seat, and command her to pull herself up.  
et la fai esternuer.	And make her sneeze. 
de ceste meisme maniere a tout la secondine	of this same manner to all of the spine
Quant il vient fuer en ceste maniere a tout la secondine, si cope la secondine a ton ungle, tant que li moistors soit vuidie;	When it comes to being in this manner throughout the whole shoulder, strike the shoulder with your finger, until all moisture is gone.
et se li enfes pent sus sa faice et sus son col, si la cope des la boude, qu’elle ne soit retenue, et muere li enfes;	and if the child falls onto its face and neck, so that the head is not held up, the child will die.  
puis boute l’enfant dedens, tant que tu l’aies mis si com il covient, et comande a la femme qu’elle se preigne aucune fois:	then put the child inside, as long as you have placed it as it should be, and command the woman to abstain from any movement: 
adonques si istra legierement.	then it will become lighter.  
de l’issue des gemelz	of the separation of the twins
Saiches que gemeil naissent maintes fois, et aucune fois en naissent III ou IIII;	Know that twins are born many times, and rarely three or four. 
et ceu n’est mie estrainge chose, et poc avient.	and this is not a strange thing, but it happens.  
Dui sont estrainge chose, et ne vivent mie, se poc nom;	Two are a strange thing, and rarely live, if they even name them; 
je sai ceu, qu’il soient multipliiet, et sont desevrez par lou syfac qui les devise, qui est liiez a la boude;	I know that they are multiplied, and their severance is by the force which divides them, which is attached to the head;  
et aucune fois issent ausi naturelment com uns tous sous, si com nos avons dit.	and sometimes they come out as naturally as one under, as we have said. 
Et s’il issent griement, si la cure si com nos avons dit, et soit li baile subtilz, et faice tost et legierement ceu qu’elle fait;	And if they come out painfully, then treat them as we have said, and let the surgeon be subtle, and do quickly and lightly what she does. 
et faice ensi com il vaut mues a salut.	and do so that it may lead to health.  
de plusors enfans	of many children
Aucune fois sont formez en la marris I ou II ou III ou IIII ou V ou VI ou VII, ou plusors jusc’a XV, et sont tout formeit en forme d’enfant par le mesurement dou saige glorious, et couvient que li baile saiche tout ceu, car par aventure semblans chose li avient;	Sometimes they are formed in the marsh I or II or III or IV or V or VI or VII, or more up to XV, and are all formed in the shape of a child by the measurement of its sage glorious, and it is necessary that the surgeon know all this, because by chance similar things happen; 
si faice selonc ceu qu’il covient.	if he does according to what is fitting.   
de l’enfant mort	of the dead child
Quant tu cures la femme de l’enfant mort ou ventre, si com j’ai dit en la division, et il ne vient fuers, et tu es constrains d’ovraige de mains;	When you cure the woman of the dead child or belly, as I have said in the division, and it does not come out, and you are constrained to work with hands;
si covient que tu saiches se li femme est de saine vertut, et n’ait accident ou elle ait paor de mort;	so it is necessary that you know if the woman is of sound virtue, and has no accident or she fears death. 
si covient que li femme soit sovinee sus son dos, et soit ses chiés enclins aval, et les jambes levees;	so it is necessary that the woman be laid on her back, and her hips inclined downward, and her legs raised. 
et li ministre la teigne de II pars, ou elle soit liie au lit si qu’elle ne soit traite au dessendement de l’enfant;	and the minister holds her from the sides, or she is tied to the bed so that she does not move during the descent of the child. 
puis frotez la bouche de la marris d’oiles moistes avec muscillaige de altee et de fenugrec et semence de lin, puis oigne li baile ses mains de ces oiles et de ces muscillaiges;	then rub the mouth of the mother with moist oils with muskmallow and fennel and flaxseed, then anoint her hands with these oils and ointments.
puis les boute en la marris legierement, puis quiere I leu ou elle boute les oncines que soient covenaubles a ceu, et pren warde se li enfes est apparilliez qu’il dessende sus son chief;	then put them in the mother gently, then guide her where she puts the forceps so that they are suitable to it, and take care if the child is appearing that he descends upon his head. 
si fiche les oncines en ses eulz ou en son col ou en sa bouche ou en som palais ou desoz la barbe ou en la forcele ou pres des costez, et se li dessendemens est sus piez, se li fiche ou poignil et as costes moienes;	so put the forceps in her eyes or in her neck or in her mouth or on her palate or under the beard or in the armpit or near the ribs, and if the descent is on feet, so put it or prickle them at the middle ribs. 
et covient qu’il teigne l’oncine a sa main destre, et mette la corbeure entre ses dois de la senestre main, et li boute a tout sa main legierement, et fiche l’oncine en aucun de ces leus que nos avons dit, tant qu’il viegne a la chose vuide;	and it is necessary that he hold the awl in his right hand, and put the curve between the two fingers of the left hand, and thrust it with all his hand lightly, and stick the awl in any one of these places that we have said, until it comes to the empty place; 
et c’est li forme de l’oncine:	and this is the form of the awl:  
puis fiche encontre I autre oncine, ou le tier se tu en as mestier, si que li estractions soit igalz;	then stick it against the other awl, or the third if you need it, so that the extractions are equal;  
et puis l’estent igalment en movant d’une part et d’autre, por mues issir, et soit li oncines dentez por mues tenir, si com ci est li forme:	and then put them equally in moving from one side to the other, so that it moves easily, and let the awls be toothed to hold well, as this is the form:  
Et s’il en demoure une partie, si oigne li baile aucuns de ses dois d’oile, et les boute en celle partie, et traie l’autre partie;	And if one part remains, anoint the bail with some oil in his fingers, and thrust them into that part, and draw the other part;  
et s’il en i demoure point, si met cest oncine ou plus haut leu, et fai ceu tant qu’il s’en isse tout fuers.	and if there remains none of it, put this one or higher up its place, and do so until it comes out completely. 
Et se l’une mains vient devant l’autre, et il ne puet ramener por l’estreignement, si covient que tu envoloupes sus I drapeil, tant qu’il isse tote;	And if one hand comes before the other, and it cannot be brought back by tightening, then you must envelop it on the cloth, until it comes out completely. 
puis la cope en la jointure de la plante ou au coute, et ensi covient que tu faices en l’autre main, et as II piés.	then cover it at the joint of the foot or on the knife, and thus you must do in the other hand, and as with II feet. 
Et se li chiés de l’enfant est gros et il est estrois en l’issue, ou il ait ou chief aigue assemblee, si covient que tu boute le spatumile espinous entre tes dois, et fent le chief et estrai l’aigue;	And if the child's shoulder is large and it is stuck in its exit, or if it has a sharp point assembled, then you must put the pointed spatula between your two, and make the head and extract the point;
ou tu la ront a l’estrument qui est apelez «almidach», de coi li forme vient avec les estrumens ou chapistre qui est aprés cestui;	or you can use the instrument that is called "almidach", because its form comes with the instruments or chapter which is after this one; 
et ensi meisme faice se li enfes a grant chief naturelment;	and so likewise do if the child has a large head naturally; 
et puis traie fuer les osses as tenailles, et se li chiés saut fuer et il estraint a la forcele, si soit fendus, tant que li moistors qui est ou pis issue fuer;	and then pull the bones with forceps, and if the head jumps back and it is forced, so they are split, until the moisture which is there or worse comes out; 
et s’elle ne puet issir, si le cope par pieces au mues que tu pues;	and if it cannot exit, so cut it in pieces as much as you can;   
et s’il est enflez au ventre ou desoz les costez, si covient que tu lou perces tant que li moistors corre.	and if it is swollen in the belly or below the ribs, then it is necessary that you pierce it until the moisture flows out. 
Et se li enfes est sus ses piez, si est li attraction legiere, et li adrecemens a la bouche de la marris est legier.	And if the child is on its feet, then the traction is light, and the addressing to the mouth of the shaft is light.
Et s’il est estrois au ventre ou au pis, si couvient que tu l’estraies a I drapeil envoloupeit sus la main;	And if it is stuck in the belly or at the breast, then it is necessary that you extract it with the hand enveloped in cloth;  
et fent le ventre ou le pis, tant que li moistors qui i est corre;	and scrape the belly or the breast, until the moisture inside flows out; 
et se li autre membre sont osteit, et li chiez demoure, si boute li baile sa main em parfont de la marris, et le traie jusc’a la bouche de la marris;	and if the other members are dislocated, and the head remains, then put the hand of the one who is performing it in their mouth, and pull it until the mouth of the skull. 
puis i boute I oncine ou II, et le trai fuer;	then he puts [it] back in one place or two, and the flesh heals. 
et se li bouche de la marris est retrecie por aposteme chaut qui i est venus, si n’i covient mie travillier, ains covient amenistrer choses moistes et grasses;	and if the mouth of the abscess is contracted because of the hot cautery that has come upon it, it does not need to be worked on, but rather one should administer moist and fatty things.  
et li amenistre emplaustres, et siece en aigue mollifians et amoistans.	and [he] administers poultices, and wets with softening and moisturizing liquid. 
Et se li enfes est sus son costeit, et tu le pues mettre igal, si amenistre ceu que nos avons dit en l’enfant vif;	And if the bone is on its rib, and you can put it straight, administer what we have said about a living child; 
et s’on nen ait pooir, si lou trai fuer par pieces, et n’i laissier rien de la secondine.	and if one cannot do that, then the flesh heals in pieces, and leave nothing of the second bone.  
Et quant tu avras ce fait, se li amenistre ceu que nos avons dit ens apostemes chaus que vienent en la marris;	And when you have done this, if it comes to an abscess or a boil that is in the flesh;
et se decorremens de sanc vient, si soit mise en aigue restraignant, et li amenistre autres cures.	and if bleeding occurs, it should be put into restraining liquid, and administer other treatments.
Et je vis une femme en cui ventre uns enfes avoit esteit mors, puis consut I autre sus celui, et refut mors li autres.	And I saw a woman in whose belly one child had been dead, then she conceived another on top of that one, and refused to give birth to the other.
Aprés lonc tens li vint uns apostemes en la boude, et enfla tant qu’il ovrit, et comensa a grant porreture.	After long time there came an abscess in the buttock, and it swelled so much that it opened, and began to great purulence.
je fui apelez a la cure, et i pensai lonc tens, et ne pot soder li plaie.	I was called to heal, and I thought long about it, and could not suture the wound.
Je mis sus emplaustre de fort attraction, et en issit uns os, et aprés aucuns jors uns autres.	I put on a plaster of strong attraction, and from it emerged one bone, and after some days another.
Je me mervillai mout, por ceu c’ou ventre n’a point d’os.	I was greatly astonished because this belly has no bones.
Si pensai que c’estoit des os d’un enfant mort.	If I thought that it was the bones of a dead child.
Je quis la plaie, et en traï mains os, tant que li femme fut em millor point;	I treated the wound, and in my hands bones, until the woman was better. 
et vesquit li femme lonc tens ensi, et issoit adés un poc de bowe dou leu;	and I kept the woman long times thus, and it returned a little bit of strength from her. 
et je n’ai recordeit cest chapistre fuer que por ceu que, quant li maistres trueve une estrainge chose, qu’il i saiche mettre aide.	and I have recorded this chapter for those who, when they find a strange thing, that they may know how to help. 
dou ramener la marris a son leu	to bring the bone back to its place
Ci aprés vient li forme dou pressor, a coi on ewe les livres;	Here after comes the form of the pressor, as it is written in the books; 
et a II tornans as II chiés des II liiens.	and to its turns as it has the shoulders of the two limbs.  
Toutevoie, li cornes soit plus subtilz dou restrictoire, et soit fais de ebene ou de bux;	However, the horns should be more subtle of the restrictor, and made of ebony or boxwood; 
et soit li bouche dou fust I doi de large, et li marge des arbres I doit, et de lonc une palme et demi;	and let the mouth of the shaft be so wide, and the edge of the trees it must, and long one palm and a half;
et enmi les II liemens soient dui ajostemens de cest meisme fust, qui soient fermeit en l’un et en l’autre, de demi palme de lonc ou un poc plus;	and among the two limbs be two adjustments of this same joint, which are fastened in one and the other, half a palm long or a bit more; 
et cist dui ajostement sont bouteit en la bouche de la marris por ovrir quant on torne les II cornes.	and these two adjustments are put in the mouth of the furrow to open when one turns the two horns.  
Une autre forme, a sa semblance plus subtilz et plus legiere, soit faite de fust de ebene ou de bux, selonc la semblance des tenailles;	Another form, somewhat more subtle and lighter in appearance, is made of ebony or boxwood, according to the likeness of pliers;  
et ait as II chiés II ajostemens, si com tu vois, d’une palme de lonc, et II dois de large;	and have at its two ends two adjustments, as you see, of one palm long and two in width.
et quant tu vues ovrir la marris a tout l’estrument, si fai seoir la femme sor I lit, les piez pendant et les jambes overtes, puis boute les II ajostemens ajostez ensamble en la marris, et tien le chief de l’estrument desoz entre ses cuixes;	and when you see to open the womb with all the instrument, so make the woman sit on the bed, the feet apart and the legs open, then put the two instruments adjusted together in the womb, and hold the head of the instrument below between her thighs;  
puis oevre ta main a tout l’estrument, si com tu as fait as tenailles igalment, selonc la quantiteit que tu vues ovrir la bouche de la marris, tant que li baile faice ceu qu’elle vuet.	then work your hand with all the instrument, just as you have done with the pliers equally, according to the quantity that you see opening the mouth of the womb, until the patient does what she wants. 
Cist estrument sont tuit sormontez, et sont multiplies lor semblances;	This instrument are all superimposed, and are multiplied their appearances; 
et quant li mires les ait apareilliez, tant est plus hastans li oevre, et plus haute as homes por lor quantiteit.	and when the mirrors have appeared to them, so much is more Hastings the work, and higher the men for their quantity. 
Si ne despire mie l’estrument que tu ne l’aies apparelliet, car lor necessitez n’est mie escusauble.	If you do not despise the instrument, so long as it is well equipped, because its necessity is not excusable.
Quant li secondine est retenue a l’enfantement, si covient que tu comandes a la malaide qu’ele reteigne son alaine, et puis la fai esternuer de condisi, et li estraint tes mains a la bouche et au neis;	When the secondine is held back in childbirth, so it behooves that you command the patient that she retain her breath, and then make her sneeze of condiment, and hold her hands to her mouth and nose;
et s’elle saut per ceu, bien est.	and if it jumps for this, well is.  
Se ceu non, si prent I pot, et fai I pertus ou cuvercle, et i met herbes que puissent ovrir la bouche de la marris, si com calament, rue, anis, camomille, cassialigne et centoire;	If this does not happen, take a pot, and make it pierced or covered, and put in herbs that can open the mouth of the marsh, such as calamint, rue, anise, chamomile, cassoligine and centaury; 
toutes ces herbes, ou aucunes d’eles, soient cuites ou pot en aigue sus le feu;	all these herbs, or any one of them, should be cooked or put in water on the fire;  
puis met une caine ou pertus dou pot, et l’autre chief en la bouche de la marris, et la teigne tant que li vapors viegne dedens la marris;	then put a chain or pierced pot, and the other end in the mouth of the marsh, and keep it there until the vapors come out inside the marsh;
puis la fai esternuer, si com nos avons dit.	Then make him sneeze, as we have said. 
Si saut li secondine hastanment.	If you jump the second joint violently.
Et s’elle remaint aprés ceste cure, et n’ist mie fuer, si comande a la baile qu’ele moille sa main senestre en oile de sesement ou en muscillaige de altee, et puis la boute en la nature, et quiere la secondine;	And if it remains after this cure, and there is no more force, command the midwife to moisten her left hand in sesame oil or in a poultice of alum, and then put it into the vagina, and stir the second time.  
et quant elle l’avra trovee, si la preigne et l’estende poc et poc droitement, si que li marris ne chiece a l’estraction;	And when she has found it, seize it and extend it piece by piece straightly, so that the veins do not break during extraction.  
mais la covient movoir legierement a destre et a senestre, et puis traie;	but then it must be moved gently to the right and left, and then pulled. 
si venra et se desaerdra.	if it comes and dislocates again.  
Et se li bouche de la marris est jai estrecie, nos avons dit la cure d’esternuer, et de fumigation des herbes;	And if the mouth of the mare is narrow, we have said the cure of sneezing, and fumigation of herbs. 
et s’elle n’ist de tout ceu que nos avons dit, si garde que tu ne foloies au traire;	and if it is not of all that we have said, then guard that you do not use the milk;
mais il couvient que ceu qui est a la bouche de la marris, que tu le lies a la cuixe de la femme, puis la clisterize d’oignement tetrafarmaçon;	but it is necessary that what is at the mouth of the mare, you bind it to the hip of the woman, then clysterize with ointment tetra-pharmacon. 
si la porrira et remettra, et venra fuer;	so she will bear and put back, and come again;
mais toutevoie, quant elle porrist si en vient male odor au stomac et au chief, et blece la malaide.	but nonetheless, when she bears, if it comes bad smell to the stomach and head, and pales the patient. 
Si covient donques fumigations covenaubles a ceu:	So then it is necessary fumigations suitable for those:
aucun des anciens ont esproveit fumigation de cresson et de figues seches.	None of the ancients have tested the fumigation of watercress and dried figs. 
Li forme de l’estrument a coi on fumige la femme a la retenue des flors et de la secondine si est ceste:	The shape of the instrument for which one fumigates the woman for the retention of flowers and the second is this:
Et est de voirre semblant a une caine, et met on le chief subtil en la nature, et les chiés larges sus le feu;	And it is like the appearance of a dog, and it sets the head subtly in nature, and the shoulders wide above the fire; 
et soit li fumigations sus les charbons, et la teigne tant qu’elle soit gastee, et rencomence une autre.	And let the fumigation be above the coals, and the tinder until it is burned out, and begin another one.  
de percier lou fondement	To examine the foundation
Maint enfant naissent qui n’ont mie le fondement perciet, ains l’ait estoupeit uns subtilz syfac:	Many children are born who do not have the foundation pierced, but are stopped with subtle instruments.
si covient donques a la baile qu’ele perce celui syfac a son doit, et ne lou perce mie de spatumile agut, et garse le lacement qu’elle ne le touche;	Therefore it is fitting for the midwife that she pierce that instrument in its proper place and does not pierce it with a sharp spatula, and guards the bandage so that it does not touch it; 
puis met sus lainne moillie en vin et en oile, puis la cure d’oignement tant qu’il soit sanez.	Then she puts on linen moistened in wine and oil, then the ointment treatment until it is healed.  
Et se tu doutes qu’il ne restoupe, si met ou pertus une caine de plonc, et li laisse mains jors, et soit ostee quant li enfes vuet aler en chambres.	And if you doubt that it will not reset, put in a splint of wood, and leave it for several days, and remove it when the child wants to go to bed.
Et aucune fois vient cist estoupemens de soudement de plaie ou d’aposteme;	And no time comes this stopping from a sudden wound or abscess
si covient coper celui soudement:	if it is necessary to cover it tightly 
si soit curez, si com nos avons dit de la caine de plonc.	if so cured, as we have said of the chain of plomb.  
de la fistule dou fondement	of the fistula of the foundation
Fistules qui vienent desoz le fondement sont nodation, et groissor que vienent delez lou fondement defuer, ou en l’espaice des II parties, si a une fistule ou plusors;	Fistulas that come from under the foundation are nodules, and greater than those that come near the foundation outside, or in the space of the two parts, if there is one fistula or more. 
et quant celle nodation est anciene, si aoeuvre, et encort moistor awouse blainche ou subtilz bowe, et aucune fois sont ces fistule persans;	and when that nodule is old, if it works, and still moisture causes blisters or subtle bows, and sometimes these fistulas are pierced.
et sont conues par ceu qu’il en ist ou egestion ou ventositeit quant li malaide fait egestion, et par aventure en saut uns vers.	and they are known by those who have it or by the emission or windiness when the patient makes an emission, and by chance one jumps forward.
Et si a fistules que percent jusc’a la vessie, et jusc’a la moitiet de la verge;	And if there are fistulas that pierce to the bladder, and to the half of the penis; 
et parvienent jusc’a la jointure de la cuixe, et jusc’a nout de la kowe.	and reach to the junction of the hip, and to the outside of the buttock.  
Et ensi conoist on la fistule persant au fondement, et ne mie persant:	And thus one knows the fistula piercing to the base, and not piercing.  
et est que tu boutes ton doi indice ou fondement, et boute une aguille subtil d’arain ou de fer en la fistule quant il n’i a tortuositeit.	And that you insert your index finger or base, and thrust a subtle needle of iron or steel into the fistula when there is no twisting. 
Et s’il ait tortuositeit, si i boute une tente de plonc subtil, ou I poil de cheval, tant que tu sentes la tente ou le poil a ton doit;	And if it has twisting, then you insert a tent of fine cloth or horse hair, as long as you feel the tent or hair on your finger. 
et se tu ne le sens, et il ne vient dou pertus egestion ne ventositeit ne ver, si com nos avons dit:	And if you do not feel it, and there is no discharge coming through nor windiness nor pus, as we have said:
saiches qu’elle ne perce mie;	Know that it does not pierce. 
si te haste dou curer.	If you hasten to cure.  
Et quant li fistule est persans jusc’a la vessie ou jusc’a conduit de l’urine, si en saut li urine, et ne puet soudeir par medicines.	And when the fistula is pierced up to the bladder or to the urinary tract, then the urine leaks out, and cannot be healed by medicines.
S’elle est percie jusc’a la jointure de la cuixe, si est li tente venans jusc’au leu;	If it is pierced up to the junction of the hip, then the tendon comes to its place. 
s’il n’i a tortuositeit et li invention de la dolor entor, si est qu’il en ist adés bowe, et n’i vaut medicine ne soudement par oignement;	If there is no twisting and the pain of inflammation is in the middle, then it is that there is a boil, and it does not require ointment or treatment. 
et en ces fistules persans n’a point de cure fuer que labor, et vaniteit des folz mires qui s’en entremettent.	And in these fistulas Persians have no cure except labor, and vanity of the fools who meddle with them.
En celle qui n’est mie persans et n’est mie anciene, a esperance de saniteit par fer, si com j’ai esproveit, et est que li malaides gise entre tes mains sus son dos;	In those that are neither Persian nor ancient, there is hope of healing by iron, as I have experienced, and it is that the patient lies between your hands on his back; 
et li lieve les jambes jusque sus ses cuixes, et ait ses cuixes enclinees a son ventre;	and lifts his legs up to his hips, and has his hips inclined to his belly;  
puis boute une tente d’arain, ou de plonc s’il i a tortuositeit, tant que tu saiches ou li tente vient.	then put an arrow tent or of lead if there is twisting, as long as you know where the boil comes from.  
Se li malaides la sent entor le fondement, si covient que tu i boutes ton doi indice, se sens adonques que li tente l’ait perciet;	If the patient feels it near the foundation, then you must put your index finger there, and then feel if he can perceive it. 
et soit descoverte ou tu sens entre ton doit le syfac ou la char, adonques saiches qu’elle est persans;	And be discovered or you feel between your finger the sinew or the flesh, then you know that she is present. 
si n’i travillier mie c’on ne la puet saner.	If it does not work and one cannot heal her.  
On dist toutevoie c’on em puet bien saner aucuns, mais ce avient poc;	It is said nonetheless that one can heal them well, but this happens rarely. 
et li aide c’on i fait, si est c’on eschaufe le cautere subtil selonc la largesce de la fistule, si com il est devant dit;	And the aid that one does to it, is if one heats the subtle cautery according to the wideness of the fistula, as it has been said before.
et le boute tout chaut en la fistule, tant qu’il viegne delez le fondement;	And puts it whole hot into the fistula, until it comes near the foundation. 
et faice ceu II fois ou III, tant que tu saiches que ces chars fautrees soient arses, qui sont semblant a une penne d’oiseil;	And do this two or three times, as long as you know that these fleshy strands are burned, which are seeming to an eye feather.
et puis le cure de tentes moillies em burre, tant que celle chars isse fuer, puis le cure d’oignement enjanrant char et soudant.	And then the cure of moist cloths in butter, until that flesh is issued, then the cure of ointment closing and joining flesh. 
S’il est ensi sanez, c’est bien.	If it is thus healthy, then well.
Se ceu, nom autrement ne puet estre sanez;	If this, otherwise cannot be healed; 
et se li tente entre, et ne perce jusc’au doit qui est ou fondement, et a entre ton doi et la tente une coverture espesse de char ou de syfac, et tu vois la fistule a ceu qui enseut la coverture dou keur;	And if the tent enters, and does not pierce to the bottom which is the foundation, and between your bottom and the tent there is a thick covering of flesh or  syfac, and you see the fistula at this following the covering of the heart; 
si le cope des l’encomencement de la fistule, et boute adés avant la tente, et pues le cautere aprés, tant qu’il viegne au chief de la tente;	if you cut from the beginning of the fistula, and push ahead before the tent, and then the cautery after, until it comes to the head of the tent.
et sera delivré li tente, et cherra;	And will be delivered the tent, and will seek out; 
puis mondefie celles chars fautrees que semblent une penne d’oisel, et n’en remaigne niant.	Then  examine those ones that seem like a feather of an owl, and remain nothing from them. 
Et si li sans te vaint, et cort entre toi et l’uevre, si le cauterize de feu ou de medicine ague.	And if the wound gets worse, and goes between you and the work, then cauterize it with fire or sharp medicine.
Car li cauteres de feu assemble II bones choses:	For the fire cautery assembles II good things: 
c’est a savoir, l’arsure de ces chars ajostees, et l’esteinchement de sanc et la sechor de la moistor;	that is to say, the burning of these joined together, and the stopping of blood and the drying of moisture; 
puis le cure de tentes moillies em burre ou en choz broiez, tant que li leus giete bowe, et isse fuer li chars arse en la bowe;	then the cure of tents moistened in butter or in crushed things, as long as the wounds are low and if the joined ones have burned to the bottom. 
puis cure la plaie des oignemens soudans enjanrans dure char, et sont les medicines seches.	Then  cure the wound of sudden swellings by means of hard joined things, and they are the dry medicines.
Car quant il est restoree, si est sanee et ne revient mie.	For when it is restored, it is healed and does not return.
Et se fistule vient jusc’a parfont dou fondement, et est esloigniez dou cors, se li boute ton doi ou fondement, et enquier ceu.	And if a fistula comes up to the very bottom of the foundation, and is separated from the body, then you should probe its opening and examine it carefully.
Se tu sens la tente, et entre II est li toile ou li syfac ou chars, ou il est pres a percier, si n’i ait fuers que voie de fiance et d’esperance, par l’aministrement de l’une des III manieres:	If you feel the tent, and between II there is the cloth or the  syfac or joined things, or where it is near to breaking through, if there is no other way than a path of faith and hope, by the administration of one of the III manners:
ou tu le cauterizes si com nos avons dit, ou tu le cope jusc’a fons, ou se tu pues si i met tentes et cure si com premier;	or you cauterize it as we have said, or you cut it to the bottom, or if you can put a tent and cure it as before; 
et n’aler mie trop em parfont, que tu ne coper le tenement qui tient le fondement, et viegne li egestions par lai sens volenteit;	and do not go too deep in cutting, so that you do not cut the base which holds the foundation, and let the secretions come by its natural will; 
puis le cure, si com nos avons dit;	then cure it as we have said. 
par aventure si sera sanez, ou tu esloigne celle coverture et la munde puis qu’elle est copee delez lou fondement, ou par tente ou par autre estrument apointé;	by chance if it will be healed, or you remove that covering and the wound since it is cut near its foundation, or by tent or by another pointed instrument;
puis mondefie cele char fautree qui est en la plaie, tant com tu pues;	then cleanse the foul matter which is in the wound, as much as you can. 
puis estudie a restorer la plaie, et a demorer la fistule en la partie defuers le fondement:	then study to restore the wound, and to keep the fistula in the part outside the foundation:
si iert plus legiere chose au malaide.	so it is a lighter thing for the patient. 
Et aucune fois sont fistules selonc ceste maniere:	And sometimes fistulas are made in this manner:  
et est quant tu boutes la tente en la fistule, et elle est ou costeit dou fondement delez lou cuir desus, si pren une tente percie au chief selonc ceste forme:	and when you put the tent into the fistula, and it is or cost by the foundation against the skin above, then take a tent pierced at the head according to this form: 
Et i boute I fil tort en II, et boute la tente a tout le fil en la fistule tant qu’il soit au chief.	And he puts the thread twisted in it, and puts the tent to all the thread into the fistula until it is at the head.
S’elle est persans en la marge dou fondement dedens, adonc estrai lou fil de celui pertus, ensi que tu boutes ton doi ou fondement;	If it is placed in the margin of the foundation inside, then extract the thread of that one pierced, as you put your dough or foundation; 
et trai le chief dou fil, et assemble les II chiés ensamble, et estraint l’un a l’autre, et le laisse I jor ou II;	and carry the head of the thread, and assemble the two heads together, and bind them to each other, and leave it one day or two; 
et le restraint aucune fois, tant que li filz cope ces chars que sont entre dous, et chiecent;	and restrain it no longer until the threads catch these characters which are between two, and shrink; 
puis cure la plaie tant qu’elle soit soudee et sanee.	then cure the wound until it is soldered and healed.  
Se li fistule ne perce, si la fai percier en toutes les manieres que tu pues, s’ele n’est trop em parfont.	If the fistula does not pierce, make it pierce in all ways that you can, if it is not too deeply embedded.
Car il ne covient mie faire por le lacement coper si em parfont, et puis le cure, si com nos avons dit, tant qu’il soit sanez.	For it is not right to make a ligature cover so when it is made, and then cure it as we have said, until it is healed.
Li forme dou spatumile espinous dont on fent la fistule si est mout agus d’une, part et trenchans;	The form of the spatula spine from which one makes the fistula is very much a one part and trenching; 
et d’autre part non, por ceu c’on ne cope mie ceu c’on ne doit mie copeir, si com tu vois ci:	and on the other hand no, because one does not cut what one should not cut, as you see here: 
des emorroydes	of hemorrhoids
Emorrydes sont selonc II manieres:	Hemorrhages are according to II manners:  
ou elles sont dedens le fondement, ausi com grain de resin, et s’en i a petites et grans, et en cort adés sanc, et s’en i a une ou plusors, et sont defuer le fondement et au chief dou fondement;	or they are inside the foundation, as much as a grain of resin, and there are small and large ones, and in short close blood, and there are one or more, and they are outside the foundation and at the top of the foundation;  
mais celles qui sont defuer si ont poc de moistor, et encort adés ou un poc d’aigue citrine ou un poc de sanc, et ont la color dou cors;	but those that are outside have little moisture, and in short one or a little bit of water clear or a little blood, and they have the color of the body;
et li cure de ces qui les ont dedens le fondement, si est que tu comandes au malaide qu’il s’espreigne por aleir en chambres, tant que li fondemens li isse fuer, et c’aperent li filz;	and the cure of those who have them inside the foundation, it is that you command the patient to stretch for them to go in rooms, as long as the foundations are sore, and they appear the children; 
si te haste, et le pent as tenailles, ou tu le tien a ton ungle, puis le cope en ses racines;	If you hurry, and can hold it with pincers, or you hold it with your finger, then cut it at its roots. 
et se li uncine ne les pueent tenir por ses moistors, si les prent a I drapeil, ou a couton, ou d’une piece de chamelot;	And if the forceps cannot hold it because of its moisture, then take it with a cloth, or with cotton, or with a piece of felt. 
et les estrai a tes dois, puis les cope, et poudre desus aucunes chaudes poudres que soient en leu de cautere;	And hold it with your fingers, then cut it, and put hot powders above it in place of cautery;  
ou tu les cauterize si com il est dit ou chapistre de cautere, pues les cure d’autres cures tant qu’il soit sanez;	or you cauterize it as is said in the chapter on cautery, then cure it with other cures until it is healed; 
et se li fondemens ne puet issir, si clisterize le malaide de clistere mordant et aspre por laver ceu qui est ou fondement, si qu’il puist issir apertement;	And if the base cannot come out, then enema the patient with a harsh and biting enema to wash what is in the base so that it can come out openly; 
cant li malaides se preint, et se li fil sont fuer dou fondement, si est li cure legiere;	But if the patient resists, and if the threads are too thick from the base, then the cure is light;
et est que tu les preignes a ton ungle ou as tenailles, et les cope, puis les cure si com nos avons dit, tant qu’il soit sanez, et qu’il redoute l’incision par fer.	And it is that you prick them with your finger or pliers, and cut them, then treat them as we have said, until they are healed, and he fears the incision by iron. 
Si covient que tu amenistre la costure selonc ceste maniere:	If it is necessary that you administer the suture in this manner:  
pren I fil tort, et le boute en une aguille, et puis trai le fil au desus et fai percier l’aguille d’autre part, et torne les II chiez dou fil desoz l’aguille, et si soit dou large;	Take a twisted thread, and put it in a needle, and then lead the thread above and make the needle pierce on the other side, and turn the two ends of the thread below the needle, and so be wide; 
et estraint le fil forment, puis noe le fil, et estrai l’aguille, et fai ensi de toz les autres, et en laisse I por corre la superfluiteit dou sanc;	And tighten the thread firmly, then knot the thread, and remove the needle, and do so for all the others, and leave one open to correct the superfluity of blood; 
puis met sus le fondement I drapeil moilliet en oile roset ou en cerote, et met sus le fondement, et comande au malaide k’il repose;	Then put on the foundation a soft cloth soaked in rose oil or cerate, and place it on the foundation, and instruct the patient to rest. 
et puis le laisse tant qu’il chiecent, et quant il seront cheut, si les cure d’oignement et d’autre cure, tant qu’il soit sanez.	And then leave it until they weep, and when they are dry, care for them with ointment and other remedies until they are healed. 
dou sechement dou fiens ou fondement	of drying of the veins or foundation
Maintes fois avient sechement de fiens en l’intestine, et par constrignement de nature, et quant li maladie est vielle et medicine n’i vaut.	Many times there happens drying of humors in the intestine, and by constriction of nature, and when the illness is old and medicine no longer works there.
Si covient que tu reses a la point d’un spatumile ou a ton ungle l’escorce desus, qui ne le laisse a moistir;	It is necessary that you cauterize the point of a spatula or with your fingernail the bark above it, so that it does not get moist. 
puis le cure tant qu’il soit sodez si com il covient;	Then care for it until it is healed as necessary.  
et s’il ne puet soder, si rencomence la rasure plus fort que devant, tant qu’il saine mout, et soit escorchiez;	And if it cannot heal, begin the scraping again more strongly than before, until it heals well and is well-scraped.  
puis le cure tant qu’il soit sanez.	Then care for it until it is healed. 
dou fremit	from shaking
Formice est une petite apparance fautree antor le cors, et va mout em parfont;	A formice is a small appearance of pus before the body, and it goes very deep;
et aucune fois la trueve li frois, et le sent on ausi comme mort de fremit, et vient en tout le cors, et plus as mains que autre part.	And sometimes it is found cold, and one feels it like death from chill, and it comes throughout the body, and more to the hands than any other part.
Et li cure si est que tu pren une cainne d’une penne d’oie, ou une penne de vultul fort, et met celle caine sus le fremit, tant que li cercles porpreigne le fremit tot entor;	And the cure is that you take a cane of an ostrich feather, or a very strong vulture feather, and put that cane on the wound, until the purple circles tinge the wound all around.  
puis torne ta main a tout la cainne tant que tu copes tout entor le fremit, et le met em parfont, et esraiche le fremit de ses racines.	then turn your hand over the entire cane until you cover the whole wound, and place it in place, and scrape the wound from its roots. 
Et se tu vues, si fai ceu d’une caine d’arain ou de fer selonc ceste forme, et soit subtilz desoz et traians desus:	And if you see, so do this of a serpent of iron or steel according to this form, and be subtle below and trailing above:
ne mie perciet, por mues tenir au doi, et mues presser.	Do not let it pierce, for to hold at the joint, and press.  
Et se tu vues, si cauterize lou fremit, si com il est devant ou chapistre de cautere.	And if you see, then cauterize the wound, as it is in front or chapter of cautery. 
de la forme dou clistere	of the shape of the clyster
Aucune fois fait on clistere d’argent ou d’archaut, ou d’arain fondut ou mailliet;	At times one does a clyster of silver or lead, or molten iron or mesh;  
et aucune fois fait on de ces estrumens petis et grans, selonc ces a cui il sont amenistrez.	and at times one does these instruments small and large, according to those to whom they are administered. 
Cil donques c’on amenistre en la cure des enfans et qui sont foible et dolorous, sont petis.	Those therefore who are administered to in the treatment of children and who are weak and painful, are small.
Li forme dou clistere petit et grant si est desus large, ou li ventres est liiez selonc ceste maniere:	The form of the clyster small and great is above wide, where the belly is tied in this manner:
et i ait une desevrance ou li ventres soit liiez, si com tu vois, et li chiez soit dedens perciez;	And there is an opening where the belly is tied, as you see, and the head is pierced inside. 
et ait a l’un des costez II pertus, et en l’autre I;	And on one of the ribs II is pierced, and on the other I; 
et soit li ventres ou om met les medicines d’une vessie de beste ou de parchemin, et soit perciez tout entor de menus pertus, et ait entre chescun pertus I doit d’espaice, puis boute en ces pertus I fil fort de fil crut tort en X ou enqui entor, et assemble le ventre si com est une chievre;	And the belly is where one puts medicines in a bladder of animal or parchment, and it is pierced all around with small holes, and between each hole there should be some space, then put into these holes I thread strong thread twisted in X or however around, and assemble the belly like a kid; 
et quant li medicine est dedens, si la lie a l’estrument devant d’un fil fort, puis clisterize;	And when the medicine is inside, tie it to the instrument in front with strong thread, then administer an enema;
et c’est li forme dou cercle:	And this is the shape of the circle: 
Et soit li medicine ne trop chaude ne trop froide, et oint le chief dou clistere d’oile ou d’aubun d’uef, ou de semblant chose, puis le boute ens legierement;	And let the medicine not be too hot nor too cold, and grease the head of the enema with oil or yolk of egg, or something similar, then put it in gently;
