puis l’espreigne li ministres a ses II mains ensamble, tant qu’il soit toz vuis, puis estrai lou clistere, et lieve li malaides ses jambes a la paroit, et se li medicine vuet issir, si la teigne tant com il puet;	then the minister with his two hands together, until it is all visible, then remove the blister, and raise the patient's legs to the side, and if the medicine wants to pass, then pull on the skin as much as he can 
et s’il dort une nuit atot, si est plus grans aide.	and if he sleeps a whole night flat, then it is more help.  
Et se tu le clisterizes em maladie de decorrement de ventre, et li medicine se haste d’issir, si le rencomence tant qu’il soit sanez.	And if you treat it with a disorder of the belly and the medicine hastily issues from there, repeat it until it is cured.
Et se li emorroide sont ou fondement, ou aposteme, si soit li clistere ausi subtilz com por I enfant;	And if the hemorrhoids are at the base, or abscess, then let the enema be as subtle as for a child; 
et c’est li forme dou clistere subtil sus coi li cuir soit estraint:	and this is the form of the subtle enema on which the skin should be stretched:  
des plaies	of wounds
Nos avons jai dit en la division la cure des plaies;	We have already said in the division the cure of wounds;
or vos dirons les cures de mains et de medicine, selonc l’acomplissement.	or we will tell you the cures for hands and medicine, according to completion. 
Je dis que les plaies sont diverses selonc ceu qu’elles sont faites, et selonc les leus ou les plaies sont faites, et de coi elles sont faites.	I say that wounds are diverse according to how they are made, and according to the places where the wounds are made, and of what they are made.
Les choses par coi plaies sont faites sont par gitement de piere, et taille d’espee et de couteil, ou de lance ou de fust ou de siette, ou de semblans choses;	The things by which wounds are made are by the blow of a stone, and the cut of a sword and knife, or of a spear or club or arrow, or similar things; 
ou que sont faites selonc les leus dou cors, si com plaie que chiet sus le col, ou sus le chief, ou le peis, ou le ventre, ou le foie, et semblans membres;	or which are made according to the parts of the body, such as a wound that falls on the neck, or on the head, or on the back, or on the belly, or on the liver, and similar members. 
et je vos dirai la cure de chescune plaie, et encomencerai as plaies dou chief simples, car li remenbrance venra en son chapistre.	and I will tell you the cure of each wound, and I will begin with the wounds of the head simple, for remembrance will come in its chapter.  
Je dis que quant simple plaie vient ou chief, et li os n’est brisiez, si pren garde se c’est de gitement de piere ou de semblans choses, et li cuir est toutevoie rompus et est li plaie grans, et tu doutes levement d’aposteme chaut:	I say that when a simple wound comes to the head, and the bone is not broken, then take care if it is from a stone or similar things, and the skin is immediately torn and the wound is large, and you doubt strongly of an abscess hot: 
si le fai tantost sainier de la cephalique meismement s’il vient poc de sanc de la plaie, et soit li sainie au contraire de la partie navree;	if it should happen to be bled promptly from the cephalic vein even if there is a little blood from the wound, and let the bleeding be on the contrary side of the wounded part;
et eschuisse li malaides repletion de vin et de viandes grosses.	and avoid the patient's repletion of wine and thick meats.  
Et s’il ne vuet sainier, si soit amenuisie sa viande, et ne boive point de vin, ne ne menjuce point de char;	And if he does not want to bleed, let him lessen his meat, and drink no wine, nor eat much of meat.  
et met sor la plaie, se apostemes chaus i vient, coton moilliet en oile roset soulement, ou en vin stiptice;	and put on the wound, if an abscess comes there, moistened cotton in rose oil only, or in ptisana wine.  
et s’il n’i a aposteme chaut, si met sus la plaie, s’elle est fresche a tout son sanc, et elle n’est muee par l’air, poudre, que je dirai un poc ci aprés;	and if there is no abscess, put on the wound, if it is fresh in all its blood, and it is not moved by the air, powder, which I will say a little later.
et se li ars l’ait muee, si met sus aucuns oignemens, tant qu’il soit sanez.	and if the artist has moved it, put some ointment on it, until it is healed. 
Et se li plaie est grans si com de tailleure d’espee et de semblans, et les levres ne se pueent assembler par tentes, si les assemble par cousture, si com je dirai as plaies dou ventre, de la costure.	And if the wound is large like a sword cut and similar, and the lips cannot be brought together by tents, then bring them together by suture, as I will say for wounds of the belly, of the suture.
Se li plaie est descoverte de l’os, et pent, et ne tient mais que a un poc, si le cope;	If the wound is open to the bone, and hanging, and only holds by a bit, then cut it;   
puis cure la plaie de medicine, et restoure char dure en leu de cuir, et comande au malaide a mengier grosses viandes, si com testes et froment cuit, ausi com poulz, et semblans choses.	then cure the wound with medicine, and restore tough flesh in place of skin, and instruct the patient to eat large meats such as beef and wheat bread, as well as pulses, and similar things.  
Et se tu trueves ou cuir porriture, et il n’aert a l’os, si cope lou porrit tot, et giete fuer, puis le cure;	And if you find rotten skin, and it doesn't reach the bone, then cut out all the rot, and throw away the pus, then cure it;  
et se il ait artere en la plaie ou voine, dont sans cort, et il ne puet estainchier par medicines, si quier l’artere, et se tu la trueves desloie, si la lie d’un fil;	and if there is an artery in the wound or vein, which without cutting, and it cannot be stopped by medicines, then tie the artery, and if you find it dislocated, tie it with a thread; 
et se ceu ne profite mie, si la cauterize.	And if this does not help, then cauterize it. 
Et se ces plaies sont petites et simples, si est li cure legiere:	And if these wounds are small and simple, then the cure is light: 
et est que tu mettes ens ceste poudre qui soude ainsois que li ars l’ait muee.	and that you put in this powder which joins as if the fire had healed it.  
Et li maniere de la poudre si est:	And the manner of the powder is: 
pren encens une partie;	Take incense one part; 
sanc de dragon II parties;	dragon's blood two parts;  
chalz vive III parties, et le poudre subtilment, et emple la plaie, et l’estraint forment, tant qu’elle s’aerse bien et se joigne a tout son sanc;	Quicklime three parts, and grind the powder finely, and apply it to the wound, and hold it firmly, until it dries well and joins with all its blood; 
et puis la lie bien, et la laisse sens desliier, s’elle n’enfle;	and then dress it well, and leave it undisturbed, if it does not swell;   
car on n’oste la madicine tant qu’ele soit sanee.	for one removes the medicine only when it is healed. 
Et aucune fois fait on ceu de chalz soulement, quant on n’ait l’encens ne lou sanc de dragon, mais que li ars n’ait muee la plaie.	And no times is this done with just chalks, when one does not have incense nor the blood of dragon, but that the fire has closed the wound.
Et se li ars ait mueit la plaie, meismement en esteit, si n’i met om mie ceste poudre;	And if the fire has already healed the wound, even if it is still inflamed, put no powder in it; 
mais met sus aucuns oignemens digestis, ou poulz de farine d’orge faites d’aigue et de miel, tant qu’ele giete bowe;	but put some dressings digested, or poultices of barley flour made with water and honey, as long as it swells. 
puis le cure d’autres cures tant qu’il soit sanez.	then treat other wounds until it is healed.  
Et se li brisure d’os vient avec la plaie, et elle est petite, si l’estrai as pinceures subtilz;	And if the fracture of bone comes with the wound, and it is small, then extract it with subtle pincers. 
et je vos dirai ci aprés les brisures dou chief.	and I will tell you afterwards about fractures of the head.  
de la plaie dou col	Of the wound of the neck
Se plaie vient ou col et elle est simple, si n’a point de difference entre li et celi dou chief, mais se li ners dou col ou li artere est copee.	If a wound comes to the neck and it is simple, there is no difference between this one and the other of the head, but if the nerve of the neck or the artery is cut.
Se c’est li ners, si n’i a autre engien que laissier la cure, et n’i mettre nulle chose restraignant, car il nuit as ners et les fait retraire;	If it is a nerve, there is no other thing to do but leave the wound alone and put nothing in to restrain it, for it harms the nerve and causes it to retreat. 
et ne mettre sus la plaie rien froit, car li substance des ners est froide, et li continuation d’aus si est avec le cerveil, qui est li plus haus membres;	And do not put anything cold on the wound, for the substance of the nerves is cold, and its continuation is with the brain, which is the highest member.  
mais soit li medicine souez, si com chalz lavee en aigue douce, et mellee avec oile roset, et cucie lavee ausi en aigue douce, et autres pieres de mine selonc ceste maniere, et oignemens moistes.	but let the medicine be warm, such as calf washed in sweet water, and mixed with rose oil, and cuckoo's flower also washed in sweet water, and other stones of mine according to this manner, and moist dressings.   
Et se li plaie est grans, si la cout et lie de bendes, puis la cure tant qu’il soit sanez.	And if the wound is large, so the side and tie with bandages, then care until it is healed.
Et se les plaies sont parfondes et ele est chevee et pleinne de bowe, si la perce ou plus bas leu;	And if the wounds are deep and the flesh is swollen and full of pus, pierce or lower than that. 
et se li artere est copee, et decorremens de sanc en vient, si la desoivre, et la loie, et la cauterize se mestier est;	And if the artery is cut and bleeding comes, then stop it with a ligature, and bandage it, and cauterize it as is necessary.  
et se li espinee de la gorge est copee, ou li keurs, et li conduiz est gardez, par coi la viande va, si cout le keur sus la cainne de la gorge, et ne touchier la gorge mais la remet selonc sa figure naturel;	And if the spine of the throat is cut or the windpipe and the conduit is kept, so that the flesh goes, stitch the heart on top of the neck of the throat, and do not touch the throat but put it back according to its natural shape.  
et puis l’estraint avenanment, et le laisse aucuns jors, puis le cure d’oignemens desechans tant qu’il soit sanez;	And then restrain it properly, and leave it for some days, then cure it with medicinal ointments until it is healed.  
et se li plaie a fait empression en l’os, si la quier;	And if the wound has made an impression on the bone, then cover it.
et s’il i a pieces d’os, si les trai fuers toz se tu pues, et ces que tu ne pues avoir, si laisse tant que li plaie porrisse, et soit desevree et aligie li issue;	And if there are pieces of bone, then try to remove all of them as best you can, and what you cannot have, leave it until the wound is rotten, and be careful and apply a splint.
et se li plaie est fresche, si poudre sus la poudre que j’ai dit.	And if the wound is fresh, then powder on top of the powder that I said. 
Et s’il a en la plaie os et il i a fistule, si la cure ensi com j’ai dit en son chapistre.	And if there are bones in the wound and there is a fistula, then treat it as I have said in my chapter.
de la plaie de lance ou de coutel	of the wound of lance or knife
Se c’est cop de lance ou de coutel, et li plaie est parfonde, si regarde se de la plaie saut ventositez cant li malaides alainne:	If it is a blow from a lance or knife, and the wound is deep, then look if from the wound there arises windiness as the patient breathes: 
saiches adonques que li plaie est mortelz;	Then know that the wound is mortal. 
et s’elle n’est parfonde, et elle est fresche a tout son sanc, si n’i mettre mie a la premiere houre la poudre, ne ne la liier mie por le sanc que ne demorse em parfont, et reviegne au cuer, et ocie lou malaide;	And if it is not deep, and it is fresh with all its blood, then do not put any powder on it in the first hour, nor bind it so that the blood does not remain deep, and return to the heart, and kill the patient. 
mais i met oignement atractif, et le lie II fois le jor;	But put attractive ointment, and bind it twice a day:
et se tu n’as oignement, si met en la plaie viel coton por succier fuers la moistor, et fai dormir le malaide sus la plaie III jors, ou IIII, ou plusors;	And if you don't have ointment, put old cotton in the wound to suck out the moisture, and make the patient sleep on the wound for three days, or four, or more.
si n’i venra mie spasme, ne tremor male de cuer n’estraingnemens d’alainne;	if there come not spasms, nor evil trembling of heart nor straining of the arm; 
et quant tu vois les bones dispositions, si saiches que li plaie est sauve.	and when you see the good arrangements, then you know that the wound is saved.  
Cure la donques de tentes et d’autres cures, tant qu’il soit sanez;	Treat therefore with tents and other treatments, as long as it is sound; 
et s’elle ne puet saner, et oevre, adés saiches que il i a fistule;	and if it cannot heal, and works, then you know that there is a fistula;
si la cure si com on doit.	treat it as one must. 
Et se li plaie est d’incision d’espee ou de coutel, et elle est simple, ou pis ou au dos, si la cure de ceu qui est devant;	And if the wound is from a sword or knife incision, and it is simple, or worse, or on the back, then treat it as above. 
s’elle est grans, de cousture;	If it is large, sew it together;  
et s’elle est petite, de poudre, et s’elle est empressee en l’os, et en a copeit pieces, si quier la plaie, et les trai fuers s’il sont desevrez;	and if it is small, with powder, and if it is pressed into the bone, and has broken pieces, then close the wound, and pull out the fragments if they are loose. 
et s’il ne sont desevrez, si laisse porrir la plaie, si aligera li estractions;	And if they are not removed, let the wound fester, so it will lighten the extractions. 
et des autres plaies as autres membres est li jugemens si com nos avons dit.	And for other wounds on other members, judgment is made as we have said.  
dou derrompement dou ventre	of the displacement of the belly
Li derompemens dou ventre est grans et moiens et petis;	The rupture of the belly is great and medium and small; 
de la grant plaie saut aucune fois li intestine, ou li ners des intestines, par coi li intromission d’aus;	From the large wound sometimes the intestine or the nerves of the intestines protrude, so by which the intrusion of others occurs;  
et li costure est plus malaisie, et aucune fois vaut pis li petite plaie que li grans, por ceu c’on remet plus a poinnes les intestines en, s’on ne les i remet de chaut en chaut;	And the suture is more difficult, and sometimes the small wound is worse than the large one, for that reason it is put back in more carefully, if one does not put them in hot to hot. 
por ce que li intestine enflent tantost qu’il sentent le froit, si rentrent plus a poinnes, et por ceu vaut mues li moieinne plaie, por ceu c’on ramoine mues l’intestine a son leu que as autres II.	Because the intestines swell as soon as they feel the cold, so they go back in more carefully, and for that reason the middle wound is worse, for that reason one must reset the intestine to its place like the others. 
Et saiches que li routure dou ventre est selonc IIII manieres:	And know that a rupture of the belly is according to IV manners. 
les II costures communes avienent en la costure dou ventre, et li costure des autres plaies dou cors et II autres costures propres sont communes as autres plaies;	The two common sutures occur in the suture of the belly, and the sutures of the other wounds of the body and two other special sutures are common to other wounds. 
et toutevoie elles sont plus propres avec la costure dou ventre, et je dirai une chescune et declairerai.	And nevertheless they are more proper with the suture of the belly, and I will say each one and declare.  
Je di que quant li plaie est petite, et aucune chose de l’intestine ist fuer, et griés chose est dou remettre, ceu est par l’une des II manieres:	I say that when the wound is small, and nothing of the intestine has come out, and it is a thing to be put back together, this is by one of the two manners. 
ou por la petitece de la plaie, si com nos avons dit, ou por ce que li intestine est enflez por le froit.	or for the smallness of the wound, as we have said, or because the intestine is swollen from the cold.  
Et quant il est frois, eschaufez lou en teil maniere:	And when it is cold, warm it in this manner:
moillie une esponge ou I mol drapeil en aigue tede soulement, ou tu cuis en aigue squinant et cipre et spique, et arose l’intestine tant que li enfleure soit ostee;	Half an sponge or I soft cloth in boiling water only, or you cook it in boiling water adding juniper and pepper, and raise the intestine until the swelling is removed.
et aucune fois fait ce vins restraingnans, et est muedre que awe soule por desenfler.	And sometimes this wind restraining is done, and it moves only so that it deflates. 
Et quant tu vois l’enfleure departir, si amoiste l’intestine d’aigue ou altee et malves soient cuites, car par ceu est aligie li entree a poc de chose;	And when you see the swelling departing, moisten the intestine with water or wine and herbs be cooked, because by these is aligned the entrance to little things. 
et s’il n’i puet entrer, si fent un poc la plaie a l’estrument de coi on cope les emorroydes;	And if it cannot enter, make a hole in the wound with the instrument with which hemorrhoids are treated. 
et li premiere cure est muedre que li taille, que nus n’i doit taillier sens grant necessiteit n’i ait;	And the first cure is to move it that it be cut, that one should not cut it without great necessity being there.
et c’est li estrumens por le fendre:	And this is the instrument for splitting it. 
si trenche dedens en la corbeure et defuer non, et vez ci la forme:	So cut inward at the curve and outward not, and see here the form.  
Et quant li plaie est enlargie, et li intestine saut fuer, si le remet arer selonc la forme naturel en son leu propre, se tu en as pooir, car ce vaut mues.	And when the wound is enlarged, and the intestines have jumped out, put them back in their natural form in their proper place if you are able, for this is valuable to heal.
Quant li plaie est large, et elle est en la partie desoz lou ventre, si covient que tu faices gesir lou malaide sus son dos, et met ses jambes plus haut que son chief;	When the wound is wide and it is in the part below the belly, it behooves you that you make the patient lie on his back, and put his legs higher than his head.
et s’elle est en la partie desoz le ventre, si met le chief et le pis plus haut que les parties desoz, et ausi se li routure dou ventre est en l’une des II parties si met t’entente en ceu que li partie navree soit plus haute que li autre;	and if it is in the part below the belly, place the head and buttocks higher than the parts below, and also if the rupture of the belly is in one of the two parts, put your attention to that the sunken part be higher than the other. 
et ensi covient amenistrer ceu que je dis en plaies grans et moienes.	and thus it is necessary to administer what I say in large and small wounds.  
Es plaies petites met ceu que t’est apparilliet, puis aies entre tes mains I ministre pitous ki teigne toute la routure a sa main, et assemble les levres;	In small wounds put what you have appeared, then have between your hands the minister pitiful who holds all the rupture in his hand, and bring together the lips; 
et c’est la maniere commune de costures, et est que tu preignes une aguille ou plusors, selonc la quantiteit de la largesce de la plaie, puis laisse des le chief de la plaie I doi d’espaice, et i fiche une aguille ou il ait I boin fil fort;	and this is the common manner of sutures, and it is that you prick a needle or more, according to the quantity of the breadth of the wound, then leave from the head of the wound one part of space, and there pierce a needle where there is the good strong thread;  
et perce les II chiés dou cuir avec les II chiés dou siphac, qui est desoz le cuir dedens, tant que tu la faices percier de celle partie, et assemble les II chief dou siphac les IIII ensamble;	and pierce the two ends of the skin with the two ends of the fascia, which is below the skin inside, as long as you make it pierce from that part, and bring together the two heads of the fascia the four together; 
puis l’estrain d’un fil double entor l’aguille de II pars, puis assemble les II chiés de la plaie avenanment, et puis laisse I doi d’espaice, et i fiche une autre aguille;	then the strain of a double thread around the needle of one part, then assembles the two ends of the wound together, and then leaves the space of two fingers, and there it puts another needle;  
puis la lie dou fil si com tu as fait la premiere aguille, et ne cesser de ceu faire selonc ceu que tu as mestier des aguilles, tant que toute li plaie soit restrainte;	then the thread of the needle like you have done the first one, and do not cease doing so according to what you need the needles, until all the wound is restrained;  
et soient les aguilles moienes, entre subtilz et grosses, car les aguilles subtilz copent toute la char, et les trop grosses si ne pueent mie bien entrer:	and let the needles be medium-sized, between fine and coarse, because the fine needles cut all the flesh, and the too coarse ones cannot enter well:
por ceu covient qu’elles soient moienes;	for this reason it is necessary that they are medium-sized; 
et ne covient mie bouter les aguilles trop au defuer de la char et dou cuir, k’elles ne copent et oevrent la plaie devant la soudure;	and it is not necessary to push the needles too far out of the flesh and skin, lest they cut and open the wound before the suture; 
et puis cope les chiés des aguilles, qu’elles ne blecent lou malaide au dormir, et i met tentes ou drapelz au chiés des aguilles por mues tenir, et les laisse tant que li plaie soit soudee;	and then cut the ends of the needles so that they do not prick the patient while sleeping, and put bandages or cloths on the ends of the needles for them to remain in place, and leave them until the wound is healed.  
et ceste maniere de costure as aguilles est plus covenauble en petites plaies, car il i soffist une aguille ou II.	And this way of suturing with needles is more convenient for small wounds, because one needle or two are used there. 
Li seconde costure si est commune, et est que tu assemble les II chiés dou cuir et les II chiés dou syfac ensamble a une aguille ou il ait I fort fil moien;	The second suture is common, and it is that you assemble the two pieces of skin and the two pieces of the fascia together with a needle through which passes a strong medium thread. 
et quant tu avras perciez ces chiez toz IIII ensamble, si ramoinne l’aguille a la partie ou tu as encomenciet, en la maniere c’on cout les dras;	And when you have pierced these four pieces together, you move the needle back to where you began, in the manner one sews fabrics.
et met d’espaice entre chescune costure la grossece d’un menor doi;	and put space between each stitch the thickness of a man's finger. 
ceste costure sevent li home, et je cousi une plaie c’uns hons avoit ou ventre, qui estoit navrez d’un coutel, et estoit li plaie plus d’une palme de grant, et issoit des intestines bien II palmes de grant, et estoit li plaie enmi le ventre.	This stitch belongs to a man, and I sutured a wound that one man had on his belly, which was pierced by a knife, and the wound was more than a palm in size, and it protruded from the intestines well two palms in size, and the wound was in the middle of the belly.  
Je li ramenai l’intestine puis k’il ot esteit XXIIII houres fuer, et fut li plaie soudee jusc’a XV jors, et le curai, et fut sanez.	I brought back the intestine after it had been out for XXIV hours, and the wound healed up to fifteen days, and I cured him, and he was healthy.
Et li mire l’avoient jugiet qu’il morroit, et ce fut miracle;	And the doctors had judged that he would die, and it was a miracle; 
et ne le curai mie d’oignement, car je estoie en I leu ou on n’en trovoit point, ne nule medicines;	and I did not cure him with ointment, because I was in the place where one could not find any, nor any medicine;
et metoie sens plus sus la plaie coton viel II fois le jor, et le lavoie d’aigue de miel tant qu’il fut sanez.	and I put more than twice a day fresh cotton on the wound, and washed it with water of honey until he was healed. 
Or vos dirai les II propres manieres de cousture:	Now I will tell you the two proper ways of suturing:
pren l’aguille, et la boute des la partie defuers jusc’a celi dedens;	Take the needle, and thrust it from the outside part to the inside. 
quant elle a perciet le keur de droit en droit, si lai le chief dou siphac ou cousteit ou tu as bouteit l’aguille, et la fai percier d’autre part des la partie dedens jusc’a celi defuer;	When it has pierced the right heart straight through, then lay the head on the side of the scalp where you thrust the needle, and make it pierce from the other side from the inside to the outside. 
et li entendemens de ceste costure si est que tu cous ausi com li peletier font les pelz, et que tu laisses une fois le syfac d’une part, et le reprent d’autre, tant que li costure soit toute acomplie.	And the understanding of this suture is that you sew as the furrier does furs, and that you leave the scalp on one side, and take it back on the other, until the suture is entirely completed. 
Li seconde maniere de costure, que Galiens dist proprement, si est si com aucun font, qui assemblent les II parties ensamble naturelment, et apploient l’un des chief dou syfac a l’autre chief, en teil maniere:	The second manner of suturing, as Galens states properly, is like any one who joins the two parts together naturally, and applies one side of the scalp to the other side, in such a way:
fiche une aguille ou chief dou mirach prochiene, et fai percier celui leu soulement, et laisse les II chiés dou syfac;	Insert a needle or head of the scalpel near it, and make it pierce only that place, and leave the two sides of the scalp. 
puis torne l’aguille, et la fai percier des la partie defuers jusc’a celi dedens, as II chiés dou syfac;	Then turn the needle, and make it pierce from the outside part until the inside one, just like two shoulders.  
puis fai percier l’un et l’autre des la partie defuers jusc’a celi dedens, en II autres chiés dou mirach que sont on l’autre costeit;	Then make it pierce both from the outside part until the inside one, in two other shoulders of the miracle that are on the other side.  
et c’est li muedre maniere de costure et li plus commune.	And this is the most common and usual way to suture. 
Galiens si dist ceste parolle, et aucun le tesmoignent, c’on doit coudre le ventre a II aguilles, ou il ait fil en chescune;	The Gauls say this word thus, and no one testifies it, it is necessary to sew the belly with two needles, or there is thread in each. 
et doit on bouter l’une aguille d’une part, et l’autre d’autre, en la maniere de ces qui cousent corroies;	And one must thrust one needle on one side, and the other on the other, in the manner of those who sew corsets.  
et saiches que quant li routure est enmi lou ventre, si est li cousture plus griez que des autres leus dou ventre.	And know that when the rupture is in the middle of the belly, the suture is more grievous than in the other parts of the belly. 
Li jugemens de la plaie si est telz com li jugemens des autres plaies:	The judgements of the wound are like the judgments of other wounds: 
et est que quant tu trueves la plaie fresche a tout son sanc, ainsois que li ars l’ait muee, si remet arer l’intestine, et lou cout;	And it is that when you find the wound fresh with all its blood, so that the artery has moved, then put back the intestine and sew it up.  
puis met sus la poudre enjanrant char, et se li ars l’ait muee, si met sus aucun oignement que soit present, tant que li plaie bowe;	then put on powder of ginger and if the artery has been moved, put on any ointment that is present, as long as the wound weeps. 
et chicent li fil, et soient soudez li sifac, et li mirach;	and sew up the threads, and let the sides be joined together, and the stitch.
puis cure la plaie si com les autres, tant qu’il soit sanez;	then treat the wound like the others, until it is healed. 
et se tu n’as medicines, si met sus, tantost qu’ele comance a giter bowe, coton viel, et le remue II fois le jor tant k’il soit sanez.	and if you do not have medicine, then put on, as soon as it begins to weep, old cotton, and move it two times a day until it is healed. 
Car tu n’as mestier d’autre medicine en plusors dispositions cant les plaies sont simples;	Because you do not need other medicine in many cases when the wounds are simple.
et se tu doutes que li plaie ne faice communiteit as membres principelz, si covient ke tu moilles lainne legiere en oile de tempree chalor, ou en oile roset, et la met entor les angres, et desoz les asselles;	And if you doubt that the wound does not make connection with the principal members, it is necessary that you moisten a linen cloth lightly in oil of temperate heat, or in rose oil, and place it around the angles, and under the buttocks.  
et s’il sent dolor ou porriture en bouelz, et maintes fois avient, si les clisterize de vin noir tede, et meismement se li porriture vient jusc’a l’intestine;	And if he feels pain or putrefaction in his bowels, and this happens many times, then administer enemas of black wine, and even if the putrefaction comes to the intestine. 
et le perce dedens, et saiches que quant c’est li gros intestines, si est plus legier a saner que li petis.	And pierce it inside, and know that when it is the large intestine, it is easier to heal than the small one.  
Li intestine qui est apelez «jeun» ne puet saner quant il est navrez, et c’est por la planteit des voinnes que i sont, et por la subtiliteit de tout le cors, et l’aprochement de sa nature des ners.	The intestine that is called "jeun" cannot heal when it is pierced, and this is because of the proximity of the veins, and for the subtlety of the whole body, and the approximation of its nature to the nerves.
Et si li zirbe saut de la plaie, si le remet arrier ausi com l’intestine, tandis qu’il est fres;	And if the worm jumps out of the wound, put it back in as if it were the intestine, while it is fresh.
et s’il est vielz et devenus vers ou noir, si covient que tu lies le leu qui est noir, que decorremens de sanc n’i viegne, car il i a voinnes et arteres;	And if it is old and has become maggot-ridden or black, then you must tie the place that is black, so that no bleeding comes from there, because there are veins and arteries. 
puis cope ceu qui est entre le liien, et met les II chiés pendans des la partie desoz la plaie jusque defuer por aligier l’estraction quant li zirbes chiet, et li plaie bowe.	then cut that which is between the ligaments, and place the two heads during from below the wound to outside in order to align the extraction when the bone falls, and the wound bows. 
de la routure dou boueil	of the rupture of the bowel
Quant li intestine est rons, et li plaie est petite, si la puet on restorer en aucuns homes, por ceu que je vis que uns hons fut navrez ou ventre d’une lance;	When the intestine is torn, and the wound is small, if it can be restored in some people, because I saw that one man was pierced or belly of a lance; 
et estoit li plaie au destre de l’estomac, et fut envillie et devint fistule, et en issoit li egestion et li ventositez;	and the wound was on the right side of the stomach, and it became infected and became a fistula, and through it came excrement and flatulence; 
je i mis cure selonc ceu que je poi, et ne cessai de subtilier tant qu’il fut sanez, et li leus soudez.	I put it under treatment according to what I could, and did not cease to sweat until it was healed, and the ends were closed.
Et quant je le vis souder, je doutai que li malaides n’eust mal en son ventre;	And when I saw it closing, I doubted that the patient would have ill in his belly; 
et il n’i ot point de mal, mais demora en millors dispositions, et menjans et bevans;	and he had no pain, but remained in better conditions, eating and drinking;
et dirent aucun experimentors que quant il a petite plaie en l’intestine, qu’il doit estre liiez en teil maniere:	and some experimenters say that when there is a small wound in the intestine, it must be bound in such a manner: 
pren fremis a grans testes, puis assemble les levres de la plaie, et quant li fremis ait overte la bouche, si la met sus les II levres, si qu’elle estraigne sa bouche sus;	take strips of cloth with large threads, then assemble the edges of the wound, and when the strip covers the mouth, place it on top of the two lips so that it pulls its mouth upwards; 
et puis li cope la teste, et ce se tient si qu’il ne puet desliier, puis met I autre fremit aprés en celle maniere que devant, tant que li plaie soit toute porprise;	and then cover the head with cloth, so that it cannot be untied, then put another strip after in the same manner as before, until the wound is completely enclosed; 
et cout la plaie.	and sew the wound.  
Cil chief si s’aerdent en l’intestine, et ne vient nulle nuisance au malaide, et se puet on liier l’intestine d’un fil subtil qui est copez de l’intestine d’une beste, en teil maniere:	This method is used for wounds in the intestine, and no harm comes to the patient, and one can bind the intestine with a fine thread that is cut from the intestine of an animal, in such a manner:  
pren le chief de cest fil d’intestine que soit mout descharnez, et puis lie au chief de cest fil I fil de lin subtil tort, puis boute le fil en l’aguille, et en cout l’intestine, et le ramoinne en la routure;	Take the head of this intestinal thread that is very smooth, and then tie it to the head of a fine linen thread twisted together, then put the thread into the needle, and sew the intestine, and pull it through the opening; 
et ceste maniere de costure de fremis nen est fuers que selonc la voie de fiance et d’esperance;	and this manner of stitching with threads is not against the way of faith and hope; 
et se li plaie est grans et large, meismement quant elle est en l’un des grailes intestines, si n’i a engien ne santeit, fuer que subtiliteit.	and if the wound is large and wide, even when it is in one of the lower intestines, there is nothing to be done except subtlety; 
de fistule ou qu’ele soit	of fistula wherever it may be
Saiches que toute plaie ou aposteme, quant il enveillist, si est apelee universement «fistule», et meismement quant elle est chevee et rent bowe.	Know that every wound or abscess, when it opens, is universally called "fistula," and also when it is healed and turned inwards.
Et fistule est selonc la verteit nodation fautree dure et blainche, ou on ne sent dolor, et est ausi chevee com li penne d’un oiseil;	And a fistula is according to the truth a hard and white node which one does not feel pain in, and is also shaped like the feather of a bird; 
et aucune fois en saut clere bowe, et autre fois espesse;	and sometimes it appears clear and thin, and other times thick. 
aucune fois poc, et autre fois assez;	sometimes small, and other times quite large; 
et je en ai jai parleit en la division des plaies, que toute plaie que n’est sanee, et il n’i a char, ce n’est fuers que par une des VIIII causes:	and I have spoken of it in the division of wounds, that every wound that is not healed and there is no flesh, it is only by one of the IX causes: 
c’est a savoir, par la petitece dou sanc ou cors;	that is to say, because of the little blood or flesh; 
ou por sa malice;	or for its wickedness; 
ou por ceu qu’il i a char dure dedens, et sus les levres, que n’i laisse naistre char;	or because there is hard flesh within it, and on the lips, which does not allow flesh to be born;  
ou il i a trop de bowe;	or where there is too much bulge; 
ou li leus est porris, et li matiere est de male qualiteit;	or where the wound is poor, and the matter is of bad quality;  
ou li medicine n’est mie bone en la cure;	or the medicine is not good in the cure; 
ou por ceu que li corruption est maniere de pestilence;	or because the corruption is of a pestilential manner;  
ou por la proprieteit en la region est tardive li digestion, et tarde li santeit, et enflee par nature;	or because the property in the region is slow to digestion, and late to healing, and inflated by nature; 
ou il i a voinnes ou os:	or where there are veins or bones;  
et j’ai ja mostreit toutes ces causes, et les signes, et les cures de medicines en la division.	and I have already shown all these causes, and the signs, and the cures of medicines in the division. 
Or covient que je te faice a savoir la cure de fistule qui est faite par oevre de mains.	Or it is necessary for me to tell you the cure of a fistula which is done by the work of hands.
Saiches que fistule avient en tous membres dou cors;	Know that fistula occurs in all members of the body; 
car il i a fistules que vienent as grans voines, et as arteres, et as ners, ou au syfac, ou a l’intestine, ou a la vessie, ou a aucunes des costes, ou a l’espinee dou dos, ou a aucune jointe des mains ou des piez;	for there are fistulas that come to the large veins, and arteries, and nerves, or to the liver, or to the intestine, or to the bladder, or to any of the ribs, or to the spine of the back, or to any joint of the hands or feet. 
et si a teil que vient a la proprieteit dou membre principeil, et as semblans leus.	and if there is one that comes to the property of the main limb, and similar parts.  
Et toutes les fistules que sont de ceste maniere sont de grief sanation, et n’i a fors que labour, et ignorance;	And all the fistulas that are in this manner are of grievous healing, and there is only toil and ignorance. 
et se il i a aucune fistule que ne veigne mie jusc’a leu que j’ai dit, et tu as fiance de la cure, et tu la vues conoistre, si pren une tente d’arain ou de fer, se li fistule est droite, si la quier;	And if there is any fistula that does not come up to where I have said, and you have faith in the cure, and you see it known, then take a tent of lead or iron, if the fistula is straight, if you will. 
et se li fistule est torte, si la cerche d’une subtil tente de plonc, car li plons se ploie mues entor la tortuositeit;	And if the fistula is crooked, then make a circle of a subtle tent of lead, because lead bends easily to the twists and turns.  
et se li fistule a mains pertus et tu ne la pues mie bien cerchier par tentes, si la clisterize par l’un des pertus, car la moistors si cort d’un pertus a autre, et la mundifie;	and if the fistula is opened by hand and you cannot easily search it with tents, then clench it through one of the openings, because moisture flows from one opening to another, and cleanses it.  
puis la quier saigement a ton pooir, que tu conoisses s’il i a os ou nerf, et est chevee em parfont, et demande bien au malaide de la dolor qu’il sent au presser de ta main, et le leu ou il la sent;	then carefully probe with your power that you know if there are bones or nerves, and whether it is covered by membrane, and ask the patient well about the pain he feels when pressing your hand, and where he feels it. 
et quant tu savras vraiement le leu ou elle est, et s’elle est loing de jointure, ou de nerf, ou d’artere ou de voine, ou en aucuns des leus que je t’ai dit, si la cope selonc ceu que je t’ai dit, et oste fuer la fautreure et les chars corrumpues que sont dedens;	and when you will truly know the place where it is, and whether it is far from a joint, or a nerve, or an artery or vein, or in any of the places that I have told you, then treat it according to what I have said, and remove the pus and corrupted matter that are inside; 
et puis la cure tant qu’elle soit sanee, et se li fistule est bien parfonde de droit endroit, si covient que tu copes em parfont, tant com tu pues, puis i met tentes moillies en medicine ague, et les boute jusc’au chief de la fistule, tant que li medicine corrode la superfluiteit qui est demoree au fons;	and then cure it until it is healed, and if the fistula is deep and straight, it is necessary that you cut into it as much as you can, then put moistened tents in a medicinal ointment, and push them to the top of the fistula, until the medicine corrodes the superfluity which is at the bottom; 
et puis i met oignemens enjanrans sainne char, tant qu’il soit sanez;	and then he puts ointment for healing flesh until it is healed. 
et s’il n’est sanez par ceu, si le cauterize si com nos avons dit, et se li os est corrompus de la fistule, si le cope.	and if it is not healed by this, then cauterize it as we have said, and if the bone is corrupted by the fistula, then cut it away. 
Se voinne ou ners ne te greve ou membres principelz, si com nos avons dit;	If a vein or nerve does not affect the principal members, as we have said;
et se li os est descovers, et il i a corruption et noiror, si lou reis tant que li corruption soit toute ostee, puis le cure de choses enjanrans char tant qu’il soit sanez;	and if the bone is exposed, and there is corruption and blackness, then  scrape it as long as all the corruption is removed, then treat with healing things as long as it is healed; 
et s’il n’est sanez, et rent bowe si com devant, saiches que tu n’es mie alez jusc’a font:	and if it is not healed, and returns like before, know that you have not gone as far as should be done;
si descuevre et quier tant que tu soies au fons, et oste toute la corruption, puis restore le leu;	If it is open and you wish as long as you are at the bottom, and remove all the corruption, then restore its place; 
et s’il est ensi sanez, c’est bien.	and if it is thus healed, it is well. 
Se ceu non, saiches que la corruption est trop en parfont, que tu n’i pues avenir;	If this does not happen, know that the corruption is too deep, that you cannot reach it;
si n’i a autre engien que dou lassier a nature;	if there is nothing else but to leave it to nature;
et s’il i a i petit os corrumput, et tu le pues traire as tenailles, si l’estrai a I estrument covenauble a ceu, et s’il i a maint os, si les trai trestoz, ne n’en laissier nes un;	and if there is a small bone corrupted, and you can extract it with tweezers, then extract it with the instrument suitable for this, and if there are many bones, extract them all, leaving none. 
et se li moistor te fait contraire, et il n’i a error ne paour, si cope et moistor et char, et delivre les os.	and if the moisture opposes you, and there is no error or fear, cut and remove both moisture and flesh, and deliver the bones. 
Et se tu ne les pues oster a une houre, si met sus la plaie chose enjanrant porriture, et laisse tant que li leus soit porris entor les os, et adonc si avront plus legierement les os;	And if you cannot remove them in an hour, put on the wound something preventing rot, and leave it until the flesh is rotten around the bones, and then they will be more easily removed; 
et se c’est uns grans os, si com de jambe ou de cuisse, si reis tant soulement la corruption tant que li noiror soit toute ostee, puis restoure la plaie;	and if it is a large bone, such as of the leg or thigh, then set only so much as the corruption until the blackness is entirely removed, then restore the wound. 
et s’il en i a grant partie dou corrumput, et vient jusc’a mole de l’os;	and if there is a great part of the corruption, and it comes right up to the flesh of the bone; 
si le covient soier et coper tout jusc’a la corruption, et puis le cure tant qu’il soit soudez;	then it is necessary to be and cut all the way to the corruption, and then cure it until it is healed.  
et je te dirai d’une fistule qui avint I home en sa jambe, si que tu i preignes exemple et aide en ton ovraige.	and I will tell you of a fistula which happened to the man in his leg, so that you may take example from it and help in your work.  
Il fut I jovencelz entor XXX ans, qui ot une dolor en sa jambe d’une cause que vint dedens le cors, tant que les matieres vinrent a la jambe, et fut enflee d’un gros aposteme, et n’ot point de cause defuer por ovrir;	He was a young man around thirty years old, who had pain in his leg from a cause that came from within the body, so that the matter came to the leg, and it was swollen with a large abscess, and there was no external cause for opening; 
mais li mire par lor folie ovrerent tant sus que li apostemes ovri, et en corroient mout de matieres, et devint fistule, et i vint mout de pertus que tuit gitoient bowe et moistor dou cors;	but the wounds by their folly work so much that the abscesses open and they corrupt much of matter, and become fistula, and there came much pus that all lying bowed and moist from the body;  
et maint mire i mirent cure entor II ans, et n’i ot nul saige en l’art de mains, tant que je i fui apelez, et vi sa jambe et les medicines dont on le curoit, et ceu que corroit par les pertus a grant cors;	and many wounds they did care for over II years, and there was no wise man in the art of hands, until I came to them called, and I saw his leg and the medicines with which they were treating him, and what corrupted by pus to great corruption; 
et devenoit rouges li cors dou jouvenceil, et avoit color citrine.	and becoming red the body of the youth, and had a color of citron.  
Je boutai une tente en l’un de ces pertus, et puis cerchai toz les pertus, et trovai que li uns venoit encontre l’autre de toutes les parties de la jambe.	I set up a tent in one of these pits, and then searched all the pits, and found that some came against each other from all parts of the leg.
Je me hastai donques, et copai en l’un des pertus tant que je descovri une partie de l’os, et le trovai corrumput et perciet, et venoit li corruption jusc’a l’os dedens;	I therefore hastened, and dug into one of the pits until I discovered a part of the bone, and found it rotten and pierced, and the corruption came up to the inside bone. 
je soiai ceu qui m’aparissoit de l’os corrumput, et cuidai qu’il n’i eust autre corruption, fuer que celi que je ostai;	I was certain that what appeared to me of the rotten bone, and I thought there was no other corruption, except that which I had removed; 
et comensai a restourer la plaie de medicines sodans par lonc tens, et ne pot souder;	and began to restore the wound with hot medicinal poultices for a long time, and could not heal it;
et puis rencomensai, et descovri l’os si com devant, et trovai la corruption continuee en l’os, et la soiai, et puis l’ostai, et me penai de souder le leu;	And then I started again, and discovered the bone as before, and found the corruption continued in the bone, and removed it, and then tried to solder the place; 
mais je ne pou tant que je copai entor une palme de l’os, et le traï fuer a tout son mole, puis le restourai de medicines;	but I could not heal until I dug around a palm's breadth of the bone, and found it entirely rotten. Then I restored it with medicines; 
et il fut sanez et soudez hastanment, et ne covint plus rencomencier l’ovraige fors por la foibleté dou malaide, qui ne pooit soffrir, et por la paour de mort que je avoie de lui.	And he was healed and joined soundly, and it did not again become necessary to begin the work except for the weakness of the patient, who could not endure, and for the fear of death that I had of him.  
Car por l’evacuation sanglotoit sovent, mais il fut sanez entierement, et nasquit en leu de l’os une char dure, et fut de bone disposition et n’ot point de nuisement ne de contraire dou tout en tout, ne a l’aleir ne a venir.	For the evacuation of blood often occurred, but it was cured completely, and in place of the bone grew a hard cartilage, and it was well-disposed and did not have any inconvenience or contrary at all, neither going nor coming.
Et se li os est brisiez en aucun leu dou cors, si le covient soier en ceste maniere:	And if the bone is broken in any place of the body, then it should be treated in this manner: 
pren I liien, et l’estrain au chief de l’os qui apert, et comande aucun k’il l’estende en haut;	Take a linen cloth and strain it at the head of the bone that is open, and command any one to extend it upwards. 
et met I autre lien de lainne plus gros dou premier liien, et le lie sus la char qui est desor l’os, et estent le chief, si que tu traies la char corrumpue au desoz, et descuevre la char sus le leu ou tu vues soier, que li soie ne blece la char;	And put another linen cloth, thicker than the first one, and tie it over the skin that is above the bone, and extend the head upwards so that you pull the corrupted flesh downwards, and uncover the flesh in the place where you wish to be, so that the bone does not bleach the flesh;
et met I tison ou une tauble desoz l’os por mues coper la char corrumpue;	and put a piece of wood or a board under the bone so as to completely cover the corrupted flesh.
et covient tant soier com on puet veoir et sentir la corruption, et soier ancor autre fois.	and it is necessary to treat as much as one can see and feel the corruption, and to treat again other times.  
Et se li os est corrumpus, et n’apert mie, et li corruptions est en mileu ou en une partie, si descuevre la char toute;	And if the bone is corrupt, and does not open, and the corruption is in the middle or in one part, then uncover the flesh entirely. 
puis met I tison desoz, et puis soie des l’une partie a l’autre la corruption, et soit li soieure dou lonc de la corruption I poc, si com nos avons dit;	then put the charcoal underneath, and then take it from one part to the other of the corruption, and be the ligature of the long end of the corruption by a point, as we have said.
et se li corruptions est en la jointure, si cope la jointure corrumpue, et soie l’os ou elle contient de l’autre part;	and if the corruption is in the joint, then cut the corrupted joint, and be the bone where it contains on the other side.  
et se li corruptions est en la continuation des II jointes, si n’i a autre angien que dou coper;	and if the corruption is in the continuation of the two joints, then there is nothing else to cut.   
et se li corruptions est ou poignil de la main, ou ou poignil dou piet, si est mout fort celle chose, mais toutevoie il covient que tu enquieres celle corrosion, coment elle t’apert;	and if the corruption is or in the finger of the hand, or or in the finger of the foot, then that thing is very strong, but nonetheless it is necessary that you inquire about that corruption, how it opens to you.
et la mundifie en toutes les manieres que tu pues, mais que li voine ou li nerf ne te faicent contraire;	and cleanse it in all the ways that you can, but that the vein or nerve do not hinder you.  
et saiches que li incisoire et les soies por coper ces os sont maintes, selonc l’assise des os et l’aparance d’ous, et lor grossece et lor subtiliteit, et lor grandor et lor petitece, et lor duresce;	and know that the instruments for cutting these bones are many, according to the position of the bones and their appearance, and their thickness and thinness, and their size and smallness, and their hardness.   
et por ceu covient il apareillier a chescune semblance d’ovraige son estrument;	and for this reason it is necessary to prepare each kind of work with its instrument; 
et saiches que l’uevre te moustrera l’estrument dont tu avras mestier, selonc la conissance de cest art, et le tesmoignaige des manieres des maladies;	and know that the work will show you the instrument of which you will have need, according to the knowledge of this art, and the testimony of the ways of the diseases.  
si porpense l’estrument dont tu as mestier selonc ceu qu’il le covient.	so consider the instrument which you need according to this.   
dou feu	of fire
Li chiés porrissent ou par cause dedens, ou par cause defuer;	The shoulder can be dislocated by means of internal or external causes;
et quant tu avras medicinee celle corrosion par la cure des medicines, et il ne profitent mie, si covient coper celui membre jusques au leu ou li corrosion vient, si que li malaides eschaipe par ceu de la mort, ou par la malice, qui est plus grans, de la defaute dou membre;	and when you will have medicated that corrosion by the cure of medicines, and they do not help, then it is necessary to cover that limb up to the place where the corrosion comes from, so that the patient escapes through this from death, or from malice, which is greater, from the defect of the limb. 
et li signes si est que li membres devient noir, si qu’il semble qu’il soit ars dou feu, et porrist aprés la noiror, pues va celle corrosions de membre em membre, et prent par tout le cors;	And the signs are that the limb becomes black, so that it seems that it is burned by fire, and after the blackness, then comes the corrosion of limb to limb, and takes hold throughout the body; 
si te haste dou coper, et se c’est par la percussion d’aucunes venimouses bestes, si com scorpion de mer et wivre et semblans, se li corrosion est au chief dou doi, si le cope, et ne li doner mie espaice de venir jusc’a la main.	If you hasten to cut it, and if it is by the percussion of some venomous beasts, such as a sea scorpion and viper and similar ones, if the corrosion is at the head of the thigh, then cut it off, and do not give him any space to come until his hand. 
Et s’elle vient jusc’a la main, si la cope a la jointe, si que la corrosion ne viegne jusc’a bras;	And if it comes as far as the hand, then cut it at the joint, so that the corrosion does not come as far as the arm; 
et s’elle vient au bras, si le cope au coute;	and if it comes to the arm, then cut it off at the elbow.  
et s’elle passe le coute, c’est li mors, et n’i vaut amenistremens fuers que li quantitez de sa vertut;	And if it passes the elbow, it is death, and there is no remedy left except the quantity of its virtue; 
et tot ensi fai quant li corrosion vient ou piet:	and so do all this when the corrosion comes or pit:  
s’elle vient en la premiere jointe, si la cope aprés l’autre jointe;	if it comes in the first joint, then cut after the other joint; 
et s’elle vient ou piet, si cope tout le piet;	and if it comes at a pit, then cut all the pit;  
et s’elle monte en la jambe, si cope a la jointure dou genoil;	and if it rises in the leg, then cut at the knee joint; 
et s’elle vient desus le genoil, si n’i a autre engien que dou lassier le malaide a mort;	and if it comes above the knee, there is no other remedy but to leave the patient to death.  
et li maniere dou coper ou dou soier le membre si est que tu le lie desus et desoz, et estende uns menistres l’un des liiens aval, et uns autres ministres l’autre liien amont, et tu dessevre la char qui est entre les II liiens a I spatumile large, tant que li os soit descovers;	and the manner of cutting or sawing the limb is that you bind it above and below, and extend one minister to one of the bonds below, and another minister to the other bond above, and you sever the flesh which is between the two bonds at a spatula wide, as far as the bone is uncovered;
puis le cope ou soie, et met de chescune part I drapeil de lin, si que li soie ne touche le leu sain, et viegne au malaide autre lesion et aposteme chaus.	then cut or saw, and put on each side the drapery of linen so that the saw does not touch the healthy place, and comes to the patient another lesion and abscess chaus. 
Et se decorremens de sanc vient quant tu oevres, si cauterize le leu hastanment, ou tu met sus aucunes poudres restraignans;	And if bleeding occurs when you work, cauterize the place diligently, or put on some restraining powders;  
puis revien a ta medicine tant qu’elle soit acomplie, puis lie le membre navreit d’un liien covenauble, et le cure tant qu’il soit sanez;	then return to your medicine until it is completed, then tie the affected limb with a suitable bandage, and care for it until it is healed; 
et je te conterai k’il avint a I home en som piet:	And I shall tell you that it happened to a man in his foot:  
il li avint une noiror qui sembloit arsure de feu, et celle corrosion vint premier en son doi dou piet, tant qu’elle porprist tout le piet;	He had a blackness that seemed burned by fire, and that corrosion first came in his heel of his foot, until it consumed the whole foot; 
et quant li hons vit la corrosion, si se hasta de coper le piet, et fut sanez;	and when the man saw the corrosion, he hurried to cover his foot, and was healed;
et lonc tens aprés li revint li corrosion ou doi de la main, et il vint a moi, et je li mis sus choses repercussives aprés la mundification dou cors, et ne pot cesser li corrosions;	and long after that the corrosion returned in his heel of his hand, and he came to me, and I put on him things to counteract it after the purification of the body, and could not stop the corrosion. 
et il vot que je li copasse la main, et je ne vou, que je avoie esperance de repercuter la matiere;	and it would be that I might grasp his hand, and I do not want, that I have hope of rejoining the matter;  
et doutai ausi que se je tailloie sa main, qu’il ne morist, car li vertus de l’ome estoit foible;	and I doubt also that if I cut his hand, he would not die, because the virtue of man was weak;  
et il se despera toz, et revint en sa terre, et se hasta de coper sa main, et fut sanez;	and he despaired entirely, and returned to his land, and hastened to cover his hand, and was healed; 
et je n’ai ceu conteit fuers que por ceu c’on faice autreteil, s’on en a mestier.	and I have this story related only for that reason if one needs it to do otherwise.  
Aucune fois vient aposteme en leu charnut, et demore si longement qu’il fait grant assemblee de bowe;	Sometimes an abscess comes in its fleshy place, and remains so long that it makes a great gathering of pus;   
et puis ront et perce, et en saut li bowe, et demoure li leus vuis, ausi com uns vasselz;	and then it bursts and pierces, and out comes the pus, and remains in its place like a vessel;   
et li cuir qui est desus est ausi subtilz com I drapelz deliiez, et ne corront mie jusc’a l’os, ne jusc’au nerf, et telz maladie si est apelee «sain», et n’est mie apelee «fistule»;	and the skin that is above it is also as subtle as fine linen, and does not break until the bone, nor until the nerve, and such a disease is called "healthy," and is not called "fistula";   
mais s’elle est si alongie qu’elle viegne jusc’a l’os em parfont, si est apelee «fistule»;	but if it is so lengthened that it comes to the bone by force, it is called "fistula"; 
et li cuire si est que tu cope celui cuir tout entor, et meismement quant il est subtilz, ausi com uns drapelz;	and the cure for this is that you cut all around that skin, and also when it is thin, like a cloth; 
et ne s’aert mie por sa corruption.	and do not let it be treated for its corruption.  
Et se tu as fiance que li cuirs s’aerde, et li corruption n’est mie en parfont, et li cuir est espés de char, si le cure de clistere ensi:	And if you are convinced that the skin is hardening and the corruption is not in depth, and the skin is thick with flesh, then cure it with a clyster like this:  
regarde se li seins est grans, et li bowe qui en ist est de puant odor, adonques le clisterize de medicine egiptiaine qui est ensi faite:	look if the chest is large and the part inside it has a foul smell, then clysterize with Egyptian medicine which is made like this: 
prenez aisil, et oile, et litargire, igalment, et metez cuire en I vassel au feu, tant que li medicine soit rouge, et deviegne ausi espesse com miel;	Take equal amounts of ashes, oil, and litharge, and put them in a vessel over the fire until the medicine is red and becomes as thick as honey; 
et puis pren de ceu selonc ta necessiteit, et le font en aigue et en miel, et en clisterize lou sein, et estraint le pertus;	and then take of this according to your need, and make it in sharp and honey, and in a clyster the breast, and restrain the wound; 
et laisse la medicine ens par II houres, puis l’estrai en espreignant;	and let the medicine stay in for two hours, then remove it by squeezing.  
fai ce mout de fois, tant que li seins soit mondefiiez, et soit ostee li puor;	do this many times, until the breasts are softened and the pain is gone; 
et aucune fois est clisterizeis d’aigue de cendres, quant ceste medicine n’est presens, et est que tu preignes cendres de fust de vigne, et giete aigue desus, puis la coule, et en clisterize, tant que tu saiches que li seins est bien mondez;	and at no time is it clystered with water of ashes when this medicine is not present, and that you take ashes from vine wood and pour water over them, then let it drain, and in the clyster until you know that the breasts are well softened. 
et se li malaides ne le puet soffrir, ne la medicine egiptiaine ne l’aigue de cendres, si le clisterize d’aigue et de miel ou il ait un poc de litargire broiet;	and if the patient cannot bear it, neither the Egyptian medicine nor the water of ashes, then clyster with water and honey or where there is a pinch of litharge ground.  
ou tu la clistirize de miel et de vin melleit, que li mielz ait proprieteit de mundifiier et de laver, et li vins fait aerdre le sain;	or you cleanse it with honey and sweet wine, that the honey has the property of purifying and washing, and the wine makes it breathe. 
et quant tu as ce fait, et tu as fiance que li seins est bien mundifiiez, si le clisterize de ceu que fait naistre char en li, et est que tu preignes emplaustre diafinit, et le font avec oile roset et en vin;	and when you have done this, and you are certain that the bowels are well purified, then cleanse it with what causes stool to emerge from them, and make a plaster of diaphinite, and make it with rose oil and wine; 
ou tu le clisterize d’aucunes medicines et d’oignemens, dont j’ai dit les proprietez ou traitier des oignemens;	or you cleanse it with certain medicines and ointments, of which I have spoken the properties or treatment of ointments;
et se li pertus dou sein est petis, et li cainne dou clistere n’i puet entrer, si l’eslarge d’un fer un poc, et met ens une tente de l’oignement egiptiein, ou oignement basilicon, tant k’il soit eslargiez;	and if the opening of the chest is small, and the tube of the clyster cannot enter, enlarge it with an iron a little, and put inside a tent of Egyptian ointment, or basil ointment, until it is enlarged. 
et se li plaie est trop large, si la cout et i laisse tant soulement I leu ou li clistere puisse entrer, et se li pertus que giete bowe est au desus, si le cope ou plus bas leu que i est.	and if the wound is too wide, so let it be left only as much as the clyster can enter, and if the opening that lies above is lower, so cover or raise it as high as it is. 
Car quant li bowe est en parfont, si n’i laisse enjanrer char;	For when the bowel is in place, let no flesh enter.
et se tu ne pues coper lou sein desoz si com tu vues, si appareille en tel maniere que li bowe corre au plus bas leu que i est, car quant li bowe est parfont, si n’i laisse enjanrer char et se tu ne pues coper lou sein desoz si com tu vues, si apareille en teil maniere:	And if you cannot cover the chest below as you wish, so arrange it in such a manner that the bowel runs to the lowest point where it is, for when the bowel is in place, let no flesh enter and if you cannot cover the chest below as you wish, so arrange it in such a manner: 
que li bowe corre legierement aval, et n’i lassier rien de la bowe;	That the bowel move gently down, and leave nothing of the bowel. 
et pren medicines consolidatives por mettre sor le sain, et estent sus I drapeil de lin que cuevre tout le sain;	And take consolidating medicines to put on the healthy part, and be on the linen sheet that covers the whole wound.  
puis cope as forces endroit le pertus dou sein I poc plus large dou premier, pues estent oignement souef sus I autre drapel selonc la quantiteit dou pertus, et le met sus le pertus dou sain por aligier la bowe, et n’oster mie le grant drapeil fuers que aprés maint jor une fois;	Then cope as forces to the opening of the breast which is more wide than the first, then ointment be put on the other sheet according to the quantity of the opening, and put it on the wound of the healthy part to align the bowel, and do not remove the large sheet outside except after many days once.
et celui qui est sor le pertus dou sein, oste sovent por oster la bowe, et saiches ceu que corra de la bowe, se c’est venin ou poc ou assez, ou digeste, ou indigeste;	And he who is on the opening of the breast, often remove to remove the bowel, and know what runs from the bowel, if it is venom or little or enough, or digested, or undigested. 
et pren warde se li patiens sent dolor ou nom, et s’il i a aposteme ou non, et quant ta medicine s’est en teil maniere estendue et tu vois la nature que saut sus le pertus dou sain, si saiches que li seins s’aert ja, et aproche li santez;	And take heed if the patient feels pain or not, and if there is an abscess or not, and when the medicine is in such a manner extended and you see nature that rises on the wound of the healthy part, then know that the breasts are now healing, and approaching health.
et puis le deslie le matin, ou le tier jor, et quant tu delies la plaie, si chainge I autre drapeil, et renovele l’oignement.	and then you untie it in the morning, or on the third day, and when you untie the wound, change the other bandage, and renew the ointment. 
Et se li seins giete bowe indigeste aprés maint jor, saiches que li seins ne s’aert mie.	And if the breast lies bowed undigested after many days, know that the breast does not heal well.
Et se venins subtilz cort aprés lonc tens, si ne te desperer mie de la santeit, car li santez aproche.	And if subtle poisons cut after a long time, if it does not make you despair of health, for the cure is approaching.
Car il i a homes cui tarde enjanremens de char en ses plaies, et de ces que font le contraire;	For there are men who delay healing of flesh in their wounds, and some that do the opposite.  
et se bowe indigeste saut dou sein aprés maint jor, saiches que li seins ne s’aert mie;	and he bows indigestion from his chest after many days, knowing that the breast does not heal. 
et se li seins tarde d’aerdre, et est porloigniez, si ajoste medicines sechans moistes en substance et seches en vertut, si com oignement diafinit, car il i a grant partie de vitriole, et c’est li derriene medicine;	and if the breast is slow to heal and is pulled away, he applies medicines drying moisture in substance and dry in virtue, such as ointment diaconite, because it contains a large part of vitriol, and this is the last remedy.  
pren oignement dyafinit, et le font avec oile roset, et l’arose de viel vin igal en substance;	take ointment diafinit, and make it with rose oil, and the rose of old wine equal in substance.   
puis le confit et en use;	then boil it and use it.  
et ceu meisme fait mielz cuit engroissiez, quant oignemens dyafinit n’est presens, ou tu pren mirre et aloen et encens, et le broie, et le poudre sus le miel quant il est sor le feu;	And that same thing is best cooked with honey, when the definition of an offering isn't present, or you take myrrh and aloes and incense, and grind it, and powder it on the honey while it is over the fire. 
et puis en glue I drapel, et l’estent sor le sein, et aucune fois i aministre on aristologe longe, et racines de lis celeste, qui est ausi com farine de veces et centoire;	And then in a cloth you wrap it, and the one placed over the chest, and sometimes it administers an aristolochia long, and roots of lilies celestial, which is also like flour of beans and centaury. 
et en use de simples ou de compostes:	And in use of simple or of composites:  
broie les, et en fai poudre, et met sus le miel que j’ai dit, et en use;	Grind them, and make powder of it, and put on the honey that I said, and use it; 
et se li cure est alongie, et n’est curez par ceste cure, adonc saiches que la corruptions est em parfont, et fait empression en l’os, ou as membres durs, ou as liemens;	And if the cure is prolonged, and isn't cured by this cure, then know that the corruption is in depth, and makes impression in the bone, or in the hard members, or in the limbs;
si le cure de la cure de fistule, si com nos avons dit ci devant.	if the care of the fistula, as we have said before. 
de l’aposteme de l’ungle	of the abscess of the angle
Panarice est un aposteme que naist desoz l’ungle dou pouchiet de la main, ou dou piet, ou par aventure naist en autres dois;	Panacea is an abscess that arises from under the knuckle of the hand, or the foot, or perhaps arises in other places. 
et quant il est envielliez, et on n’i prent garde, si i vient I aposteme chaus, et corront et giete bowe tant qu’elle corront la racine de l’ungle, et par aventure la corront toute;	and when it is neglected and one does not take care of it, then the abscess comes forth, and runs and hollows out a furrow until it runs to the root of the knuckle, and perhaps runs the whole way through. 
et vient li corrosions jusc’a l’os, tant qu’il i vient dolor puant, et est li chiés dou doi larges, et est li color fuxe.	and the corruption comes to the bone, so that there is fetid pain, and the joint of the limb becomes wide, and the color is foul.
Quant tu le cures si com nos avons dit en la division, et li cure ne profite mie, si covient que tu copes a i. fer toute la superfluiteit qui est demoree de l’ungle, puis cauterize la plaie aprés.	When you treat it as we have said in the division, and the treatment does not benefit, then it is necessary that you cut away all the superfluity which is remaining from the bone, then cauterize the wound afterward.
Li cauteres est mout grans aide se li os est sains, et li ungle est sainne;	The cautery is a great aid if the bone is healthy, and the knuckle is healthy; 
et se li ungle apresse la char ens, et l’encomence a poindre, et la blece, si covient que tu mettes lou rait desoz l’ungle que point la char, et la boute en haut, et cope celi char subtilment et legierement, et met sus le remenant de la char medicines ardans et corrosives por oster tout;	and if the knuckle after the flesh heals, and it begins to prick, and to blush, then it is necessary that you put the root under the knuckle that pricks, and drive it upward, and cut this flesh subtly and lightly, and put upon the remaining flesh medicines burning and corrosive in order to remove all. 
puis le cure d’oignemens tant qu’il soit sanez.	then the care of dressings until it is healed. 
Et se li corrosion est en l’os, si le cope, et trai fuer, car tant com li os corrumpus i est, si ne puet saner;	And if the corruption is in the bone, cut it out and treat it, because as long as the bone is corrupt, it cannot heal. 
et se tu vois le doi corrumpre, si le cope en I des nous si com il est devant dit, puis le cure tant qu’il soit sanez;	And if you see the two [bones] corrode, cut them in one as it was said before, then the care until it is healed. 
et s’il est ferus, et boutez, et il sent grant dolor, si covient que tu le sainnes premier;	and if it is broken and bruised, and it feels great pain, then you must first heal it;
puis cope l’ungle dou spatumile agut en taillant de travers desus, et warde que li taille ne viegne jusc’a la char qui est desoz l’ungle, car li malaides sentiroit trop grant dolor;	then cut the [bone] with a sharp spatula by cutting across above, and guard that the cut does not come to the flesh which is below the bone, because the patient would feel too much pain; 
et s’il avient, si met chose sus qui apaise.	and if it happens, put something on top that soothes.  
la dolor dou sourdoit de la main	The pain of the shoulder
Li dois ajostez qui naist en mains d’aucuns homes par aventure est toz charnus, et par aventure i a teil ou il a osses, et aucune fois i a ungle, et aucun d’aus naissent en la racine de la jointure, ou li naissance est en aucuns nous des dois.	The two joints that are born in the hands of some men by chance are all fleshy, and by chance there is where it has bones, and sometimes there is a nail, and none of them are born at the root of the joint, or the birth is in some of us of the two.
Cil qui naist en aucune nout dou doi ne se muet, et cil qui naist a la jointure dou doi, par aventure se muet;	One who is born in any knot of the two does not move, and one who is born at the joint of the two, perhaps moves;
la taille de celui qui est charnus si est legiere, en teil maniere:	The size of one who is fleshy is light, in such manner: 
taille le en sa racine d’un large spatumile.	cut it at its root with a wide spatula.  
Cil qui naist en la racine de la jointure si est grief a curer:	He who is born at the root of the joint is hard to cure: 
si te tien dou coper.	if you hold him down to cover.  
En celui qui naist ou doit au derrien nout, si covient que tu copes premier la char reondement jusc’a l’os, puis cope l’os a une soie convenable a ceu, puis le cure tant qu’il soit sanez.	In the one who is born or must at the back of our, it is fitting that you cut first the flesh roundabout until the bone, then cut the bone to a suitable length for him, then cure it until it is healed.
Li soudemens que vient as dois ensamble vient par naissance, ou par soudement de plaie, ou par arsure de feu, ou par semblans choses.	The blows that come to two joined together come by birth, or by binding of a wound, or by burn of fire, or by similar things.
Si couvient que tu copes celle soudeure, si que li doit repairent selonc lor formes naturelz;	If it is necessary that you cover that suture so that it may heal according to its natural forms; 
puis met entre dous tentes ou drapelz moilliez en oile roset, qu’il ne se soudent;	then place between two tents or cloths moistened in rose oil so that they do not stick together; 
ou tu met entre dous pieces de plonc subtilz, tant que li leus soit soudez, si com il covient.	or you put between two pieces of fine lead until the skin is joined, as it befits.  
Se soudemens vient a aucun de ses dois avec la paume, si cope celle sodure si com il covient.	If it happens to come together with the palm of any of its hands, bind that suture as is fitting.
des vils	of villages
Vis sont voinnes grosses envoloupees pleines de superfluitez melancoliouses, que vienent em plusors membres dou cors;	Veins are thick enclosures full of melancholic superfluities that come into many limbs of the body; 
et plus avient en jambes de ces qui vont a piet et qui travaillent et portent, que a autres.	and they more often happen in the legs of those who walk and work and carry things than in others.  
Il covient donques que tu li aministres aucune fois espurgement de cole, et puis le saine de la basilique.	It is therefore necessary that you administer to him once purging of col, and then the health of the basilica.
Li cure de fer si est selonc II manieres:	The cure of iron is according to II manners: 
l’une est c’on les cope, et traie on fuer le sanc noir;	one is that they are cut open, and blood is drawn out black.
et li autre maniere si est que tu lieves la voinne, et la trai toute fuer.	and the other manner is that you cut open the vein and drain it completely. 
Li taille si est selonc ceste maniere:	The cutting is done in this manner:
arose li premier la jambe d’aigue chaude mout fort, tant que li gros sans soit subtiliiez, puis estrain la jambe dou malaide des desus la cuixe jusc’a la partie desoz le genoil;	First, the leg is immersed in very hot water, until the large vein is soft, then the leg of the patient is strained from above the hip to the part below the knee; 
puis cope la voinne en I leu, ou en II ou en III, d’une taille large, puis eslieve et trair fuer le sanc noir a ta main, des l’un chief jusc’a l’autre, tant que tant de sans en isse com li vertus dou malaide puet soffrir;	then cut the vein in this place, or in II or in III, with a wide blade, then empty and completely drain the black blood from one end to the other, as much blood as the virtue of the illness can withstand;
et puis la lie, et li comande qu’il se teigne de viandes enjanrant cole noire;	And then to the wound, and command him to apply a poultice of black pitch.
et recomence l’evacuation et la sainie quant les voinnes sont plainnes, et nuist au malaide.	And resume bleeding and bloodletting when the veins are full, and harming the patient. 
Li alevemens de li est selonc ceste maniere:	The elevation of this is according to this manner:
reis la jambe dou malaide, s’il i a mout de poil, puis le met ou bain, et li arose la jambe d’aigue chaude tant qu’elle deviegne rouge, et enflent les voinnes;	Raise the leg of the patient, if there is much hair, then put it in water, and raise the leg with hot water until it becomes red, and the veins swell; 
et se tu n’as point de baing, si le chaufe au feu, et puis le cope endroit la voinne dou lonc au chief dou genoil, ou en la partie desoz a la cheville;	and if you have no bath, then heat it by the fire, and then cut the place of the vein from the top of the knee, or in the part below to the ankle; 
puis aoevre le cuir a l’oncine, et escorche la voinne de chescune part, tant qu’ele apere quant on la sent;	then open the skin with an instrument, and scarify the vein on both sides, until it appears when you touch it;
et on la voit rouge et noire, et quant elle entre ou cuir si semble ausi com une corde blainche;	and you see it red and black, and when it enters the skin, it seems like a white cord; 
puis boute le rait desoz, tant qu’ele soit alevee dou cuir, et puis la pent a l’oncine legier, puis le cope en I autre leu ensus III dois;	Then put the razor underneath, until it is lifted from the skin, and then place it lightly on the incision, then cut into the other place above III times. 
puis escorche le cuir sus la voinne tant qu’ele apere, puis la lieve au rais, si com tu as fait, et la pent a un autre uncine, si com tu as fait premiers;	Then scrape the skin above the vein until it appears, then lift it to the point, as you have done, and place it on another incision, as you did first. 
puis cope une autre taille, ou plusors se tu en as mestier, puis la lieve, et la cope au doi dou piet, puis la trai et lieve jusc’a la seconde taille;	Then cut another piece, or more if you need it, then lift it, and cut at the point of the foot, then scrape and lift until the second incision. 
puis l’estrai de taille en taille, tant qu’elle isse toute fuer, puis la cope;	Then extract it piece by piece, until it is all pulled out, then cut. 
et se tu ne la pues traire et lever, si i boute une aguille a tout I fil fort double, et la lie et la trai, et i boute desoz I rait, et torne ta main d’une part et d’autre, tant qu’il en isse;	And if you cannot scrape and lift it, then insert a needle into the whole thread strong and doubled, and tie and scrape it, and insert it below the razor, and turn your hand from one side to the other, until it is pulled out.
