et garde qu’elle ne cope, car s’elle cope, si ne la puet on traire ne lever, et en vient nuisement au malaide;	And guard that it does not break, for if it breaks, then one cannot draw or lift it, and it comes to a nuisance for the patient. 
et quant tu l’as toute traite, si met sor le leu de la plaie laine moillie en vin et en oile roset;	And when you have treated it fully, put on top of the wound's place wool soaked in wine and rose oil; 
et le cure tant qu’il soit sanez.	and treat it until it is healed.  
Et se li vis est contraite et torte et envoloupee ensamble, et ele n’est mie droite, si com nos avons dit, si covient que tu la fendes tortement, mais ne la coper mie;	And if the vein is contracted and twisted and enclosed together, and it is not straight, as we have said, then you must cut it twistedly, but do not break it;  
et la trai si com nos avons devant dit.	and treat it as we have said before.   
Li forme dou fer dont on cope la vis si est corbes, et ne trenche mie, qu’il ne cope la voinne;	The shape of the iron with which one cuts the vein is curved, and does not cut, so that it does not cut the vein;  
et est de grosse corbeure, car s’il estoit subtilz, si coperoit la voine, mais soit gros si com nos avons dit, et ci est li forme:	and is of thick curvature, for if it were subtle, it would cut the vein, but let it be thick as we have said, and this is the shape:  
de la voinne civile	of the civil vein
Ceste voinne est enjanree en jambes, en chaudes parties ou il ne naist herbes ne arbre, et en terre ou il n’a point de moistor;	This vein is established in legs, in hot parts where it does not grow herbs nor tree, and in earth where there is no moisture; 
et par aventure naist autre part qu’en jambes, et ceu avient de la porriture que vient desoz le cuir, si com il vient dedens le cors serpens et vers, enjanrez entre cuir et char.	And by chance it may be born elsewhere than in the legs, and this happens from the rot that comes under the skin, as it comes inside the body serpent and worms, lodged between skin and flesh. 
Et se li signes de l’encomencement de ceste voinne si est qu’il vient en la jambe une tres grans enflammation, puis se chainge li leus, et comence li voinne fors issir, ausi com une racine d’une plante.	And if the signs of the beginning of this vein are such that a very great inflammation comes in the leg, then it changes its color, and the vein begins to burst forth, as if a root of a plant.
Quant li chiés apert, si covient que tu envoloupes entor une piece de plonc des une З et demi jusc’a II З., et la noe, et laisse le plonc pendant a la jambe, et totes les fois qu’il en ist point au defuer, si l’envoloupe entor le plonc, et la nowe;	When the shoulder is opened, it is necessary that you wrap around a piece of plank from one and a half to two fingers, and tie it, and leave the plank on the leg, and every time he is in pain outside, then wrap again around the plank, and tie it.
et s’elle est trop longe, si en cope une partie, et envoloupe le remenant, et ne la coper mie en sa racine, tant qu’elle soit toute issue;	and if it is too long, then cut a part of it, and wrap the remaining part, and do not cut it at its root, until it is completely out. 
car se tu la copes, si rentre en la char, et fait venir aposteme et porriture ou leu, et male maladie;	because if you cut it, then it goes back into the flesh, and brings an abscess and rot there, and bad disease.  
por la queil chose il covient qu’elle soit traite poc et poc jusc’a chief, et n’en remaigne rien ou cors;	Therefore for this reason it is necessary that it be treated little by little until the end, and that nothing remains in the body.   
et est aucune fois ceste voinne quant elle est traite de V paumes de lonc, ou de X, et uns hons vint ja a moi, a cui elle issit de X paumes de long, et quant tu la copes, si boute I rais ou pertus, et la perce jusc’a fons, si que tout en isse;	And sometimes this vein when it is treated with the palms of long, or of X, and one fellow came to me once, whose vein was X palms long, and when you cut it, it throws out I rays or threads, and pierces it to the bottom so that all in goes;  
et soit vuidie li matiere qui est dedens, et amenistre au leu medicines enjanrans porriture aucun jor, puis le cure si com les apostemes.	And let it be emptied of the material which is inside, and administer to its place medicines preventing corruption any day, then cure it as the abscesses. 
Et aucune fois a ceste voinne mains rains, et meismement quant elle apert en la jointure dou piet, ou ou piet, et i vient mout de pertus, et dont il saut rains;	And sometimes in this vein many rains, and even when it opens in the joint of the foot, or foot, and there comes much of threads, and from which it leaps rains; 
cure le donques si com nos avons dit devant.	Cure then as we have said before.  
des vers qui naissent entre cuir et char	of worms that are born between skin and flesh
Ceste maladie est apelee en nostre terre «maladie de buef», por ceu qu’elle avient maintes fois as bués, et est un petis vers qui naist entre cuir et char, et va par tout le cors montant et dessendant, et le sent om bien a l’aler de membre en membre, tant qu’il desront le cuir ou il vait, et saut fuer;	This disease is called in our land "disease of ox" because it happens many times to oxen, and is a small worm which is born between skin and flesh, and goes all over the body going up and down, and it is felt well at the turn of limb to limb, until they reach the skin where it goes, and leaps forth;
et est enjanrez de porriture d’aucunes humors, si com vienent vers et serpens et lumbris et ascarides ou ventre;	and is endangered by putrefaction of some humors, such as come worms and vermin and ascarides in the belly; 
et doute on de son malice, car quant il va par le cors, et il monte au chief, et il vient a l’oil, par aventure rentre, et destruit l’oil;	and one doubts of its malice, for when it goes through the body, and it ascends to the head, and comes to the eye, by chance enters, and destroys the eye;  
et ceu avient maintes fois.	and this happens many times. 
Quant tu le vues curer et traire, si ne puet on fuers que quant il vait:	When you see it being cured and milked, then one cannot help but when it goes:
si covient donques que tu lies le leu desus et desoz d’un fort liien bien estroitement, puis cope sus et le trai fuer, et se li vers est em parfont en la char, et tu ne le trueves, si le cauterize de feu sus, tant qu’il muire;	so it behoves you to tie the place above and below with a strong ligature tightly, then cut above and milk out the pus, and if the worm is driven deep into the flesh, and you do not find it, then cauterize it with fire until it dies; 
et li plus grans nuisemens que il fait, si est qu’il corront l’oil, si com nos avons dit;	and the greatest harm that it does is that it corrodes the eye, as we have said;  
et se tu le vois venir ou chief pres de l’oil, si estraint desoz lui le sorcil forment, puis cope sus, et le trai fuer;	and if you see it coming or near the eye, hold under it a formed eyebrow then cut above, and drive the treatment. 
et covient user le malaide de mundifiement de cors de medicines solutives por les males humors porries, et se warse de viandes enjanrans porriture.	and it is necessary to use the patient of purification of body of medicine soluble for the bad humors corrupted, and avoid from meats causing rot. 
de la dolor qui vient de ventositeit	of the pain which comes from windiness
Ceste maladie est apelee en nostre terre «vakirir», et est une dolor que vient en aucuns membres, et pues se mue de membre en membre;	This illness is called in our land "vakir," and is a pain that comes in certain limbs, and then moves from limb to limb; 
et je vis ceu que je vos di.	and I see what I tell you.  
Je fui apelez a une femme malaide, et me descovrit som bras, et vis une petite enfleure en la voinne dou brais;	I was called to a sick woman, and discovered her arm, and saw a small swelling in the vein of the arm; 
et I poc aprés, li vis monter ausi com un ver a l’espaule, plus tost que nulle chose, ausi com vif argent quant il cort de leu a autre;	and I after, saw it rise as well as a worm to the shoulder, faster than anything, as if alive silver when it cuts from its place to another; 
li dolor se departit de celui leu, et se ficha en l’espaule, et puis un poc aprés corrut par tout le cors, tant qu’ele vint en l’autre brais;	the pain departs from that place, and fixes in the shoulder, and then a little after it corrodes throughout the body, until she came to the other arm;
puis me contait qu’elle tornioit adés entor le cors, si com je la vis.	then she told me that she was turning around her body, as I saw her. 
Je me mervillai mout coment elle se movoit ensi de membre em membre, car je n’avoie onques veut ceste maladie selonc ceste maniere.	I marveled greatly how she moved thus from limb to limb, for I never had seen this illness in this manner.
Toutevoie, je avoie veut maint que bien avoient veut movoir dolor de leu a autre, mais je ne l’avoie mie veut, si com je le vis en la femme;	Nevertheless, I wanted it that they might move pain from one place to another, but I did not want it so, as I saw it in the woman. 
et je me pensai que c’estoit por ceu que li femme avoit sec cors, et les voinnes descovertes, et por ceu apparoit celle ventositez constrainte;	and I thought that it was for this reason that the woman had a dry body, and her veins uncovered, and for this appeared that constrained windiness.
et n’aperent mie selonc ceste raison a ces qui sont delicious, et qui ont moistes cors et voinnes reponues.	and did not appear according to this reason to those who are delicate, and who have moist bodies and veins covered. 
Et quant tu vues curer ceste maladie, et li malaides sent celle dolor, s’elle t’apert si com nos avons dit, si la lie desus et desoz hastanment, et puis cope sus tant que cele ventositez constrainte au leu isse fuer;	And when you see curing this illness, and the patient feels that pain, if it appears to you as we have said, then lay it above and below carefully, and then cut up until that constrained windiness from its place emerges.  
et cauterize le leu;	and cauterize the place. 
et se tu ne la vois a tes eulz, si le cure de ceu qui deboute les ventositez, si com pilules fetides, et pilules de serapin, et semblans autres.	And if you do not see it with your eyes, cure it with those who treat the wind ailments, such as fetid pills and pills of serpent and similar others. 
des saiettes	of arrows
Les saiettes sont diverses, selonc lor semblances et selonc les leus dou cors ou elles chient.	The arrows are diverse, according to their appearances and according to the places of the body where they strike.
Li diversitez de lor si est qu’il i a de celles qui ont grans pointes, et petites, et chevees, et soudees;	The diversity of them is that some have large points, and small, and hairy, and soldered.  
et de celles qui ont II angles, et de celz qui ont lengues, et de celles ou il a pieces;	And of those which have two angles, and those which have tongues, and those which have pieces; 
et celle qui chiet en aucun membre si chiet selonc II manieres:	And those which fall in any member they fall according to two manners:  
ou en membre principeil cheveit, si com cerveil, cuer, foie, pormon, rains, intestine, vessie, et semblans membres.	or in the principal member such as brain, heart, liver, lungs, intestines, bladder, and similar members. 
Quant elle chiet donques en aucun leu de ces membres, et li signe de mort, que je te dirai ci aprés, t’aperent:	When it falls therefore in any place of these members, and the sign of death, which I will tell you after, appear to you: 
si covient que tu te warses de l’estraction de ceste saiette, car li mors vient aprés en plusors dispositions;	then it is necessary that you refrain from the extraction of this arrow, because death comes afterwards in many cases.  
et quant cist mal signe ne t’aperent mie, et li saiette n’est mie em parfont, si la trai, et cure la plaie.	and when this bad sign does not appear to you, and the arrow is not entirely in place, then treat it, and cure the wound. 
Et li signe dou cerveil quant li saiette i chiet et perce l’os, et saut li syfac fuer qui est sus le cerveil, est quant scotomie et sode et esvertin et roujor ens eulz, et enflammation et roujor de lengue, et spasme et permixtion d’entendement, et vomissemens de cole;	And the sign of the brain when the arrow falls and pierces the bone, and leaps the syvface which is above the brain, is when scotomy and sode and esvertin and redness in the eyes, and inflammation and redness of the tongue, and spasm and permixtion of understanding, and vomiting of mucus; 
et per aventure ist sans fuer des narines, ou des oreilles;	and perhaps it is without a furor from the nostrils, or from the ears;  
et par aventure pert la parole et la voix;	and perhaps it loses the speech and voice; 
et saut de la plaie moistor blanche semblant a poulz, et en saut ausi com bruee de char;	and leaps from the wound moisture white seeming to poultice, and leaps also as bruise of flesh;   
et se cist signe t’aperent, si te tien de la cure, et trai la saiette s’elle n’est ens.	and if this sign appears to you, then hold from the cure, and treat the arrow if it is not in place.   
Li signe de la siette quant elle chiet ou cuer, sont qu’elle est pres de la mamele senestre, et sent ausi com s’elle estoit fichie en chose dure, ne mie vuide;	The sign of the seven when it falls or heart, are that it is near the left breast, and it feels as if it were fixed in a hard thing, not empty. 
et par aventure li siette se muet ausi com li poulz, et en cort noir sanc, et vient froidor et suor froide, et sincope:	And by chance the seven moves also like the pulse, and in short black blood comes, and cold sweat, and syncope: 
saiches adonc sens doute ke li mors dessent.	Know then without doubt that death is coming.  
Et li signe de la saiette que nevre lou pormon est que sans plains d’escume saut de la plaie, et li gorge enfle, et li malaides mue color, et sospire haut et quiert le froit ar.	And the sign of the arrow that does not come out is that without plains of foam jumping from the wound, and the throat swells, and the patient turns pale, and sighs high and seeks the cold air.
Et se li saiette chiet en la coverture dou pis, si est delez les petites costes;	And if the seven falls into the covering of the hip, it is near the small ribs; 
et giete grant alainne et grant dolor et sospire;	and throws great pain and great sorrow and sighing;  
et li muevent tuit li membre des espaules.	and it moves all the limbs of the shoulders. 
Et se li saiette chiet ou stomac, par aventure si saut de la plaie aucune chose de la viande indigeste.	And if the arrow falls or stomach, perchance it leaps from the wound any thing of the undigested flesh.
Et se li saiette chiet ou ventre, et en saut point de fien par l’intestine rout, si n’a point d’esperance en la cure, ne en l’estraction de la saiette.	And if the arrow falls into the belly, and in a no point of fiber by the intestine route, then there is no hope in the cure, nor in the extraction of the arrow.
Et se li saiette chiet en la vessie, et li urine en saut et vient defuer, et li malaides sent fort dolor:	And if the seven falls into the bladder, and the urine leaps and comes out, and the patient feels great pain: 
saiches que li plaie est mortelz.	Know that the wound is mortal.  
Li autre membre, si com li faice et li colz et li gorge et li espaule et li adjutoire et li espinee dou dos et li forcele et li cuixe et les jambes, et li membre semblant, sont sauf selonc plusors dispositions.	The other members, such as the arms and necks and throat and shoulder and helper and spine of the back and ribs and hips and legs, and similar members, are safe according to more dispositions.
Quant li saiette est en lou nerf ou l’artere, et elle n’est venimouse, si com je vos dirai qu’il m’avint, por ceu que vos faciez autretel.	When the arrow is in the nerve or artery, and it is not venomous, as I will tell you that it happened to me, for that you may do otherwise.
Il avint a I home c’une saiette li chut ou larmier en la racine dou neis:	It happened to a man with an arrow in the root of his nose: 
je la tentai, et la traï d’autre part desoz la graisse de l’oreille, et fut sanez sens nusement.	I tried it, and pulled it from another side under the ear fat, and he was healed without feeling much pain. 
Et traï a un jeu une saiette que li chut en la graisse de l’oil desoz la papiere desoz, et li saiette estoit reponue, et n’en poi ataindre que la pointe devers lou fust, et estoit li saiette grans d’un arc turcois, a tout I fer legier sens oreilles;	And  I pulled out an arrow that had stuck in the fat of the eye under the eyelid, and the arrow was embedded, and I could only reach the point towards the shaft, and the arrow was as large as a Turkish bow,  all light iron without ears. 
li jeus fut sanez, et ne li vint nulz mavais accidens.	The man was healed, and he suffered no bad consequences. 
Et traï une saiette de la gorge a un crestien, et estoit li saiette arabique a oreilles:	And I pulled out an arrow from the throat of a Christian, and it was an Arabic arrow with ears: 
je soiai les barbions, et subtiliai tant que je la traï, et fut sanez li crestiens.	I softened its barbs, and carefully pulled it out until I reached the end, and the Christian was healed.  
Et traï une saiette a I home, que li estoit cheue ou ventre, et pensai qu’il moroit;	And treat an arrow to the man, who was wounded in the chest or belly, and thought he would die; 
et puis qu’il ot passez XXX jors, si ne mua point sa disposition;	and then that after passing XXX days, his condition did not improve;  
je taillai sus la saiette, et l’engignai, et la traï fuer, et n’ot point de mavais accident.	I cut above the arrow and extracted it, and treated him further, and there was no bad outcome. 
Et si vis I home cui une saiette chut ou dos, et fut li plaie soudee sus;	And if you see the man who had an arrow strike his back, and the wound closed above;  
et demora li saiette dedens li, et ne chainja point ses dispositions naturez, ne ne trova nuisement en aucune de ses oevres naturelz.	and the arrow remains inside him, and does not change his natural disposition, nor finds inconvenience in any of his natural works. 
Et vis I autre homme, cui il chut une saiette en sa faice, et fut soudee li plaie;	And if you see another man who had an arrow strike his face, and the wound closed; 
et demora ensi sens soffrir grant dolor;	and remains so without suffering much pain;
et mout d’autres semblans.	and many other similar things.  
Et traï une saiette a I home des princes le roi, que li estoit cheue enmi lou neiz, et estoit un poc declinans a la destre partie;	And treat an arrow to the man of the princes the king, who was wounded in his side, and was slightly declining on the right side; 
et estoit li saiette toute reponue.	and the arrow was entirely pulled out. 
Je fui apelez a la cure aprés ceu qu’elle fut cheue III jors.	I was called to care for him after three days had passed.  
Si trovai la plaie mult estroite.	If I found the wound very narrow.
Je la quis a tout une subtil tente, et ne la sentis mie;	I took hold of it with all my skill, and felt nothing at all. 
et il sentoit pointure et dolor desoz sa destre oreille.	And he felt pricking and pain below his right ear.  
Je pensai que c’estoit de la pointe de la saiette Je mis sus lou leu emplaustre atratifet digestif, por ceu que li leus n’enflast;	I thought it was from the tip of the arrow. I put a plaster of soothing and digestive herbs on top, because the ears did not swell.  
et m’aparut li leus de la saiette.	and the ears of the arrow appeared. 
Je i mis l’emplaustre mains jors, et resouda li plaie derechief, et demora ensi li malaides lonc tens, tant qu’il sentit la saiette I jor dedens son neis;	I put the plaster on again for a few days, and it closed the wound directly, and the patient stayed like that for a long time, until he felt the arrow one day inside his nose; 
et il le me dist.	and he told me so.  
Je mis sus la plaie medicine ague corrosive par mains jors, tant qu’elle fut overte, et la tentai, et sentis le chief de la saiette qui s’aerdoit au leu;	I put on the wound a caustic medication for a few days until it was open, and I probed it, and felt the head of the arrow which was hardening in place. 
puis ajostai en l’overture de la plaie par celle medicine ague, tant que li chiés de la saiette m’aparut visablement;	then I placed in the opening of the wound by that medicine sharp, as long as the head of the arrow appeared visibly to me; 
et trespassa bien li termines entor IIII mois, et puis eslarja si li plaie que je i boutai les tenailles, et le meus d’une part et d’autre, et ne pot issir;	and it pierced well the ends for IV months, and then I widened so the wound that I put in pliers, and my on one side and the other, and it could not escape; 
adonques ne cessai de subtiliier et d’engignier de manieres d’estrumens, tant que je la pris I jor as tenailles bien faites, selonc ceu que sa forme venra en la fin de cest chapistre, tant que je la traï, et restourai la plaie.	therefore I did not cease to refine and devise ways of instruments, until I took on the day pliers well made, according to those that its form will come at the end of this chapter, as long as I treated it, and restored the wound.
Et li mire jugent que li cartillaige dou nez ne puet restorer:	And the wise judges that cartilage of the nose cannot restore: 
je la restourai adonques, et fut soudee li plaie, et fut sanez li malaides entierement.	I therefore restored it, and the wound was joined, and the patient was completely healed. 
Or t’ai dit la qualiteit de l’estraction d’aucunes saiettes, si que tu mettes ta cure sus ceu que je ne dis mie, car li livres ne puet mie tout porprendre;	Now I have told you the quality of the extraction of some arrows, so that you put your care on those that I do not say, for the books cannot encompass everything;
mais li saiges maistres compere sus bien poc grant chose, et sus ceu que li est present et defaillant, trueve nueve oevre, et nuef estrument, au dessendement des choses estrainges qui avienent en cest art.	but the wise masters compare to a great thing, and to those that are present and failing, find new work, and nine instruments, in the descent of strange things which happen in this art. 
Je dis que les saiettes n’issent des membres ou elles sont fichies fuer que selonc II manieres:	I say that the arrows are not from members where they are fixed further than according to two manners: 
ou par lou leu ou elles entrent, ou par d’autre part;	or by the place where they enter, or by another part; 
et celle que saut fuer par lai ou elle entre, c’est saiette entrans en leus charnus, et saut fuer aucune fois maintenant.	and that one which is further by the place where it enters, is an arrow entering into their flesh, and never has been any other time.
Et s’elle ne saut maintenant, si la laisse tant que li chars soit porrie entor, et soit alegie li issue;	And if it does not now exit, let it remain as long as the flesh is pulled inwards and the exit is loosened; 
et ausi s’elle est fichie en l’os, et elle ne puet issir, si la laisse ensi aucuns jors, et la muef chescun jor;	and also if it is fixed in the bone and cannot exit, let it remain so for some days, and move it each day;
et adonques elle saut, et s’elle ne saut, si perce entor a tout I foret subtil, tant que li leus entor soit eslargiez, et puis la trai.	and therefore she leaps, and if she does not leap, then pierce around the entire forest subtly, until the forest around is enlarged, and then treat it. 
Et se li saiette est fichie en l’os dou chief, et vait jusc’a l’un des ventres dou cerveil, et aucuns des accidens que j’ai dit apert au malaide:	And if the arrow is lodged in the bone of the head, and goes up to one of the ventricles of the brain, and some of the accidents that I have said appear to the patient: 
si ne la traire mie, mais la laisse tant qu’elle soit igalz aprés aucuns jors, car se li saiette vient jusc’a syfac, c’est li mors.	do not treat it, but leave it as long as it is even after some days, for if the arrow comes up to the sinus, it is death. 
Et se li saiette n’est fichie fuer qu’en l’os soulement, et ne vient jusc’a syfac, et demoure li malaides aucuns jors sens mavais accident, si l’engigne dou traire.	And if the arrow is only lodged in the bone and does not come up to the surface, and the patient remains for some days without ill effect, then the instrument of extraction.
Et s’elle est mout fichie ensi et ne puet issir fuer, si i aministre tareres entor, si com je t’ai dit;	And if it is very deeply lodged and cannot be pulled out further, then administer tarantulas around it, as I have told you.
puis cure le leu tant qu’il soit sanez.	then cure the wound until it is healed. 
Et se li saiette est reponue en leu dou cors si c’on ne la puisse veoir, si la quier a tout la tente;	And if the arrow is lodged in the body and cannot be seen, then search for it with all your might;
et se tu la sens, si la trai a aucun estrument covenauble;	And if you feel it, then treat it with a suitable instrument. 
et se tu ne pues por l’estrecement de la plaie, et por la parfondesce de la saiette, et il n’i a os ne nerf ne voine, si la fens tant que li plaie soit grans;	And if you cannot by the stretching of the wound, and by the depth of the arrow, and there are no bones or nerves or vein, then cut as much as the wound is large.  
et trai la saiette se tu pues, et s’il ait en la saiette oreilles a coi elle tient, si oste la char qui est ens fichie de II pars au mues que tu pues, et puis brise ou ploie les oreilles de la saiette, tant que tu la puisses traire;	And treat the arrow if you can, and if it has ears to which it is attached, remove the flesh that is stuck on either side as much as you can, and then break or bend the ears of the arrow as much as you can pull it out.
et subtilie bien que tu ne brisier la saiette, que tu la trairoies plus griement.	And be careful that you do not break the arrow, but that you pull it out more easily. 
Et se tu ne pues a une fois, si la lai jusque li leus entor soit porris, puis la trai, car li estraction iert alegie.	And if you cannot do it at once, then let him lay until his leg is soft, then treat it, because the extraction is painful.
Et se li decorremens de sanc te fait contraire, si amenistre ceu que nos avons dit de la cure en son chapistre;	And if the flow of blood opposes you, then administer what we have said about treatment in its chapter;
et te warde de l’incision dou nerf et de la voinne, et met engien coment tu pues mues traire la saiette sens peril, ou tost ou tart, ou fermement ou belement;	And guard against the incision of the nerve and vein, and put everything as much as you can to pull out the arrow without danger, quickly or slowly, firmly or gently. 
et met le malaide selonc la forme qu’il estoit quant li saiette li chut ens, car c’est li plus grans aide que i soit, et se tu ne pues, si lou met selonc ceu que li signe lou te mostrent.	and set the patient according to the form that it was when the arrow struck it, for this is the greatest help that there is, and if you cannot do so, put it according to what the signs show you.  
Li saiette que vient fuer d’autre part, ou il apert aucune chose de li, ou li cuir est enflez endroit si c’on le voit ou sent aparamment:	The arrow that comes from another place, where one sees or feels nothing apparent, or the skin is swollen in place: 
taille donques sus, tant que les tenailles i puissent prendre, et puis l’estrai:	cut then below, as much as the tongs can take, and then extract it:  
si saut fuer maintenant.	if it jumps out now. 
Et s’elle est retenue en l’os, si tornoie ta main rondement, tant qu’elle entre en l’os, et eslarge l’os, puis la trai.	And if it is held within the bone, then turn your hand roundly, until it enters the bone, and widen the bone, then treat it.
Et s’elle ne puet issir, si la laisse encor, et puis rencomence l’estraction tant qu’elle isse fuer;	And if it cannot be extracted, leave it still, and then begin the extraction again until it comes out.   
et se li fust de la saiette i est, se le boute a tout le fust;	and if the shaft of the arrow is in there, put out the whole shaft; 
et se li fust chiet, et tu vues aministrer boutement, si i aministre I estrument cheveit, si que li pointe de la saiette entre en la cheveure de l’estrument;	and if the shaft has broken off, and you see administer pounding, you administer the instrument so that the point of the arrow enters into the head of the instrument:  
et puis boute fuer, et se li saiette est chevee, se i boute I estrument a pointe entrant ens, por alegier l’estraction.	and then thrust forward, and if the arrow is broken, put the pointed instrument inside, to ease extraction. 
Et se li saiette est entouchie, si covient que tu copes toute la char entor ou li venins est, se tu pues, puis cure la plaie si com il couvient.	And if the wound is surrounded, then it is necessary that you cut all the flesh around where the poison is, if you can, and then treat the wound as it is proper.
Et se li saiette chiet ou peis ou au ventre ou a la vessie ou au costeit, et elle est prochiene, et tu pues coper sus, se i cope;	And if the arrow lies in the thigh or belly or bladder or ribs, and it is close, and you can cover it, then cut it. 
et te garde de coper la voinne et lou nerf, et puis l’estrai, et puis cout la plaie, se mestier est;	and keep from cutting the vein and nerve, and then extract it, and then sew the wound, if necessary. 
et la cure tant qu’elle soit sanee.	and tend to the wound until it is healed. 
Li forme des tenailles dont on trait les saiettes sont semblans au bec d’oiseil, et vez ci la forme:	The form of pliers used to treat arrows resembles an eye's beak, and see here the shape:
Et en sont mout de manieres:	And there are many ways of doing this:  
grans, moienes, et petites, selonc la quantitei de la saiette.	large, medium, and small, according to the quantity of the arrow. 
Li forme dou boutant cheveit est ausi com li penne d’un oisel, por bouter a la pointe de la saiette, si com ci est li forme:	The shape of the pointed arrow is like the feather of a bird, to put at the tip of the shaft, as this is the shape:
li forme des tenailles por bouter et por sachier si est ci:	The shape of the pliers to push and to know if it is here.
des voinnes dou cors communes	of the veins of the body common
Des voinnes dont on se saine sont XXXI, de coi il a ou chef XVI, c’est a savoir:	There are thirty-one veins from which one heals, so it has sixteen heads, that is to say:
II batans qui sont aprés les oreilles, qui sont apelees les dous «herbech»;	two bats behind the ears, which are called the two "herbes"; 
et les II arteres qui sont en II temples apparans;	and the two arteries which are in the two temples appear; 
et II voines que sont en II larmiers des II eulz, que sont apelees «aspires»;	and the two veins that are in the two tear ducts of the eyes, which are called "aspirates";  
et li voine que est emmi le front;	and the vein that is in the middle of the forehead; 
et li voinne que est au chief dou neis;	and the vein that is at the back of the neck; 
et les II guindeges qui sont ou col;	and the two veins that are in the throat; 
et les II voinnes que sont en levres desus de la bouche, et ce sont les voines que sont apelees «augeherich»;	and the two veins that are in the upper lips, and these are the veins that are called "augeherich"; 
et II voinnes que sont desoz la lengue.	and the two veins that are under the tongue.
Les voinnes dont on saine communement sont V en chescun bras:	The veins of which one commonly finds five in each arm: 
l’une est li cephalique, et est dou senestre costeit, et l’apelent li laie gens «voinne dou chief»;	one is the cephalic, and is from the inner side of the elbow, and the common people call it "vein of the head";
et li moiene est apelee «faste», et est composte de la cephalique et de la basilique, et l’apelent li laie gens «voinne dou cuer»;	and the middle one is called "fascia" and it is composed of the cephalic and the basilica, and the common people call it "vein of the heart"; 
et li basilique si est ou destre costeit, et l’apelent li laie gent «voinne dou ventre», et est sus le foscile, et est celle dont on saine, qui apert manifestement sus le pouchet.	and the basilica is where the right rib is, and they call it by the common people "vein of the belly", and it is above the fossil, and it is the one that we drain, which opens clearly above the pouch. 
Et li salvatelle est li voine qui est entre l’auriculaire et l’anulaire, et si a II rains;	And the saphenous vein is the vein that is between the ring finger and the little finger, and there are two of them. 
et en la jambe et ou piet sont III voinnes:	and in the leg and foot there are three veins:
l’une si est desoz la corbeure dou pochet dou senestre costeit, et li seconde sophene qui est a la cheville dou destre costeit;	one is below the curve of the pouch of the left rib, and the second saphenous which is at the ankle of the right rib.
et li voine qui est apelee «nesse», que est en la cheville de l’autre costei;	and the vein that is called "nesse", which is in the ankle of the other side. 
et en l’autre jambe sont III voinnes desoz celles.	and in the other leg there are three veins below those. 
Li sainie des voinnes que sont aprés les oreilles si aide as catharres anciens, et a emigraine;	Draining the veins that are after the ears helps with old cataracts and migraines.
et li qualiteis dou sainier, si com je te dis, et est que tu reises lou chief dou malaide, et frote lou leu ou les voinnes sont d’un drap aspre;	and the qualities of the vein, as I tell you, and is that you raise the head of the patient, and rub the place where the veins are with a rough cloth.  
puis estrigne li malaides son col a une vis, tant que les II voinnes aperent derrier les oreilles en II leus dependens dou chief:	then tighten the patient's neck to a vise, until the two veins appear behind the ears in their places depending on the head. 
quier les donques a ton doi, et ou tu sens lou poulz desoz ton doi, si seigne d’enche;	then where you feel your pulse below your shoulder, feel for it there too.  
puis pren la lancette, et la boute par desoz la voine jusc’a l’os, puis lieve ta main a tout la voinne amont, et cope et lou cuir et la voinne bien II dois dou traver, et fai issir dou sanc tant que tu vues;	then take the lancet and thrust it below the vein to the bone, then raise your hand over the entire vein above, and cut through the skin and vein well at their intersection, and let blood flow out as much as you see.  
puis l’estrain et lie, tant qu’ele soit sanee;	then strain and tie it, until it is healed; 
et j’ai ja dit l’incision et le cautere ou premier livre.	and I have already said incision and cautery in the first book.  
Li sainie des II arteres que sont en II temples, si vaut a emigrainne anciene, et sode, et obtalmie acostumee, et au cors des larmes agues as eulz;	The bloodletting of the two arteries that are in the two temples, it is good for old migraine, and sudden, and habitual ophthalmia, and to the body of the eyes' sharp tears.   
et li qualitez dou sainier si est si com je dis:	and the qualities of bloodletting are as I say:  
et est que li malaides estraigne son col, tant que les II voinnes aperent apertement;	And that the patient strains his neck so that the two veins appear openly; 
et sent lou polz desoz ton doi, et puis seigne d’enche;	and feels the pulse below his ear, and then he should direct (the bloodletting);
puis lieve lou keur sus la voinne en haut a ton doi indice, et boute la lancette desoz, et lieve la voine en haut, et la cope, si com tu as fait en II autres voinnes, et fai corre dou sanc selonc ta necessiteit;	Then raise the heart above the vein on high with your index finger, and thrust the lancet beneath, and lift the vein upward, and cut it, as you have done with other veins, and make correction of blood according to your need. 
puis deslie lou malaide, et met ton doi sus la voine une houre, puis met sus coton;	Then untie the patient, and put your finger on the vein for an hour, then put cotton on it; 
et puis la lie forment, et la laisse tant qu’elle soit sanee;	and then the scab forms, and let it remain until it is healed.  
et nos en avons jai parleit et de lor copement et de lor estraction, ou comencement dou livre.	and we have spoken of their treatment and extraction, as the beginning of the book. 
Li sainie de la voine dou front si vaut autant com li sainie de la cephalique as maladies de la faice ancienes, et a emigraine, et a roujor;	The blood from the vein on the forehead is as valuable as the blood from the cephalic vein for old facial ailments, and migraines, and redness; 
et li qualitez si est que li malaides estraigne son col en tordant, tant que li voine apere;	and its quality is that the patient strains their neck by twisting, until the vein appears; 
puis pren l’estrument qui est apelez «fosseur», dont ci est li forme:	then take the instrument called "digger," whose form is:  
Et met la pointe sus la voinne, et fier sus de ta main, ou d’autre chose, et laisse dou sanc issir selonc la quantiteit que tu vues;	And place the tip on the vein, and press down with your hand, or something else, and let the blood flow according to the quantity you see; 
puis delie au malaide le col, et lie la voine tant qu’elle soit saneel et aucune fois l’uevre on d’un flaime large.	then loosen the patient's neck, and tie the vein until it is healed, and never do the work with a wide flame. 
Toutevoie, il ne covient mie que li flaimes soit trop agus;	Nevertheless, it does not behoove for the flames to be too strong. 
et le saine de travers, car li os est pres, et par aventure brise li flaimes quant il est subtilz.	and the healthy tissue be scorched, because the bone is near and by chance the flames break when they are subtle.  
Li sainie des II voines que sont en II larmiers si aide as eulz, et a la tigne, et a la roujor, et a l’oriuel en l’oil, et as maladies de la faice;	The healthy tissue of the two veins that are in the two eyelids helps the eyes, and the head, and the throat, and the root in the eye, and the diseases of the face; 
et li qualitez de lor sainie si est que li malaides estraigne son col en tordant d’aucun liien, si com devant;	and the qualities of their healthy tissue are that the patient strains their neck by twisting from any linen, as before; 
puis le saine, et soit li sainie dou traver, un poc dou lonc dou flaime un poc large, car il n’i a point de char.	then the healthy tissue, and whether it be the healthy tissue through the traverse, a little of the long of the flame a little wide, because there is no flesh.  
Et se li flaimes est subtilz, par aventure si brise;	And if the flames are subtle, by chance they break. 
puis fai corre dou sanc, tant com tu en as mestier, et puis lie sus couton, et le lie bien.	Then make a cut of blood, as much as you need, and then bind it with cloth, and tie it well.  
Li sainie de la voine dou neis si vaut a ague, et a sode forsenee, et a maladies de faice, si com emigraine et roujor que vient en la faice, et meimement quant elle est anciene;	The blood of the vein of the arm is good for fever and for sore throat, and for diseases of the face, like migraine and redness that comes in the face, and even when it is old. 
et li qualitez de la sainie si est que li malaides estrigne son col, puis estrain son neis a ta main senestre, et pren lou flaime subtil lonc, et le fiche emmi la levre en l’espaice qui est entre les II narines, car li voinne n’apert mie bien enqui, et li sans comencera maintenant a corre;	and the qualities of the blood is that the patient constricts his neck, then draws his arm to his left hand, and takes a fine long thread, and puts it in the space between the two nostrils, because the vein does not open well there, and the blood will now begin to flow;  
et n’aler mie trop em parfont, et fai corre dou sanc selonc ta necessiteit, puis la lie une nuit, car elle est mout tost restoree;	and do not let it go too far in depth, and make the blood flow according to your need, then tie it up for a night, because it is very quickly restored; 
et c’est li forme dou flaime:	and this is the shape of the thread:  
Li sainie des II guindeges si aide a l’estrecement de l’alainne, et a l’encomencement de meselerie, et a mout de maladies, et a empetigine, et a corrodens, et a herpes, et estiomenes;	The blood of the two armpits helps with the easing of the breast, and for inflammation, and for many diseases, and for gangrene, and for corrosions, and for herpetic ulcers,  
et li qualitez de la sainie si est que li malaides estraigne son col desoz l’une et l’autre, si com nos avons dit;	and the qualities of the vein are such that the patient restrains their neck below on both sides, as we have said.  
et soit li maistres estans sus lou chief dou malaide, et li malaides siece sus I siege, puis saine la voine dou lonc un poc largement, puis trai dou sanc tempreement, ou tant com mestier est;	and let the master stand above the head of the patient, and the patient sit on a seat, then open the vein in the long place a little widely, then draw out blood moderately, or as much is needed. 
puis refai autreteil en l’autre voinne, puis deslie lou liien, et estraint andous les voines moienement, que li malaides n’estrangle;	then redo the other side in the other vein, then untie the ligature, and restrain both veins moderately so that the patient doesn't strangle.  
et le laisse jusc’au matin, que li plaie soit sanee.	and leave him until morning, so that the wound is healed. 
de la sainie des leivres	of the veins of the books
Li sainie des voinnes des levres desus si aident a cole en la bouche, et a corruption de gencives, et fendures de levres, et dou neis et entor.	The blood of the veins above the lips helps in healing wounds inside the mouth, and to corruption of gums, and fissures of the lips, and to sores and inflammation.
Et li qualitez de la sainie si est de faire seoir lou malaide devant toi, et estraint son col si com j’ai dit;	And the qualities of the vein are to make the patient sit in front of you, and restrain their neck as I have said. 
puis torne la levre, et regarde as II voinnes, dont l’une est a la destre levre et li autre a la senestre, et les conoist on par ceu qu’elles sont noires, et par ceu que entor elles a voines menues noires:	Then turn the lip, and look at the two veins, one is on the right side of the lip and the other on the left side, and recognize them because they are black, and because around them are small black veins. 
cope donques l’une et l’autre, et se tu ne les conois, et tu en es en doutance, si cope la plus grosse de chescune part, et tout ausi fai des II voinnes que sont desus et desoz, car c’est une meisme maniere.	Therefore one and the other, and if you do not know them, and you are in doubt, so cut the largest of each side, and also make two veins that are above and below, because it is the same manner. 
de la sainie desoz la lengue	from the vein under the tongue
Li sainie des voinnes que sont desoz la lengue si aide aprés la sainie de la cephalique, et c’est a l’estrecement de la gorge, et as maladies de l’uve, et as maladies de la bouche;	The bleeding of the veins that are below the tongue helps after the bleeding of the cephalic, and it is at the stricture of the throat, and to the diseases of the eye, and to the diseases of the mouth. 
et li qualitez dou sainier si est que li malaides siece entre tes mains devant lou soleil, et li lieve la lengue, et regarde desoz en chescun costeit une voinne noire:	And the qualities of the bleeder is that the patient lies between your hands in front of the sun, and he lifts the tongue, and looks below on each side a black vein: 
saine donques l’une et l’autre, et n’aler mie trop em parfont, car desoz sont les arteres.	Therefore bleed one and the other, and do not go too far into them, because below are the arteries.  
Les voinnes dou coute dont on saine communement sont sainies selonc II manieres:	The veins of the arm which we commonly bleed are bled according to two manners: 
ou em poignant a tout I flaime mirtin large, ou olivaire subtil si com coutez trenchans, et est apelez «anesil»;	or they prick at all flame martin broad, or olive subtle as you hear trenching, and it is called "ancil";  
et sont large et subtil selonc la largesce et l’estrecement des voinnes.	and are wide and subtle according to the width and the narrowing of the veins. 
Li forme dou flaime mirtin si est mout renommee, et est large si com tu vois:	The form of the flame martin is very well known, and it is wide as you see.
Et ait mestier por ovrir les voinnes chevees plaines de gros sanc apparent, et que contienent gros sanc et trouble;	And it is necessary for opening the deep veins plain of thick blood appearing, and that contain thick and troubled blood;  
et c’est li forme dou flaime olivaire:	and this is the form of the olive flame: 
et est plus subtilz apointé, et est por sainier les voinnes subtilz, ou il a subtil sanc citrin.	And it is more subtly pointed, and is for bleeding the veins subtly, where there is subtle yellow blood.
Li sainie de la basilique, qui est une de ces voinnes, si aide as maladies que sont desoz la gorge, et ou col, et ou peis, et ou ventre;	The vein of the basilica, which is one of these veins, so aids the sicknesses that are below the throat, and at the neck, and at the chest, and at the belly; 
et covient au sainor qu’il saine saigement, et qu’il se warse de l’artere qui est desoz.	and it is necessary for the lancet to cut wisely, and that he avoid the artery which is below.  
Et s’il cope l’arterre, et decorremens de sanc vient, si le covient estainchier, si com j’ai dit;	And if it cuts the artery, and a torrent of blood comes, then it must be stopped as I have said;
et ne doit mie estre poignans li flaime, mais taillans si com anesil.	And the flame must not be pricking but cutting like a knife. 
Et se li basilique n’apert manifestement, si covient que tu l’estrainges, et chainge une autre;	And if the basil doesn't open manifestly, then it is necessary that you extract it and change another.  
ou tu quieres aucun rain de li, ou tu saine en leu de li la voinne emmi le bras:	or you wish no vein of it, or you heal in its place the vein in the arm: 
elle apert manifestement;	it opens manifestly. 
et la cope au flaime anesil, si com nos avons dit.	And the cup to the knife like we have said.  
Et se tu vues conoistre le leu de la sainie, si covient ainsois que tu estraignes lou bras, que tu touches le leu tant que tu conoisses le poulz;	And if you want to know the place of the vein, then it is necessary thus that you extract the arm, that you touch the place as long as you know the pulse;  
puis signe le leu d’enche, et puis lie lou bras, et cope la voine dou flaime anesil;	then sign the place with ink, and then tie the arm, and cut the vein with the knife. 
et warde que tu ne ferir en l’artere quant tu vois le leu enfleit, car c’est de l’artere:	And guard that you do not wound in the artery when you see the place inflamed, because it is of the artery.  
eschui la donques.	Then follows. 
Et se tu vois saillir en haut ausi com l’urine d’un enfant, et li sans est rouges et subtilz, saiches que c’est sans de l’artere:	And if you see it rise up also like the urine of a child, and its color is red and subtle, know that it is blood from the artery: 
haste toi donques, et met ton doi sus longement, puis oste ton doi se li sans estainche, que maintes fois avient;	Hurry then, and place your hand lengthwise on top of it, then remove your hand if the flow stops, which often happens;  
se lie lou bras, et laisse ensi, et ne lou mueve li malaides;	if the arm is bleeding, and let it be so, and do not move it for the patient;
et soit sus paour, et ne lou mueve tant qu’il soit sanez.	and be wary, and do not move it until it is healed. 
Et se li sans n’est estainchiez, et il te vaint, et li medicine ne t’est presens, si cope l’artere s’elle apert, car li chief de li retraient;	And if the flow does not stop, and it is bothering you, and the medicine is not present, then cut the artery if it opens, for the head of the retraction; 
et estainche li sans.	and stop the blood flow. 
Et pren une escorce de fistice, et la fent, et pren l’une des moitiez et lie sus bien jusc’a l’autre jor;	And take a strip of licorice, and make it, and take one of the halves and tie it well up to the other day. 
se li sans estainche, c’est bien;	If the skin is stretched, it is good. 
se ce non, si le cure, si com nos avons dit, des poudres qui estainchent sanc;	If not, cure it, as we have said, with powders that stretch the skin.  
et li estainchemens n’est mie griés em plusors dispositions por le petit leu de la plaie, et la possance dou liien dou bras.	And the stretching is not grieved in more positions for the small place of the wound, and the possession of the arm's bond. 
Li sainie de la voinne em mileu si aide qu’elle trait sanc dou chief desus, et dou cors desoz, por ceu qu’elle est composte de la basilique et de la cephalique, si com nos avons dit;	The vein in the middle helps so much that it treats blood from the head above and from the body below, because it is composed of the basilica and cephalic, as we have said. 
et covient au sainor qu’il se warse por lou nerf qui est desoz, et s’il point trop em parfont, et il trueve lou nerf, et il enfle et li santez soit griés, et par aventure ne puet saner;	And it befits the surgeon that he place himself near the nerve which is below, and if he does not go too deep, and he finds the nerve, and it swells and the wounds are grazed, and perhaps cannot heal; 
et cist nerf apert mult de fois, et s’il n’apert en aucuns homes por sa subtiliteit, si covient que tu lou saines de l’estrument anesil;	And this nerve is opened many times, and if it does not open in any man because of its subtlety, then you must clean it with the anointing instrument. 
et eschui lou nerf a ton pooir.	And push the nerve to your power.  
Et se il a voinne entre les II ners, si la fent dou lonc.	And if he has a vein between the two nerves, then make it long.
Li sainie de la cephalique si aide, qu’ele atrait sanc dou chief, et aide as eulz;	The cephalic vein's draining helps, that it draws blood from the head, and helps the eyes; 
et covient sainier em poignant au flaime olivaire ou au flaime mirtin, car c’est li plus sauve de toutes les voinnes, car il n’a desoz li ne nerf ne artere.	And it is necessary to drain by pricking at the olive vein or the myrtle vein, because that one is the most safe of all veins, for it does not have a nerve nor artery.  
Toutevoie, covient querir lou plus legier leu, et ne grieve rien s’on faut la premiere fois, et on rencomence;	However, it is necessary to seek the lighter spot, and do not grieve if one must try the first time, and one tries again. 
et par aventure enfle li leus a aucuns homes, cant on faut la premiere fois, mais il ne grieve rien.	And by adventure it swells the eyes in some men, as soon as one tries the first time, but it does not cause any harm. 
La qualitez de la sainie si est selonc ta pensee.	The quality of the blood is according to your thoughts.
Li premiere chose que tu dois savoir de sainier, si est que sainie n’est amenistree fuer que por garder santeit, et por eschuir les maladies a venir;	The first thing you should know about healing, is that bleeding is administered only to preserve health, and to avoid future diseases. 
et soit li sainie faite en l’une des III voinnes que sont ou coute:	And let the bleeding be done in one of the three veins that are or cotte:  
c’est a savoir, cephalique, faste, et basilique;	that is to say, cephalic, femoral, and basilica; 
et se doit on sainier en l’encomencement de prientens a geun, et en autompne et en yver aprés mengier, quant li signe de repletion aperent;	And one must bleed at the beginning of Lent, in spring and winter after eating, when the sign of repletion appears. 
et se doit on sainier le premier jor ou le tier, aprés II houres ou III dou jor.	and one must bleed the first day or third day, after two hours or three days.  
Li sainie qui est aministree as maladies n’a point d’oure determinee, mais que quant besoing est de jor ou de nut, en toutes houres et en toz tens;	Bleeding that is administered for illnesses has no determined hour, but when need is of the day or of the night, at all hours and in all times.
et ne covient mie sainier les enfans jusc’a XIIII ans, ne femme portant fuer que des lou quart mois jusc’a septime.	and it is not fitting to bleed children until fourteen years old, nor women carrying for more than the fourth month until the seventh.
Ne ne se doient mie sainier li viel qui ont passez LX ans.	Do not bleed those who have passed sixty years old.
Et quant aucuns se vuet sainier, en quel maniere que ce soit, si covient k’il mondefie les intestines d’un clistere legier, s’il a mout de fiens retenut, si que les voines n’atraient des intestines les superfluitez porries nuisans as membres principelz;	And when some wants to bleed, in any manner that it may be, it is necessary that they clear the intestines with a light clyster, if they have much phlegm retained, so that the veins do not attract the superfluous and harmful fluids to the principal members;
ne ne se saine mie cil qui est trop saolez de viandes, ne qui est yvres, tant k’il en soit fuer, ne ydropiques;	Nor does one bleed well who is too full of meats, nor who is drunk, as long as he is, nor the dropsy-stricken. 
et se warse on de sainier aprés colique passion, et vomissement, et decorrement de ventre, et multipliement d’abiter a femme, et de traval, de veiller et de juner, et ceu que tot la vertu, ou par chose de l’arme ou dou cors;	and worse still to bleed after colic passion, and vomiting, and diarrhea, and multiple of labor in women, and childbirth, and vigil, and fasting, and that which totally the virtue, or by thing of the arm or of the body;
puis subtilie les humors, se li sans est gros, par viandes et par bevraiges et par medicines, se tu en as lou poir;	then purify the humors, if he is thick with meats and drinks and medicines, if you have his permission for it.
puis entre ou bain, s’aucune chose ne lou deffent, por subtiliier lou sanc, et te saine de la voinne dou pis entor la tierce, si com nos avons dit;	Then between baths, if nothing prevents it, to purify the blood, and heal from the vein of the arm or the third part (of the body), as we have said. 
et te garde celui jor de travail, et de poinne, et de luxure, et de semblans choses;	And keep yourself on that day from labor, and from pain, and from lust, and similar things;  
et soies liez et joians, et soit li sainieres plus haut que cil cui on saine, et li frote lou bras II fois ou III, puis estraigne lou liien desus moienement, car quant il est trop estrois ou poc, si ne puet corre li sans;	And be lying and joyful, and let the  shoulders be higher than him who is healed, and rub the arm two or three times, then restrain the linen on top in the middle, because when it is too tight or loose, he cannot correct it without a surgeon. 
et puis le frote le leu as mains, tant que les voines enflent, et les sente on;	And then rub the area with your hands until the veins swell and are felt.  
puis moille li sainieres le flaime d’un poc d’oile viel, puis mette son doit de sa main senestre sus celle voinne desoz lou leu un poc ou il vuet sainier, que li voinne ne fue et faille au ferir.	Then moisten the shoulders with a little bit of old oil, then put his finger of his left hand above that vein below the armpit one finger's breadth where he wants to bleed, so that the vein does not go and fail to be pierced. 
Car il i a voinnes que fuient ausi com cordes au sainier, et si a de telz que sont plainnes de ventositeit, si que quant on met sus le flaime, si retrait a flaime, et ne puet ovrir li voinne, et ensi est on de ceus;	For there are veins that are as taut as cords in the body, and some that are full of airiness, so that when one puts the flame upon them, they withdraw from the flame and cannot open the vein, and thus it is with some of these; 
et s’il aoevre la voinne, si est li plaie trop estroite, por ceu si covient que li sainieres soit avisez en ces choses.	and if they open the vein, the wound is too tight, for this reason it is necessary that the surgeons be advised in these matters. 
Et se li voine oevre la premiere fois, c’est boin;	And if the vein is opened for the first time, it is good;
se ceu non, si rencomence ancor un poc desoz celui leu ou sus hastanment, se li leus n’est enflez.	if not, then it begins again a little below that place or where it has been opened, if the place is not inflamed.  
Et se li leus est enflez, et li malaides s’espoante, se li laisse I jor ou II, et ne liier mie le bras:	And if the place is inflamed, and the patient fears it, then let him leave it for a day or two, and not tie up his arm: 
par aventure i venra apostemes chaus;	for by chance there may come boils or abscesses.  
ne n’entre ou bain, puis rencomence la sainie s’elle li plait;	Do not enter into a bath, then restart the bleeding if he wishes. 
et se li pertuis est petis, ou li sans cort subtilment et tu doutes qu’il n’isse mie tant de sanc com tu vues, si fier en celui pertuis meisme a tout le flaime droitement;	And if the wound is small, or the vessel is subtle and you doubt that it is not as much blood as you see, then pierce in that same wound all the way straight through. 
et l’uevre un poc hastanment, ainsois que li leus soit enflez;	And put a point gently, so that the veins are swollen.  
car ceu avient maintes fois, quant li plaie est petite.	For this happens many times when the wound is small. 
Se tu vois le leu enfleit, si ne rencomencier mie la sainie, et met sus un poc de lie d’oile, car elle alige lou cors dou sanc, et est muedre en cest leu li lie que li oile;	If you see the place swollen, then do not restart the bleeding, and put on a bit of oil dressing, because it stops the body from bleeding, and is good for this wound.
et ensi aministre la lie de oile en chescune sainie que tu saines les voines, por estanchier lou cours dou sanc;	and thus administer the paste of oil to each vein that you open, to stop the flow of blood. 
et ceu meisme fait triaicle et bowe d’eus, quant on le met sus le leu;	and the same thing is done with a triangle and a bow, when it is placed over the place; 
si subtilie li sans et s’espart quant il est trop gros.	so that it shrinks the veins and spreads apart when it is too large.  
Et s’il i vient uns apostemes gros, qui avient maintes fois, meismement quant il n’est sainiez fuer que a celi fois ou li overture de la voinne est petite, si te haste, et met sus le leu esponge moillie en aigue et en seil un poc chaut, et l’estraint une houre;	And if it comes to an abscess that grows large, which happens often, even when it is only opened once and the opening of the vein is small, then hasten and put a sponge soaked in water and salt on it, lukewarm, and hold it for one hour;
et covient que tu faices ceu aprés l’issue dou sanc de la voinne, et s’il demoure au leu aprés aucuns jors aucune noiror ou verdor, si ne li nuist mie;	and you must do this after the blood has flowed from the vein, and if it remains in place for several days without any blackness or discoloration, it will not harm him; 
et se tu vues, met sus aucune chose de aloes ou de mirre remise en jus de calament, monstastre, ou semblant.	and if you see, put on nothing of aloes or frankincense, mixed with juice of calamus, mintwort, or the like. 
Et maintes fois avient aposteme et aparance a la sainie de la basilique:	And many times abscesses and appearances appear at the basilica of the saint. 
met donques ta main sus, et se tu trueves le leu mol a la compression de la main, si est celle aparance male.	Put therefore your hand upon it, and if you find the place soft to the pressure of the hand, then is that appearance evil.  
Eschui donques que tu ne mettes sus aucune chose de ceu que nos avons dit, car par aventure en cort sans de l’artere;	Therefore, I warn you not to put anything on it of what we have said, because by chance it may cut off the artery.  
mais li fai I emplaustre sec por endurcir le leu, puis le cure d’autre cure, tant qu’il soit sanez.	but the wound should be bandaged dry to harden the place, then treat it with other remedies until it is healed.
Et trai a chescun dou sanc selonc la quantiteit de sa vertu, et de la color dou sanc.	And treat each wound with blood according to the quantity of its virtue, and the color of the blood.
Car se li sans est noir, si en laisse issir tant qu’il soit rouges;	For if the wound is black, let it seep out until it is red.  
et se tu lou vois gros, si lou laisse tant qu’il soit subtiliiez;	and if you see it growing large, let it remain until it subsides. 
et s’il est trop chaus, si le laisse refroidier.	And if it is too swollen, let it cool down.   
Et covient a celui qui est plains et fors, et ait mestier d’estraction de sanc, c’on li faice plus large plaie, et soit li flaimes larges;	And for him who is pale and thin, and needs the extraction of blood, one makes a larger wound, and let the flames be wide. 
et a celui qui est foibles, fai le contraire, et le covient sainier poc et sovent, et le doit on sainier en taillant de travers, ne mie en poignant;	And to one who is weak, do the opposite, and he should be bled little and often, and it should be bled by cutting across, not by pricking. 
et ceste maniere de sainie est sauve de decorrement de sanc et de copement de nerf, et vaut mues que li sainie dou lonc ne dou large.	And this manner of bleeding is safe from the decrease of blood and the cutting of nerves, and is worth more than the bleeding done long or wide. 
Et a celui cui li cors faut a la sainie, covient doner pain moilliet en jus de pomes grenates;	And to one whose body needs bloodletting, it is fitting to give soft bread in pomegranate juice;
s’il est eschaufez, si trai dou sanc III fois ou IIII Et s’il est de froide complexion, si menjuce devant la sainie pain moilliet en sirop muzé, ou en sirop de miel aromatique avec espices, si com poivre, canelle, gingibre, et chiches, et sirop bien odorant.	If he is heated, treat him with bloodletting three or four times. And if he is of cold complexion, let him eat soft bread dipped in mucid syrup, or in honey syrup with spices such as pepper, cinnamon, ginger, and chickpeas, and a well-scented syrup.
Et s’il paume a la sainie, aprés l’issue de mout de sanc, si covient qu’il hume brouet de char, et sirop odorant subtil, et use des autres choses que nos avons dit en la division ou chapistre de sincope, por l’evacuation de voinne.	And if it bleeds at the vein, after the issue of much blood, then it is necessary that he moisten broth of flesh, and fragrant syrup subtle, and use the other things that we have said in the division or chapter of fainting, for the evacuation of the vein.
Et s’il vuet esventer som bras, et sainier autre fois, si covient, quant il est afoiblis par grant sainie, k’il se saine poc et poc, selonc la quantiteit de sa vertu continueement.	And if he wants to drain his arm, and bleed another time, if it is necessary, when he is weakened by much bleeding, that he bleed little by little, according to the quantity of his strength continuously.
Et qui vuet esventer som bras aprés la premiere sainie, et il a cors fort, si se saine VII houres aprés la premiere sainie, ou aprés la nuevime houre.	And whoever wants to empty his arm after the first vein is opened, and he has a strong body, so it will heal seven hours after the first opening, or after the ninth hour.
Et qui se vuet sainier d’autre part, si se doit sainier lou secont jor ou le tier.	And whoever wishes to bleed from another side, he must bleed on the second day or the third.
Car il a mout de sanc dedens le cors qui est ja eschaufez, et fait venir fievre;	Because he has much blood within the body that is already heated, and brings fever;
si en covient traire grant quantiteit, et eslargir le pertus tant qu’il chiece em pameson;	if it is necessary to drain a great quantity, and widen the opening until it reaches the bone.  
puis que tu rewardes toutes les conditions de sainie, et met ta main sus som poulz quant il saine, que li mors ne viegne en leu de pameson, et ceu avient maintes fois, quant li sainieres est negligens;	then that you fulfill all the conditions of health, and place your hand upon his pulse when he is healthy, so that death does not come to him from bone, and this happens many times when the healer is negligent. 
et ne covient mie quant tu vues desliier lou bras, et faire issir sanc la seconde fois, et li pertus est clos, que tu presses forment sus;	and it is not fitting when you see the arm dislocated and to make blood flow a second time, and the opening is closed, that you press hard upon it.  
ne s’il est corbes, qu’il estende lou bras hastanment, car ce seroit malz;	if it is crooked, let him extend his arm fully, because this would be bad; 
mais le laisse tant qu’il saine la seconde fois;	but let him leave it so until he heals the second time.  
ou tu i point a la pointe dou flaime, tant que li sans qui est congelez a pertus de la voinne isse fuer, et met sus I poc de seil remis en aigue, et presse sus legierement.	or you point it to the tip of the flame until the blood that is frozen at the opening of the vein flows out, and place upon his fingernail returned sharp, and press lightly.   
Et se li voine est enflee, si la laisse et ne l’estreindre mie, tant que li aposteme soit apaisiez.	And if the vein is swollen, leave it and do not constrict it, until the abscess is appeased.
Et se necessitez est dou traire dou sanc la seconde fois, si le saine en celui leu meisme, ou en un autre voinne, ou en l’autre bras.	And if necessity is to draw blood a second time, if the vein in that same place, or in another vein, or in the other arm.
Li voinne emmi le bras est sainie en leu de la voine dou chief por ceu qu’elle est composte.	The vein in the arm is bled in the place of the vein of the head because it is composed.
Et li maniere de la sainie si est que li malaides boute sa main en aigue chaude, tant que li foscile soit rouges;	And the manner of the cauterizing is that the patient puts his hand in hot water, until the bone is red. 
puis soit liiéz moienement, si que li voinne apere bien, puis le saine maintenant dou travers, ne mie dou large ne dou lonc;	Then it is bound moderately, so that the vein appears well, then cauterize it now through, neither too wide nor too long; 
et soit li pertus larges, et soit sainiez bien pres de la jointe de la main, et se sans n’en puet issir, si remet la main en aigue chaude, et laisse corre lou sanc en l’aigue, tant que tu en aies assez;	And let the opening be wide, and cauterize well near the joint of the hand, and if it cannot be removed, put the hand back in hot water, and leave it to bleed in the water until you have enough;
et se c’est en esteit, si ne rebouter mie la main en aigue chaude, car on l’i met plus en yver que en esteit;	And if it is in summer, do not put the hand back in hot water, because one puts it more there in winter than in summer;
et li sainie de ceste voine est plus sauve de toutes autres voinnes, qu’il n’i a ne artere ne nerf.	And the cauterizing of this vein is safer of all other veins, because there is neither artery nor nerve in it.
Li sainie de la salvatele de la main destre si vaut a toutes les maladies dou foie, et c’est li maniere:	The cauterizing of the salvation vein on the right hand is good for all diseases of the liver, and this is the manner: 
estrain la main, et boute en aigue chaude, tant que li voinne soit enflee, si c’on la voie;	Restrain the hand, and put it in hot water, as long as the vein is swollen, if one can see it. 
et se la saine de travers, et se tu la copes dou tout en tout, si ne grieve rien;	And if it heals crookedly, and if you cut it completely off entirely, if it causes no harm;  
et n’aler mie trop em parfont, car li nerf sont desoz toz desnuez de char, et puis remet la main en aigue chaude, se li sans est congelez en la plaie, et n’en puet issir.	and do not pierce it too much, for the nerves are all beneath the skin, and then put the hand in hot water, if the sinew is frozen in the wound, and cannot be pulled out.  
Et quant tu avras trait dou sanc tant com mestier t’est, si met sus la voinne oile et seil por souder hastanment, et ensi fai de chescun rain.	And when you have treated the blood as much as is necessary, then put on the vein oil and wool to close it tightly, and do this with each one.
Li sainie de li en la main senestre si vaut a la maladie de la mice, et fai tout ausi com je t’ai dit devers destre.	The vein of him in the left hand is as good for the disease of the mouse, and do all as I have told you towards the right.
Li sainie de la sophene si vaut a toutes les maladies que sont desoz le cors, si com maladies de la marris, et retenement de flors, et maladie des rains, et des cuixes et des jambes ancienes, et semblans maladies.	The blood of the sophene is good for all illnesses that are below the body, such as diseases of the belly, and retention of flowers, and illness of the hips, and thighs and old legs, and similar illnesses.
Et li qualitez de sa sainie si est que li malaides boute som piet en aigue chaude, et frote sus la voinne tant qu’elle pere, et lie desus la jointure dou piet;	And the qualities of its healing are that the patient puts his foot in hot water, and rubs on the vein until it softens, and binds above the joint of the foot;  
et li voinne si est a la cheville, et par desus lou piet en vont mout de rains;	And the vein is at the ankle, and above the foot go many veins; 
saine la donques ou plus large rain, ou a la cheville, que mues vaut.	So heal there, in the larger vein or at the ankle, whichever is worth more.  
Et se tu la saines sus lou piet, si te warde des ners qui sont desoz, et la saine de traver ausi com en copant;	And if you heal it upon the foot, guard the nerves that are below, and heal by traversing also as in cutting; 
et soit li flaimes anesil.	and let the flames be gentle.  
Et se li sans n’en puet issir, si remet lou piet en l’aigue, et laisse bien vuidier la voine.	And if the vein cannot be issued forth, put the foot in water again, and let it bleed well.
Et se li sainieres faut la premiere fois, si rencomence la seconde au desus un poc, car li leus est salz;	And if the healing fails the first time, begin again the second at a point above, because the flesh is salty;  
ne ne douter de nerf, si com nos avons dit, et ensi fai de la sophene de l’autre piet igalment.	Do not doubt of nerve, as we have said, and in this way do from the other foot equally.   
Li leus de la voinne sciatique est a la cheville de fuer, et sa sainie vaut a la dolor de la hainche, quant c’est por sanc chaut.	The veins of the sciatic nerve are at the ankle of the leg, and its pain reaches to the hip when it is hot with blood.
Et li qualitez de sa sainie si est que li malaides entre ou bain, et estraigne desus la cheville IIII dois en tordant, car autrement n’apert li voinne;	And the qualities of its healing are that the patient enters hot water, and is stretched above the ankle IV times in twisting, for otherwise the vein does not open.  
et s’elle apert, si le saine en toutes les manieres que tu pues, et en traversant;	And if it opens, heal it in every way that you can, and by traversing.
et vaut mues que tu la copes, car li leus est saus, et elle est mout reponue a mains homes.	and it is better that you cut it, because the flesh is dry, and it is much well-supplied with blood of men. 
Et se tu ne la trueves, si saine aucun rain de li qui apert ou dos dou piet, et vers lou petit doi, et te warde des ners;	And if you do not find it, so search any vein of him who opens or back of the foot, and towards the small thigh, and guard the nerves. 
et fai tant corre dou sanc que tu vues, et puis deslie lou lien, et met sus coton et l’estraint;	and make so much bloodletting as you see, and then untie the ligature, and put cotton on it and restrain.  
ele est maintenant sanee.	it is now healed.  
des sainies de ventouse	of the suction cups
Ventouses sont fait de cornes, ou d’arain, ou de voirre;	Suctions are made of horns, or of skin, or of glass; 
et ventosation si est faite selonc II manieres:	and suctioning is done in two ways:   
ou par ferir et atraire sanc, ou sens ferir.	either by pricking and drawing blood, or without pricking. 
Et ceste ventosation qui est sens ferir si est selonc II manieres:	And this suctioning which is without pricking is done in two ways:
ou elle est a tout feu, ou sens feu;	either it is with fire, or without fire;  
et ventosation qui est faite par ferir et par estraction de sanc si est faite en XIIII leus dou cors, de coi li uns est tout en som le chief;	and suctioning which is done by pricking and drawing blood is done in fourteen places of the body, of which one is entirely at the top of the head;  
et li autres est emmi le col;	and the others is removed the neck; 
et II autres en II costeis dou col;	and the others in the ribs of the neck; 
et li ventouse desoz lou menton;	and the cupping glass below the chin;  
et li ventouse des II espaules;	and the cupping glass on the shoulders;  
et li ventouse sus les crupies;	and the cupping glass on the hips; 
et les ventouses emmi les II bras;	and the cupping glasses removed from the arms;
et les ventouses des II jambes;	and the cupping glasses from the legs; 
et les ventouses des II chevilles;	and the cupping glasses from the ankles;
et li ventosation ne trait point de sanc, fuer que des menues voinnes que sont esparses en la char, et por ceu n’en afoiblist om mie, si com on fait de sainie de voinne;	and cupping does not treat blood but rather the small veins that are spread throughout the flesh, and for this reason it does not weaken as much as opening a vein;  
et ne covient mie qu’elle soit aministree, ne a tout feu ne sens feu, en aucune maladie qui vient de repletion, tant que toz li cors soit vuidiez.	and it is not appropriate to administer it with heat or cold fire in any illness that comes from repletion until the whole body is emptied.   
Et se par necessiteit de maladies covient ventoser, ou por acostumances, si l’amenistrons chescune houre en l’encomencement dou mois, ou en la fin, et emmi et en chescun tens;	And if by necessity of illnesses it is necessary to blow up, or for customs, then we administer each hour at the beginning of the month, or at the end, and every time. 
car il i a de telz qui, quant il ont mestier de ventoser, si ont pesant chief;	because there are some who, when they have need to blow up, have heavy heads;  
et si a telz qui truevent repletion et roujor en lor faice, et en lor chief, et au col, et tenebrour as eulz;	and there are those who have fullness and redness in their face, and in their head, and neck, and darkness in their eyes; 
et telz qui truevent une goute de sanc en lor bouche, et ont enflee la lengue, et raichent sanc;	and there are those who have a drop of blood in their mouth, and have a swollen tongue, and bite their tongues.
et si i a de telz qui songent, et voient par nut sanc et navrez et mors et semblans choses.	And there are some who dream, and see by blood and numbness and death and similar things. 
Et quant nos voions ces signes, et meismement quant c’est emmi lou mois, nos lou commandons a ventoser aprés III houres dou jor.	And when we saw these signs, and even when it is gone for one month, we order them to vomit after three hours of the day.
Li sainie de la muze si aide a la grieteit dou chief … que vient as eulz, et ne covient mie que ce soit aprés l’evacuation de tout lou cors;	The vein of the temple helps in the greatness of the head... that comes to the eyes, and it is not proper that this be done after the evacuation of all the body;
et ceste ventosation si est en leu de la sainie de la cephalique, et ne covient mie que cil qui est de froide complexion en use, ou qui ait chatharre, car ce lor fait mout grant nuisement;	and this ventilation is in place of the bloodletting of the cephalic, and it does not become those who are of cold complexion in use, or who have a catarrh, because this causes them great discomfort. 
et por ceu ne covient mie que li veillart en usent, ne qui ont ou chief froides maladies.	and for this reason it does not become the elderly in use, nor those who have or cold diseases.  
Et cil qui s’en saine sovent, si devient oblious, et por ce covient mettre la ventouse un poc plus aval par la doutance d’obliance.	And those who are cured of it often become oblivious, and for this reason it is necessary to place the suction cup a little lower down due to the doubt of oblivion.
Li ventosation emmi le col est en leu de la sainie dou chief et de la basilique, et por ceu vaut elle a l’estrecement dou pis, et a fendure de la chenal dou pormon, et a toust, et a repletion;	The ventilation in the neck is in place of bloodletting of the head and the basilica, and for this reason it is good for the alleviation of the pain, and for cutting open the channel of the pharynx, and for all, and for repletion.
et la covient poc bouter, car s’elle tient trop fermement, si enjanre obliance ou stomac et ou cuer.	and it should not be applied too strongly, because if it is held too tightly, it may cause blockage in the stomach and heart.  
Li ventosations as II costelz dou col si vaut as dolors dou chief, et obtalmie et emigrainne, et a l’estranglement, et a la dolor as racines des dens, et est en leu de la sainie de la basilique;	The ventilation at the two costals of the neck is good for pains in the head, and ophthalmia and migraine, and strangulation, and pain at the roots of the teeth, and it is in place of bloodletting of the basilica.  
et covient que tu comandes au sainor qu’il espresse sa main au mettre, qu’il ne cope l’artere, et ne veigne decorremens de sanc.	And it is necessary that you command the healthy one that he press his hand when putting it, so that he does not cut the artery, and that there comes no flow of blood. 
Li ventosations desoz lou menton si vaut a maladie de bouche, et a corruption de gencives, et semblans maladies qui sont en la bouche;	The incisions under the chin are good for mouth sickness, and gum rot, and similar illnesses which are in the mouth. 
et est en leu des sainies des II levres.	and are in the place of the veins of the two lips.   
Li ventosations des espaules vaut a maladie que vient de chalor et de remplissement.	The ventilation of the shoulders is good for illnesses that come from heat and fullness.
Li ventosations des coutes si vaut autant com des III voinnes dou bras, car elle atrait sanc de ces grosses voinnes;	The incisions on the arms are as useful as the three veins of the arm, because they draw blood from those large veins.
et comande au sainor qu’il ne fiere mie trop em parfont, car li leus est nus de char, et sait desoz ners et arteres.	and instruct the patient not to pull too much on it, for the skin is bare and shows nerves and arteries.
