Li ventouse qui est sus la croupe si vaut as emoroydes dou fondement, et as maladies desoz, et covient que li ventouse soit grans, et soit d’arain, qu’elle a mestier de bien traire;	The suction cup that is on the rump is good for hemorrhoids of the base, and diseases below, and it should be large and made of brass, so it needs to draw well; 
et par aventure, s’elle estoit subtilz, si briseroit;	and by chance, if it were thin, it would break;  
et i fai grans plaies.	and this makes great wounds. 
Les ventouses des jambes si sainent apertement, car elles atraient sanc de tout le cors, et valent as dolors ancienes des rains, et de la marris, et de la vessie, et ramoinnent les flors;	Suction cups on the legs heal openly, because they draw blood from the whole body, and are good for old pains in the hips, groin, and bladder, and loosen up the flowers;
et sont en leu des II sophenes, et des II chevilles, et toutevoie elles afoiblissent lou cors aprés lonc us, et font venir paumison em plusors dispositions.	and are in place at the two shoulders, and the two ankles, and all ways they weaken the body after long use, and bring weakness in many positions. 
Li maniere de mettre la ventouse si est que tu la mettes premier vuide, et succe tempreement, et la met hastanment, et remue igalment, et ne cesser de ceu faire, tant que tu voies lou leu rouge et enfleit, et apere li roujor dou sanc;	The manner of applying the suction cup is that you put it first empty, and successively, and place it firmly, and move it evenly, and do not cease doing this, until you see the skin red and inflamed, and appears the red color of blood. 
puis fier, et remet les ventouses, et pren warde en la disposition des cors, car il i a telz qui ont tanre char, et clers porez:	then firmly, and reapply the suction cups, and take heed to the position of the body, for there are some who have tender flesh, and clear pores: 
si covient ferir une fois soulement, et covient faire larges plaies, et un poc parfondes;	so it is necessary to cut only once, and it is necessary to make large wounds, and a deep incision; 
et suce legierement.	and suck gently.  
Et se li sans est gros, si couvient ferir II fois:	And if the vein is thick, it is necessary to cut twice.
la premiere fois por subtiliier la voie dou sanc gros.	The first time to subtilily open the vein of blood thick. 
Et se li sans est tres espés, si covient ferir la tierce fois;	And if the vein is very thick, then it behooves to cut a third time;  
et quant nos volons traire dou sanc poc et poc, si nos soffist soulement une fois.	And when we want to draw blood little by little, then we suffice with only one incision. 
Et se nos volons mout de sanc, si rencomensons sovent;	And if we want much blood, then we frequently repeat the incisions;  
et se li sans est espés, si fier em parfont, et li termines si est que li keurs soit perciez soudement, et couvient a celui qui a gros cuir et dur, et qui ont estrois porelz, que tu oignes les leus des ventouses d’oile aperitif et dissolutif:	And if the vein is thick, we pierce it in full force, and the end that the keyers be pierced very strongly, and it behoves the one who has coarse and hardened skin, and whose pores are closed, that you apply to their leus suction cups of oil appetizing and dissolving:
se c’est en esteit, d’oile violet, ou d’oile d’amandres douces, ou d’oile de semence de cucurbite;	if it is in this state, of violet oil, or of sweet almond oil, or of oil from pumpkin seeds;
et se c’est en yveir, d’oile de cresson, ou de lis, ou de camomille, ou autre semblant.	and if it is in summer, of watercress oil, or of lily, or of chamomile, or something similar. 
Et se li superfluitez est grosse et froide, si pren oile amaratin, ou de balsamite, ou oile d’anet, et les semblans.	And if the superfluities are large and cold, then take oil of wormwood, or of balm, or of anise, and similar things.
Et se cil cui on saine a tendre char et larges porelz, se n’i covient mettre point d’oile, mais le covient laver aprés la ventosation d’aigue rose, ou d’aigue froide, ou d’aigue de morelle, ou d’aigue de cucurbite, ou d’aigue de porcelainne, ou autre semblant.	And if the one whom one heals has tender flesh and large pores, there is no need to put any oil on it, but it should be washed after the inflation of rose water, or cold water, or mulberry water, or cucumber water, or porcelain water, or something similar.
Et cil qui a mout de moistor, si se leve d’aisil, ou d’aigue de mirte, et de sumac, et de semblans choses.	And he who has much moisture, let him rise from ash, or myrtle water, and sumacs, and similar things.
Et cil qui ont grosses superfluitez se levent de vin viel, ou d’aigue de seuc, ou de decoction d’anet ou de camomile, ou d’autres semblans;	And those who have great excesses shall rise from old wine, or of their own water, or of a decoction of anise or chamomile, or other similar things; 
et ne se covient mie sainier de ventouse devant le bain ne em bain, mais aprés lou bain une houre ou II;	and one should not draw blood with leech before the bath nor in the bath, but after the bath an hour or two; 
et ne dorme mie aprés la ventosacion, et covient k’il se warse, quant il se doit ventoser et quant il est ventosez.	and one should not sleep after blood-letting, and it is necessary that he warm himself when he is about to be bloodied and when he has been bled.  
Et warde se cil qui se saine est coleriques, et se li sans est trop agus et enflamez;	And guard those who are being bled if they are choleric, and if their blood is too much and inflamed; 
si covient qu’il preigne choses froides, si com pomes grenates et endives et laitues a l’aisil, et semblans choses;	if it is necessary that they eat cold things, such as pomegranates and endives and lettuces at the waist, and similar things; 
et menjuce pucins, et char de chastron, et viandes moistes.	and minced kidneys, and roast pork, and moist meats.  
Et cil qui a froide complexion, si preigne syrop de miel, et vin odorant moien, qui est entre viel et noveil, et menjuce poc, et menjuce pucins et petis oiselz et pijons;	And he who has a cold complexion, take syrup of honey, and wine smelling medium, which is between old and new, and mince parsley, and minces onions and small eggs and sparrows.  
et lou jor qu’il se ventousera, si doit plus boivre que mengier;	And on the day that he will be treated, he must drink more than eat; 
et covient doner a aucuns homes aucune fois triaicle ou muscate devant la ventosacion, ou aprés, por conforter les membres principalz;	And it is necessary to give no man at any time thyme or nutmeg before the cupping, or after, to comfort the main limbs; 
et soit subtiliiez li sans, mais il ne covient mie que cil qui sont chaut le boivent.	and be subtle the herbs, but it is not necessary that those who are hot drink it.  
Les ventouses que sont mises sens ferir sont celles que sont mises sus lou foie, et sus la mice, et podagre, et sus lou ventre et la boude et les rains et la hainche, car cil membre ne soffrent mie ferir sus oulz, et ne le fait on fuer que por atraire sanc de membre em membre, si com nos mettons sus les mameles quant li neis sainne;	The cupping glasses that are put without hurting are those that are put on the liver, and on the spleen, and gout, and on the belly and the back and the hips and the groin, because these members do not suffer to be hurt on their skin, and it is done only in order to draw blood from limb to limb, as we put them on the nipples when the child is born; 
por oster la viscositeit qui est au membre, si com nos metons ventouses sus le ventre et sus la boude por amenuisier le membre;	To remove the viscosity that is in the limb, as we place cupping glasses on the belly and on the cheek to lessen the member; 
et oste la dolor, quant il i a opilation ou piere, si oste par sa vertu atractive par aventure l’opilation, ou desaert la piere de son leu;	and to remove pain when there is an inflammation or stone, as it removes by its attractive virtue perhaps the inflammation, or moves the stone from its place; 
et ensi fait ele quant on le met sus lou foie et sus la mice quant il i a ventositeit retenue, et ces ventouses sont aministrees vuides por sucier tant soulement;	And thus it acts when it is placed upon the liver and the spleen when there is retained windiness, and these cupping glasses are administered empty to suck only; 
et aucune fois sont aministrees ensamble feu, et aucunes fois plainnes d’aigue tede, si com em maladies dou pleuresin, et en tel maniere c’on emplisse la ventouse d’aigue chaude soule, ou d’aigue ou il ait cuit herbes covenaubles a ceu.	and sometimes they are administered together with fire, and sometimes full of warm water, as in diseases of the pleura, and in such manner one fills the cupping glass with hot water alone, or with water in which herbs suitable to it have been boiled; 
Li forme de la ventouse aministré a feu si est ci:	The form of the suction cup administered with fire is here:
Et ait II dois de large et demi palme de parfont, et ait ou costeit entor lou mileu I petit pertus, ausi com por bouter une aguille, et soit d’arain, souef devant si qu’ele ne blece lou malaide au mettre sus lou membre;	And it must be two inches wide and half a palm in length, and have a small hole on the side about the middle, like for inserting a needle, and be of metal, so that it does not chill the patient when placed upon the limb;
et ait em mileu une verge de travers d’arain ou de fer, por mettre une chandoile emprise, et en soient et grans et petites selonc les maladies et l’eaige de ces qui les prenent;	and in the middle a rod of iron or steel, to put a handle and they are great and small according to the illnesses and the strength of those who take them 
car les ventouses des enfans sont autres que des vielz, et des maigres que des gras.	for the suction cups of children are other than those of old people, and of thin ones than fat ones.  
Et doit on ensi mettre ceste ventouse sus lou membre:	And thus one must put this suction cup on the limb: 
empren la chandoile de cire ou I linement, et le met emmi la ventouse au traver de la verge qui est emmi la ventouse, si que li clartez soit au fons de la ventouse qu’elle ne brule le malaide;	grasping the handle of wax or linen, and place it in the suction cup across from the rod which is in the suction cup, so that the clarity is at the bottom of the suction cup that it does not burn the patient; 
et puis la met sus lou membre, et tes dois soit sus lou pertus que nos avons dit, si que quant on vuet, si en va li vapor, et oste on la ventouse;	and then place it on the limb, and those two should be on the hole that we have said, so that when one wants, there goes the vapor, and one removes the suction cup 
et emprent on le linement si com devant, et le rencomence sovent, se tu as mestier.	and grasp the linen as before, and recommence it often, if you have need. 
En la ventouse donques qui est aministree em maladie de pleuresin, a tout aigue, n’a point de verge ne de pertus, et n’est amenistree fuer que quant ele est plaine d’aigue, et est mise sus lou membre tant soulement;	In the suction cup therefore which is administered in illness of pleuresin, to every acute pain, has no stem nor point, and is not administered unless it is full of water, and is put upon the member only so much 
et c’est li forme:	and this is its form: 
Sansues ne sont amenistrees fuer que en membres ou on ne puet mettre ventouses por lour petitece, si com levres et gencives, et semblans leus;	Suction cups are not administered unless in members where one cannot put suction cups because of their small size, such as lips and gums, and similar to them; 
et en leus desnuez de char, si com doi ou neis, et autres semblans;	and in their naked flesh, such as two or nails, and other similar; 
et li qualitez de l’user si est que quant tu trueves sansues que sont en aigues douces nettes sens porreture, si les pren;	and the qualities of the user are that when you find suction cups that are in clear sweet waters without impurities, then take them; 
et les met une nut en aigue douce, tant qu’elles soient famillouses, et n’aient rien en ventres;	and put them one nut in fresh water, as long as they are familiar, and have nothing in their bellies;
et puis soit sainiez de voinne et de ventouse, puis frote le membre tant k’il soit rouges, et met sus les sansues;	and then let it be cured of vein and cupping, then rub the limb until it is red, and put on leeches. 
et quant elles seront plainnes, et cherront, se c’est leu ou on puisse mettre ventouse, se li met, car ce vaut mout aprés.	and when they are full and fall off, if it is possible to put a cupping glass there, put one, because this is very good after. 
Se ceu non, si leve le leu d’aisil, et puis d’aigue, mout bien, et puis l’espreint;	If not, lift the place with ease, and then water, well, and then rub it;
et se li leus saine trop aprés lou cors des sansues, si moille I drapel de lin en aigue froide, et met sus, tant que li sans soit estenchiés;	and if the wounds are too painful after the leeches, moisten a linen cloth in cold water and put it on, until the swelling subsides. 
et se li sans est multipliez, si met sus vitriole broié, ou gales, et semblans choses, tant qu’il soit estenchiez;	and if the swellings are multiplied, put on top ground vitriol or alum, and similar things, until it subsides.
ou tu met sor le leu moitiez de feves pelees, et les laisse tant qu’elles s’aerdent au leu, si estanchera maintenant;	or you put on the place half of peeled beans, and leave them until they dry up on the place, it will now stop. 
et se tu en as de plus mestier, si pren autres sansues.	And if you need more of this, take other ointments. 
Et se les sansues ne se vuellent prendre, si frote le leu de sanc fres, ou tu i fiche une aguille tant que li sans en isse, et puis les met sus, et tantost com elles sentent lou sanc, si s’aerdent;	And if the ointments will not be taken, rub the place with fresh blood, or stick a needle there until it bleeds, and then put them on, and as soon as they feel the blood, they ignite.  
et quant tu vues qu’elles chieent, si poudre sus un poc d’aloen et de seil broiet, ou de cendre, si cherront maintenant.	And when you see that they are burning, put powder on a bit of aloe and silphium ground up, or ashes, and now they will subside. 
Ci comence li livre des brisures	Here begins the book of fractures
Cist chapistres est maintes fois necessaires en l’art de medicine, et est restorement de brisure et de desaluement.	This chapter is many times necessary in the art of medicine, and is restoration of fracture and dislocation.
Saichiez, chier fil, que li fol mire se gietent de cest chapistre, qu’il ne virent onques nul des anciens livres, ne lettre n’en lurent;	Know this, dear son, that the fools who are looking to this chapter, will never have seen any of the ancient books, nor read a letter from them. 
et por ceste cause est estraingie li science en nostre terre, car je n’en trovai onques nul boin;	And for this reason, science is estranged in our land, because I never found any good one.
et n’en sai nient, fuer que par la science des anciens livres, ou j’ai tant estudiiet que je en ai traite la science, et par experiment, et par l’acostumance de ma vie;	And I know nothing of it, except through the science of ancient books, which I have studied so much that I have mastered its science, and by experience, and by the custom of my life.
et je vos ai jai descrit en cest chapistre ceu qui est contenut, et l’ai abregié en la fin, et ai mostreit clerement les formes des estrumens que sont amenistrez, si com j’ai fait en ces II chapistres ci devant.	And I have shown you in this chapter what is contained, and abridged it at the end, and clearly showed the forms of the instruments that are brought, as I did in these two chapters before. 
Il covient donques que nos disons ou prologue de cest livre les sommes de la parole et les chapistres ou li saiges met son entendement, et demore sus la verteit, si que cil qui sont esproveit saichent et aprenent cest art noble, et l’aprenent a autrui.	It is therefore necessary that we say or prologue of this book the sums of the word and the chapters where the sages put their understanding, and remain on the truth, so that those who are experienced know and learn this noble art, and learn it to others.
Je dis que quant brisure ou dislocation ou torsions ou quasseure vient a aucun, si covient que tu te hastes de sainier lou malaide d’une part et d’autre, s’aucune chose ne lou te tot, si com foiblece de cors, ou enfes, ou viellars;	I say that when a fracture or dislocation or torsion or sprain comes to anyone, it is necessary that you hasten to heal the patient on one side and the other, if nothing hinders you, such as weakness of body, or infancy, or old age; 
ou se li tens n’est tres chaus, ou trop frois;	or if the heat is not very good, or too cold;  
et menjuce cholz frois, c’est a savoir froides joutes, et char d’oiseil et de chevril, et ne boive point de vin, ne menjuce nules grasses chars, et ne s’emplisse mie trop de viandes qui remplissent les voinnes de sanc, tant que tu n’aies doute d’aposteme chaut, ne d’espandement de matiere au membre;	and eat cold meats, that is to say, cold mutton and venison, and do not drink wine, nor eat any fatty meats, and do not fill yourself too much with meats that fill the veins with blood, as long as you have doubt of a hot abscess, or an expansion of matter in the limb;  
si reviegne li malaides a som premerain governement k’il a useit.	If the patient returns to his former regimen that he has used. 
Et quant li os brisiés comence a restourer, si covient que on norrisse le malaide de viandes que font gros norrissement, ou il ait viscositeit, si com froment cuit en aigue, et ris, et testes, et piez, et pance de vaiche, et oefz, et poissons fres, et gros vin, et semblans chose.	And when the broken bone begins to heal, it is necessary that one nourishes the patient with meats that make a thick nourishment, or there is viscosity, such as wheat cooked in water, and rice, and testes, and pies, and belly of calf, and eggs, and fresh fish, and strong wine, and similar things.
Car a teil norrissement se reprent mues et plus tost li brisure.	For with such nourishment they recover strength and the fracture heals more quickly.
Et saichiez que li os brisiez des vielz et des decrepites ne se pueent mie bien reprendre ne souder selonc lor nature por la sechor des membres, ne cil ausi qui sont trop tendre, si com os de petis enfans;	And know that bones broken in the elderly and decrepit people cannot be well set or healed according to their nature because of dryness of the limbs, nor those who are too soft, such as the bones of small children. 
mais n’a cure, ramoinne sus l’os brisiet I gros tenrons qui s’aert et joint le membre ensamble, tant qu’il enforce si com il fut devant;	But if there is no cure, put the broken bone back into the big tendons that are tight and join the limb together, as much as it can until it is strong as before. 
et ne li tot point de son oevre, et por ceu le covient norrir de grosses viandes, si com nos avons dit.	and to all points of his work, and for this reason he should be fed with thick meats, as we have said. 
Et saiches que les briseures sont diverses em maintes manieres.	And know that fractures are diverse in many ways.
Car li brisure dou chief est autre que li brisure dou pis, ou de la jambe, et je vos dirai en cest chapistre toutes manieres de brisure.	For the fracture of the head is different from the fracture of the leg or hip, and I will tell you in this chapter all kinds of fractures.
Car il i a brisure que vait a arvol, et autre en aguisant, si com li taille d’une penne por escrire.	For there is a fracture that goes into a groove, and another in sharpening, like the edge of a pen for writing.
Et si a brisure avec plaie, et brisure a tout une petite fendure.	And if with fracture and wound, and fracture to a small crack all around.
Et a chescune maniere ait son engien, et son estrument propre en la restauration, selonc ceu que li remembrance vient en son leu;	And to each manner has its own instrument and tool proper in the restoration, according to what comes to mind in its place. 
et est conue li brisure de l’os par ceu que li leus est tors, et apert bien par defuer, et sone au presseir de la main;	And it is known the fracture of the bone by those that the skin is twisted, and opens well outward, and sounds upon pressure of the hand.
et quant il n’i a tortuositeit ne son au tochier, et li malaides ne sent mie grant dolor, se n’i a point de brisure;	and when there is no twisting or deformity at the touch, and the patient feels no great pain, there is no fracture. 
mais il puet bien avoir tortuositeit, ou fendure, ou petite brisure.	but it can still have twisting, or a split, or a small fracture. 
Si ne covient mie que tu lou mueves a la main, mais met sus medicines que vienent ci aprés, et puis l’estraint maintenant subtilment.	If you must not move it by hand, but put on the medicines that come after here, and then restrain it subtly.
Et saiches que li brisure que vait en arvol, et sont les II parties desjointes, il les covient maintenant mettre a point igalment, ainsois que apostemes chaus i viegne;	And know that the fracture that goes in a circle and its two parts are disjointed, it is necessary now to put them together equally, so that an abscess may come from it. 
et se apostemes chaulz i vient, si lou laisse aucun jor, tant que li apostemes soit apaisiez;	And if an abscess does come there, let him leave it alone for no day until the abscess is appeased.
puis le met igal au mues que tu pues legierement et saigement, et saiches que li restauration de li est plus legiere que li restaurations de celi ou il ait pieces;	Then put it together as gently and wisely as you can, and know that the restoration of this is lighter than the restoration of that which has fragments. 
puis l’estraint, si com il covient ci aprés.	Then restrain it, as it should be hereafter.  
Et se en l’os a piéces brisies, si l’estent de II pars, se c’est mains ou piet, ou a ta main se c’est uns petis membres, ou a II cordes, ou a une corde et a ta main;	And if the bone is broken into pieces, if it is of two parts, whether hand or foot, or to your hand if it is one small limb, or two cords, or one cord and to your hand; 
et met le membre selonc sa figure natureil, si que quant les parties dou membre brisiet sont desevrees, si ramoinne par toz engiens les additions en lor leus au mues que tu pues, et garde que par ton ovraige ne viegne au malaide lesion ne doulor;	And put the limb according to its natural figure, so that when the parts of the broken limb are separated, you move by all means the additions in their places as much as you can, and keep that through your work no damage or pain comes to the patient. 
et ajoste bien les II chiés des os selonc les millors formes.	And adjust well the two heads of the bones according to the best forms. 
Et le sent bien a la main s’il te semble k’il ne soit mie bien:	And feel it well with your hand if it seems to you that it is not well.
si la dresce bellement, et ne l’estraindre mie trop, ne presser si com font cil qui i font venir par lor ovraige aposteme chaut et contraction au membre, si com nos avons veut maintes fois.	If it is well aligned, and do not restrain it too much, nor press as those who make come from their work abscesses hot and contractions to the limb, as we have wanted many times. 
Et quant li membres est a point, si chastie bien lou malaide qu’il ne lou mueve, ne en veillant ne en dormant, ne en tornant, ne en autre maniere;	And when the limb is in place, carefully instruct the patient that he does not move it, neither while awake nor sleeping, nor turning, nor in any other way;
et warde bien que li membres soit si asseurez qu’il ne sente nule dolor.	And guard well that the limb be so secure that it feels no pain at all. 
Car quant il sent nulle dolor, si n’est mie a point, et le covient mettre en teil disposition qu’il ne sent nule dolor;	For when it feels no pain, it is not in place, and it is necessary to put it in such a position that it feels no pain.  
et te garde k’il soit mis droitement, que tortuositez n’i veigne quant il iert restorez;	And guard that it be set straight, that no twisting may come when it is restored. 
et li qualitez dou membre brisiet est selonc ceu que je te dis.	And the qualities of the broken limb are according to what I tell you.  
Saiches que li membre brisiet sont divers em petitece et en grandor et en forme.	Know that broken limbs are diverse in smallness and in greatness and in form.
Car il i a petis membres, si com brais et dois et semblans:	For there are small limbs, such as arms and legs and similar things:
si covient envoloupeir drapelz de lin molz et subtilz;	so it is necessary to envelop them with soft and fine linen cloths; 
et cil qui sont gros, si com cuixe et jambe:	and those that are large, such as hips and thighs:
si covient envoloupeir d’un liien large et dur, car li larges liiens embraice tout le grant membre, et l’estraint de toutes pars igalment, si qu’il n’i a nule taiche;	so it is necessary to envelop them with a wide and firm linen, because the broad linens enclose the whole large limb, and restrain it from all sides equally, so that there is no gap; 
puis lie entor estoupes legieres, III tours ou IIII selonc lou membre, et estraint ta main un poc a tout le liien, puis vai au desus de la brisure et l’estraint moins, que la brisure puis esloigne un poc la brisure;	Then bind with light bandages, III or IV turns according to the limb, and hold your hand a little on all the linen, then go above the fracture and restrain it less, that the fracture then move away a little from the fracture; 
et mollifie lou liien poc et poc, tant que tu preignes grant partie dou leu sain, puis repren I autre liien, et torne entor derechief sus lou leu brisiet;	And soften the linen a little at a time, as long as you feel most of the healthy part, then take the other bandage, and turn it back over the broken part; 
puis revai a la partie desoz de la brisure, et l’estraint moienement, ne mie trop fort ne trop molement, si com nos avons dit en la premiere lieure desus;	Then go back to the part below the fracture, and restrain it moderately, neither too tightly nor too loosely, as we have said in the first hour above; 
puis met entre les liiens estoupes de lin ou drapelz, tant qu’il soit toz igalz, puis lie tout par desus I bendeil, et puis met tes esteles bien faites sus, s’il n’i a aposteme ou enfleure.	Then put between the bandages padding of linen or cloths, as long as it is all equal, then tie everything above with the bandage, and then put your well-made splints on top, if there is no abscess or swelling. 
Et s’il i a enfleure ou aposteme, si met sus chose apaisant aposteme chaut, et qui oste l’enfleure, et le laisse ensi aucuns jors;	And if there is a swelling or abscess, put on it a soothing thing for the abscess hot, and which removes the swelling, and let him thus for some days.  
puis estrain sus tes esteles, et soient de moitiet d’une large cainne rese saigement, ou de fust dont on fait les clives, ou de rains de palme, et soient selonc ceste figure:	Then restrain above the edges, and let them be half a cane's breadth carefully drawn, or of wood from which one makes clips, or of palm branches, and let them be according to this figure:   
mais il covient que li estele que om met sus la brisure soit un poc plus grosse et plus large que les autres;	But it is necessary that the edge that one puts on the fracture be a little bigger and wider than the others; 
et soit ausi longe com il covient au membre de petitece ou de grandor;	And let it also be as long as it is necessary for the limb of smallness or greatness;  
puis estraint sus les esteles ausi com tu as fait a la premiere lieure, puis lie desus un fil avenanment, si com en la premiere lieure sus la briseure;	Then restrain on the edges also as you did in the first hour, then tie above a thread evenly, as in the first hour on the fracture; 
plus estroit est ensus, adés moins;	More strict is above, less below;   
et covient que li fil soient moien, ne trop gros ne trop menus, et soient de lin mol;	And it is necessary that the thread be medium, neither too thick nor too fine, and be of soft linen. 
car se li fil sont gros, si com j’ai veut des oevres des folz qui font lor lieures des cordes de linement tort, et c’est grant error, car li lieure ne puet estre igal s’il est trop subtilz, et ne covient mie qu’il ait entre chescune estele moins dou doi d’espaice.	For if the thread is thick, as I want works of fools who make their stitches with coarse linen cords, and it is a great error, because the stitch cannot be equal if it is too fine, and it should not be that between each star there is less than two points of space. 
Et se li malaides est navrez par les chiés des esteles aprés l’estrignement en leus sains, si met desoz elles estoupes de lin, ou lainne charpie, si qu’il ne se blece.	And if the patient is sore at the sites of the stitches after the tightening in their healthy parts, put under them poultices of linen, or wool felt, so that it does not become blistered.
Quant li plaie est avec la briseure, et li keurs est rompus, je en dirai la cure ci aprés.	When the wound is with a fracture, and the bone is broken, I will say its cure here after.
Et saiches qu’il ne covient mie estraindre d’esteles toz les membres brisiez le premier jor.	And know that it does not behoove to straighten all the broken limbs on the first day.
Car quant li membres est grans, se n’i covient mie mettre esteles fuer que aprés V jors ou VII, ou plus selonc ta seurteit d’aposteme chaut sorvenant;	Because when the member is large, it is not necessary to put stitches further than after 5 or 7 days, or more according to your surety of abscess heat appearing.
et vez ci la maniere des emplaustres anciiens por restorer brisure, dislocation, et torsion:	And see here the manner of ancient plasters for restoring fracture, dislocation, and torsion: 
et est que tu pren de la farine que se tient as parois dou molin, et la confis avec abun d’uef, et met ceste confection, ne trop clere ne trop espesse, et en use, et c’est li commune maniere de l’emplaustre restorant la brisure a plusors dispositions, et meismement as femmes et as petis enfans, car il n’est mie ne trop chas ne trop frois.	And it is that you take flour that is held to the walls of the mill, and mix it with abundance of egg, and put this preparation, neither too clear nor too thick, and in use, and this is the common manner of the plaster restoring the fracture to many dispositions, and also to women and to small children, because it is neither too hot nor too cold.
Autre maniere d’emplastre restorans la brisure et la dislocation et la torsion:	Another manner of plaster restoring the fracture and dislocation and the twist: 
pren З abareis et ladani et enule et asefetide et gomme arabique et mugat, ana X З.;	Take bayberry and lead, and mule, and asafoetida, and gum arabic, and mugwort, an ounce ten. 
mirre et aloes, ana V З.;	myrrh and aloes, an ounce five.  
alechil VIIII З.;	and alechil nine ounces. 
et en fai poudre, et les melle avec aubun d’uef;	and make it powder, and mix them with yolk of an egg;
se li complexion de l’ome est chaude, si use de cest emplaustre, car il est de bone composition, et restoure les os brisiés hastanment, et vaut a plusors homes.	if the complexion of the man is hot, he should use this plaster, because it is of good composition, and restores broken bones completely, and is worth to many men.  
Autre maniere d’emplaustre que vaut a torsion:	Another manner of plaster that is good for twist: 
pren mugat et vismalve, ana X З.;	take mugwort and wormwood, an ounce ten.  
mirre et aloes, ana VIIII З.;	myrrh and aloes, an ounce nine. 
acaice VI З.;	and acai six ounces. 
bolic armenic X З., et broie bien, et confit avec aigue ou abun d’uef, et l’aministre.	Bolic armenic X Z., and grind well, and confit with water or yolk of an egg, and administer it. 
Autre maniere d’emplaustre a jointes et as os desevrez de lor leus, et apaise la dolor sorvenant, et le taille usent de l’os, et la briseure:	Another manner to plaster joints and bones dislocated from their places, and appease the pain arising, and the usage of bone, and the fracture: 
pren lainne novele, et la moille en aisil et en oile cuit, et met sus lou leu.	Take new wool, and moisten it in oil and heat, and put it upon the place.
Cist emplastres ne restoure mie, mais il est boins por apaisier d’aposteme chaut, et oste proprement les dolors.	This plaster does not restore, but it is good for soothing a hot abscess, and removes pain properly.
Autre maniere d’emplaustre qui restoure les os brisiez:	Another manner to plaster which restores broken bones: 
pren foilles de figuier seches, et foilles de pavol terrestre, et broie ensamble, et fai emplaustre.	Take dried fig leaves, and earth walnut leaves, and grind together, and make a plaster. 
Autre maniere d’emplaustre a la restoration de la brisure de l’os et por amenusier lou remenant de l’aposteme.	Another manner of emplastering for the restoration of a broken bone and to lessen the remainder of the abscess.
Pren racine de vismalve, camomille, flors de violettes, farine de veces, de chescune une partie;	Take root of mallow, chamomile, flowers of violets, flour of quince, of each one part; 
et broie, et confis avec vin, et se li membres est eschaufez, se le confis avec aigue de coriandre moiste, ou d’aigue, et en use.	And grind, and confit with wine, and if the limb is withered, confit it with coriander water, or water, and use it. 
Autre maniere d’emplaustre plus fors que li premier, quant aposteme dur vient a la restauration dou membre.	Another way of setting a bone more forcefully than the first, when a hard abscess comes to the restoration of the limb.
Pren racines de vismalve, et semence de lin, balauste, mellilote, et sansuce, et flors de violetes et de camomille, de toutes ana une partie;	Take roots of mallow, and seeds of flax, borage, melilot, and wormwood, and flowers of violets and chamomile, of all one part. 
et broie, et confit avec aigue de salz, ou aigue douce, ou avec vin, selonc la chalor du membre, et son repos.	and grind it, and confit with water of salt, or sweet water, or with wine, according to the heat of the limb, and its rest. 
Ypocras dist en son livre c’on ne mette sus lou membre brisiet por restorer fuer que cerote fait de cire et d’oile, et nulle autre chose plus, et dist qu’il soit entre dous ne trop molz ne trop durs.	Ipocras says in his book that one should not put on the broken limb for restoration other than a certain one made of wax and oil, and nothing else more, and he says that it should be between two, neither too soft nor too hard.
Et il semble galien c’on doit mettre sus lou membre brisiet, por restoreir, choses seches un poc chaudes, si com mirre et aloes et encens et semblans choses, si com nos avons dit.	And it seems Galen one must put on the broken member, to restore, things dry and a little warm, such as myrrh and aloe and incense and similar things, as we have said.
Autre maniere d’emplaustre que vaut a lesion et a dolor:	Another manner of ointment that is good for the lesion and pain:  
pren mugath et chevolz d’omes decopez, ou pennes d’oiseil, et vismalve, et seil igalment, et les broie, et en fai emplaustre et lou lie.	take mugwort and heads of doves cut off, or feathers of bird, and mallow, and wool equally, and grind them, and make an ointment from it and bind it.  
Et puis lou deslie un poc aprés, et pren garde se li malaides ne sent nule dolor, ne ne s’est meus li os de son leu;	And then unbind it a little afterwards, and take care if the patient feels no pain, or if his bones have not moved from their place;  
si ne lou deslie par mains jors.	if not unbind it not for many days. 
Et se dolor vient au leu, ou prurite, sens repos ou enfleure, si te haste, et le deslie, et oste l’emplaustre maintenant;	And if pain comes to the place, or itching, no rest or swelling, then hasten, and untie it, and remove the plaster now.  
et pren drapeil legier, et esponge de mer moiste, et plonge en aigue, et en leve lou leu, tant que li prurite cesse, et soit apaisie li dolor;	And take a light cloth, and sponge of moist sea, and dip it in water, and lift the place up, as long as the itching ceases, and the pain is appeased.  
puis laisse reposer lou membre une houre, puis met sus lainne seche, moillie en aigue ou en oile roset, et lie sus une nut, tant que tu soies seur d’aposteme chaut;	Then let the limb rest for an hour, then put on a dry cloth, moistened in water or rose oil, and tie it with a bandage, until you are sure of the hot abscess;
et repose li enflammation dou membre, et soit ostee li dolor, puis rencomence la lieure subtil, et un poc d’emplaustre, et ne l’estraindre mie si fort com devant;	And soothe the inflammation of the limb, and the pain is removed, then begin the delicate bandage again, and a little plaster, and do not bind it as tightly as before;
et subtilie tant qu’il soit sanez.	and gently until he is healed.  
Et se tu vois que aposteme chaus et roujor et dolor et enfleure sont jai osteit dou tout, et tu as mestier d’emplaustre et de liien, si le rencomence, si com tu a fait premier igalment.	And if you see that the abscess is hot and red, and the pain and swelling are all gone, and you need emplastrum and binding, then begin it again, just as you did at first.
Et s’il ne vient au membre nient de ceu que nos avons dit, si ne le desliier fuer que aprés III jors ou IIII ou V ou VII;	And if it does not come to the limb as we have said, do not unbind it except after III days or IV or V or VII. 
et aucune fois le laisse XX jors, selonc ce c’on voit, tant que li briseure s’aert, et aproche li ajostement de la char sus;	and no time leave it for XX days, according to what we see, until the fracture is joined, and approaches the setting of the bone.  
adonques lou restraint plus que premier, et li engroisse sa viande, si com j’ai dit devant;	Therefore, restrain it more than before, and make its flesh thicker, as I said earlier.  
et se tu vois lou leu sechier plus que mestier n’est, saiches que norrissemens n’i puet venir;	And if you see the place drying more than is necessary, know that there cannot come any nourishment; 
arose lou donques d’aigue chaude tede, toutes les fois que tu lou deslies, et ce soit chescun tier jor, et eslaiche un poc la lieure;	Therefore, use hot water, every time you untie it, and every third day, and moisten the place a little.  
par cest ovraige donques cort li norrissemens au membre, et esmende hastanment ceu que font li fol mire, que restourent le membre tortement:	Through this work then nourish the limb, and heal quickly those who do foolish things, that they return the limb twisted; 
c’est malvais, et si est ovraiges paourous, et je n’i voi autre chose que dou lassier et de l’ovrer droitement.	This is bad, and this work is dangerous, and I see nothing else than to let it be and work it straight.  
des diverses manieres de brisure	of diverse ways of breaking (bones)
Maintes manieres de brisures sont, et diverses figures, et les causes sont destintees;	There are many ways of fractures, and diverse shapes, and the causes are destined; 
car il a brisures que sont faites de percussion d’espee, et li colz oste tout l’os jusc’a syfac qui est desoz l’os, si com fait haiche ou fust;	for there are fractures that are made by the percussion of a sword, and the collarbone all the bone up to the surface which is below the bone, as if made high or low; 
et por ceu est apelee ceste maniere de briseure «haichure».	and for this reason this kind of fracture is called “haichure.” 
Ou li espee cope l’os par desus sens percier, et est apelee ceste maniere de brisure «absolue»;	When the sword cuts through the bone from above without piercing it, and this kind of fracture is called “absolue”; 
et est li plaie de ces II brisures grans ou petite.	and is the wound of these two fractures large or small.  
Et s’il i a percussion emboee, ou fendure ou de colz de piere, ou de cheoir sus piere, ou d’autres semblans.	And if there is an enmeshed percussion, or a split or of the bone's neck, or of the head on a bone, or similar things.
Et s’il a brisure persant, qui aproiche jusc’a la toile qui est desoz l’os, ou elle est sus l’os, et est ceste plaie ou grans ou petite.	And if it has a fracture penetrating, which approaches up to the skin that is below the bone, or it is above the bone, and this wound is great or small.
Et si a plaie qui est reponue en l’os ausi subtil com uns chevous, et est li fendure petite, et por ceu est apelee ceste brisure «capillaire»;	And if the wound which is put back into the bone as subtly as a hair, and is the fissure small, and for this reason this fracture is called “capillaire”; 
et si la plaie qui est faite ou par ferir de piere, ou par cheoir, ou par semblant chose, et fait entrer la piece de l’os aval, et est li leus chevez si com font li chaudelier quant il fierent sus les chaudieres;	and if the wound which is made either by hitting with stone, or by falling, or by similar thing, and makes the piece of bone enter inside, and is the  piece like how smiths do when they hit on cauldrons; 
si entre li piere dedens.	if it goes between the pieces inside. 
Et ceu avient plus a sous qui ont ou chief moistes os, si com chief d’enfant;	And this happens more to those who have or whose head is moist bone, like that of a child.  
et avient a toutes ces manieres de brisure que pieces menues en sont desevrees si com esteles;	and it happens in all these ways of fracture where small pieces are dislodged as if stars; 
et je em parlerai en son leu.	and I will speak of them in their place.  
Et conoissons toutes manieres de briseures par la detraction sus elles, et l’inquisition a tentes, et par la char corrumpue qui est sus.	And let us know all the ways of fractures by retracting upon them, and by probing with probes, and by the corrupted flesh that is on it.
Li semblance capillaire est conue par ceu que quant on a descovert l’os, et on frote enche sus, si apert li brisure noire.	The seeming capillary is known by this: when one has uncovered the bone, and rubs upon it, the fracture appears black.
En la cure de la brisure, pren garde as accidens dou malaide, et se tu vois nul malvais accident, si com vomissement de cole, et amission d’entendement, et estension, et paumeson, et fievre ague, et les eulz issir fuer et rougir, et autres semblans em plusors dispositions, si ne puet saner sens doute.	In the cure of a fracture, take care of the accidents of the patient, and if you see no bad accident, such as vomiting of bile, and loss of understanding, and extension, and paleness, and fever ague, and eyes becoming inflamed and red, and other similar things in more dispositions, then it cannot heal without doubt.
Et se tu ne vois accident espoantauble, et tu esperes salut, si comence la cure.	And if you do not see an escapable accident, and you hope for salvation, so commence the cure.
Et quant li navrez vient premier a toi, et c’est en yver, si covient oster l’os devant lou quatorzime jor au mues que tu pues.	And when the fracture comes to you first, and it is in winter, then it is necessary to remove the bone before the fourteenth day as much as you can.
Et se c’est en esteit, si te haste d’oster l’os devant lou septime jor, ainsois que li toile desoz l’os soit corrumpue, et vienent li accident que nos avons dit.	And if it is in summer, then hasten to remove the bone before the seventh day, so that the tissue under the bone does not rot, and comes the accident that we have said.
Et se li brisure de l’os vient jusc’a la toile que cuevre lou cerveil, si covient que tu fendes la partie fendue ensi:	And if the fracture of the bone comes to the membrane that covers the brain, then you should split the fractured part like this: 
et est que tu preignes lou chief dou malaide navreit, et descuevre sus l’os en toutes les manieres que tu pues, et sus la figure de la plaie plus souef que tu pues, et se decorrement de sanc vient au descovrir l’os, ou aposteme chaus, se li aide de ceu qu’il covient, et est que tu emplisses lou leu de drapelz moilliez en oile roset;	and that you press the head of the patient down firmly, and uncover it on the bone in all ways that you can, and on the figure of the wound more carefully than you can, and if bleeding comes when uncovering the bone, or abscess put a bandage on it, if it is needed, and that you fill the place with cloths moistened in rose oil; 
et fai reposer la plaie tant que li apostemes chaus soit apaisiez, et soies asseurez de decorrement de sanc;	and make the wound rest until the abscess is healed, and be assured of bleeding cessation;
puis comence entor l’os a oster, et c’est fait selonc II manieres d’ovraige:	Then begins to remove the bone, and it is done according to two ways of work:  
l’une manieres si est que tu copes au taillement estroit devant, et c’est li forme:	One way is that you cut at the narrow edge in front, and this is the form: 
Et puis i boute .i. autre taillement plus grant que lou premier.	And then put another incision larger than the first one.
Et li seconde maniere si est que tu aies nombre de taillemens divers, les uns estrois et les autres larges, et soient a pointe, et soient de fer inde;	And the second manner is that you have a number of different cuts, some narrow and others wide, and some pointed, and some blunt; 
et en oevre legierement, que tu ne bleces le chief.	and in work lightly, so that you do not break the head.
Et se li os est fors et durs, si covient que tu lou perces entor, ainsois que tu i aministres taillemens avec tareres, ne mie parfont qu’il ne percent outre l’os dou test, et doit avoir desus la pointe une marge ou I cercle, que ne laisse passer la pointe outre l’os;	And if the bone is hard and stiff, then it behooves you to pierce it around, so that you administer cuts with chisels, no more deeply than that it does not go through the test of bone, and it must have above the point a margin or circle that does not allow the point to pass beyond the bone;  
et t’en covient avoir plusors, si que chescuns viegne en son leu de l’espés de l’os, si que tu aies tareres por toz test;	And it behooves you to have several, so that each comes in its place of the thickness of the bone, so that you have chisels for all tests;  
et c’est li forme des III manieres de tareres:	and this is the form of the III manners of bandages: 
Li qualitez por percier entor l’os brisiet est que tu mettes I tarere sus l’os, et torne a tes dois tant que tu saiches que li os est perciez;	The qualities to perceive around the broken bone is that you place a bandage on the bone, and turn to your two until you know that the bone is pierced. 
puis remet lou tarere autre part un poc aprés, et ensi fai tout entor, puis cope as incisoires l’espaice de l’os qui est entre les pertu, et fai ceu plus subtilment que tu pues, et legierement, si com nos avons dit, tant que tu en traies l’os a ta main, ou a aucun des estrumens que tu as si com tenailles, pinceures;	then place the bandage elsewhere a little after, and thus do all around, then cut with the incisors the space of the bone that is between the perforations, and do these more subtly than you can, and lightly, as we have said, until you draw the bone to your hand, or to any of the instruments that you have such as pliers, pincers;
et garde que tu ne touchier au cerveil ne au syfac.	and keep that you do not touch the brain nor the spinal cord. 
Et quant tu avras l’os perciet, et trait, si couvient que tu reses l’apreteit qui est demoree de l’os a tout I autre estrument semblant a un incisoire, mais il covient qu’il soit plus tenves et plus subtilz que li autre incisoire;	And when you will have the bone pierced, and treated, it is fitting that you reset the apparatus which is detached from the bone to all other instruments similar to an incisor, but it is fitting that it be more tenacious and more subtle than the other incisor.
et s’il demore rien des petis os, ne nulles escailles, si les oste legierement a I des estrumens;	and if it remains any of the small bones, or no scales, so carefully to the bone with instruments.  
puis cure la plaie de tentes et d’oignemens que nos avons dit.	then cure the wound with tents and dressings as we have said. 
Et li autre maniere d’ovraige si est cil que Galiiens dist, qui est plus saus;	And the other manner of work is that which Galien says, which is drier. 
et le loa molt fort, et c’est sa parole.	and the load much strong, and that is his word.  
Il covient premier que tu descuevres une partie de l’os, lai ou li brisure apert mues, si que quant tu avras descovert celle partie, si metras desoz lou chief de cest incisoire lenticulaire, de coi ci est li forme:	It is necessary first that you uncover a part of the bone, where the fracture appears to move, so that when you have uncovered that part, then place under the head of this lentil-shaped incisional instrument, for this is its form:
Et ne trenche mie d’une part, et est li partie ague en II costez, si que li trenchans est devers l’os;	And do not trench from one side, and is the party acute in II coasts, so that the trenching is towards the bone; 
puis fier d’un petit maillet sus, si que tu copes legierement l’os tout entor, et te done bien en garde de la toile que est desoz;	then strike with a small hammer above, so that you tap lightly the bone all around, and give yourself well guard of the cloth that is underneath;  
s’elle est aerse a l’os, si l’oste legierement, car on l’oste bien sens nuisement, et sens paor.	if it is adhered to the bone, then gently remove it, because it is well removed without annoyance, and without fear. 
Et se li brisure de l’os ne perce jusc’a la toile, et li os est copez tant soulement par desus, et il i a petites pieces, si couvient rere celle asperiteit, et oster les escailles au raseur subtil dont tu dois avoir diverses quantitez, por amenistrer en chescun leu le plus covenauble, selonc l’ovraige et la figure de la brisure.	And if the bone fracture does not reach the skin, and the bone is broken only from above, and there are small pieces, it is necessary to first apply this asperity, and remove the scales with a fine rasp which you must have in various quantities, to administer in each place the most suitable one, according to the work and the figure of the fracture.
Si reis devant de grant raseurs, et aprés de plus subtilz, et ne cesser de ceu faire tant k’il soit bien.	If you begin with coarse rasps, and afterwards with finer ones, and do not cease doing this until it is well.
En chescune des autres tailleures capillaires et brisure subtil, covient que tu amenistres cause selonc son adrecement;	In each of the other capillary cuts and subtle fracture, you must bring cause according to its arrangement;  
et c’est chose que n’est mie reponue a celui qui a mis son estude en cest art.	and that is thing which is not replied to him who has put his study in this art. 
Et se li syfac est descovers, si covient que tu preignes I drapeil de lin, selonc la quantiteit de la plaie, et le moille en oile roset, et le mete sus la plaie;	And if the wound is uncovered, it is necessary that you take a linen cloth, according to the size of the wound, and moisten it in rose oil, and place it on the wound. 
puis pren I autre drapeil doublé en II ou en III, et le moille en vin et en oile roset, et le met sus le premier drapeil;	then take another cloth doubled in two or three, and moisten it in wine and rose oil, and place it on the first cloth;  
et fai ceu plus legierement que tu pues, que tu ne grever lou syfac, puis aministre par desus I autre liien, et ne l’estraindre mie fuer que tant k’il teigne la plaie soulement;	and do this more gently than you can, so that you do not injure the wound, then administer above it another linen cloth, and do not bind it too tightly except to keep the wound closed; 
et le laisse ensi I jor ou II, tant que li apostemes chaus soit apaisiez, puis le deslie, et i aministre medicines si com racines de lis, et farine de veces, et poudre d’encens, et aristologe, et semblans choses;	and leave it thus for one or two days, until the abscess is calmed, then untie it, and administer medicines such as roots of licorice, and chickpea flour, and frankincense powder, and arnica, and similar things. 
et de ces choses fai poudre, et met sus la plaie, et i aministre adés medicines mondefians sens mordication;	and from these things make a powder, and put it on the wound, and administer other medicinal ointments without biting.  
et warde que li plaie soit adés nette, que tu n’i laissier mie l’oignement, ne n’i laissier mie assembler bowe, car quant bowe s’asemble sus la toile dou cerveil, si la corront et porrist, et avient au malaide grans malice;	and guard that the wound be quite clean, that you do not leave there any ointment, nor let it join together with flesh, because when flesh joins on the brain's membrane, it inflames and hurts, and brings great evil to the patient; 
car quant on met sus lou syfac chose mordant, si nercist par desus.	because when one puts upon it a biting thing, it is burned from above.  
Pren warde donques, se nulz mavais accidens vient au malaide, si com nos avons dit, si est doutable sens doute.	Take ward then, if no bad accidents come to the patient, as we have said, so it is doubtful without doubt.
Et se noiror n’i vient fuers que por la medicine c’on a mise sus, que teil vertu ait, si covient que tu preignes une partie de miel, et III parties d’oile roset et en glue I drapel, et lou met sus lou syfac;	And if blacking does not come forth except for the medicine that has been put upon it, and if it has virtue, then it behooves you to take one part of honey, and three parts of rose oil and in glue one drape, and place it upon the wound.
puis lou cure de manieres de cures qu’il couvient, tant qu’il soit sanez.	then treat it with the ways of treatment that are proper until it is healed.  
Saiches que aucune fois sont brisies les II parties dou neis desus, ou li une par li soulement, car ce sont II os;	Know that at times the two parts of the nose are broken above, or one by itself, because they are two bones;
et cil desoz est cartillaginous, et ne brise mie, si ne fait fuer k’enbower ou tordre, et puis saine.	and this below is cartilaginous, and does not break, unless it is forced to bend or twist, and then it heals.  
Et se l’une des II parties est brisie, si covient que tu boutes ton petit doi ou pertus dou neis, et met igal cele brisure dedens a ton doi indice, et au pouchet par defuer, tant que li neis reveigne selonc sa figure natureil;	And if one of the two parts is broken, then you must put your small finger or the other into it, and place that fracture inside your index finger, and on the palm outward, until the bone returns according to its natural shape.  
et fai ce legierement, et warde que li malaides ne sente dolor par ton ovraige.	and do this lightly, and guard so that the patient does not feel pain from your work. 
Et se li brisure est en la partie desus lou neis, et ne puet venir li dois au leu, si couvient que tu lou mettes igal au chief d’un rait un poc gros.	And if the fracture is in the part above the nose, and it cannot come to its place, then you should put it even on top of a rail a little thick.
Et se li brisure est de II pars, si refai autretel, et te haste de restorer lou premier jor, se tu pues;	And if the fracture is of two parts, do this again, and hasten to restore it on the first day, if you can. 
se ce non, aprés lou septime ou le disime, quant li apostemes chaus est apaisiez, puis bouthe au chief dou neis tentes de drapelz de lin, se li brisure est en une partie.	If not, after the seventh or tenth day, when the abscess has subsided, then put on the head of the finger bandages of linen, if the fracture is in one part.   
Ou tu boutes I autre d’autre part, se li brisure i est;	Or you break the other side if there is a fracture there; 
et soient les tentes si grosses qu’eles emplissent les pertus dou neis.	and let the tents be so large that they fill the openings of the wounds.  
Et dirent aucun restorour c’on doit moillier les tentes em burre, et muer chescun jor.	And they said any restorer one must moisten the tents in butter, and change each day.
Il ne me semble mie que ce soit bien, mais covient qu’elles soient moillies en confection d’aubun d’uef, et de poudre de molin;	It does not seem to me that this is good, but it is necessary that they be moistened in the preparation of a mixture of egg yolk and ground pepper. 
puis laisse la tente, tant que li os soit fers, et li cartilaiges endurcis.	Then leave the tent until the bone is hard and the cartilage is hardened. 
Et aucune fois boute on ou neis pennes d’oie en leu de tentes, et si a I souef drapeil entor, et se tient la briseure, et soffle li malaides parmi;	And at no time should one put goose feathers in their place, and if the wind blows through there, and it holds the fracture, and it causes the patient to blow among them;  
or fai lou kel ke tu vues.	or do what you see fit. 
Et se apostemes chaus vient au neis tandis com tu i oevres, si i met cerote ou coton moilliet en oile roset, ou en .i. poc de dyaquilon.	And if an abscess comes to the new while you work on it, put cerote or cotton moistened in rose oil, or in i. p. of diaquilon.
Et se apostemes chaus n’i vient, si met emplastre par defuer, de farine de sisament, et de poudre d’encens, confites avec aubun d’uef, puis met sus estoupes legieres, et ne liier mie lou neis;	And if an abscess arises, apply a poultice from the outside of ground sesame seed and powdered incense, mixed with egg yolk, then put light bandages on top and do not bind the wounds tightly; 
et se li brisure dou neis est petite, et il est brisiés em menues pieces, si l’estrai as estrumens covenables a ceu, puis cout la fendure, et la cure de choses enjanrans char, et soudant, si com emplastres et oignemens covenables a ceu;	And if the fracture of the bone is small, and it is broken into small pieces, then extract them with suitable instruments, then stitch the wound, and care for it with appropriate things like flesh, and bandage, as with plasters and ointments suitable for that; 
et s’il n’a dedens lou neis nule plaie, si lou cure de tentes, et i met cainnes de plonc, tant qu’il soit sanez.	And if inside the bone there is no wound, then cure it with bandages, and put in some splints, until it is healed. 
de la routure de la mandibule	Of the jaw fracture
Quant li mandibule est route desoz, et il n’i a point de plaie defuer, et li brisure est defuer tant soulement, et n’est mie brisiez en dous, fuer que corbelz dedens, si le conoist on legierement.	When the jaw is broken below, and there is no external wound, and the fracture is only outside, and is not broken in two, except for a bulge inside, if one knows it lightly.
Il covient, se li brisure est en la destre partie, que tu boutes ton doi indice en la bouche dou malaide;	It is necessary, if the fracture is in the right part, that you put your index finger into the mouth of the patient. 
et se li brisure est en la mandibule senestre, si boute ton doi indice de la main destre, et boute la brisure dedens legierement, et l’afaite a l’autre main par defuer, et met igal.	And if the fracture is in the left jawbone, then put your right index finger into the mouth, and gently push the fracture inwards, and hold it with the other hand from outside, and make it even. 
Et se li brisure de la mandibule est desevree en .ij., si covient que tu aministres extension de .ij. pars, tant qu’il soit igalz.	And if the jawbone fracture is broken in two, it is necessary that you administer an extension of two parts, until it is straight.
Et se commovemens des dens avient, ou routure, si les estrain d’un fil d’or ou d’argent ou de soie, puis met sus la mandibule brisie cerote, et met sus I drapel double;	And if movement of the teeth happens, or a rupture, then restrain them with a thread of gold or silver or silk, then put on top of the broken jawbone a cerot, and put a double cloth over it;
et met sus lou drapel une grant estele bien faite, ou une piece de cuir igal, longe et large selonc la mandibule, et la lie sus au mues que tu pues, et comande a malaide qu’il se repose, et menjuce viandes legieres.	And place on the cloth a large plate well made, or a piece of leather even, long and wide according to the jawbone, and tie it onto the wound as much as you can, and command the patient to rest, and eat light meats. 
Et se tu vois que li figure se chainge, si le deslie au tier jor, et puis remet a point ceu que c’est chaingiet;	And if you see that the figure changes, then untie it on the third day, and then put back in place what has changed. 
et met emplaustre sus, de la poudre dou moulin avec abun d’uef ou farine de sisament, aprés ceu que tu as osteit lou cerote;	And place a plaster on top, of the powder from the mill with an abundance of egg or sesame flour, after what you have removed the cautery.
et met sus l’emplaustre lainne legiere, et se li emplaustres s’aert, et li disposition dou malaide ne se chainge, laisse le tant k’il soit sanez;	And place a light linen bandage on top, and if the plasters dry, and the patient's condition does not change, leave him as long as he is healthy.
maintes fois est sanez en III semainnes.	Many times it heals in three weeks. 
Et se apostemes chaus vient, si amenistre ceu que nos avons dit maintes fois.	And if an abscess comes, administer what we have said many times.
Et s’il i a brisure et plaie ensamble, rewarde se nule piece de l’os en est ostee;	And if there is a fracture and wound together, reward if no piece of the bone is removed;
si subtilie de l’oster as estrumens covenaubles a ceu.	If subtle of the bone instruments are suitable to these. 
Et se li plaie est estroite, si l’eslarge a flaime selonc ta necessiteit.	And if the wound is narrow, then enlarge it with flame according to your need.
Et quant tu avras ostees toutes ces pieces, et il n’i demore nule, si cout la plaie, s’ele est large, et met sus .i. des emplaustres covenaubles a ceu, por enjanrer char, tant qu’il soit sanez.	And when you will have removed all these pieces, and there is none remaining, then cover the wound, if it is wide, and put upon it one plaster suitable to that, in order to hinder flesh, until it is healed.
de la forcele	of the forceps
Li forcele brise plusors fois devant, devers l’espaule, et li brisure si est selonc III manieres:	The fracture breaks more often in front, towards the shoulder, and the fracture is according to three manners:
ou elle est brisie et desevree en II, et i a pieces, et est li plus legiere a restorer;	Where it is broken and separated in two, and there are pieces, and it is the lightest to restore; 
ou il i a brisure avec plaie.	Or there is a fracture with a wound. 
Et li ovraiges si est quant li brisure est sens plaie, que tu aies II ministres, si que li uns teigne l’ajutoire que sent la forcele brisie;	And the work of this is when the fracture is without a wound, that you have two ministers, so that one holds the arm that feels the broken bone;  
et li autres estende lou col vers la partie;	and the other extends the neck towards the part; 
puis met igal la brisure a tes dois, si que li forme soit si com il covient, et n’i ait ne apparance ne chevement.	then put the fracture equal to your two, so that the form is as it should be, and there be no appearance or gap. 
Et se tu a mestier de plus estendre, si met desoz l’espaule au malaide une spere reonde de drap, ou de lainne, et soit grosse selonc ta necessiteit;	And if you need to extend more, so put under the shoulder of the patient a round sphere of cloth, or wool, and be thick according to your necessity; 
et estent et lieve la forcele, et estraint le spere a ta main, si que tu mettes igal la brisure, si com il covient.	and are gently the force applied, and restrain the spear in your hand, so that you put equal the fracture, as it befits. 
Et se tu ne pues traire le chief de la forcele au defuer, por ceu qu’elle vient em parfont, si covient que li malaides gise sovin sus son hatereil, et met desoz l’espaule .i. oreillier moien, et boute li ministres l’espaule aval, tant que li os de la forcele soit levez.	And if you cannot draw the head of the shoulder with force because it comes back in place, then it is necessary that the patient lie prone on his arm and place below the shoulder 1 hour glass, and push the ministers' shoulder down until the bone of the shoulder is lifted.
Et puis adrece la brisure a tes dois, et se tu lou trueves debrisiet, si covient que tu fendes sus;	And then apply the fracture to your two hands, and if you find it broken, it is necessary that you divide upon.  
et trai fuer les pieces legierement, et se li os ne puet joindre por aucun sormontement, si le cope a l’un des incisoires que tu as;	and treat the pieces lightly, and if the bone cannot join by any raising, then it cut with one of the incisions that you have. 
mais que tu mettes desoz la forcele cest estrument, por warder lou syfac:	but that you place under the force a this instrument, to keep the soft tissue.
et semble une cuiller, et n’est mie chevez, et soit ausi large com il lou covient, selonc la grandor de l’os et la possance de l’uevre;	and resembles a spoon, and is not quite hollowed out, and be as wide as it suits, according to the size of the bone and the strength of the work. 
et ait II chiés, si com tu vois, et soit li uns larges, et li autres estrois, si com est li routure de la plaie que tu as fait quant tu as trait les os;	and it has two ends, as you see, and one be wide, and the other narrow, as is the break of the wound that you made when you treated the bones;
et quant tu es asseurez d’aposteme chaut, si cout la plaie, et se li routure est petite, ou tu doutes aposteme chaut, si emple la plaie de drapelz et de tentes, selonc sa quantiteit.	And when you are assured of the hot abscess, if cut the wound, and if the rupture is small, or if you doubt hot abscess, if employ the wound with cloths and tents, according to its quantity. 
Et se apostemes chaus i vient, si moille .i. drapel en oile roset et en aisil et en vin, et met sus.	And if a hot abscess comes, then moisten one bandage in rose oil and in honey and in wine, and place it on top.
Li estrignement de l’os, quant il est sens plaies et sens tailleure, est que tu mettes sus l’os l’enplaustre de la poudre dou molin et d’aubun d’uef, et met estoupes legieres sus, et met une spere desoz l’assele, se tu en as mestier;	The tightening of the bone, when it is without wounds and without cutting, is that you put on the bone the plaster of powder from the mill and beaten egg white, and put light dressings above, and put a sphere under the seat, if you need it. 
puis pren une tres grant bende d’une palme de large, puis met I drapeil double sus estoupes, et l’emplaustre;	Then take a very wide bandage of one palm width, then put the double cloth above the dressings and the plaster.   
puis pren une estele subtil de III dois de large et de lonc, et l’envoloupe entor celui bendeil, si que li chief dou bendeil soient pendant;	Then take a slender stick of three fingers wide and long, and wrap it around that bandaged one, so that the head of the bandage hangs down. 
et met l’estele sus la briseure, et torne le bendeil sus lou col, et desoz l’asselle sainne, et desoz l’asselle malaide;	and put the stick on the bruise, and turn the bandage around the neck, and under the healthy armpit, and under the affected armpit; 
et la ramoinne de chescune partie, et quant tu vois ke li lieure tient la briseure avenanment, et tu vois clerement que li estele ne se muet desus l’os brisiet, si le rewarde chescun jor, et quant li liiens eslaiche, si lou restraint;	and tighten it on each side, and when you see that the bandage holds the bruise well, and you clearly see that the stick does not move above the broken bone, then reward (bind) it every day, and when the bandage loosens, then bind it again; 
et fai gesir lou malaide sus son dos, et li met quant il dort I petit orillier desoz l’assele, por lever l’ajutoire en haut;	and make the patient lie on his back, and put a small pillow under the armpit when he sleeps, in order to raise the shoulder higher; 
si aligera li brisure de la forcele par l’aligement de l’espaule, ou tu li lie lou bras au col, et ne lou desliier se malvais accidens n’i vient, jusc’a XX jors;	so it will lighten the bruise from the pain by aligning the shoulder, or you bind his arm to his neck, and do not unbind it unless a bad accident happens, until twenty days;
puis rencomence l’emplaustre, se tu vois qu’il en ait mestier, et l’estraint et le laisse ensi, tant qu’il soit restorez;	then restart the bandaging if you see that it is necessary, and restrain it and leave it like this until it is restored 
et elle est restoree au plus en XXVIII jors, et en moins a aucuns homes.	and it is restored within at most XXVIII days, and in less for no man 
de la brisure de l’espaule	of the fracture of the shoulder
Poc avient que li espaule brise ou large leu ne em mileu, et ne lou seit on fuers que par lou touchement;	It happens sometimes that the shoulder breaks or its socket is displaced in the middle, and it is not known if there was a fracture except by touch; 
si l’apareille selonc la figure de la brisure, et la ramoinne selonc sa forme natureil, en toutes les manieres que tu pues;	so set the joint according to the figure of the fracture, and reset it according to its natural form, in every way that you can; 
puis met sor le leu poudre dou molin avec abun d’uef, et estoupes legieres, et met sus I drapeil double;	then put on top of the wound powder from the mill with an abundance of egg, and light dressings, and put a double cloth above; 
puis met sus une estele large et subtil, un poc plus large de l’espaule, et se desoz l’estele est chevemens en aucun leu de l’espaule, si emple celle cheveure d’estoupes de lin, si que li estele siece igalment;	then put on top a wide and thin pad, a bit wider than the shoulder, and if any part of the pad touches the shoulder, then place cotton dressings beneath it so that the pad lies evenly; 
et puis l’estraint a tout une grant bende fermement, si que li estele ne se mueve de son leu, et regarde le liien chescun jor;	and then binds it with a very strong bandage firmly so that the bone does not move from its place, and look at the joint every day. 
et toutes les fois k’il amolist, si l’estraint, et met igal l’estele s’elle est fuer de son leu, et gise li malaides sus son costeit;	and every time it softens, binds it again, and places the bone straight if it is out of place, and lies the patient on his side. 
et li espaule est restouree en XX jors ou en XXV.	and the shoulder is restored in twenty days or in twenty-five.
Et quant cist nombres est acomplis, si le deslie, et soies seur, car ce n’est mie os qui se mette fuer legierement.	And when this number is complete, then untie it, and be sure, because it is not bone that is easily put out of place. 
Et se une piece de l’os tent avant, et point desoz lou keur, si fent sus, et l’oste, et fai ceu que nos avons dit en la brisure de la forcele d’apaisier aposteme chaut.	And if a piece of bone protrudes forward, and not below the joint, so do it above, and the bone, and do what we have said in the fracture of the collarbone to soothe the hot abscess.
de la brisure dou pis	of the fracture of the leg
Li peis est aucune fois brisiez em mileu, mais ce avient poc;	The bone is sometimes broken in the middle, but this happens rarely;
mais il brise sovent au defuer.	but it often breaks at the edge. 
Et quant il est brisiez emmi, si decline au desoz, et sent li malaides grant dolor, et faute d’alainne, et toust, et par aventure vomist sanc, et apert li chevemens en l’os brisiés, et lou sent om bien.	And when it is broken in its marrow, it sinks to the lower part, and the patient feels great pain, and lack of strength, and all things, and perhaps vomits blood, and opens the passages within the broken bone, and it smells quite bad.
Et li restoracion si est que li malaides gise sovin sus son dos, et li met I cussin entre les espaules, puis presse les espaules, et li assemble les costes des II costelz a tes mains, et subtilie dou mettre igal a toutes les manieres que tu pues, tant que li figure de l’os soit si com il covient;	And the restoration is that the patient lies often on his back, and puts one cushion between the shoulders, then presses the shoulders together, and joins the ribs of the two ribs with your hands, and carefully tries to put them straight in every way as you can, until the figure of the bone is as it should be; 
puis met sus emplaustres et estoupes desus l’estele subtil de salz, ou d’autre fust legier, et l’envoloupe en I drapeil, et la lie sus l’os brisiet, si qu’elle ne se mueve;	then put on plasters and bandages over the thin layer of salt, or other light wool, and wrap it in a cloth, and lay it on top of the broken bone so that it doesn't move 
et torne le liien reondement au dos, et l’estraint avenanment, et rewarde chescune houre la liure, et s’elle ramolist, si l’estraint;	and turn the band around to the back, and restrain it firmly, and reward each hour the linen, and if it softens, restrain it; 
et s’il lou covient desliier, por corrosion ou por prurite que vient au leu, ou dolor ou aposteme, si te haste, et lou deslie, et raie l’emplaustre, et adresce ceu qui i est venus de manieres de cures;	and if it is necessary to loosen it, for corrosion or for itching that comes to the place, or pain or abscess, then hurry and loosen it, and scrape away the plaster, and address what has come up there with methods of healing; 
puis ramoinne l’emplaustre, et l’estraint tant qu’il soit sanez.	then put back on the plaster, and restrain it until it is healed.  
de la brisure des costes	of the breakage of the ribs
Saiches que li briseure des costes ne vient fuer que en leus gros aprés le dos, et au chief dedens, et ne ploient fuer que por ceu qu’eles sont glairouses;	Know that the fracture of the ribs comes only in their thick parts after the back, and at the head within, and they bend only for that reason that they are glassy; 
et le sent om bien a l’inquisition as dois.	and one feels it well at the inquiry so does.  
Et li restoremens si est que tu met igal la brisure, si com il covient.	And the restoration is that you set the fracture equal, as it is right.
Et puis met l’emplaustre, et l’estraint d’une estele, se tu en as mestier.	And then put the splint on it, and restrain it with a stick, if you need it.
Et se li brisure des costes est declinans au dedens, si sent li malaides tres grant dolor, et pointure, ausi com de pleuresin, car li os point la toile;	And if the fracture of the ribs is declining inwards, one feels the patient great pain, and prickling, as well as from pleurisy, because the bone points the skin. 
et alaine a poinnes, et toust et vomist grant planteit de sanc, et c’est de grief santeit, et li ancien i ont mis grant engien.	and besides pains, and coughs and vomits great planty of blood, and this is of grave sickness, and the ancients put great engine upon it. 
Et si a de ces qui dient qu’il le covient aministrer viandes qui enflent le ventre, por bouter la briseure au defuer.	And if some say it is necessary to administer meats that swell the belly, to expel the wind outward.
Nos ne faisons mie ceu, que apostemes chaulz n’i viegne, s’il n’i est venus.	We do not do this, except for hot abscesses, if they have not yet come.
Et s’il i est venus, si le saine.	And if it has come, then treat it.
Et dirent aucun d’ous c’on met ventouses sor le leu, por sucier forment, et c’est semblant a raison;	And they said of these [ventouses], one puts on the place to suck strongly, and this seems reasonable.  
toutevoie, doutance i a que li ventouse n’atraie les superfluitez au leu por la disposition de foiblece.	Nevertheless, there is doubt that the suction does not draw the superfluities to the place for the disposition of weakness. 
Et dirent aucun d’ous c’on doit covrir le leu de lainne moillie en oile chaut, et met on tentes entre les costes por metre igal la lieure entor, puis soit curez de la cure de pleurisin, de viande et de medicine.	And they say any one of you should cover the place with a woolen cloth in hot oil, and put tents between the ribs to make equal the lying wound, then be cured of the plague of pleurisy, meat, and medicine.
Et se li malaides sent grant dolor qu’il ne puet soffrir par l’os qui point la toile, et doutance est au malaide, si covient fendre sus lou leu de la coste brisie, et covient mettre desoz I estrument por warder lou syfac;	And if the patient feels great pain that he cannot bear because of the bone that pokes the skin, and there is doubt for the patient, then it is necessary to split above the place of the broken rib, and it is necessary to put underneath an instrument to ward off the lung.
et adonques doit on trenchier l’os, et traire legierement, et puis coudre les II levres de la plaie, s’elle est grans, et le curez d’emplaustres, tant qu’il soit sanez.	And then one must cut the bone, and drain slightly, and then sew the two lips of the wound, if it is large, and cure it with ointments until it is healed.  
Et se apostemes chaus vient, si met sus drapelz moilliez en oile roset, et met sus lou leu;	And if an abscess comes, then put on a soft cloth in rose oil, and put it on the place. 
et cure tandis le leu de ceu qu’il covient a aposteme, et soit gisans sovins sus lou costeit ou il doit, tant qu’il soit sanez.	and cure while the place of those that it is fitting to abscess, and be lying soundly on the ribs where it should, until it is healed.  
de la brisure dou col	of the breaking of the neck
Aucune fois vient briseure as os dou col, et poc avient k’il ploie;	Sometimes a fracture comes to the bones of the neck, and sometimes it happens that it bends; 
et ausi a l’espinee dou dos.	and also to the spine of the back.  
Et quant ce avient a aucun, et tu vues savoir s’il sera sanez ou non, si pren warde se tu vois ses mains mollifiies et enflees et mortes, et ne les puet movoir ne estendre, et quant tu les poins d’une aguille, si ne lou sent.	And when this happens to someone, and you want to know if he will be healed or not, then take note if you see his hands softened and swollen and dead, and he cannot move them nor extend them, and when you prick them with a needle, he feels nothing.
Saiches qu’il est mortelz em plusors dispositions, et s’il les muet et sent bien quant on les estraint et point, saiches que li jointure de l’os est sauve, et que li malaides iert curez, s’on i met cure.	Know that it is mortal in many dispositions, and if they move and feel well when they are pulled and held still, know that the joint of the bone is saved, and that the patient will be cured if one puts care to it.
