Et se semblans chose vient a l’espinee dou dos, et tu vues savoir s’il iert sanez ou non, si pren warde se li piez sont amollis, et se li accident i sont qui sont em mains, et sus lou dos saut ventositeit et egestion sens volonteit;	And if such a thing comes to the spine of the back, and you want to know if it is healed or not, then take ward if the limbs are softened, and if the accident is that which is in hands, and on the back there is looseness and discharge without will; 
et quant on l’a sovineit sus son ventre, si saut egestion sens volonteit.	and when one has it settled on its belly, then there is discharge without will.  
Et quant il est sovinez sus son dos et il vuet asseller, si ne puet.	And when it is set on its back and he wants to sit up, he cannot.
Saiches qu’il est mortelz:	Know that it is mortal: 
si ne laboreir mie en sa cure.	if he does not labor in his care.  
Et se cist accident ne li vienent, si est li chose plus legiere.	And if this accident does not happen to him, then the thing is lighter.
Et li cure si est que tu rewardes s’il i a aposteme chaut, si met sus l’espinee oile roset ou oile de moieuf d’uef, tant qu’il soit apaisiez;	And the cure is that you should warm it if there is an abscess, and put on its spine rose oil or oil of egg yolk, until it is appeased. 
puis met sus un des emplaustres confortans et sechans, et le lie d’un liien, et comande au malaide a reposer;	Then put on top one of the comforting and drying plasters, and tie it with a bandage, and instruct the patient to rest. 
et ne dorme mie sus celle partie ou il sent la dolor, tant k’il soit sanez.	And do not sleep on that part where he feels pain, until it is healed.  
Et se aucuns os se dessevre, si covient coper sus lou keur;	And if any bone becomes dislocated, then you should cover it with the heat; 
et oste l’os, puis assemble les II levres de la plaie, s’elle est grans, a une costure, puis le cure d’oignement enjanrant char, tant qu’il soit sanez;	and set the bone, then bring together the two edges of the wound, if it is large, with a suture, and then treat it with ointment that promotes flesh growth, until it is healed.  
et se li chiés de l’os est brisiez, ki est apelez li «chiés de la kowe», se i boute ton pouchet de ta main senestre, et le met igal a l’autre main a ton pooir, puis met l’emplaustre et l’estele sus, se tu en a mestier;	And if the bone of the arm is broken, which is called the 'bone of the elbow', then you put your pouch on your left hand and set it level with the other hand at your power, then put the plaster and splint on top, if you need it; 
puis l’estraint, et s’il i a os desevreit, si fent sus, et l’oste, et cure la plaie tant qu’elle soit sanee.	Then restrain it, and if there are displaced bones, do likewise to them, and set the bone, and treat the wound until it is healed. 
de la brisure de l’os de la hainche	of the break of the bone of the hip
Poc avient que li os de la hainche soit brisiez, et s’il avient, si n’avient fuer c’un poc d’amenuisement au chief;	Sometimes it happens that the hip bone is broken, and if it happens, there should be a little lessening at the top.  
et fent dou lonc, et decline au pardedens, et vient au malaide dolor au leu, et pointure, et enfle ceu que brise.	And make it long and sloping to the side, and come to the patient pain at the place, and tingling, and swelling of what breaks. 
Et li restoration si est que tu estendes ta main sus, tant que tu soies sus la briseure;	And the restoration is that you extend your hand above, as long as you are on the fracture;
et saiches quelz est li brisure et li figure de li;	and know what is the fracture and its shape. 
et se li brisure est au chief soulement, si met igal cele brisure, tant qu’ele soit a figure natureil.	And if the fracture is at the top only, set it straight, as long as it is in natural form.
Et se li brisure est dou lonc, ou elle decline au dedens, si fai gesir le malaide sus son ventre, tant que li restauration de cele brisure te soit aparillie.	And if the fracture is long, or it declines inward, so make the patient lie on his belly, as long as the restoration of that fracture be apparent to you.
Et quant tu l’avras mise igal, si met sus l’emplaustre, puis met sus une estele de fust ou de keur, et estraint la briseure, si qu’ele ne se mueve;	And when you have set it straight, put on the plaster, then put on a splint of wood or of bark, and restrain the fracture so that it does not move.  
et emple le leu desoz les costes, tant que li lieure soit igalz.	and place the piece under the ribs, until the bone is level.  
Et comande au malaide k’il dorme sus son costeit sain, ou sus son dos.	And command the patient that he sleep on his healthy side or on his back.
Et se apostemes chaus i vient, si n’i tochier, tant que li apostemes chaus soit apaisiez, et met sus ceu que nos avons devant dit;	And if an abscess comes there, do not touch it, until the abscess is calmed, and put upon it what we have said before. 
et puis revien a la restauration, et l’estraint si com il covient, s’il n’i a nul mavais accident;	and then return to the restoration, and restrain it as is fitting, if there are no bad accidents.   
et c’est li maniere.	and this is the manner.  
de la brisure de l’ajutoire	of the fracture of the shoulder
Li adjutoires est ceu qui est entre lou coute et lou chief de l’espaule, et s’il est brisiez, si le doit on restorer selonc l’une des II manieres:	The shoulder is that which is between the rib and the head of the shoulder, and if it is broken, one must restore it according to one of two ways. 
dont l’une est que tu pren I fust plain de moiene groissor, selonc ceste forme:	one of which is that you take a piece of medium thick wood, according to this form:   
Et lie as II chiés II liens, et les pent en haut, et siece li malaide sus I siege;	And tie the two pieces with two bands, and bend them upward, and set the patient on a stool.  
puis li giete som bras brisiet sus le fust, tant qu’il viegne a l’aissele, et ait em mi une corbeure de fust, puis pent sus aucune pesant chose ou li ministres l’estende aval;	Then the bone of his arm is broken above the armpit, until it comes to the shoulder, and has in the middle a curvature of stick, then leans on no heavy thing or the minister stretches it down. 
puis mette li mires la briseure igal a ses mains ensamble, tant que li briseure retorne si com il covient.	Then put the splints the fracture even to his hands together, until the fracture returns as it should.  
Et li autre maniere si est que on sovine le malaide sus son hatereil, et li lie la main a son col, puis comande a .ij. ministres que li uns teigne ceu qui est sus la briseure a ses mains, et li autres teigne desoz a tout .i. liien, et estende chescuns a sa partie.	And the other way is that one supports the patient on his bed, and ties his hand to his neck, then commands two ministers that one holds what is above the fracture in their hands, and the other holds below at all .i. point, and extends each to its part.
Et se tu vues que li estraction soit plus fors, si estraint I liien desoz la briseure, et sus la briseure, et estende chescuns des ministres a sa part.	And if you see that the extraction is too far, restrain the limb below the fracture and above the fracture, and extend each minister to its side.
Et se li briseure est prochiene au chief de l’espaule, si covient que tu mettes I liien moien desoz l’assele, et I autre vers lou coute, desoz la briseure;	And if the fracture is near the head of the shoulder, then it behooves you to put one linen halfway under the armpit, and the other towards the side, below the fracture.  
et ausi se li briseure est devers lou coute, si i covient mettre I liien legierement, sens labor, tant que li briseure soit igalz sus lou leu, et sus lou coute;	And also if the fracture is towards the side, then it behooves to put the linen lightly, without labor, until the fracture be even on the place, and on the side; 
puis met igal la brisure, si com il covient, et l’estraint, se apostemes chaus n’i vient.	Then put the fracture even, as it should, and restrain it, if abscess comes there.  
Et se apostemes chaus i vient, si ne l’estraindre mie jusc’a VII jors, et met sus lainne moillie en aisil et en oile roset, tant que li apostemes chaus soit apaisiez;	And if an abscess comes there, do not restrain it until the 7th day, and put on a half-linen cloth in  oil of roses, until the abscess is calmed.
puis l’estraint, et li maniere de l’estraindre si est que tu mettes l’emplaustre sus la briseure, puis assemble le bras sus l’ajutoire, et met ta main sus l’espaule ou sus lou sein;	Then restrain it, and the manner of restraining it is that you put the bandage on the break, then assemble the arm onto the auxiliary, and put your hand on the shoulder or on the chest; 
et met le drapeil, et estraint sus l’ajutoire, et sus lou bras, si que li bras soit en leu d’esteles, s’aucune chose ne le te deffent, ou se li os n’est muez.	and put the bandage, and restrain on the auxiliary, and on the arm, so that the arm be in its place of stars, if nothing prevents it, or if the bone is not moved. 
Et se tu doutes que li os ne se mueve, si use d’esteles, et met sus la brisure une estele plus large et plus fort des autres, et ait entre chescune estele I doi d’espaice, et soit chescune estele si grans qu’elle passe la briseure III dois de chescune part;	And if you doubt that the bone moves, then use splints, and put on the break a splint wider and stronger than the others, and have between each splint 1 finger's width of space, and be each splint so large that it passes the break 3 fingers on each side;
puis estrain sus les esteles, ensi com j’ai dit au comencement dou chapistre sus la briseure, plus fort et moins en aloignant.	then restrain above the bones, as I have said at the beginning of the chapter on the bruise, more strongly and less in distancing 
Et se tu vois l’assise des esteles, et l’estrignement, si com nos avons dit, en l’oure que tu restoures le membre brisiet, et tu doutes l’aposteme chaut, si le laisse a liier jusc’a septime jor, si com nos avons dit;	And if you see the position of the bones, and the tightening, as we have said, in the hour that you restore the broken limb, and you doubt the hot abscess, so leave it bound until the seventh day, as we have said; 
puis regarde chescuns III jors lou lien, que prurite ne enfleure n’i viegne au leu, ou li norrissemens ne puist venir au membre por ceu k’il est trop estrois.	then look every three days the bandage, that itching or swelling does not come to the place, or the nourishment cannot come to the limb for because it is too tightly bound 
Si l’adrece, si com nos avons dit.	If the address, as we have said.
Et se nulz telz accidens n’i vient, si ne lou desliier fuer que aprés III jors ou plus, et dorme li malaides sus son dos, et ait ses mains sus son stomac;	And if no such accidents come, so do not unbind it before three days or more, and let the patient sleep on his back, and have his hands on his stomach;
et met desoz l’ajutoire I cussin plain de laine igalment, et regarde chescune houre dou jor ou de la nut, que li figure dou membre brisiet ne se mueve, ou ne soit amollis li liiens;	and put under the shoulder one cushion of plain wool equally, and look each hour of the day or of the night that the shape of the broken limb does not move, or that the bonds are softened.
si l’adrece par la vertu de medicine, et li done la viande que nos avons devant mis, en teil maniere que li viande soit au premier subtilz;	if he addresses it by the virtue of medicine, and gives him the meat that we have placed before, in such a manner that the meat is first finely minced; 
et quant il comance a reprendre, si soit grosse.	and when he begins to recover, let it be coarse.  
Et est costume que li ajutoire et li jambe doient estre repris en XL jors dou tout;	And it is customary that the shoulder and leg should be taken back in 40 days from all; 
et adonques lou doit on desliier et aministrer bain et medicines d’oignemens por le leu adrecier.	and then one must unbind it and administer baths and medications for the place to be treated.  
Et se li estricture est laide et emboee, si demore a desliier L jors ou II mois.	And if the stricture is bad and obstructed, it remains for 1 day or 2 months to loosen.
de la brisure du bras	of the fracture of the arm
Li bras est compos de II os, qui sont apelez li dui «foscile», de coi li uns est petis, et est cil qui enseut le pouchet;	The arm is composed of 2 bones, which are called the "fossil," because one is small and it follows the socket;  
et li autres est grans, et est cil qui est desoz, devers lou petit doi;	and the other is large and it is the one that is below, towards the small one; 
par aventure brise li grans foscile soulement, ou li petis, et par aventure andui ensamble.	Sometimes the large fossil breaks alone, or the small one, and sometimes both together.  
Quant li petis fosciles est brisiez, li restaurations est legiere, et li sanations;	When the small fossil is broken, the restoration is light, and healing;
et quant li grans est brisiez, si est li sanation male, et plus griés que quant il sont brisiez andui ensamble.	And when the bone is broken, its healing is bad, and more painful than when they are broken together.  
Se c’est li petis foscile qui est brisiez soulement, si le covient poc estendre legierement, et mettre igal.	If it is the small bone that is broken alone, then it should be gently extended and made even.
Et se c’est li grans foscile, si le covient estraindre plus fort;	And if it's the big bone, then it should be pulled harder.  
et l’estende sus I cussin, et teigne le pouchet de la main plus haut des autres, et li petis dois plus bas des autres dois, et soit li malaides croisiez sus lui meisme, et I cussin devant lui plus haut, que li malaides ne soffre nule labor;	and extend it over the cushion, and hold the pouch of the hand higher than the others, and the small ones lower than the other hands, and let the patient be crossed on himself, and the cushion in front of him higher, so that the patient does not suffer any labor; 
puis estende li ministres som bras a la partie desoz a sa main, ou a I liien, et uns autres ministres a I autre au desus.	Then extend the minister's arm below to his hand, or on the rope, and one other minister to the other above. 
Et puis le mette li mires igal, selonc sa millor forme.	And then put the mirrors equal, according to its best form.
Et se en la brisure a pieces, si met chescune en son leu, et s’il en i a nule desevree ke poigne lou keur, et tu ne la pues restorer en son leu, si fent sus et l’oste, si com nos avons dit devant.	And if in the fracture there are pieces, put each one in its place, and if there is any detached that pricks the heart, and you cannot restore it to its place, then do as and the bone, as we have said before.
Et se avec la briseure a plaie, je en ai parleit au chapistre singuler;	And if with the breaking there is a wound, I have spoken of it in the singular chapter;
si pren la cure.	then take the care. 
Et se en l’encomencement dou restorement sorvient apostemes chaus, si glue I drapeil de cerote fait d’oile roset et de cire blainche, que ne soit mie ne trop durs ne trop molz;	And if at the beginning of restoration abscesses appear, then glue the veil of cerate made of rose oil and white wax, so that it is neither too hard nor too soft;
et lie I drapeil par sus subtilment, tant que li apostemes chaus soit apaisiez.	and lay him covered gently on top, until the abscess is calmed. 
Et puis oste lou cerote, et i met l’emplaustre de la poudre dou molin avec abun d’uef, pues met les esteles, et soit li estele de la briseure adés plus fors, et un poc plus large que les autres;	And then remove the cautery, and put on the plaster of ground powder with abundance of egg white, then put on the stitches, and let the stitch of the scalpel be more outward, and a little wider than the others. 
et saiches que il doit avoir VI esteles ou bras em plusors dispositions:	and know that it must have six stitches or arms in more positions:
soit que li briseure soit en l’un des os, soit en II;	whether the cut is in one of the bones, or two.
et estraint plus sus la briseure que autre part, et toz jors moins en aloignant, si com j’ai dit au comencement dou chapistre;	and pull it more upwards above the cut than elsewhere, and all days less in moving away, as I said at the beginning of the chapter. 
et soient li drapelz que sont sus la briseure molz et moistes, et ne soient mie dur ne aspres;	and let the bandages that are on the cut be soft and moist, and not hard nor rough;
et soit li filz, dont il est estrains, de lin, ne trop gros ne trop menus, si com nos avons dit.	and let the thread, with which it is stitched, be of linen, neither too thick nor too thin, as we have said.
Et rewarde lou membre et lou liien aprés aucuns jors.	And reward the limb and the ligament after some days.
Et se aucuns mavais accidens vient au membre, si com prurite ki vient au membre, si covient que tu aroses lou membre d’aigue chaude, tant que cil prurites soit apaisiez;	And if any bad accidents happen to the limb, such as itching that comes to the limb, it is necessary that you raise the member with hot water, until the itching is appeased; 
et laisse le membre ne mie estroit reposer.	and leave the limb not too tight resting.  
Et puis rencomence l’estrignement, et se li liiens est amolis et li os desevrez, et semblant chose, si l’adresce.	And then begin again the tightening, and if the ligaments are loosened and the bones dislocated, and similar things, so the bandage.
Et se pren warde se li norrissemens ne puet venir au membre, por ceu qu’il est trop estrois, si covient que tu l’amollisses .i. poc, et laisse ensi aucuns jors, tant que li norrissemens i corre, et puis l’estraint.	And if it happens that the numbing cannot come to the limb, because it is too tight, it is necessary that you soften it a little, and leave it so for some days, until the numbness passes, and then restrain it.
Et se nules de ces choses que nos avons dit ne vient au malaide, si ne lou desliier jusc’a XX jors.	And if none of these things that we have said come to the patient, do not loosen him until 20 days.
ou enqui entor, puis li pent les mains a son col, et soit ses cols igalz, et se warde de movement et de degitement, et dorme sus son dos;	Or if it's a wound, then he places his hands on his neck, and keeps his necks equal, and guards against movement and agitation, and sleeps on his back; 
et saiches que ceste briseure est restoree en XXX jors ou en XXXV, et par aventure en XX jors, selonc les compositions et les complexions des vertus.	and know that this sprain is restored in XXX days or in XXXV, and perhaps in XX days, according to the compositions and the complexities of the virtues. 
de la brisure de la main	of the fracture of the hand
Saiches que au dos de la main et as nous des dois avient poc de briseures, et n’i vient mais que ploieure maintes fois.	Know that on the back of the hand and on us there are few fractures, and it comes but rather often a sprain many times.
Et quant li plante de la main est brisie ou ploie, si covient que li malaides siece croisiet, et siet droitement devant lui igalement;	And when the plant of the hand is broken or bent, it is necessary that the patient sit crossed, and be straight in front of him equally;
puis met sa main sus la toie estendue, et estende li ministres les os brisiez, et les mete igalz li mires, tant qu’il soient bien joint;	then put his hand on the board outstretched, and extend the minister the broken bones, and put them equal in sight, until they are well joined; 
et met l’emplastre et les estoupes, se apostemes n’i vient, puis i met une estele selonc la quantiteit dou leu;	and put the plaster and bandages, if an abscess does not come, then put a splint according to the quantity of the place; 
et soit envoloupee en I drapeil de lin.	and be enveloped in a linen sheet.  
Et se li briseure est au pardedens entor lou ventre de la plante, si fai une spere de drapelz, et comande au malaide qu’il l’estrigne a sa plante brisie;	And if the fracture is at the bottom of the foot, near the plant of the foot, make a ball of cloths, and instruct the patient to press it against his broken plant.
et puis l’estrain d’un lonc drapeil, et soit li estele de keur souef ausi grans com li plante de la main, et l’estraint, si com il covient.	and then tighten it with a long cloth, and let the splint of hard wood be as large as the palm of the hand, and tighten it, as is necessary.  
Et se li brisure est au defuer, si covient que tu mettes une estele sus, et une autre desoz en la plante, si que li mains soit overte et droite, puis le lie tot entor la main, et estanche lou liien entre les dois.	And if the fracture is at the forearm, it is necessary that you put a splint on top, and another below in the palm, so that the hand be open and straight, then tie it tightly around the hand, and seal the linen between the two.
Et se li briseure vient a aucun des nous des dois, se c’est li pouchés, si le met igal, si com il covient;	And if the fracture comes to any of the two bones, if it is the bone, set it straight, as necessary.  
et l’estraint avec la plante, et se tu vues si met une estele droite petite por lever la briseure, et ne se mueve;	and tighten it with the plant, and if you see that it is put a small straight splint to raise the fracture, and do not move. 
et se li brisure est as autres dois, si com en l’indice ou l’un des autres, si le met igal, et lou lie avec lou doi sain qui est aprés;	And if the fracture is as the other two, such as in the index or one of the others, set it straight, and bind it with the healthy finger that is after. 
ou tu les lie toz en I tenant, que mues vaut, ou tu met sus une estele, si com ou pouchet;	Or you tie them all in a line, as much as it is worth, or put on a splint, such as our pouch. 
et pren warde en la restauration et en la disposition d’aposteme chaut, et secor ceu qui i vient, si com j’ai dit.	And take care in the restoration and in the arrangement of a hot abscess, and help those who come to it, as I have said. 
de la cuixe brisie	of the broken hip
Li os de la cuixe est maintes fois brisiez, et bien le voit on quant elle torne devant et derrier;	The bones of the hip are many times broken, and one sees it well when it turns forward and backward.
et li restauration si est c’on lie I liien desus la briseure, et I autre desoz.	And the restoration is done by tying one linen above the fracture, and the other below. 
Et li malaides gise sus sa faice, puis estende chescuns ministres son lien a sa part igalment;	And the patient lies on his face, then extend each minister his tie to his side evenly;
et c’est quant li brisure est emmi l’os.	and that is when the fracture is in the bone. 
Et se li brisure est prochiene a la racine de la cuixe, si soit li uns des liiens devers lou poignil, et li autres liiens desoz la briseure.	And if the fracture is near the root of the hip, so one of the ligaments towards the groin, and the other ligaments below the fracture.
Et ausi s’elle est prochiene au genoil, et adonques soit li liens delez lou genoil, et soit li extension aval;	And also if it is near the knee, then let the bandage be below the knee, and let the extension be downwards.  
puis mette li mires l’os igal a ses II mains, tant qu’il soit selonc sa figure natureil, et puis met l’emplaustre, et lou lie, se apostemes chaz n’i vient.	Then put the two hands on the bone equal, until it is according to its natural shape, and then put the splint and the bandage, if pus does not come. 
Et s’il i a aposteme chaut, si le laisse apaisier puis revien a ton ovraige et a ta cure;	And if there is a hot abscess, let it calm then return to your work and your cure;
li lieure est faite en teil maniere.	The bandage is made in this manner. 
Il covient que tu envoloupes sus la briseure I bendeil dur doublé en II ou III, et en demoure li superfluitez, puis torne la jambe tant que li talons veigne a la racine de la naige, et boute I fil lonc entre la cuixe et la jambe, delez lou genoil desoz, et veignent li chief dou fil au desus;	It is necessary that you envelop the wound with two or three layers of hard bandage doubled, and remove the superfluities, then turn the leg so that the heel comes to the root of the thigh, and put the long thread between the hip and the leg, below the knee, and bring the end of the thread upwards; 
puis torne sus la jambe et sus la cuixe le bendeil, puis met sus la briseure esteles, et met une estele sus l’os de la jambe;	Then turn over the leg and on the hip the bandage, then put on the broken bone splints, and place a splint on the leg bone.
puis emple le leu vuit entre la jambe et la cuixe de drapelz souef por mettre igal l’estrignement, puis comence a liier forment III tors ou IIII sus la briseure;	Then fill the space between the leg and hip with soft cloth to make even tightening, then begin to bind in three or four turns around the fracture.  
et quant plus vas en sus de la briseure, et moins l’estraint;	and as you go higher above the fracture, and less restrict it; 
puis enten as II chiés dou fil que tu as bouteit entre la jambe et la cuixe, et en lie III esteles que sont desus, puis revai au desoz au chief dou fil, tant que tu veignes delez le piet;	then tighten the two ends of the thread that you have put between the leg and hip, and bind three splints that are above, then return to below at the head of the thread, as far as you come near the foot;
et l’estraint, si qu’il ne se mueve de son leu, puis le laisse ensi, puis k’il n’i vient ne aposteme ne enfleure n’autre semblant.	and restrain it, so that it does not move from its place, then leave it thus, until there comes neither abscess nor swelling nor any other sign.  
Et s’il i avient, si le deslie, et adresce ceu que i vient, si com nos avons dit maintes fois;	And if it occurs, untie it, and dress those that come, as we have said many times. 
et se il i a pieces de l’os que poigne, si le covient ewer, s’om puet;	and if there are pieces of bone that pierce, it is necessary to remove them, if one can.
et s’on ne puet, si covient fendre le leu, et traire fuer;	and if one cannot, it is necessary to split the place and drain pus.
et le cure si com nos avons dit, tant k’il soit sanez.	And treat it as we have said, until it is healed. 
Et aucune fois est brisie li cuixe ensi c’on i met esteles, si com en l’ajutoire et ou bras;	And at no time is the hip broken in this way when one puts splints on it, as in the shoulder and arm;
toutevoie, en la restauration ensi faite ne cloche mie li malaides.	however, in this restoration made, the patient does not feel any pain.   
Et saiches que li cuixe est restoree en .l. jors, ou poc moins ou poc plus, selonc les diversitez des complexions.	And know that the fracture is healed in one day, or a little less or a little more, according to the varieties of constitutions.
de la ruelle dou genoil	Of the rue of the knee
Saiches que en la ruelle dou genoil avient poc brisure, mais elle ploie maintes fois.	Know that in the area of the knee there are few fractures, but it bends many times.
Et s’elle brise, si n’est mais c’une fendure, ou I pertus, et avient a tout plaie, et sens plaie, et ce sent om bien.	And if it breaks, it is no longer than a fissure, or opening, and it happens to all wounds, and without wounds, and this everyone feels well.
Et li restauration si est c’on mette igal ceu qui est rons a ses dois, tant qu’il soit assemblez mues c’on puet;	And the restoration is so when one puts it equal to those that are rounded to its sides, as long as it can be moved together.  
puis met l’emplaustre, et i met une estele reonde, se tu en as mestier, et l’estraint si com il covient, puis rewarde toutes les dispositions que nos avons dit ens autres briseures, si com aposteme chaut et autre semblant;	Then put the splint on, and put a round piece of wood on top if you need it, and restrain it as appropriate, then follow all the precautions we have said in other fractures, such as hot poultices and similar things; 
si met a chescun accident ceu k’il li covient, tant qu’il soit sanez.	Apply to each injury what is fitting for it, until he is healed.  
de la brisure de la jambe	of the fracture of the leg
Saiches que en la jambe ait II os, de coi li uns est apelez par droit non «mustelz», et li autres est apelez «foscile»;	Know that in the leg there are two bones, so one is called by right "femur," and the other "tibia"; 
et avient tout auteil briseure com il vient au bras, et por ceu est li restauracion si com celle dou bras igalment, et li ovraiges est tout i. Et se li dui os sont brisiet ensamble, si torne li jambe de toutes pars.	and all fractures come about like those in the arm, and for this reason the restoration is similar to that of the arm, and the work is all here. And if both bones are broken together, the leg turns in every direction. 
Et se li os subtilz est brisiez, si torne devant.	And if the small bone is broken, it turns forward.
Et se li gros os est brisiez, si sent on grant dolor, et le voit on bien;	And if the thick bone is broken, one feels great pain, and it can be seen well;  
et torne desoz.	and turns downwards. 
Adonques amenistre extension, et le met igal, et lie les esteles igalement;	Then administer an extension, and place it even, and tie the straps evenly; 
mais toutevoie, il covient se li brisure est laide, et il i a plusors pieces, que li extension soit menor et plus legiere;	But nonetheless, if the fracture is bad, and there are many pieces, that the extension be less severe and lighter;
et l’alige selonc ta vertu.	and the splint according to its virtue. 
Et quant tu as tout acomplit ton ovraige, si pren II faixes de fust chevees que porpreignent la jambe d’une part et d’autre, et soient dou lonc de la jambe des le genoil jusque desoz;	And when you have completed your work, take two strips of thick fur that encircle the leg on both sides, and be long from the knee down; 
puis envoloupe en II leus I bendeil desus et desoz, et le lie em mileu ausi, et a ceste lieure ne pora li jambe decliner a destre ne a senestre, et ensi est bien;	then wrap them around the legs with two bandages above and below, and tie it in the middle as well, and at this junction the leg will not be able to decline to the right or left, and thus it is good;
et aucun i aministrent I bers dou lonc de la jambe, et s’est de fust, et i met on la jambe por warder de movement, et proprement fait on ceu en la brisure ou il a plaie;	and none administer  bars along the length of the leg, and if it is of fur, and it is placed on the leg to prevent movement, and properly made are these in the fracture where there is a wound;
et remue chescun jor la jambe, por veoir s’il i a aposteme chaut n’autre accident;	and move each day the leg, to see if there is a hot abscess or another accident. 
si le cure tant qu’il soit sanez.	if it cures as long as it is sound.  
de la brisure des os dou piet	of the fracture of the bones of the foot
A la cheville ne vient point de brisure, mais as os dou piet vient aucune fois brisure et as dois poc, et n’i avient fuer que quassure em plusor dispositions.	At the ankle there comes no fracture, but the bones of the foot come at any time fracture and to two places, and there is not there been other than that which causes in many positions.
Et s’il avient as os dou piet brisure, et tu vois ces os sormonter l’un l’autre, si mette si malaides som piet sus la terre, ausi com s’il voloit aler, et puis met maintenant ton piet sus lou sien, lai ou li os sont levez, puis le presse tant k’il reveignent en lor leus;	And if there happens as bone of the foot broken, and you see these bones overlap each other, put the patient on his foot on the earth, as if he wanted to walk, and then put now your foot on his, where the bones are raised, then press it so much that they return into their places; 
puis met l’emplaustre et estoupes sus, et met desoz lou ventre dou piet une petite tauble a II chiés plains, puis l’estraint au piet avenanment, puis que tu as envoloupez drapelz entor, et autres choses dont tu as mestier.	then put the splint and bandages on top, and put under the belly of the foot a small table at II shoulder high, then restrain it to the foot according, then that you have wrapped cloths around, and other things which you need.   
Et quant .iij. jors ou .iiij. seront passez, si deslie lou liien, car tu troveras les os igalz, soient brisiez, soient desaluez.	And when three days or four will have passed, undo the bandage, because you will find the bones equal, whether broken or dislocated.
Et s’il i a aucuns des dois brisiez, si les restoure, si com nos avons dit as dois de la main;	And if there are any of the wrists broken, restore them, as we have said to the wrists of the hand; 
puis met au doi brisiet une estele selonc la longesce dou doi, et soit un poc plus large, puis met desoz le piet celle tauble que j’ai dit, et l’estrain avenanment;	then put on the broken arm a splint according to the length of the arm, and be one point more wide, then put under the foot that table that I said, and strain evenly. 
et s’il en i a II ou III, ou plus, brisiez, si met sus chescun doi une estele selonc sa quantiteit, envoloupee en I drapeil de lin, et estraint la tauble desoz lou piet;	and if there are two or three, or more, broken, if put on each arm a splint according to its quantity, wrapped in one linen cloth, and strain the table under the foot; 
et soit estans sus lou chief de la tauble defuer lou ventre dou piet, si qu’il le teigne bien.	and be standing on the top of the table farther from the belly of the foot so that it holds well.  
Et covient que tu n’oblier mie les autres choses que j’ai dit as autres briseures, des que nos avons dit;	And it is necessary that you not forget the other things that I have said to other fractures, as we have said;
et secor chescun accident si com il covient.	and care for each accident as it is necessary. 
de la brisure de l’os dou poignil	of the fracture of the bone of the hand
Quant li os de la nature la femme est brisiez, si la fai seoir enlargie, puis l’encline a la partie dou dos, et soit tenue par derrier;	When the bone of nature in a woman is broken, make her sit with her thighs spread apart, then incline her to the part of the back, and hold her from behind.  
puis emplisse li baile la nature de la malaide de couton, et en i mette ausi gros com I sto;	then fill the cavity of the woman’s body with cotton, and put as much in as the space allows; 
puis deboute la femme, et lieve lou dos poc et poc, et adonques saut li coton, tant qu’il vient a l’entree de la nature, et revient li os avec lou sto;	then turn the woman, and lift her back up and down, so that the cotton is pushed until it comes to the entrance of the vagina, and returns the bone with the stomach. 
et quant elle vuet pissier, si oste lou coton, et quant elle a pissiet, se li remette, et ensi faice VII jors ou entor:	And when she wants to urinate, remove the cotton, and when she has finished urinating, put it back in, and do this for seven days or until.
si sera restoree li brisure, et se tu vues, pren une vessie de berbis, et lie au pertus une cainne, et boute toute la vessie en la nature;	then the fracture will be restored, and if you see it, take a sheep’s bladder, and tie a chain to the opening, and put the whole bladder into the vagina. 
puis soffle en la cainne forment, tant que li vessie soit enflee dedens:	Then blow into the groin region, until the bladder is swollen inside. 
la nature si revenra li brisure;	Nature will return the fracture itself; 
puis soit emplie de coton, et le laisse ensi aucuns jors, tant qu’il soit sanez.	then be filled with cotton, and leave it so for some days, until it is healed.  
Et quant li os dou poignil de l’ome est brisiez, ou de la femme, si le restoure ensi com nos avons dit en l’os de la hainche;	And when the bone of the finger of a man or woman is broken, restore it as we have said for the bone of the hip; 
et ne sont mie occultees ces briseures prochienes a celui qui i met son estude et son us, et entent mon livre.	and these fractures close to this are not hidden from those who put their study and use into it, and read my book. 
Car li brisure li signifie em plusors dispositions la droite voie de la restauration:	For the fracture signifies in more postures the right way of restoration:
enten le donques.	Therefore, understand this. 
En la verge, quant elle est brisie, pren une gorge d’oie et i boute la verge;	In the shaft, when it is broken, take a goose's gizzard and put it into the shaft;  
puis envoloupe drapelz entor, et le laisse III jors ou enqui entor, et il sera sanez hastanment.	then wrap it in bandages, and leave it for three days or until it is fully healed, and it will heal completely. 
de brisure avec plaie	of fracture with wound
Il covient a celui qui a brisure avec plaie, meismement s’elle est grans, si com li os de la cuixe ou de l’ajutoire ou semblant, qu’il soit sainiez maintenant, si que les sainies que nos avons dit le tesmoignent.	It behooves him who has a fracture with wound, even if it is great, like the bone of the hip or shoulder or similar, that he be healed now, so that the healings that we have said testify to it.
Et se li plaie saine, si la restainche de vitriole, se tu n’as autre chose, puis rencomence a restorer la briseure en cele meisme houre, ou celui jor, se apostemes chaus n’i vient.	And if the wound heals, then let the restraint of vitriol remain, if you have nothing else, and then begin to restore the fracture in that same hour, or on that same day, if an abscess does not come.
Et se apostemes chaus i vient, si laisse la restauration jusc’a nuevime jor, tant que li apostemes soit apaisiez, et n’i touchier ne au tier jor ne au quart, car tu i feroies venir malvais accident.	And if an abscess does come, then leave the restoration until the ninth day, as long as the abscess is calmed, and do not touch it on the third or fourth day, for you would bring about a bad accident.
Et se li os brisiez est aparans sus lou keur descovert, si covient que tu lou mettes a point legierement a tes mains, a extension petite.	And if the broken bone is appearing on the uncovered heart, then it behooves you to put it in place gently with your hands, by small extension.
Et se li extensions ne t’est apareillie por mettre igal a tes mains, si le ramoine a cest estrument qui est de fer, qui a VII dois ou VIII de lonc, et li largesce est selonc la quantiteit de la plaie;	And if the extension is not prepared for you to put it equal with your hands, then use this instrument which is of iron, which has seven or eight inches in length, and the width is according to the quantity of the wound; 
et por ceu est mestier au mire qu’il empreigne III ou IIII, selonc ceu qu’il en ait mestier en chescune cure de briseure;	and for this it is necessary that the one using it grasp three or four, according to what he needs in each cure of a fracture; 
et soit rons et un poc gros, k’il ne ploie mie a la compression sus lou membre a ton ovraige, et soit agus devant, et gros des le mileu en avant, ensi:	and be round and a little thick, that it does not bend at the compression upon the member in your work, and be pointed in front, and thick from the middle forward, thus:
Et est apelez «palainche», por coi il covient que li chiés corbes soit mis sus lou chief de l’os apparent;	And it is called "palainche," for which reason it is necessary that the curved part be placed upon the head of the visible bone;
et le boute a une fois, tant k’il reviegne, et soit igalz l’un encontre l’autre.	and the but at once, so long as it revives, and be equal one against another. 
Et se li brisure est subtilz, et li estrumens ne puet bien prendre l’os, si covient que tu copes lou chief de l’os, tant que li estrumens en ait possance.	And if the fracture is subtle, and the instruments cannot well take hold of the bone, then it is necessary that you cut the head of the bone, until the instruments have purchase.
Et se tu ne pues ramener l’os, si com nos avons dit, si lou cope d’un estrument covenable a ceu, ou incisoire ou soieure, a ton pooir;	And if you cannot bring back the bone, as we have said, then cut it with a suitable instrument, either a chisel or saw, to your power. 
puis reis ceu qui est demorez en l’os d’aspreteit et de menues escorces.	Then remove that which remains in the bone of sharpness and small fragments.  
Et quant li os est ramenez, et li malaides sent grant dolor aprés, saiches qu’il n’est mie en son leu natureil.	And when the bone is returned, and the patient feels great pain afterwards, know that it is not in its natural place.
Si fai tant qu’il soit en son leu, puis moille I drapeil en vin stiptique noir, et proprement se c’est en esteit;	Do this until it is in its place, then soak the bandage in dark red wine and properly that's where it lies.  
et ne mettre mie sus la plaie cerote ne autre chose ou il ait oile, qu’il n’i faice venir porriture et corruption;	And do not put on the wound anything else or oil except what is fitting for the healing, so that it may not bring about decay and corruption.  
puis aministre esteles quant tu as restoreit l’os, et laisse la plaie descoverte, et cope la coverture tout entor, selonc la quantiteit de la plaie, et te done bien en garde que li plaie ne soit estrainte avec la brisure;	Then administer splints when you have restored the bone, and leave the wound uncovered, and cut away the covering all around, according to the amount of the wound, and take good care that the wound be not strained with the fracture.   
et maintes fois ont ce fait li fol mire, et ont fait venir sus le malaide ou mort ou corrodent aucune fois;	And many times this has been done foolishly, and brought upon the patient either death or corruption at any time.  
et soit li estrignemens plus molz et plus souef des autres brisures.	and let the strapping be softer and more slack than other fractures. 
Et se li plaie est male ou grans, et tu doutes que mavais accidens n’i veigne, si com nos avons dit, et tu trueves dolor au leu, si n’i covient mie mettre sus esteles;	And if the wound is bad or large, and you doubt that a bad accident has occurred, as we have said, and you find pain in the place, then it is not necessary to put on splints. 
mais envoloupe entor, en leu d’esteles, drapelz durs, et les lie.	but wrap around it, in place of splints, hard cloths, and tie them.  
Et quant tu vois aprés I jor ou II enjanrer bowe a la plaie, si oste ceu que tu as mis sus a tout vin, et i met oignement sanant plaies, si com oignement tetrafarmaçon et semblans.	And when you see after one day or two that the wound is bowing, remove what you have put on top and put healing ointment for wounds, such as ointment tetra-formation and similar things.
Et covient que tu deslies lou membre .ij. fois le jor, lou matin et au vespre, tant qu’il soit soudez et sanez.	And it is necessary that you untie the limb two times a day, in the morning and in the evening, until it is united and healed.
Et covient que li membres soit aparilliez en teil maniere que li bowe corre aval legierement.	And it is necessary that the limb be supported in such a manner that the bone goes down gently.
Et se maint jor trespassent, et il ne puet souder mais rent adés bowe, saiches k’il i a petites pieces d’os, por coi il covient que tu quieres la plaie avec tente, et oste toutes ces pieces desevrees que font venir celle dolor.	And if the next day, and it cannot unite anymore but returns back bone, know that there are small pieces of bone, so it is necessary that you cover the wound with a bandage, and remove all these loose pieces which bring that pain.
Et se fistule vient au leu, ou autre maniere de corruption, si covient que tu le cures, selonc ceu qu’il dist en son chapistre ci devant.	And if a fistula comes to the place, or another manner of corruption, it is necessary that you cure it, according to what he says in his chapter before.
Et quant li os est brisiez, et apert sus lou membre, si com li os de la cuixe ou de l’ajutoire, et autres semblans des grans membres, si ne le traire mie, car maintes fois en vient li mors, mais le laisse tant qu’il porrisse;	And when the bone is broken and open on the limb, such as the hip or shoulder bones, and similar large members, do not touch it, because many times death results, but let it be until it can heal. 
par aventure cherra par lui aprés XX jors ou XXX, puis cure la plaie, se tu pues;	Perhaps after twenty or thirty days it will fall out by itself, then you can care for the wound if you are able.
et se tu ne pues, si la laisse.	And if you are unable, leave it alone. 
des brus qui vienent sor la sodure	of the boils that come from the swelling
Nous vienent maintes fois aprés la santeit de la briseure, meismement quant c’est pres de la jointure, et laide chose est a veoir li figure dou membre;	We often come after the health of the fracture, even when it is near the joint, and a bad thing is to see the figure of the limb; 
et par aventure ne puet faire li membres ses ovraiges naturelz.	and by chance cannot make the limb its natural works.  
Pren warde donques se li nous est fres:	Take care therefore if it belongs to us: 
si li aministre medicines stiptiques, si com aloes, encens, et mirre, et sarcocolle, acaice, et semblans autres, ensi que tu preignes aucune de ces choses, ou toutes ensamble, et les confit avec vin stiptique ou avec abun d’uef ou avec aisil;	If he administers astringent medicines such as aloes, incense, and myrrh, and sarcocolla, acaice, and similar others, in the way that you take any of these things, or all together, and confit them with astringent wine or with abun of egg or with aisil; 
et les met sus le nout en estoupes, et l’estraint bien, et ne la desliier en mains jors;	and put them on the wound in bandages, and restrain it well, and do not untie it for days;
et puis la desloie, et rencomence une autre, tant que li nodations soit ostee;	and then untie it, and recommence another one, as long as the swelling is removed; 
ou tu estrain sus une piece de plonc bien faite;	or you restrain on a piece of plank well made; 
car li proprietez dou plonc si est qu’il oste toutes les enfleures desus les membres;	for the properties of the plank are that it takes away all the swellings from the limbs;  
et se li nodation est ja convertie en durteit ausi com piere, et il est besoing de l’oster, si la cope desus, et fent la superfluiteit apparent;	and if the knot has already become hardened like a stone, and it is necessary to remove it, then the skin above, and make the superfluity appear;
ou tu la reis a aucun raseur, tant qu’ele soit ostee, et la cure tant qu’ele soit sanee.	or you put it back on no razor, until it is removed, and the cure as long as it is healed. 
dou membre qui est foibles aprés la garison	of the limb that is weak after the healing
Quant li brisure de l’os est restoree, et demoure aprés li membres foibles et subtilz, si avient por mout de causes:	When the fracture of the bone is restored, and remains after the limbs weak and thin, it happens for many reasons: 
de coi l’une est por ceu qu’il fut liiez trop estroit, et ne fut mie liiez si com il covenoit;	for one reason is because it was tied too tight, and was not tied as it should;
ou por ceu qu’il i ot trop de liiens, et ne pooit venir li norrissemens au membre;	or for the reason that there were too many ties, and cannot come the nourishment to the limb; 
ou por multitude d’arosement;	or for multitude of arsement; 
ou por trop grans movements, ne mie en son houre;	or for too great movements, not at its hour;  
ou por ceu qu’il a poc de sanc en son cors, si est foibles.	or because he has little blood in his body, so he is weak. 
Et li cure si est que tu faices mengier le malaide, et faire le cors tendre, tant que li sans soit multipliiez en lui;	And the cure is that you feed the patient, and make the body soft, until the blood is multiplied in him; 
et li aministre bain, et li done joie et liesce;	and administer baths to him, and give him joy and leisure;  
puis met poix sus le membre, si que li poix atraie a li grant norrissement, et l’arose sovent d’aigue tede, tant que li norrissement corre au membre;	then put poultices on the limb so that the poultice attracts to it great nourishment, and the swelling often of water is reduced, until the nourishment comes to the limb; 
et reviegne a sa figure natureil.	and returns to its natural figure.  
dou membre tort aprés la santeit	the limb after the healing
Quant li membres est tors aprés la restauration, et li os brisiez apert, et li forme dou membre est laide, toutevoie ne pert mie son ovraige natureil:	When the limb is twisted after restoration, and the broken bones are apart, and the form of the limb is ugly, nevertheless it does not lose its natural function: 
si ne croire mie les folz qui dient c’on doit brisier lou membre tout de noveil, et maint fol mire ont ce fait en nostre terre;	If you do not believe the fools who say that one must break a limb anew, and many fools have done this in our land; 
et cist ovraiges est blamez, et en vient grans malz, et par aventure li mors;	and these works are blamed, and great harm comes from it, and by chance death;  
toutevoie, se li nodations et li torture sont fres, si covient k’il soient arosez d’aigue chaude, ou herbes mollifians soient cuites, si com foilles de vismalve, et racines, et mellilote, et semblans choses;	Nevertheless, if the dislocations and tortures are fresh, then it is fitting that they be bathed in hot water, or softening herbs be boiled, such as leaves of willowherb, and roots, and marshmallow, and similar things;  
et li fai I emplaustre mollificatif, si com dyaquilon bien fait, et tu pren le muscillaige de vismalve, et la confit avec graisse de geline ou oile de sisament, et fai emplaustre sus;	and the boil with a softening plaster, such as diacylum well made, and take the mucilage of willowherb, and confit it with lard or oil of sesame, and make a plaster on top.   
ou tu pren figues graisses, et les broie avec fien de colon, et semblans medicines que amenuisent le soudement.	Or you take fat figs, and grind them with flaxseed, and similar medicines that reduce swelling.  
Et aucune fois est ostee li nodacion por froter continuelment et longement a mains moistes.	And sometimes dislocation is removed by rubbing continuously and lengthwise with wet hands.
Et soit amenistrez movement au membre chescune houre.	And make the member move each hour.
Et se li tortuositez est enveillie et endurcie, ausi com piere, et besoins est de l’oster au fer, si la covient coper jusc’a l’os, a l’incisoire subtil legierement;	And if the crookedness is ingrained and hardened, as with stone, then it is necessary to remove it with iron, so it should be cut up to the bone, with a sharp and light scalpel. 
et mettre cusenson et estude en la cure.	and put care and study into the treatment.  
Ci encomence li livres des dislocations	Here begins the book of dislocations
Dislocations est issue d’aucune jointe de son leu, por coi il ne se puet muevre, et est li membres mal figurez, et sent li malaides grant dolor et grant lesion.	Dislocation is an exit from any joint from its place, for which it cannot move, and the limb is badly shaped, and the patient feels great pain and great injury.
Quant dislocation vient a aucun, si le covient maintenant ramener sens targier.	When dislocation comes to anyone, it should now be brought back without splinting.
Car s’on tarde, si enfle li leus, et par aventure si le remet on a poines au leu;	For if one delays, then the limbs swell, and by chance if it is set back in place with pain; 
por ceu ne covient mie c’on le mueve a l’oure k’il est enflez:	for because of this it is not fitting to move it while it is swollen.
maintes fois fait venir spame et autres dolors;	many times brings forth spasms and other pains; 
toutevoie, quant ce avenra, si fai sainier lou malaide, puis le laisse, tant que li apostemes chas soit apaisiez;	Nevertheless, when this happens,  if it is healed the patient, then leave him, until the abscesses are all appeased; 
puis arose le membre d’aigue chaude et d’oile, puis le ramoinne legierement, et cure chescun membre si com li cure venra en son leu.	then raise the limb with hot water and oil, then set it gently, and cure each member as the wound comes in its place. 
Et j’ai ordenez les chapistres des dislocations des lou chief jusc’a piez.	And I have ordered the chapters of dislocations of the head to the foot.
des mandibules	of the jawbone
Poc avient que les mandibules soient desaluees andous, et li dislocations d’ambedous est selonc II manieres:	It happens sometimes that the jaws are dislocated, and the dislocations of both are according to two manners. 
ou elles sont un poc ostees de lor leus, et mollifies un poc;	or they are a little bit displaced from their places, and softened a little; 
ou elles sont desaluees entierement, et pendent vers lou pis, et cort li salive de la bouche qu’il ne la puet tenir, ne ne puet clore sa bouche, et envoloupe sa langue avec la parole.	or they are dislocated entirely, and hang towards the chin, and cut the saliva from the mouth that he cannot hold it, nor can he close his mouth, and envelops his tongue with the word. 
Quant li dislocations est petite, si revient par li em plusors disposicions.	When the dislocation is small, it returns by the many more dispositions.
Et s’elle est entiere et acomplie, si covient que tu la ramoinne hastanment, et ne targier mie;	And if it is entirely and completely dislocated, then you must reset it gently, and do not delay at all;  
et en tel maniere que li ministres teigne le chief dou malaide, et boute li mires som pochet de l’une de ses mains en la racine de la dislocation de la mandibule dedens la bouche, se li dislocations est de II pars;	and in such a manner that the assistants hold the head of the sick person, and puts his middle finger into the root of the dislocation of the jaw inside the mouth, if the dislocation is of two parts;  
et li autre doi des mains soient defuer, por mettre igal;	and the other two fingers of both hands be outside, to put it equal; 
et comande au malaide qu’il les amollisse, ses mandibules, et les mueve de toutes pars.	and command the patient to soften his jaws, and move them in all directions. 
Et li mires la mete igal, tant qu’elle reveigne en son leu.	And the finger puts it straight, until it returns to its place.
Et se li ramener est griés, meismement se ce sont les II mandibules ensamble, si les arose d’aigue chaude et d’oile, tant que les ramoinnes legierement;	And if bringing them back is painful, even if they are the two jaws together, then apply hot water and oil, until they soften gently; 
ne ne targier mie dou ramener, si com nos avons dit.	do not delay bringing them back, as we have said.  
Et quant elles sont ramenees igalment, et li bouche dou malaide clot bien sens mollifiier, si met sus drapelz moilliez en cerote fait d’oile roset et de cire, puis le lie legierement de molz liiens;	And when they are brought back evenly, and the mouth of the patient is well closed with soft material, it is placed on damp cloths in a cloth made of rose oil and wax, then it is lightly tied with soft bandages; 
et dorme li malaides sus son dos, et ses chiés soit estans entre II cussins, si qu’il ne lou mueve ne a destre ne a senestre, ne ne s’efforce mie de maixier, mais preigne legiere viande, tant que les dolors soient ostees, et soient noees les mandibules;	And the patient sleeps on his back, and his shoulders be between two pillows, so that he does not move them to the right or to the left, nor does he strive to chew, but takes light food, until the pains are removed, and the jaws are numb. 
et puis menjuce ce qu’il vuet legierement, et ne se travaille mie d’ovrir la bouche au mengier et au boivre, tant que li mandibule soit bien noee et sanee.	And then he eats what he wants lightly, and does not strive to open his mouth when eating or drinking, until the jaw is well numbed and healed. 
Et se les .ij. mandibules ne pueent estre remises a point a une houre, et ne sont mie converties a lor leus, si en vient fievres et sode acostumees, et par aventure solution de ventre, et par aventure vomist cole pure.	And if the two jawbones cannot be set back in an hour, and are not brought back to their places, then come fevers and accustomed swellings, and perhaps a solution of the belly, and perhaps vomiting of cold phlegm.
Et quant tu verras ceu, adonc saiches que c’est perdicions;	And when you see this, then know that it is a healing;
et maintes fois muert cil cui il avient, en VIIII jors.	and many times die those who have it, in nine days. 
de la forcelle	Of the fork
Li forcele ne puet desaluer dou costeit dedens la continuation de li et dou pis, et est desaluee aucune fois au defuer, et bien le sent on.	The forceps cannot dislocate from within the side of the rib and from the hip, and it is dislocated no time at the outside, and well one feels it.
Et li restauration si est que li malaides gise sovin sor son dos, et estende ses bras;	And the restoration is that the patient lies supine on his back, and extends his arms; 
et puis presse le leu forment a ta palme, et elle revenra;	and then press the place firmly with your palm, and it will return; 
puis met sus l’emplaustre et lou bendeil, et l’estraint;	then put on the splint and bandage, and restrict it; 
et li chiez qui est devers lou coute ne puet desaluer;	and the joint which is towards the outside cannot dislocate;  
se poc non, et se il desalue aucune fois, si le ramoinne a son leu, si com nos avons dit;	if it does, and if it dislocates at any time, reset it to its place, as we have said; 
puis met sus l’emplaustre et le bendeil, et l’estraint, et coumande au malaide qu’il se repose tant qu’il soit sanez;	then put on the splint and bandage, and restrict it, and command the patient to rest until he is healed;
et ensi meisme est ramenez li chiés de l’espale, quant il est desevrez de son leu.	and in the same way bring back the joint of the shoulder when it is dislocated from its place. 
de la dislocation de l’espaule	of the dislocation of the shoulder
Saiches que li espaule n’est desaluee fuer que selonc III manieres:	Know that the shoulder is dislocated in only three ways:
de coi l’une est qu’ele desalue a la partie de l’assele au desoz;	one of which is that it dislocates to the side of the axilla towards the groin; 
et li seconde est a la partie dou pis;	and the second is to the part of the hip; 
et par aventure desalue a la partie desus, et ceu avient poc;	and by chance dislocated to the upper part, and this happens rarely;  
et ne desalue mie derrier por l’espaule, et ne desalue mie dedens por les ners;	and does not dislocate behind for the shoulder, and does not dislocate inside for the nerves; 
et plusors fois desalue desoz vers l’assele, meismement a ces qui ont poc de char, car a ces saut ele fuer hastanment;	and many times dislocated downwards towards the seat, even to those who have little flesh, because in these it is easier to be displaced ; 
a ces qui ont assez char, saut ele a poines, et rentre a poines.	to those who have enough flesh, it is with difficulty, and returns with difficulty.  
Et par aventure avient a aucuns homes percussion ou casseure, et enfle li espaule d’un aposteme chaut, et cuide qu’elle est desaluee par ceu.	And perhaps it happens to some men percussion or fracture, and swells the shoulder with a hot abscess, and they think that it is dislocated because of this.
Il covient donques que tu l’esprueves, tant que tu en soies certains;	Therefore it behooves you to prove it, as long as you are certain of it; 
et adonques encomence la cure.	and then begin the cure.   
Et est conue li dislocations quant il est aval vers l’assele, et met difference entre l’espaule malade et la saine, et tu troveras entre lor diversiteit manifeste;	And it is known the dislocation when it is down towards the seat, and put a difference between the diseased shoulder and the healthy one, and you will find between them a manifest diversity; 
et troveras au chief de l’espaule une fosse, et desoz l’assele au tochier le chief de l’espaule, ausi com se ce soit uns oes;	and you will find at the head of the shoulder a hollow, and under the seat to touch the head of the shoulder, as if it were one; 
et ne puet li malaides ramener sa main a son neis, ne movoir de nulz movemens;	and the patient cannot bring his hand back to his side, nor move in any way; 
et ausi, s’elle est desaluee en haut, si n’est mie occultee, car tu le trueves manifestement au tochier;	and also, if it is dislocated upwards, it is not hidden, because you find it manifestly by touching;
et ceste maniere de dislocation n’est mie fors a ramener, quant elle est novele, ou se li enfes est malaides.	and this kind of dislocation is not difficult to bring back, when it is new, or if the child is ill; 
Et li maniere est que li ministres lieve la main dou malaide en haut, puis met tes peuchas desoz l’assele, et lieve la jointure a force en haut au leu;	And the way is that the ministers lift the hand of the sick person upwards, then put their hands under the seat, and lift the joint with force upwards to its place;
et li ministres lieve la main, et l’estende en haut, pues le mette desoz;	and the ministers lift the hand, and extend it upwards, then put it downwards;  
si venra hastanment.	then they come (or it comes) gradually. 
Et s’elle ne vient si com nos avons dit em mains jors aprés, si covient ke li malaides soit baigniez en aigue chaude;	And if it does not come as we have said within a few days, then it is necessary that the patient be bathed in hot water. 
et li amenistre arosement mollifiant et assouajant, si com decoction de altee et de fenugrec et de mellilote en aigue, et soit amenistree;	and administer a soothing and softening ointment such as a decoction of aloe and fenugreek and melilot in water, and let it be administered. 
puis soit sovinez li malaides sus son dos, et mette on desoz l’assele un sto de lainne igal, ne trop mol ne trop dur, puis mette li mires son talon sus le sto, et lieve le chief de l’espaule vertuousement, et traie la main dou malaide;	then have the patient lie on their back, and place under the seat a piece of wool even, neither too soft nor too hard, then put the heel of the foot on the cloth, and lift the head of the shoulder carefully, and pull on the hand of the sick person. 
et uns autres ministres teigne lou chief dou malaide, si qu’il ne se mueve aval;	and another minister hold the head of the patient so that it does not move down;  
celle espaule revient tout maintenant, et se tu vues si le ramoinne selonc ceste maniere:	That shoulder now returns all by itself, and if you see this happening follow this way. 
et est que tu faices estre present I home qui soit plus grans que li malaides;	and that you have a strong man present who is stronger than the patient;
et soit drois devers lou costeit, et boute s’espaule desoz l’assele dou malaide, et lieve l’assele en haut, si que li malaides pende en l’ar;	and be right towards the rib, and push the shoulder under the armpit of the patient, and raise the armpit up, so that the patient hangs on the arm. 
et uns autres ministres traie la main dou malaide aval devers lou ventre.	and some other ministers pull the hand of the patient down towards the belly.  
Et se li malaides est trop legiers, si pent avec lui aucune chose pesant, et li dislocation revient maintenant.	And if the patient is too light, he can lift anything heavy with him, and the dislocation returns now.
Et le ramoinne on ausi en autre maniere:	And reset it also in another way: 
et est c’on fiche I lonc tison en terre, dont li chiés soit ausi reons com I pistal, et ne soit ne trop gros ne trop graile;	and then one puts a long stick in the ground, so that the head of the shoulder is also as straight as a post, and it be neither too big nor too thin;
puis soit mis desoz lou malaide, mais k’il ait drapelz souef sus, et li malaides soit estans dou lonc dou fust;	then it is put under the patient, but that it have drapes above, and the patient be standing on the length of the stick; 
puis soit estendue sa main aval d’autre part forment, et li jointure revenra en son leu hastanment;	then its hand is stretched down on the other side, forming, and the joint returns to its place quickly; 
et s’elle ne vuet revenir por toutes ces choses que nos avons dit, si fai ceste cure:	and if it does not want to return for all these things that we have said, then do this cure:
pren I tison de II bras de grant et IIII dois de large, qui ait le chief reont por mues entrer em parfont desoz l’assele, selonc ceste forme:	Take a splint of the arm's length and four fingers wide, which has the head rounded to enter from below the armpit, according to this form: 
puis lie sus le chief dou fust drapelz souez, que li fust ne blece lou malaide, puis le met desoz l’assele dou malaide;	then tie above the head of the staff drapes down so that the staff does not prick the patient, then place it below the armpit of the patient; 
et estende som bras sus le fust dou lonc, et lie l’ajutoire sus le fust, et lou bras au chief de la main, puis met le bras sus I eschillon d’une eschiele dou large, et soit estendue li mains aval, et soit laissiez li cors pendans d’autre part:	and extend the arm on top of the staff's length, and tie the humerus to the staff, and the arm at the hand's head, then place the arm on the edge of a board broad enough, and let the hands be extended downwards, and let the body hang from the other side:  
li jointure reva ens maintenant.	The joint is now reset. 
Et quant elle est ens, en quel maniere que ce soit, si covient que tu mettes desoz l’assele une spere de laine igal, puis met l’emplaustre aparilliet de poudre dou molin, avec encens et aubun d’uef, sus toute l’espaule et entor, puis l’estrain desoz l’assele avenanment, et torne le liien sus l’emplaustre, et embraice la main a son col, et soit li mains demorans ensi.	And when it is in, in whatever manner that it is, it behoves you to put under the saddle a sphere of wool even, then put the emplasters prepared powder from the mill, with incense and auburn of egg, on all the shoulder and around, then restrain it under the saddle evenly, and turn the linen on the emplasters, and embrace the hand to its neck, and let the hands remain thus.
Et covient qu’il menjuce poc, tant que li membres soit confortez, car il sanera plus tost;	And it is necessary that he keep quiet as much as the limb is strengthened because it will heal faster;
et puis menjuce plus aprés V jors ou VII, et le mueve;	and then be quiet more after five or seven days, and move it;
et s’il est fermeis et il n’est mollifiez, si est sanez.	and if it is hardened and not softened, then it is healed. 
Et se li jointure est fuer de leu por moistor que i est venue, ou por autre cause, si covient que tu i aministres cauteres a III pertus, si com il est mis devant ou chapistre des cauteres.	And if the joint is out of place due to moisture that has come, or for another cause, then you must administer cautery to III places, as it is shown in front of or chapter of cautery.
Et se tu fais tout ceu, et il deslie aprés VII jors, et li jointure ne se tient, et ne puet lever som bras amont, adonc saiches que li nerf au chief de l’espaule sont copeit ou estendut ou amollis;	And if you do all these things, and it dislocates after seven days, and the joint does not hold, and cannot lift his arm up, then know that the nerve at the head of the shoulder is cut or stretched or softened. 
et saiches que li jointure n’iert jamais fichie en son leu.	and know that the joint is never fixed in its place.  
Li dislocation qui est devers lou pis, et les mameles, ou derrier, si est faite par impulsion, et estendement de mains, et i aministre on autre lieure;	The dislocation that is toward the buttock, and the breast, or behind, is done by impulse, and stretching of the hands, and it administers in another place. 
et cure tant qu’il soit sanez.	and treat until it is healed.
Et se aprés la sanation vient grietez au membre, et tardemens em movement, si use li malaides bain maintes fois, tant que celle grietez soit alegie, et reviegne a sa premiere nature.	And if after the healing comes pain to the limb, and slowness of movement, then use the patient baths many times, until that pain is alleviated, and returns to its first nature.
de la dislocation dou coute	of the dislocation of the shoulder
Saiches que li jointure dou coute est desaluee a poinnes, et a poinnes revient;	Know that the joint of the elbow is dislocated with blows, and returns with blows.
et s’est desaluee de toutes pars, et meismement devant et derrier, et li dislocations n’est mie reponue, car on la voit bien et sent bien;	and if it is dislocated from all sides, and even in front and behind, and the dislocation is not put back, because one sees it well and feels it well.
et desalue selonc chescune figure.	and dislocates according to each form. 
Et quant tu joins le coute malaide avec lou sain, si le pues veoir apertement.	And when you join the diseased knife with the healthy one, if you can see it clearly.
Car li jointure est chevee, et ne puet ploier lou bras, ne touchier son espaule a tout.	For the joint is dislocated, and cannot bend the arm, nor touch his shoulder at all.
Et covient que tu le ramoinnes ainsois que apostemes chaus i viegne, car se apostemes chaus i venoit, si seroit grief li ramener;	And it is necessary that you reset it thus as abscesses come, because if abscesses came, then it would be grievous to reset it. 
et par aventure ne puet estre ramenez dou tout en tout, meismement quant ele est au derrier;	and by adventure cannot be brought back entirely at all, even when it is in the rear;  
si vaut pis que les autres dislocations, et est de plus grant dolor, et par aventure i vient li mors.	it is worse than other dislocations, and causes greater pain, and by adventure death comes. 
Et li restauration si est, quant elle est telz c’on la puet ramener, que tu li estendes sa main a tes II mains;	And the restoration is, when it is such that one can bring it back, that you extend your hand to its two hands.
et ses bras soit espandus, et les mains dou mire selonc le coute entor, desor et desoz, et boute la jointure a ses peuchas ensamble, ou a la racine de sa palme, tant qu’ele reviegne a son leu.	and his arms be spread, and the hands of him according to the blade around, above and below, and puts the joint to its shoulders together, or at the root of its palm, until it returns to its place. 
Et se li dislocations est au devant, si revient quant il double sa main a sa main, et fier de la racine de la palme lou coute qui est desaluez.	And if the dislocation is in front, it returns when it doubles its hand to its hand, and fire of the root of the palm the blade which is dislocated.
Et s’il ne vuet revenir au leu, si aministre fort extension;	And if it does not want to return to its place, administer strong extension;  
et est que dui ministre estendent le bras, et le teignent dui ministre, si qu’il ne se mueve a l’estension;	and it is that the two ministers extend the arm, and hold it by the ministers so that it does not move in extension; 
puis torne le bras de chescune part, puis que tu as envoloupeit un drapeil double lonc et large;	then turn the arm on each side, then that you have enveloped a double long and wide cloth; 
et quant li mires a jointe la jointure a sa main, si l’oigne d’aucun oile por amolir la jointure, puis boute la jointure forment, tant qu’ele reviegne;	and when the mire has joined the joint to his hand, if the oil of any oil to soften the joint, then push the joint together, as long as it returns;
et quant elle est au leu, si met sus emplaustre sec avec aubun d’uef, et l’estrain forment, et pent le bras au col dou malaide, et le laisse aucuns jors, puis le deslie.	and when it is in its place, put upon plaster dry with auburn of one egg, and strain together, and put the arm at the neck of the sick person, and leave it for some days, then untie.
Et se li jointure est ferme en son leu, si deslie lou liien, et le laisse;	And if the joint is firm in its place, untie the bandage, and let him;
et se tu vois que li jointure n’estrigne bien, si rencomence l’emplaustre et lou lien, et le laisse ensi aucuns jors, tant qu’il soit fermement mis;	and if you see that the joint is not well strung, then recommence the plaster and the bandage, and let him so for some days, as long as it is firmly put.
puis le deslie.	Then untie. 
Et se il sent grieteit aprés le ramenement de la jointe, et elle se muet, si le baigne et frote bellement, et presse tant qu’il soit assouagiez;	And if he feels pain after resetting the joint, and it moves, bathe and rub him well, and press until he is soothed. 
ou tu met sus la jointure une naige de mouton grasse, puis la laisse I jor et une nuit, puis l’oste, et lou fai entrer ou bain;	or you put on the joint a fleece of fat wool, then leave it for one day and night, then remove it, and let him enter into the bath. 
et quant il sue, se li frote la jointure tempreement, puis remet la naige sus, et puis entre ou bain;	and when he sweats, rub the joint moderately, then put back the fleece on top, and then enter into the bath. 
et ensi fai II fois ou III, tant qu’il soit sanez;	and thus do it two or three times, until he is healed.
et se tu vues, si met sus fien de vaiche moiste chaufeit avec burre, et l’estrain sus;	and if you see fit, put on a warm bundle of moist fleece with butter, and fasten it up. 
si revenra a sa disposition.	then it will return to its place.   
li dislocation de la main	The dislocation of the hand
Li jointure de la main desalue, et li revenue est legiere, plus que les autres jointures.	The joint of the hand dislocates, and its return is light, more than the other joints. 
Toutevoie, il la covient ramener au leu hastanment, en l’oure meisme qu’ele est desaluee, ainsois que li leus soit enflez, ou qu’il i viegne aposteme chaut.	However, it is necessary to bring it back to its place immediately, in the same hour that it is dislocated, so that the limb becomes swollen or that an abscess comes hot. 
Et li ramenemens si est que tu mettes la main malaide sus une tauble, et estende li ministres la main, et li mires la mette igal, ensi que il mette sa paume sus l’aparance de la jointure, et la boute tant qu’elle reviegne.	And the bringing back is that you put the sick hand on a table, and extend the minister's hand, and he places it equal, so that he puts his palm on the appearance of the joint, and pushes it until it returns. 
Toutevoie, il covient que vos regardez s’il est bien a leu;	However, it is necessary that you look to see if it is well in its place;  
adonc mette li malaides lou dos de sa main sus une tauble a l’estension et au ramenement.	then put the sick person's back of his hand on a table at extension and return. 
Et se li dislocations est au dos de la main, si mette li malaides son dos de sa main sus la tauble, et li mires mette sa main sus cele apparance de la jointure.	And if the dislocation is in the back of the hand, then the patient puts the back of their hand on the table, and the healer places their hand above the appearance of the joint.
S’elle revient maintenant, c’est bien.	If it returns now, it is well.  
Se ce non, si l’estrain d’emplaustres apaisans apostemes chaus, et lou laisse ensi sens rencomencier.	If not, apply poultices of soothing plasters, and let him leave so as not to restart. 
Et s’il ne le puet soffrir, et tu ne la pues mettre au leu aprés aucuns jors, si demore li jointure torte;	And if he cannot bear it, and you cannot put it back in its place after several days, the joint remains twisted. 
et ne nuist niant au malaide fuer que tant que li mains est amoillie, et ne puet estraindre aucune chose a tout:	and does not harm the patient further than that while his hand is weakened and cannot grasp anything at all.  
adonc saiches que li nerf sont copez, ou li artere;	Therefore, know that the nerve is severed, or the artery. 
si n’i a autre engien fuer que d’estraindre par cautere delez le cas, et par aventure n’i vaut autre chose.	If there is no other remedy except to constrict with a cautery according to the case, and perhaps it is worth nothing else.  
Et quant li mains est au leu, si met sus l’emplaustre que nos avons dit, puis l’estrain et le laisse .v. jors, puis le deslie et laisse ensi.	And when the hand is in place, put on the splint that we have said, then restrain it and leave it for 5 days, then untie it and leave it so.
Et s’il ne la puet bien movoir, et il i a aucune grieteit, si la moille d’aigue chaude, et le frote tant qu’il soit sanez.	And if he cannot move it well, and there is no wound, then moisten it with hot water, and rub it until it is sound.
de la dislocation des dois de la main	of the dislocation of the fingers of the hand
Aucune fois sont desaluez li doi de la main a chescune part, aucune fois au dos de la palme ou au ventre;	At no time are the bones of the hand dislocated on each side, at no time on the back of the palm or on the belly; 
adonques estent le doi, et boute la dislocation a tes pouchés tant qu’il reviegne, puis sostien lou chief dou doi, et le pent vers la partie ou il est desjoins;	Therefore, they are the bones, and push the dislocation into your pouches until it returns, then support the head of the bone, and lean it towards the part where it is dislocated;
et le laisse II jors, et puis le met igal celui jor;	and leave it for two days, and then put it even on that day. 
et de nut le lie, si com nos avons dit, et lou deslie de jor, et lou fai movoir, et le relie la nut;	and of the knot we have said, and untie it each day, and let it move, and tie the knot again. 
et fai ce sovent, tant qu’il soit estroit, et tout ausi fai, se il est desaluez au ventre de la main, et fai si com tu as fait ci devant, tant qu’il soit sanez;	And do this often, until it is tight, and just as well if it is dislocated in the palm of the hand, and do as you have done before, until it is healed. 
et tout ausi fai, quant il est desaluez d’autre part.	And just as well if it is dislocated from elsewhere.  
dou desaluement de l’eschinee dou dos	of the dislocation of the spine of the back
Quant l’eschinee dou dos ou dou col est desaluee, ou il en i a plusors desaluees, si n’i a point de cure, car li mors haste le malaide.	When the spine of the back or the neck is dislocated, or there are several dislocations, if there is no cure, because death hastens the patient.
Et li signes si est que li egestions saut fuer sens volunteit, ne ne la puet tenir, et maintes fois sont mollifiez aucun membre, ou les II cuixes ou li dui bras ou I.	And the signs are that the joints jump out without volition, and cannot be held in place, and many times are softened any limb, or the two hips or the two arms or one.  
Et maintes fois se muet li eschinee a IIII pars;	And many times it moves the joint at four parts. 
celle qui se muet au derrier si est apelee «gilbositez»:	The one that moves at the back is called "gilbositez":
li cure si est que tu rewarde se li gilbositez est venue d’enfance:	The cure of this is that you reward if the gilbositez came from childhood. 
si n’i ait point de cure ne de sanation dou tot.	if there is no cure nor healing of all.
