Et celle que vient de cheoir ou de percussions ou de semblans choses, dirent li ancien manieres de cures par grans paroles, ou il n’a mie en toutes grant profit;	And those that come from falling or blows or similar things, said the old ways of cure with great words, in which there is not much profit at all.  
mais je l’ai abregiet selonc mon entention, et ai formez estrumens en diverses manieres.	but I have shortened it according to my intention, and have formed instruments in various ways. 
Je dis que en la gilbositeit que vient au pis devant, nen a engien ne santeit;	I say that in the swelling that comes to the breast before, there is nothing nor healing;
et ausi cele que vient droitement en II costez, et ne puet on curer fuers que celi proprement qui vient au dos, si com je dis;	and also that which comes directly in the two sides, and one cannot cure except for that properly which comes to the back, as I say;
et est que li malaides soit estendus sus sa faice en I leu igal, et ait de l’estrain desoz lui, qu’il ne se blece;	and it is that the patient be stretched on his face in a level place, and have a strain below him so that he does not bleed.
puis fiche I tison au chief en terre forment, et I autre as piez, et lie un liien pardesoz les asseles dou malaide, et I autre as hainches, et as genous, et as chevilles;	then put the tinder in the head into the earth forming, and the other at the feet, and tie a linen below the hips of the patient, and the other at the waist, knees, and ankles.
et dui ministre saichent les liiens, li uns au chief et li autres as piez, parmi les II tisons;	and the minister knows the links, one at the head and the others at the feet, among the two bones. 
et soient bien fermez, li tison si com nos avons dit, et li mires mette ses paumes sus l’espinee forment, tant qu’ele reviegne.	and they should be well closed, the bones as we have said, and the mire puts his palms on the spine forming, until it returns.  
Et s’elle ne revient par ceste cure, si pren une tauble de III bras de lonc, et chevé desoz la paroit, et li malaides soit en costé, et boute le chief de la tauble desoz la paroit, puis met le mileu de la tauble sus l’espinee;	And if it does not return by this cure, then take a board of III arms long, and place it under the loin, and the patient be on his side, and push the head of the board under the loin, then put the middle of the board on the spine;
et mette li mires ses piez sus l’autre chief de la tauble, et presse bien, tant qu’il reviegne au leu;	and put the mire his feet on the other head of the board, and press well, until it returns to its place; 
et se tu vues, si le fai au tornet qui torne a la main.	and if you see, then do it with the turning crank that turns by hand.  
Et est que tu fiches II tisons au chief dou malaide d’un bras de grant, et devers les piez II autres, et ait entre chescun tison, desoure et desoz, une paume d’espaice de lonc;	And is that you put two bones at the head of the sick person of one arm of great length, and towards the feet two others, and between each bone, above and below, a palm's width of length; 
et ait en chescun tison I pertus, ou li tornet corre, et soient li tison fermement en terre, si qu’il ne se muevent;	and have in each twig a hole pierced, or the turn (of the fire) is corrected, and be the twigs firmly in earth, so that they do not move. 
et entre chescuns II tisons ait I tison tornant, sor coi li liien tornent, et ait en II tornans II petis tisons d’une paume de lonc, por torner le tornet;	and between each two twigs have one turning twig, so that the line turns, and have in each turning two small twigs of an arm's length, to turn the fire. 
et puis lie lou lien qui est parmi les asseles au tornet devers le chief, et l’autre liien devers les piez a l’autre tornet, et chescuns des ministres torne son tornet a tout le liien, et li maistres mette l’espinee igal si com nos avons dit.	and then tie the line which is among the ashes to the fire towards the head, and the other line towards the feet to the other fire, and each of the ministers turns his fire all along the line, and the master puts the spine straight as we have said.
Et quant elle est igalz, si met sus emplaustre desiccatif avec abun d’uef, et puis les estoupes, et puis l’estele d’une tablete de III dois de lonc, que porpreigne lou leu de la gilbositeit et la partie de l’espondile sainne, puis le lie d’un liien, si com nos avons dit, et use li malaides de norrissement subtil, tant qu’il soit sanez;	And when it is straightened, place on top a drying plaster with abundance of egg white, and then the bandages, and then the splint of a tablet of three fingers' length, that covers the location of the gibbosity and the part of the healthy spine, then bind it with a line as we have said, and use the patient to subtle nourishment, until he is healed; 
et s’aucune chose vient en la fin de la santez, si covient aministrer medicines amollissans et asouajans, avec l’estele que nos avons dit ci devant;	And if any thing comes at the end of health, it is fitting to administer softening and soothing medicines, with the method that we have said before; 
et aucune fois i aministre on une piece de plonc, et aucune fois vient li apparance en la derriere spondile dou dos, et cuide on que ce soit dislocations;	And sometimes one administers a piece of lead, and sometimes it comes to the appearance in the lower vertebra of the back, and one thinks that it is dislocation; 
et c’est li os qui apert, por coi on n’i doit mie avoir presumption:	and it is the bone which opens, therefore one should not have presumption there:  
par aventure feroit venir la mort.	for it might bring death by chance. 
des dislocations de la hainche	of dislocations of the hip
Saiches que as jointures de la hainche et as jointures de l’espaule ne vient fuers que dislocacions soulement, ne n’i vient mie si com as autres jointures;	Know that the joints of the hip and the joints of the shoulder come out only with dislocations, and do not come out like the other joints; 
et li jointure de la hainche est desaluee selonc IIII parties:	and the joint of the hip is dislocated according to IV parts:   
dedens et defuer ,et devant et derrier;	inward and outward, and forward and backward;  
et plus dedens c’aillors, et poc desalue devant et derrier.	and more inward then, and less dislocated forward and backward.   
Et li conoissance de sa dislocations dedens si est que quant on joint la jambe malaide avec la sainne, si est plus longe, et apert plus li malaides genous que li sains, et ne puet li malaides doubler son genoil au feu;	And the knowledge of its dislocation within it is that when one joins the diseased leg with the healthy one, it is longer, and opens more the diseased knee than the healthy one, and the diseased one cannot double his knee at the fire. 
et est li leus qui est delez enflez d’aposteme chaut, por ceu que li chiés de la cuixe vient lai.	And it is the limb which is beneath swollen with a hot abscess, because of that the head of the hip comes near.  
Et li signe de celui cui il vient au defuer, si est que cist accident sont contraire a ces devant.	And the sign of him to whom it comes on the outward side, is that this accident is contrary to those before.
Et li signes de celui cui avient au devant, si est qu’il estent bien sa jambe selonc l’acomplissement;	And the signs of him who has it in front, is that his leg is well according to its fulfillment;
toutevoie, ne double mie le genoil sens dolor, et s’on le vuet faire aler, si ne puet avant, et retient son urine, et enfle li angre, et quant il vait, si passe sus le talon.	However, he does not double his knee without pain, and if one wants him to walk, he cannot before, and retains his urine, and inflates the groin, and when he goes, he passes over the heel.  
Et li signes de celui cui il avient derrier, si est qu’il ne puet espandre son genoil, ne doubler, et est celle jambe plus torte de l’autre, et li angre est mollifié, et est li chiés de la cuixe au leu desoz les costes.	And the sign of him to whom it happens behind, is that he cannot spread his knee or double it, and his leg is more twisted than the other, and his anger is softened, and his hip is at the place below the ribs.
Li ramenemens de ceste semblance de dislocation si est que tu rewarde se li dislocations est anciainne, et elle demore selonc sa disposition, si n’i a nule cure;	The returning of this kind of dislocation is that you reward if the dislocation is old, and it remains according to its disposition, there is no cure; 
et n’i covient mie qu’il ait presumption.	and he must have no presumption. 
Et en celi dont li dislocation est fresche, et c’est des IIII manieres de dislocation, si te haste que tu tornes la jointe, et l’esten dedens et defuer, et la muef a destre et senestre;	And in this one whose dislocation is fresh, and it is of these four manners of dislocation, so hasten that you return the joint, and the length inside and outside, and the movement to right and left. 
par aventure si revenra, et n’a mestier d’autre cure.	perhaps it will return, and there is no need for other care.  
Et s’il ne revient en ceste maniere, si covient que tu apareilles I ministre fort, et esten la jambe fort a II mains, ou a I liien que soit liiez sus lou genoil;	And if it does not return in this manner, then it is necessary that you apply the minister strongly, and hold the leg firmly with two hands, or on the ligament that lies above the knee;  
et uns autres ministres estende sa main desus en teil maniere qu’il boute ses mains desoz ses asseles, puis l’estrigne d’un souef liien sus la cuixe;	and another minister extends his hand above in such a manner that he pushes his hands below his shoulders, then tightly grips with a forceful pull on the hip.   
et uns autres tigne lou chief dou liien;	and another holds the head of the ligament
et estendent amont et aval tuit a une fois, tant que li malaide soit levez de terre a une fois, et demoure pendans.	and extend upward and downward all at once, until the patient is lifted from the ground at once, and remains suspended.  
Ceste maniere d’estension si est commune as .iiij. semblances, et se li dislocation est revenue, si com nos avons dit, c’est bien.	This manner of extension is common to four similar things, and if the dislocation has returned, as we have said, it is good.
Se ceu non, si covient mettre cure a sa semblance.	If this is not so, then it is necessary to take care of its appearance. 
Quant li dislocations est au pardedens, si covient que tu sovines le malaide sus son costeit sain, puis met le liien sus la racine de la cuixe, et le leu qui est desoz l’angre, puis estent le liien en haut devers l’angre, et devers la forcele;	When the dislocation is at the hip, then it is necessary that you support the patient on his healthy side, then place the linen on the root of the thigh, and the one that is below the groin, then extend the linen upwards towards the groin, and towards the thigh; 
puis preigne uns autres ministres ses bras, et embraice le gros leu de la cuixe malaide, et l’estende au defuer forment:	then grasp with other ministers his arms, and embrace the large root of the diseased thigh, and extend it outwardly formed:  
si revenra a son leu maintenant;	if it will return to its place now; 
et ceste maniere de dislocation est plus legiere des autres.	and this manner of dislocation is lighter than the others. 
Et se tu ne la pues serrer en ceste maniere que nos avons dit, si covient que tu lies les II piés dou malaide ensamble d’un fort liien souef sus les II talons, et sus les II genous, et soit li jambe malaide estendue II dois plus que li autres;	And if you cannot tighten it in this manner that we have said, then it is necessary that you tie the two feet of the patient together with a strong linen strip above the two heels, and above the two knees, and let the diseased leg be extended two times more than the other;
puis soit pendus sus le chief d’un fust, et soit en sus de terre II bras de lonc;	Then he must be hung by the head of a pole, and on the ground two arms' length. 
puis comande a I ministre qu’il embraice le chief de la cuixe, et soit uns autres ministres pendans avec le malaide, qui embraice forment la cuixe, car li jointure revient maintenant hastanment.	Then command to the minister that he embrace the head of the hip, and let other ministers stand with the patient, who firmly embrace the hip, for the joint returns now quickly. 
Et quant li dislocations est au defuer, si gise li malaides, si com nos avons dit en celui qui a gilbositeit, et estraigne I liien sus la jambe malaide proprement, et sus le peis ausi;	And when the dislocation is at the back, let the patient lie down, as we have said in the one who has gibbosity, and restrain the limb on the leg properly, and on the foot also. 
puis met II tisons, I au chief et I autre as piez, puis fiche I tison entre les cuixes au malaide emmi la forme;	Then put two sticks, one at the head and one at the foot, then place a stick between the hips of the patient to help form it. 
et ait plantei de drapelz moistes entor, qu’il ne blece lou malaide, puis estende chescuns ministre devers lui, et li mires mette igal a sa main la dislocation.	And have bundles of damp cloths around it so that it doesn't burn the patient, then extend each minister towards him, and the minister puts his hand on the dislocation evenly.  
S’elle revient, c’est boin.	If it returns, it is good.
Se ce non, met sus .ie. table, et le presse ensi com nos avons dit en la gilbositeit, et gise li malaides sus le sain costeit.	If this is not so, put him on a table,  and press him as we have said in the glossary, and lay the patient on his healthy side.
Et quant li dislocations est devant, si covient estendre la jambe malaide hastanment, et selonc ce que j’ai dit;	And when the dislocation is in front, it is necessary to extend the injured leg as much as possible, and according to what I have said. 
et mette li mires sa paine d’estre sus l’angre malaide, puis presse a l’autre main, et l’estent aval devers lou genoil.	and puts the hands his pain on the angry sick, then presses with the other hand, and the end down toward the knee. 
Et se li dislocations est au defuer, si ne covient pas estendre le malaide aval, ne lever sus la terre, ains covient qu’il soit ausi com se li hainche estoit desaluee au defuer, si com nos avons dit dou couchement sus les II hainches;	And if the dislocation is at the back, it is not necessary to extend the sick person down, nor raise up on the ground, but rather that he be as though the hip was dislocated at the back, as we have said about lying on the two hips. 
et soit sus sa faice, et li lien estendut si com nos avons dit ci devant, et doit om presser sus la jointure a la table;	and be on his face, and the band extended as we have said before, and one must press upon the joint to the table. 
et sera a point quant li malaides estendra ses jambes, et elles seront igalz;	and it will be at point when the sick person extends his legs, and they will be equal.  
adonques ajoste les cuixes, et met l’emplaustre, et l’estrain d’un bendeil, si que li hainche ne se mueve;	then adjust the thighs, and put the splint, and the band of a bandage, so that the hip does not move.
et se repose III jors ou IIII, puis le deslie, et met l’emplaustre sus;	and rest for three days or four, then undo it, and put the splint on top. 
et se tu vois qu’elles soient igalz, si l’estrain, si com devant, et le laisse III jors;	and if you see that they are even, hold them, as before, and let it be three days; 
puis le deslie, et lou fai aler belement, tant que li membres soit confortez.	then untie it, and allow it to move freely, until the limb is fortified.  
de la dislocation dou genoil	of the dislocation of the knee
Li genous est desaluez selonc III manieres:	The knee is dislocated in three ways: 
c’est a savoir, dedens et defuer, et derrier;	that is to say, inside and outside, and behind;  
et ne desalue point devant.	and does not dislocate in front. 
Et li signes si est que tu comande au malaide qu’il plie sa jambe a sa cuixe, et s’ele ne s’aert a sa cuixe, saiches qu’il est desaluez;	And the sign is that you command the patient to bend his leg at his hip, and if he cannot bring it to his hip, know that it is dislocated; 
et li restauration de toutes si est que tu faices seoir le malaide droit, et estende sa jambe s’il puet, et li met ton dos sus sa faice, et met son piet sus tes piez;	and the restoration of all of them is that you make the patient sit upright, and extend his leg if he can, and place your back on his thigh, and put his foot on your feet;  
puis pren son genoil a tes paumes, et retrai entre tes dois, puis plie les II costez dou genoil forment;	then take his knee in your palms, and draw it between your two hands, then bend the two bones that form the knee. 
et uns autres ministres estende son piet, tant que li genous reviegne a son leu, et li signes est qu’il aert bien sa jambe a sa cuixe legierement;	And some other ministers extend their foot, so that the knee returns to its place, and the sign is that he feels his leg at his hip lightly.   
et met l’emplastre sus, et fai aerdre la jambe a la cuixe, et les loie ensamble fort III jors ou IIII, puis le deslie;	And put the plaster on top, and make him raise his leg to his hip, and let them be bound together for three or four days, then untie it. 
et ne se travaille mie li malaides d’aler, tant que li membres soit confortez.	And do not let the patient work at all to go, until the limbs are strengthened.  
Et se li membres n’est a point, si aministre estendement fort, si com nos avons dit en la cure de la hainche, tant qu’il soit sanez	And if the limb is not in place, administer a strong stretching, as we have said in the cure of the hip, until it is healed.
de la dislocation dou talon	of the dislocation of the heel
Li talons est aucune fois esmeus, et aucune fois desaluez plenement, et dedens et defuer.	The heels are sometimes dislocated and sometimes completely dislocated, inside and outside.
Et li signes si est que li cheville est enflee, et tent avant a la partie ou elle est desaluee:	And the sign is that the ankle is swollen, and tender in front of where it was dislocated: 
li ramenemens si est legier, et le doit on estendre legierement a ses mains quant il est esmeus soulement.	The return should be gentle, and one must extend it gently with his hands when he is just numbed.  
Et quant il est desaluez dou tot, si covient que tu faices seoir le malaide droit, et le tigne I ministres fors par la jambe, desus la cheville;	And when it is dislocated completely, then you must have the patient sit upright, and hold him down by one minister by the leg, above the ankle;
puis trai le piet a toi a ta main destre, et puis a la senestre II fois, puis l’estent en haut, et boute bellement lou piet en haut;	Then treat the foot with your right hand, then with your left twice, then extend it upwards, and push the foot up nicely. 
et fai ce II fois, si com nos avons dit, em boutant et en traiant lou piet;	and do this twice, as we have said, by pushing and pulling the foot; 
s’elle revient, c’est bien;	If it returns, that's good; 
se ce non, si rencomence l’ovraige, car il revient;	if not, begin the work again, for it will return.  
et s’il ne puet revenir ensi, si fai gesir lou malaide sor son dos sus terre, et fiche I passeil fermement en terre entre ses cuixes, et lie drapelz entor, qu’il ne blece lou malaide;	and if it cannot return this way, then make the patient lie on their back on the ground, and stick a  rail firmly into the ground between their hips, and tie cloths around it so that it doesn't move the patient.
puis teigne li ministres la cuixe, et uns autres ministres estende lou piet a ses mains ou a I liien, k’il lie sus le col dou piet;	then hold the hips with ministers, and other ministers extend the foot to their hands or to the rail so that they tie it above the ankle.
puis estende chescuns ministres igalment, et li passelz soit adés entre les cuixes dou malaide por retenir le malaide quant on l’estent;	then extend each minister equally, and the rail should be placed between the hips of the patient to hold them down while being extended.
puis mette li mires igal la dislocation a ses mains, et uns autres ministres teigne la jambe sainne au desoz, et li dislocation revenra hastanment.	Then put the mire equal the dislocation with his hands, and others ministers hold the sound leg at the groin, and the dislocation will return easily. 
Et quant elle iert a point, si met l’emplastre et estoupes sus, et l’estrain forment, et lie lou piet a la jambe, et warde les ners qui sont sus la cheville derrier, que li liiens ne soit trop estrois;	And when it is pointed, put the plaster and stoppings on top, and the strain forms, and tie the foot to the leg, and guard the nerves that are above the ankle behind, so that the bonds are not too tight. 
puis le laisse II jors ou III, et se li liiens amolist, si l’estrain;	Then let him leave it for two or three days, and if the bonds soften, tighten them again.
puis le deslie au tier jor ou au quart, et deffent a aler lou malaide par IIII jors;	Then unbind on the third day or the fourth, and forbid the patient from walking for four days. 
et s’il va devant cel termine, ce n’est mie seurtez qu’il ne desalue encor.	And if he goes before that term, it is not certain that it will not dislocate again.  
Et se apostemes chaus i vient, si covient que tu l’apaises, si com nos avons dit autre part, tant qu’il soit sanez.	And if an abscess comes to it then you must soothe it as we have said elsewhere until it is healed.
des dois	of two
Quant li doi sont desaluez, si les covient bellement estendre sens travail, et c’est legiere chose.	When the hips are dislocated, it is necessary to extend them well without effort, and it is a light thing.
Et se li dislocations est en aucun nout dou dos dou piet, si covient que tu faices seoir le malaide sus I leu plain ou sus .ie. table tot droit, et met ton piet sus ce qui apert de ces jointures, puis presse a ton piet forment, tant qu’il reviegne;	And if the dislocation is in any joint of the back or foot, then it behooves you to make the patient sit on a flat surface or on a table quite straight, and put your foot upon what separates the joints, then press with your foot firmly, until it comes back. 
et quant il est igalz, et il n’i apert nient, si met desoz la plante dou piet une table a II chiés, puis l’estrain forment, et le laisse III jors, puis le deslie;	And when it is aligned and there is nothing separating it, then put under the sole of the foot a board two hands wide, then restrain it firmly, and leave it for three days, then unbind it.  
et le fai reposer, tant qu’il soit sanez.	And make him rest until he is healed. 
de plaie et de dislocation ensamble	Of wounds and dislocations together
Quant plaie vient avec la dislocation, et on la vuet restorer, maintes fois avient que li malaides muert:	When a wound comes with the dislocation, and it is wanted to restore it, many times it happens that the patient dies:
si ne soies mie presumptuous en la cure, se tu n’es saiges en l’art et tu ne l’as useit longement, et se tu n’es pitous et misericors et tardis, ne mie hardis;	if you are not modest in the cure, if you are not wise in the art and have not used it for a long time, and if you are not compassionate and merciful and patient, nor too bold; 
et use au comencement de choses apaisans aposteme chaut, et laisse le malaide en la main Deu, se tu n’i vois esperance de santeit;	and use at the beginning of things soothing poultices hot, and leave the patient in God's hands, if you do not see hope of health; 
et quant tu i vois esperance, si ramoinne maintenant le membre au leu, ainsois que li apostemes chaus i viegne;	and when you see hope in it, then set the limb now to its place, so that the abscess may come to a head there;  
et quant li membres est a leu, si aministre choses apaisans aposteme chaut, et cure la plaie, si com il covient, d’oignemens desiccatis;	and when the limb is in place, then administer soothing poultices hot, and treat the wound as it is necessary, with dried dressings; 
et se avec la dislocation a brisure, et os menus desevrez, si les oste, et fai ce que nos avons dit en maladies simples;	and if with the dislocation there is a fracture, and small bones are dislocated, set them, and do what we have said in simple ailments; 
et te garde d’entrer en voie de paour, selonc ce que j’ai dit, car ce te vaut mues selonc ton Creator, et por la saveteit de t’arme et de ton cors.	And guard yourself from entering into the way of fear, according to what I have said, for it brings you misfortune according to your Creator, and for the safety of your arm and your body.
